When solution of belly comes from cold and moisture, as much as the retentive and digestive virtues which are in the stomach and in the intestine is debilitated, and cannot be cured by ways of cures; and you see the patient suffering well and of great virtue, then make one large cautery on the stomach according to what we have spoken about before or cautery of the stomach, at the circulating cautery; and four cauteries around the navel subtle to each cautery clavicle subtle, and two cauteries on the loins.
Et se tu vois les moistors habundans et le malaide soffrant, se li fai cautere sus le poignil, et .i. cautere sus chaicun yle, et .ij. petis cauteres sus l’estomac delez le grant, car li cure est profitans quant il i a bone aide.	And if you see the humors abundant and the patient suffering, make cautery on the groin, and one cautery on each hip, and two small cauteries on the stomach near the great one, because the cure is profitable when there is good aid.
de la cure des emorroydes	Of the cure of hemorrhoids
Quant les emorroydes sont ou fondement, ou une ou plusors, et sont ancienes et sont de grosses humors froides et moistes corrumpues, et sont curees si com nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne profite mie, si fai cauteres: .iij. sus l’espine dou dos, celi qui est tout defuers desoz almecdate poc et poc en triangulant, et .i. cautere desoz la boude. ij. dois;	When hemorrhoids are at the base or more, and they are old and large humors cold and moist corrupted, and they have been treated as we have said in divisions, and if it does not benefit, then make cauteries: three on the spine of the back, this one which is all outside below the waist a little and little in triangulating, and one cautery below the buttock two fingers.
et se tu penses que ses estomac soit refroidiez, et li viande ne cuise, et on voit enfler la faice, adonques li faice on .i. grant cautere sus le stomac, si com il est devant dit, et .i. autre sus le foie, et i. autre sus la mice a tout le cautere clavile; et laisse le cautere overt lonc tens. Aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you think that his stomach is chilled, and the meat does not cook, and you see the face swelling, then on the face make one large cautery on the stomach, as it was said before, and one other on the liver, and one other on the mouse to the whole shoulder cauterization; and leave the cautery open long time. After cure the place as long as it is healed.
de la charnositeit qui est nommee «thelul»	of the fleshy tissue which is called "thelul"
Quant tu copes althelul, si eschaufe le cautere qui semble .i. raseur, et puis le met tout embraseit sus cel althelul copeit; et i laisse tant ta main que li cauteres viegne a la naissance de la voine, de coi li sans cort; fai ceu une fois ou .ij., et s’il i a mout d’althelul, si cauterize chaicun si com nos avons dit; aprés les cure d’oignemens profitans tant qu’il soient sanez; et se tu cauterizes d’un cautere grant sus alchatim, si avra plus grant aide.	When you cut "thelul", if the cautery seems like a razor, then put it all blazing on that "thelul" cut; and leave it there as long as the cautery reaches the base of the vein, so the blood doesn't flow; do this once or twice, and if there is much "thelul," cauterize each one as we have said; after the cure of wounds benefitting until they are healed; and if you cauterize with a large cautery on the skin, it will have more help.
de plaie mal curee	of a poorly healed wound
Quant li malaides ne puet soffrir tailleure ne overture, que nos raconterons en son leu, si vient teil maladie que ne puet estre sanee fuer que par cautere.	When the patient cannot suffer from cutting or opening, which we will recount in its place, there comes such a sickness that can only be healed by cautery.
Quant a aucun vient fistule, et est enveillie et giete porriture et moistors corrumpues, si la doies prover a tot une tente subtil, et garde que tu saiches a tot la tente combien elle a de parfont. Aprés eschaufe le cautere qui semble .i. raseur, et le boute en la fistule selonc la quantiteit que li tente i est entrée, et rencomence lou cautere tant que cil cors porris et corrumpus soient ars, une fois, ou .ij. ou .iij., selonc la quantiteit de som besoing; et te warde d’ardre lé nerf qui sunt enqui, et des grans voinnes. se li fistule vait au cors de la vesie et a l’intestine, si te warde de ces leus, et ne faire ceu fuers que en leu charnut, et pense qu’ele n’est mie persans; aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez, et se li leus est saielez, et les matieres sont ostees lonc tens, adonc saiches que li leus est sanez entierement; et se les matieres ne sont ostees, saiche que li leus est troez, et corrumpus li os au font; et ensi com un de ces que nos dirons en son leu.	When a fistula comes to one, and is filled with putrefaction and corrupted moisture, so the doer must prove with all haste a probe fine, and guard that he knows with all haste the probe how much it has of length. After burnish the cautery which seems as a razor, and thrust it into the fistula according to the quantity that the probe is entered, and re-begin the cautery until that corrupt flesh and corrupted are burned, once, or two, or three, according to the quantity of need; and guard not to wound the nerve that are in there, and the great veins. If the fistula goes to the body of the bladder and the intestine, so guard those places, and do not make those wounds except in their flesh, and think that it is not through; after cure the place as long as it is sound, and if the place is sealed, and the materials are removed long time, then know that the place is sound entirely; and if the materials are not removed, know that the place is diseased, and corrupted the bones at the root; and thus as one of these that we shall say in its place.
de la maladie des reins	Of the sickness of the kidneys
Quant dolor de froit vient as rains, et de grosse ventositeit, et ne prent talant de femme, adonc covient il que tu li fais cautere sus les rains d’une part et d’autre au cautere clavile que nos avons devant dit; et se nos le cauterizons em mileu, si avra .iij. cauteres en ligne, et se feront plus grant aide.	When pain from cold comes to the reins, and from great flatulence, and does not take talant of woman, then it is necessary that you make a cautery on the reins on both sides with the cautery clavile that we have said before; and if we cauterize them in the middle, then there will be three cauteries in a line, and they will do more great aid.
de la vessie	of the bladder
Quant li vessie est mole et foible de froit et de moistor, si que li malaides retient l’urine, adonc li fai cautere en la partie defuers sus la vessie, la ou encomencent li poil dou poignil, et .i. a destre et .i. a senestre, et soit chescuns cauteres si lons com li nous d’un poce; et li fais .i. cautere defuers le dos, ou .ij. se tu en as besoing; et soit li cauteres clavile selon la forme devant dite.	When the bladder is soft and weak from cold and moisture, so that the patient retains urine, then make a cautery in the part outside above the bladder, where the hairs of the groin begin, and one on the right and one on the left, and let each cautery be as long as a thumb; and make one cautery outside the back, or two if you need it; and let the cauteries be clavil according to the form previously stated.
de la marris	of the groin
Quant li marrix est froide et moiste, et ne laisse mie por ceu a concevoir, et les flors sont corrumpues et lor termines tarde; et quant elles vienent, si sent grant dolor: adonques covient il c’on li faice .iij. cauteres entor la boude, si com nos avons dit ou cautere de la vessie, et .ij. cauteres defuers le dos; et soit li cauteres clavile, si com nos avons dit.	When the groin is cold and moist, and does not allow for conception because of it, and the flowers are corrupted and their ends are slow; and when they come, there is great pain: therefore it is necessary to make three cauteries around the mound, as we have said about the cautery of the bladder, and two cauteries outside the back; and let the cauteries be clavil, as we have said.
de la hainche	of the hip
Quant les moistors viscouses dessendent a la boiste de la hainche, et por ceste cause si se muet de son leu, et li signes est que li cuisse est plus longe que li autre quant on le mesure ensamble; et est trovez li leus dou departement vuis, si covient que tu cauterizes le malaide sus la boiste de la hainche a .i. cautere semblant au cercle, et seigne devant le leu entor la boiste si com elle torne, si que li boiste soit dedens le cercle; et si soit li cauteres telz com cil dont on a cauterizeit le stomac.	When the viscous humors descend to the joint of the hip, and for this cause it moves from its place, and the sign is that the thigh is longer than the other when one measures them together; and is found the seat of the viscus, then it is necessary that you cauterize the patient on the joint of the hip at i. a cautery resembling the circle, and sign before the place around the joint as she turns, so that the joint be inside the circle; and if so be the cautery such as those with which one has cauterized the stomach.
Et se cist cauteres ne t’est presens, se li fai .iij. cauteres de l’olivaire grans, et soit li cauteres ausi parfont com tous li keurs; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if this cautery is not present to you, make iij. cauteries of the olive large, and be the cautery also perfect as all the others; and the cure until it be healthy.
de la dolor de la hainche	of the pain of the hip
Quant dolor vient en la boiste de la hainche, et c’est de froidor et de moistor, et li malaides est curez de ceu que nos avons dit en la division et li cure ne vaut, et li maladie est anciene: adonc covient il que tu purges le malaide des grosses humors de pilules fetides, ou autres pilules bones semblans.	When pain comes in the hip joint, and it is from cold and moisture, and the patient is treated with what we have said in the division and the cure does not work, and the illness is old: then it is necessary that you purge the patient of thick humors with fetid pills, or other good-seeming pills.
Aprés li fai cautere; et li maniere dou cautere si est selonc .ij. manieres: c’est a savoir ensamble medicines ardans, et cautere de feu. Cautere de feu si est selonc mout de manieres, desquelz li uns est telz: que tu cauterize sus la boiste de la hainche .iij. cauteres triangulalz selonc ceste forme, et i fai bone profunditeit et grant, et ait entre chaicun cautere d’espaice la groissece d’un doi, et soit li cauteres olivaire; aucune fois fait on cautere en mileu sus lou chief de la hainche, por coi il en i a .iiij. selonc ceste forme:	After the fire cautery; and the manner of the cautery is according to two manners: that is to say, together with burning medicines, and fire cautery. Fire cautery is according to many manners, some of which are such: that you cauterize on the hip joint three triangular cauteries according to this form, and make a good depth and width, and have between each cautery a space the size of a finger, and let the cauteries be olive-shaped; sometimes one makes a cautery in the middle on the head of the hip, so there are four according to this form:
Et se tu vues, si le cauterize au cautere dou cercle que nos avons devant dit en la dislocation de la hainche; mais fai en teil maniere que li cercles conteigne toute la hainche, et tous li espés dou keur soit ars.	And if you wish, cauterize with the circular cautery that we have mentioned before in the dislocation of the hip; but make it in such a manner that the circle contains the whole hip, and all the spaces of the core be burned.
Et c’est li maniere c’on fait en sciatique, quant li dolor tient en la hainche, et ne parvient mie jusc’a la cuisse ne jusc’a la jambe. Et s’ele vient jusc’a la cuisse et la jambe, se li fai .ij. cauteres lai ou li malaides dit que li dolor li tient, et .i. cautere desus la cheville .iiij. dois, a la partie senestre un poc; et soit li cauteres cutellaire, et soit arse li espesseté dou keur; et se li malaides sent que li dolor s’estende jusc’a dois dou piet ou pres d’enqui, se le cauterize la ou il sent la dolor .iij. poins ou .iiij. au cautere qui est apelez «poins».	And this is the manner in which it is done in sciatica, when the pain holds in the hip, and does not reach to the thigh nor to the leg. And if it comes to the thigh and the leg, then one makes .ij. cauteries there where the patient says that the pain holds him, and .i. cautery above the ankle .iiij. fingers, at the left side a little; and let the cauteries be cuticular, and let them be burned with the thickness of the heart; and if the patient feels that the pain extends to two fingers of the foot or near it, then he cauterizes where he feels the pain .iij. points or .iiij. at the cautery which is called «points».
Et se mestiers est, se li en fai plus; et se il seit que li dolor soit desoz le genoil vers la cuisse, se li fais cautere au cautere cutellaire ou circulaire, et te done bien garde en tous tes cauteres que tu n’i lassier mie tant le cautere que tu brules les ners et les grans arteres, et que tu ne faices au malaide plus grant nuisance et contraction.	And if the need is, then one does more; and if it seems to him that the pain is below the knee towards the thigh, then he makes cautery with the cuticular or circular cautery, and take good care in all your cauteries that you do not leave any of the cautery there than you burn the nerves and the great arteries, and that you do not make more nuisance and contraction to the patient.
Et je meisme ai veus plusors qui ont fait cautere sus la cheville dou piet, et li lasserent tant que li jambe fut toute enflee, et li piez ausi, et fut perciez et corrumpus toz li piez. Aprés une solution de ventre dont il ot la mort.	And I myself have seen many who made cautery on the ankle of the foot, and left it so long that the leg was all swollen, and the foot too, and was pierced and corrupted all the foot. After a bellyache of which he died.
Et se li dolors est en .ij. parties ensamble, fai cautere en l’une et en l’autre, selonc ceste maniere. // Et li saige dirent en la cautere de la hainche, de coi ci est li maniere, fai .i. tel fer et soit au chief ausi gros com uns nauvillon de dacte, ou un poc moins, et soit par entrechetres et soit des l’un entrechetres jusc’a l’autre d’espaice la quantiteit d’un nou de poce; et soient li entrechetres aovers de .ij. pars, et soient aussi comme noez, et i ait .i. mainche de fer bien fait; et c’est li forme:	And if the pain is in two parts together, make cautery in one and the other, according to this manner. // And the wise men say about cautery of the hip, from this is the manner, make one such iron and be at the head as large as a thimble of a finger, or a little less, and be by interspaces and be from one interspace to the other of space the quantity of a node of the finger; and be the interspaces toward two parts, and be also like nuts, and there be one hand made of iron well; and this is the form:
Et soit eschaufez tant qu’il soit toz rouges et giete senteles, et puis le mette on sus la boiste de la hainche malaide, et soit tornez sus lou sain costeit; et lou cauterize une fois .i. cautere reont et lou laisse .iij. jors; et puis fai emplaustre de burre, et laisse la plaie aoverte lonc tens; aprés la cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	And be heated until it is all red and you feel it, and then put it on the bone of the diseased hip, and be turned onto the healthy side; and cauterize once one cautery rent and leave it three days; and then make a plaster of butter, and leave the wound covered for a long time; after the cure of ointment until it is healed.
Albucasim dit que nos usons poc de cest cautere por la paor de son regart, et se voions poc qui en usent; et toutevoie ceu est des boins cauteres, qui le puet soffrir, et lai ou il s’afiert.	Albucasim says that we use little of this cautery out of fear of its regard, and we see few who use it; and nonetheless these are good cauteries, which he can suffer, and where it is needed.
de la dolor dou dos	of the pain of the back
Quant dolor vient au dos, ou par cheoir ou de percussion ou par trop grant evacuation, ou par semblans de matiere espandue froide, a nule de ces semblances ne vaut cauteres, fuer que a celi qui vient de infusion de froide matiere.	When pain comes to the back, whether by falling or percussion or by too great evacuation, or by seeming of matter spread cold, none of these appearances is worth cautery, except for that which comes from infusion of cold matter.
Il covient c’aprés ceu que li malaides est voidiez de pilules fetides ou d’autres semblans, que on li faice sus lou dos, lai ou li dolor tient, trois lignes signies d’enche, et en chescune ligne .v. cauteres ou plus selonc la vertut et la quantiteit que li malaides puet soffrir; et soit fait li cauteres selonc le cautere qui est apelez «poins»; et se tu vues, fai .iij. cauteres ou .iiij. au cautere clavile moien selonc ceste forme:	It is necessary after that the patient is void of fetid pills or other appearances, that one makes on him over his back, where the pain holds, three lines marked with enche, and in each line five cauteries or more according to the virtue and quantity that the patient can suffer; and be made the cautery according to the cautery which is called "poins"; and if you see, make three or four cauteries at the clavile cautery mean according to this form:
Maintes fois vient ceste maladie as petis enfans, et li signes de l’encomencement si est qu’il ont estroite alainne quant il se lievent, et paor; et tu trueves en la derriene espinee dou dos et en nous l’apparance qui vient sus les autres espinees.	Many times this malady comes as to small children, and the signs of the beginning is that they have a narrow  a**l*in when they lie down, and fear; and you find in the last spine of the back and in us the appearance which comes upon the other spines.
Quant tu vois ceu et tu le vues curer, si le cauterize au cautere de celcle selonc ceste forme.	When you see this and you view it being cured, if you cauterize it with the cautery of this according to this form.
Si que li cautere porpreigne chescune partie de l’espinee egaument. Et se tu vues, si cauterize entor l’espinee au cautere poignant .ij. lignes ou .iij., et soient li poins pres l’uns de l’autre. Aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez selonc ceu que nos avons dit, et warde que tu n’amenistrer cautere en gilbositeit qui soit en spame de nerf.	So that the cautery pricks each part of the spine equally. And if you see it, cauterize around the spine with the pointed cautery 2 or 3 lines, and let the points be near one another. After cure the place as long as it is healed according to what we have said, and beware that you do not bring cautery in a place which is in the nerve's span.
de la dolor des jointes	of the pain of the joints
Quant dolor de jointes sunt de moistors que sont espandues a chaicun membre dou cors, et quant dolor vient em piez, que li mire apelent «podagre» proprement, et quant elle est de froide cause et cures de medicines ne la puent curer, si est curez par cauteres en teil maniere: fai li mout de cauteres entor la jointure dou piet, et soit li cauteres olivaire selonc ceste forme:	When the pain of the joints is from moisture which are spread to each limb of the body, and when the pain comes in the feet, that the mire call "podagra" properly, and when it is from a cold cause and cures of medicines can not cure it, then it is cured by cauteries in this manner: make the mound of cauteries around the joint of the foot, and let the cautery be olive-shaped according to this form:
Et s’il i a besoigne que tu poignes sus la faice dou piet, se li fai cautere a tot le cautere c’on claime «point». Et se les dolors viegnent jusc’a genous et as autres jointures, et ceu avient maintes fois, se li fai cautere sus chaicun genoil .iij. cauteres ou .iiij. de chescunne partie, a tout le cautere olivaire; et se tu as mestier de plus, si en fai plus, mais n’i tenir mie ta main fuers que tant que li espés dou keur soit ars.	And if there is need that you burn on the face of the foot, if to the whole cautery one claims "point". And if the pains come up to the knees and other joints, and this happens many times, if to each knee three or four cauteries of every part, to the whole olive cautery; and if you have need of more, make more, but do not hold your hand away from it for long than the edge of the heart is burned.
Et se les dolors dessendent jusc’a genoil et au dos, se li aministre le cautere que nos avons dit en son chapistre. Et se les dolors sunt as mains, si fai poins entor le foscile .ij. lignes; et s’il remaint point de dolor as dois, si fai poins sus chescune jointe et sus lou poil de la main; et se les dolors vienent jusc’as coutes ou jusc’as espaules, si cauterize chescune partie, et fai boin governement au malaide et penre medicines. Car se tu li fais boin governement et tu purges fleume, si sera saneis a l’aide de Deu.	And if the pains descend to the knee and back, administer the cautery that we have said in our chapter. And if the pains are in the hands, make points around the fossa two lines; and if there remains no pain in the arms, make points on each joint and on the hair of the hand; and if the pains come up to the ribs or shoulders, cauterize each part, and make good government of the patient and prescribe medicines. Because if you make good government of him and purge phlegm, he will be healed with the help of God.
de la routure dou syfac	of the rupture of the sciatica
Quant routure vient en angres, et li bouelz dessendent as coions et c’est novelement, si covient que quant tu lou vues curer, qu’il ne menjuce mie celui jor; et qu’il use choses qui laichent lou ventre, si que li fiens dessende de son ventre; aprés le fai seoir sus son dos entre tes mains, et li comande qu’il teigne son alaine tant que li boueil soient repairiet, et les ramoinne a tes dois, et seigne d’enche desoz la routure sus l’os dou poignil, et a tout un signe que soit semblans a la moitiet d’un cercle a desus dou cors; puis eschaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	When a rupture comes in the groin and the bowels descend to the thighs and this is new, it is necessary that when you see it cured, it should not be disturbed on that day; and that he use things which lay the belly flat, so that the entrails descend from his belly; after the fat sits on his back between your hands, and command him to hold his arm as long as the bowels are repaired, and move them to your heels, and sign on under the rupture above the bone of the hip, and at a whole mark which is similar to half a circle above the body; then heat the cautery of which this is the form:
tant qu’il soit blans et qu’il giete senteles. Puis ramoine les bouels a lor leu; et li ministres teigne sa main sus qu’il ne retornent arrier; et oevre bien les cuisses au malaide, et met desoz lui .i. cussin et .i. serjant sus les cuisses, et .i. autre sus lou pis qui li teigne les mains; puis met le cautere sus lou signe a tout ta main, et lou tien droit et lou tien tant que tu ateignes l’os, et se tu ne l’ateins la premiere fois, si le rencomence encor une autre tant que tu viegnes jusc’a l’os; et te warde subtilment que li boueil ne saille quant tu fais lou cautere; que tu ne le brulasses; et que par ceu li malaides ne muere, ou autre malz.	until it is white and that it has felt the heat. Then move the bowels back to their place; and the minister holds his hand over them so they do not return backward; and operate well the thighs of the patient, and put under him one cushion and one bandage on the thighs, and one other on the leg which keeps his hands; then put the cautery on the sign with all your strength, and hold it straight and keep it until you reach the bone, and if you do not reach it the first time, start again another time until you come to the bone; and beware subtly that the bowel does not escape when you make the cautery; so that you do not burn it; and by this means that the patient does not die, or other harm.
Et saiches que quant tu ne viens jusc’a l’os au cautere, tes ovraiges ne vaut rien. Et covient que li cauteres des enfans soit subtilz selonc la mesure d’ous, et des grans gens aussi grans selonc lor mesure; aprés .iij. jors cure lou leu dou cautere de burre tant que li eschaudure soit ostee; aprés le cure d’autres oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez, et gise li malaides .xl. jors sus son dos tant que li plaie soit bien soudee; et covient que ses norrissemens soit lassatis longement, si que li boueil ne saillent quant il se preigdra d’aler en chambres.	And know that when you do not come to the bone with the cautery, your work is worth nothing. And it is necessary that the cauteries of children be subtle according to the measure of them, and of large people also large according to their measure; after three days cure the place of the cautery with butter until the inflammation is removed; after that, cure other ointments until it is healed, and lie the patient forty days on his back until the wound is well joined; and it is necessary that its bandages be laid long so that the bowel does not escape when he gets up to go into rooms.
Et aprés .xl. jors, quant il se voudra lever, se li amenistre une faixe bien faite, et la porse .xl. autres jors; et ait boin repos, qu’il se travaille poc et se warde de trop grant repletion de boivre et de mengier, et de trop haut braire; et quant il fait cest enseignement si est sanez entierement. Et je dirai ci aprés la cure de taillier en son chapistre.	And after forty days, when he wants to get up, he is given a well-made splint, and wear it for another forty days; and have good rest, that he does not work too much and keep away from excessive drinking and eating, and from too much braiding; and when he follows this teaching he will be completely healed. And I will say here after the treatment of the thigh in its chapter.
de la routure dou ventre	of the rupture of the belly
Quant routures vienent en autres ventres et sont connisans, et tu vues qu’elles ne croissent plus, se li fai .j. cautere dou cautere reont selonc sa quantiteit, et soit ars li tiers dou keur; aprés le cure selonc ceu que nos avons dit; et aucun des anciens ont dit c’on le doit cauterizer au cautere a .iij. angles selonc ceste forme:	When ruptures come in other bellies and are recognized, and you see that they do not grow anymore, make one cautery of the cautery according to its quantity, and be it at the third of the heart; after the cure according to what we have said; and none of the ancients said that one should cauterize with a cautery in three angles according to this form:
mais signe premier le leu d’enche et fai une ligne per la largesce desus la routure, et une autre defuers, et main ta main emmi a tout le cautere clavile. Mais li premiers cauteres est plus legiers et muedres.	but first sign the place of the incision and make a line through the width above the rupture, and another below, and hold your hand over the entire cautery clavicle. But the first cauteries are lighter and more movable.
de dolor anciene en aucun membre	of old pain in any limb
Quant dolor vient en aucun membre, ou de cheoir ou de ferir, et cele dolor tient lonc tens, et li cure de medicine n’i vaut, adonc covient qu’il soit cauterizeis au cautere qui est apelez «poins», et soit li cauteres selonc la longesce dou membre et la petitece et sa foibleteit et sa vertut et sa location de torcions et de sa dolor. s’il est sanez dou premier cautere, c’est bien; se ceu nom, recomence .i. autre cautere sus celui, car teilz costume est qu’il se doit muer au membre que li est prochiens, por coi il covient que tu faices les cauteres tant que li malaides soit saneis.	When pain comes in any limb, whether from falling or being struck, and this pain lasts a long time, and the cure of medicine is not effective, then it is necessary that it be cauterized with the cautery called "point," and let the cautery be according to the length of the limb and its smallness and weakness and its virtue and its location of twists and its pain. If it is healed by the first cautery, that is good; if not, begin another cautery above the one, because such is the custom that it must change in the limb that is close to it, therefore you must do the cauteries as long as the patient is not healed.
de meselerie	of melting
Li meseil sont aidiet aucune fois par cautere par grant aide, et meismement li maladie que vient de la putrefaction de fleume et de melancolie. Cant tu la vues cauterizer, pren warde se li maladie est au comencement, et s’ele est curee selonc ceu que nos avons dit en la division, et ne dessent ne ne demoure, et tu doutes que li corruption ne porpreigne tout le malaide, adonques li fai .v. cauteres sus lou chief: .i. emmi le chief a nouf, et l’autre vers lou front a la fin des chevous; et .ij. sus les .ij. cornes, et .i. derrierre sus le haiterel; et i laise tant ta main que li cauteres viegne jusc’a l’os, et tant que les escorces en issent fors si que les vapors des grosses humors s’en puissent issir; et le cauterize sus la mice selonc ce qu’il est devant.	The melting are aided some times by cautery with great help, and even the sick person who comes from the putrefaction of phlegm and melancholy.  Since you see them cauterized, take care if the sickness is at the beginning, and if it is cured according to what we have said in the division, and do not send nor stay, and you doubt that the corruption does not spread throughout the sick person, then make .v. cautery on the head: .i.  remove the head to nine, and the other towards the front at the end of the eyebrows; and .ij. on the .ij. horns, and .i. behind on the back of the head; and leave so your hand that the cauteries come until the bone, and as long as the scours exit outwards so that the vapors of the gross humors can issue; and cauterize on the mouse according to what it is before.
Et se li meselerie est partout esparse; et elle pert manifestement, si covient que tu lou cauterizes de ces cauteres que nos avons dit ou chief, et .i. cautere en som lou neis, et .ij. cauteres sus l’espinee dou col, et .vj. cauteres sus l’espinee dou dos, et .i. grant sus la crupie et .i. autre delez, et .ij. sus les .ij. espaules; et .ij. sus les coutes, et .ij. sus les tendrons dou pis, et .i. sus chascune jointe des mains et des piez, et sus les fosses des mains; et te warde des ners que sunt sus lou derrien calcant, que tu ne les bruler; et aucune fois fait om cautere sus l’os dou poignil, et .i. autre sus l’os de l’estomac, et .i. autre sus lou foie.	And if the melting is spread everywhere; and it manifests clearly, then it is necessary that you cauterize it with these cautery that we have said on the head, and .i. cautery in some of the neck, and .ij. cautery on the spine of the neck, and .vj. cautery on the spine of the back, and .i. large one on the hip and .i. other of the buttock, and .ij. on the .ij. shoulders; and .ij. on the elbows, and .ij. on the tendons of the thigh, and .i. on each joint of the hands and feet, and on the hollows of the hands; and take care of the nerves that are on the back of the heel, that you do not burn them; and sometimes it is done cautery on the bone of the shoulder blade, and .i. other one on the bone of the stomach, and .i. other one on the liver.
Et saiches que quant plus i fais de cautere, plus li fais d’aide, et mues li profite; et saiches que li malaides ne sent point de dolor au cautere si com li sain le sentent, por ce que li cors est ja toz corrumpus. Et covient ke li cautere soient grant et petit selonc les membres et les jointures, selonc ceu que vos lou troverez en manieres des fers. Aprés cure lou leu de farine de veces avec miel et autres cures tant qu’il soit saneis.	And know that when more cautery is done, the more it helps, and it profits them; and know that the patient does not feel any pain from the cautery as healthy people feel it, for the body is already wholly corrupt. And it is necessary that the cautery be large and small according to the members and joints, according to what you will find in manners of irons. After the cure, cover it with flour of quince with honey and other cures until it is healed.
de enfleure	of swelling
Quant enfleure vient en aucun membre et est curee par medicines et oiles et emplastres, et il n’est mie sanez, adonques li fai cauteres sus le membre selonc la grandour et la petitece dou membre; et soit li cauteres un poc entrans en l’espés dou keur; puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez. Et aucune fois fait on cautere et a la main et au piet et au dos, a l’issue dou nerf que muet le membre, et ensi si est ostee li enfleure; et toutevoie ne s’en entremette nuls s’il n’est conoissans des membres et des issues des ners movans lou cors.	When swelling comes in any limb and is cured by medicines and oils and plasters, and it is not healed, then I make cauteries on the limb according to the size and smallness of the limb; and let the cautery be a point going into the thickness of the flesh. Then cure with ointments until it is healed. And sometimes one makes cautery and in the hand and foot and back, at the exit of the nerve that moves the limb, and thus the swelling is removed; but nonetheless, no one should intervene except someone who knows the members and the exits of the nerves moving the body.
de albaras	of bandages
Quant li maladie qui est apelee «albaras» est enveillie, et li engien de medicine n’i valent rien, adonques le cauterize d’un cautere un poc parfont, selonc la quantiteit de l’espés dou keur, tant que li blenchour soit ostee, et soit muee sa color; puis le cure de farine de veces et de lentilles avec oile roset et foilles de plantain, et sanc de colon et sanc d’alondre, de chescun une partie; et soit mellez tout ensamble, et soit liiez d’un drapel, et soit aers au leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the ailment called «albaras» is present and medicines do not help, then cauterize it with a cautery in a place according to the quantity of the sickness, until the swelling is removed, and its color has changed; then treat it with flour of chickpeas and lentils with rose oil and plantain leaves, and blood of colon and blood of alondre, each one part; and mix everything together, and bind it with a cloth, and air it in place until it is healed.
li cure de chancre par cautere	the treatment of syphilis by cautery
Quant chancre vient au comencement, et tu lou vues arrester, si le cauterize au cautere qui semble .i. cercle, tout entor au tour dou chancre.  Et toutevoie li saige dirent que on faice cautere ausi au mileu dou chancre; et toutevoie ceu ne me semble mie boin, car je redous que il ne soit ulcerez et corrumpus, et je l’ai ja veut avenir aucune fois; et plus droituriere chose est qu’il soit cauteriés entor, au cautere qui est apelez «circule», si com nos avons dit en mout de cauteres.	When syphilis appears at the beginning, and you want to stop it, then cauterize it with a cautery that resembles a circle, all around the edge of the chancre. And nonetheless, wise men say that one should cauterize also in the middle of the chancre; and nonetheless, this does not seem good to me, because I fear that it will be ulcerated and corrupted, and I have never wanted it to happen any time; and a more correct thing is that it be cauterized around, with the cautery which is called «circule», as we said in many cauteries.
de l’enfleure qui ne puet meurer	of the swelling which cannot move
Quant aucuns ait une maladie qui est apelee «adubelati», et elle tarde de meurer ou por la superfluiteit qu’ele fait ou por l’eaige dou malaide quant il est decrepites (c’est a dire trop vielz) et il a poc de sanc, ou por lou tens; et tu la vues haster de meurer: adonques le cauterize entor de mout de petis cauteres en poignant; aprés le laisse ensi. Car elle se hastera de meureir.	When someone has a disease called "adubelati," and it is slow to heal, or because of the superfluity it produces, or because of the blood of the sick person when he is decrepit (that is to say too old) and he has little blood, or because of the tension; and you see it hasten to heal: then cauterize it around with many small cauteries by pricking; afterwards leave it so. For it will hasten to heal.
Et se tu la vues percier a tout le cautere, si chaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	And if you see it fester all over the cautery, then heat the cautery with what is the shape:
Et met ta main en mileu de cele maladie qui est apellee «adubelati» tant que li cauteres ait perciet lou keur, et soit telz li cauteres que li malaides lou sente defuers en teil maniere que li cours de la porriture soit alegis. Aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	And put your hand in the middle of this disease which is called "adubelati" until the cauteries have pierced the core, and let the cauteries be such that the sick person feels them from outside in such a way that the course of the decay is alleviated. Afterwards cure it as long as it is perfectly healed.
li cure dou feu par fer	The cure of fire by iron
Une autre maniere de maladie i a qui est apelee «corrodens», et n’est autre chose que une mengeson de membre, car ele menjut les membres ausi com li feus les leignes seches. Se tu vois ceste maladie en leu qui puisse soffrir cautere ensamble feu, adonques eschaufe les cauteres clavile mout petit et grant, selonc ceu qu’il covient au leu ou li maladie est; aprés le cauterize de toutes pars tant que tu erraiche toute la corruption, et nen remaigne rien de li, que tout ceu qui est corrumpus ne soit osteit. Et puis le laisse .iij. jors, et met sus les leus cauterizez soffre broiet avec oile tant que les eschaudures dou feu soient ostees, et toute li corruption. Aprés lou cure d’oignemens engendrans char.  Et se tu vois aprés .iij. jors que chars saine ne naisse, c’est boin; et se ceu non, si rencomence le cautere sus ceu qui est demoreit des leus corrumpus. Et ceste mengeson est aucune fois esteit curee de medicine ague en leu de cautere de feu; mais toutevoie cautere de feu est de plus grant aide, et j’ai ja dit la cure de la medicine ague en la division: pren la quant tu en as mestier.	Another manner of illness there is which is called "corrodens", and is nothing else than a corruption of limb, because it consumes the limbs like fire consumes dry branches. If you see this illness in someone who can suffer cautery together with fire, then sear the cauteries small and large, according to what is fitting for the place where the illness is; after that cauterize all sides until you eradicate all corruption, and nothing of it remains, that all that is corrupted be removed. And then leave him .iij. days, and put on the cauterized places broiled with oil as long as the scours of fire are removed, and all the corruption. After the cure of ointment engendering flesh. And if you see after .iij. days that healthy flesh is born, it is good; and if not, then begin again the cautery on what remains corrupted from the places. And this corruption has been cured at times with medicine ague in place of fire cautery; but nonetheless, fire cautery is of greater help, and I have already said the cure of the medicine ague in the division: take it when you need it.
des porrelz qui vienent as piez	Of  spurts that come to the feet
Mout de fois avient que as piez par defuers naist une maladie qui est apelee «clos» selonc nostre entencion, et est une grosse chose fautree qui blece lou piet. Et li cauteres de ceste maladie si est selonc .ij. manieres. C’est a savoir cautere de feu, et cautere d’aigue chaude. Cautere de feu si est que tu eschaufe .i. cautere cheveit ausi com est une penne de vouteul, et soit fait de boin fer a la mesure qu’il puisse porpenre le clou de toutes pars, et qu’il i ait subtilz marges; aprés le met tout chaut sus lou clou, et torne ta main tot entor le clou tant qu’il viegne au font dou clou; et lou laisse ensi .iij. jors tant qu’il encomence giter porriture; puis li fai un emplaustre de malves savaiges broiies avec seil, et laisse l’emplaustre sus toute la nuit, et li clous cherra et sera desracinez de ses racines. Puis cure le leu d’oignement enjanrant char tant qu’il soit sanez.	Many times it happens that on the feet by fire is born a disease which is called “clos” according to our understanding, and it is a big thing faulted that bleaches the foot. And the cauteries of this disease are according to .ij. manners. This is to know cautery of fire, and cautery of hot water. Cautery of fire is that you heat .i. cautery like it is a feather of vouteul, and it be made of good iron at the measure that it can support the nail on all parts, and that it has subtle margins; after it puts all hot above the nail, and turn your hand around the nail until it comes to the bottom of the nail; and let it like this for .iij. days until it begins to get rotting; then I make a poultice of wild malves crushed with oil, and leave the poultice on all night, and the nails will fall and will be uprooted from their roots. Then cure the place with ointment healing flesh until it is healed.
Et s’il sont convertit par defuers lou cors, et maintes fois avient et en mains et em piez, si covient que tu i amenistres cautere d’aigue chaude; et est en teil maniere: pren une cainne d’arain ou de fer, ou une penne de vouteul, et met sus lou clou et l’althelul, c’est asavoir porrelz verrues; et met la cainne sus si qu’ele porpreigne tout entor, puis i met un poc d’awe chaude, et retien bien ta main, et presse ta main en tornant si que li marge de la cainne viegne a la racine dou clou, et puisse trover l’aigue chaude voie parfonde jusc’a la racine; et soffre li malaides un poc la mordication de l’aigue chaude une houre; puis le laisse ensi, et il se derracinera tous a tout ses racines. Ensi fai un aprés autre, tant que tu esraiches toz ces qui sont au cors, puis les cure des oignemens qui engenrent char.	And if they are converted by fire the body, and many times happen in hands and feet, then it is convenient that you bring them cautery of hot water; and is in this manner: take a can of iron or a feather of vouteul, and put on the nail and the althelul, that is to say pores warts; and put the can on so that it supports all around, then I put a pot of hot water, and hold your hand well, and press your hand turning so that the edge of the can comes to the root of the nail, and can find the hot water path deep until the root; and suffer the patient a little the burning of the hot water for an hour; then let it be like this, and it will break away from all its roots. Thus do one after another, as long as you eradicate all those who are in the body, then cure them with ointments that generate flesh.
li cure dou trembler	The cure of trembling
Quant aucuns tremble de froidor de ners, ou de fievre quartaine ou d’autre, si covient que tu li faices .iiij. cauteres ou .iv. sus l’espinee dou dos, .i. cautere entre chescune espinee; et .i. cautere ou pez, et .i. sus l’estomac au cautere olivaire; si laissera lou trembler, et se hastera li santez de la maladie froide.	When some tremble from cold or quartan fever or another, it is fitting that you make .iiij. cauteries or .iv. on the spine of the back, .i. cautery between each spine; and .i. cautery or pez, and .i. on the stomach at the olive cautery; so he will leave trembling, and hasten his health from the cold sickness.
des pustules puans	of pus-filled pustules
Aucune fois apperent par defuers le cors bathes, ou pustules puans, que vienent de grosses matieres corrumpues. si covient au premier quant eles apperent que on faice cautere sus chescun chief de la pustule: un cautere subtil de fust de mirte, de coi li pointe soit emprise au feu, ou de racine de aristologe longe, ou au cautere lenticulaire. Et aucune fois les cauterize on au comencement quant il aperent, selonc ceste maniere, et il ne puent croistre des enqui en avant, mais est desrompue li superfluitez dont il vienent, et sont sanez; mais il covient que ceu soit fait aprés l’evacuation de sanc.	Sometimes pustules appear by fire on the bathed body, or pus-filled pustules, which come from large corrupt matters. If at first when they appear that one makes a cautery on each head of the pustule: a subtle cautery of myrtle wood, so that the point is taken to the fire, or of a long aristolochia root, or at the lentil cautery. And sometimes those are cauterized at the beginning when they appear, according to this manner, and they cannot grow further from them, but the superfluities from which they come are broken up, and they are healed; but it is necessary that this be done after the evacuation of blood.
quant li artere est copee	when the artery is cut
Maintes fois avient grans decorremens de sanc de l’artere qui est copee a la plaie que vient au pardefuers, ou a l’incision de l’aposteme, ou au cautere dou membre, et as semblans choses; et est mout grief chose d’estenchier.	Many times there are great hemorrhages of blood from the artery that is cut at the wound that comes to the outside, or in the incision of the abscess, or in the cautery of the limb, and similar things; and it is a very grievous thing to prolong.
Et toutevoie quant ceu avient a aucun, si te haste de mettre ton doi indice sus la plaie de la voinne, et l’estrain mout tant que li sans soit apaisiez desoz ton doi, et que goute n’en isse plus; puis met au feu les cauteres olivaire plusors petis et grans tant qu’il soient tuit rouge; puis empren .i., ou grant ou petit selonc la plaie et lou leu en coi li artere est route, et met le cautere sus cele voine ou tu tiens ton doi, et tien le cautere tant sus que li sans soit restainchiez.	And nevertheless when this happens to anyone, hasten to place your finger index on the wound of the vein, and restrain it as much as possible until the bleeding is appeased under your finger, and no drop comes out anymore; then put the olive cauteries to the fire more small and large until they are all red; then take one, or a large one or small one according to the wound and its place where the artery is cut, and put the cautery on that vein where you hold your finger, and hold the cautery there as long as the bleeding is restrained.
Et s’il saut fuers quant tu lieves ton doi desus la voinne, et li cauteres estint, si pren hastivement .i. autre des cauteres qui sont au feu.	And if it jumps out when you lift your finger from the vein, and the cautery is extinguished, then take hastily one other of the cauteries that are in the fire.
Et ne cesser de faire ceu l’un aprés l’autre tant que li sans soit estenchiez; et warde que tu n’ardes lou nerf qui est delez, et que autre malice ne viegne sus lou malaide; et saiches que quant sans decourt de l’artere, c’on ne lou puet mie bien restenchier meismement quant li artere est grans, se ceu n’est par une des .iiij. manieres que nos avons dit: ou par cautere, ou par extraction quant ele n’est mie traite, ou par fort liement de fil, ou par medicines mises sus qui ont pooir de restenchier sanc; et soit liee et estrainte avennament.	And do not cease to do these one after the other until the vein is stretched; and guard that you do not burn the nerve which is beside it, and that another malice does not come upon the patient; and know that when the vein runs short of the artery, one cannot well stretch it even when the artery is large, unless by one of the .iiij. ways that we have said: or by cautery, or by extraction when it is not treated, or by a strong tying of thread, or by medicines put upon which have power to stretch the vein; and be bound and strained well.
Qui i amenistrera restenchement de liier estroitement de drapelz ou de metre choses ardans sus, ou autres semblans choses, se n’i profite se poc non.	Who will bring tightening of ligatures or tightly wrapped bandages, or putting hot things on, or similar things, if it does not profit them no.
Et se ce avient a aucun et il n’ait mie mire ne medicine present, si doit mettre son doi indice sus la plaie de la voinne si com nos avons dit, et bien estrendre tant qu’il soit restenchiez desus la plaie et desus la voinne; et ne remuer lou doit, mais lou moille d’awe froide sovent que soit mout froide tant que li sans soit congelez et engrossiez et restenchiez; et faice des enqui en avant ceu dont il a mestier de cauteres et de medicines.	And if this happens to anyone and they do not have any medicine present, then he must put his finger over the wound of the vein as we have said, and well tighten until it is stretched above the wound and above the vein; and do not move the finger, but frequently moisten with cold water so that it is very cold until the vein is frozen and thickened and stretched; and do those things in advance that are needed for cauteries and medicines.
Ci encomence li secons livre des cures de taille	Here begins the second book of the cures of surgery
Nos vos avons dit ou premier chapistre toute maladie en coi il covient cautere de feu, ou de medicine ardans, et les oquisons et les causes et les estrumens et les formes des cauteres; et ai mis celui chapistre des lou chief jusc’a piez, et je irai en cest chapistre par celi meisme voie por ceu c’on trueve plus legierement ceu c’on voura.	We have told you in the first chapter all diseases for which it is necessary to use fire cautery, or burning medicines, and the incisions and causes and instruments and forms of the cauteries; and I placed that chapter from the head down to the feet, and I will go in this chapter by the same way for those who find more easily what they want.
Et ainsois que je encomence ceu, il covient, chier fil, que vos aprenez que en cest chapistre a plus de peril et de paor que ou premier des cauteres, et por ceu il covient plus grant cautele.	And so, as I begin this, it is necessary, dear student, that you learn that in this chapter there is more danger and fear than in the first of the cauteries, and for that reason, greater caution is required.
Car en l’ovraige de cest chapistre avient maintes fois evacuation de sanc a l’ovrir la voinne, et a l’incision sus aposteme, et as cures des plaies, et a l’estraction des saiettes, et a l’incision sus la piere, et les semblans choses; ou il a doutance et paor, et en vient li mors a plusors.	For in the work of this chapter, there is often the evacuation of blood when opening a vein, and incising an abscess, and in the treatment of wounds, and in the extraction of arrows, and in cutting into stones, and similar things; where there is doubt and fear, and many die.
Et je vos amoneste que vos n’entreprenez folie. Car mout de manieres de gens vienent en cures. si vienent de telz qui s’aïrent si avec lor maladie qu’il muerent legierement por la forsenerie qu’il trueve de sa maladie, et de la grandour de son malice; et de ces doit on avoir paor.	And I warn you that you do not undertake folly. Because many kinds of people come to cures. There come those who are so consumed by their illness that they die easily because of the ignorance that they find in their sickness, and the greatness of their malice; and of these one must have fear.
Et de ces i a qui te done son sens, et dit: «atendez, je sui garis»; et li maladie est despitouse. Il ne covient mie que vos vos consentez a ces qui vienent a vos qui ont ceste maniere, mais mettez plus grant cusanson en vostre honor qu’en vostre covoitise, et n’ovrez mie folement mais saigement de ceu dont vos estes certain, et dont vos poez avoir pris et los; et usez de pronostication et de indication en cures de vos malaides a coi salus soit convertie; et ceu vos aidera a aquester bone renommee, et gloire, et memoire de loenge.	And of these there are those who give you their sense, and say: "Wait, I am cured"; and the illness is deceitful. It does not behoove that you consent to those who come to you who have this manner, but put more great caution in your honor than in your covetousness, and do not open blindly but wisely of those whom you are certain of, and whom you can have taken and praise; and use prognosis and indication in cures of your sick so that health may be converted; and these things will help you to acquire good reputation, and glory, and memory of length.
Tres chier fil, Nostres Sires vos doint boin entendement et droiture, et se vos vuelle espireir de la sainte inspiration de sa main, amen.	Very dear son, our Lords give you good understanding and rightness, and if you wish to aspire to the holy inspiration of His hand, Amen.
Or je vos ai ordeneit cest chapistre en devisant par chapistres, selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre des cauteres, que je vos ai deviseit des le chief jusc’a piez, por ceu que vos trovez plus legierement ceu dont vos avrez mestier.	Or I have ordered you this chapter in dividing by chapters, according to that which it is before or chapter of cauteries, that I have devised them from the head to the feet, for that you may find more easily those which you will need.
dou chief plein d’aigue	the head full of water
Saiches que ceste maladie vient mout de fois as enfans a l’enfanter, et quant li baille estraint trop fort le chief de l’enfant; et aucune fois vient ceu de cause reponue que on ne seit.	Know that this illness comes many times to children at birth, and when the midwife pulls the head of the child too hard; and sometimes it comes from a cause unknown.
Et je ne vis onques ceste maladie fuers qu’en enfans, et a toz ces que j’ai veus se hastait li mors; et por ceu me semble qu’il me vaut mues lassier l’ovraige en teilz cures.	And I never saw this illness outside of children, and to all those that I have seen it hastened death; and for that reason it seems to me that it is better to leave the treatment in such cures.
Et je vis .i. enfant de coi li chiés estoit plains d’aigue, et li chief engroissoit chescun jor tant qu’il ne lou pooit sostenir; et crut tant li moistor qu’il fut mors, et ceste moistor si est assemblee desoz l’os sus lou syphac, entre lou keur et l’os; et li ovraiges si est telz se li moistor est entre lou keur et l’os, et li apostemes est petis, que tu fendes emmi lou chief une fendure large; et soit ausi longe com .ij. nous, tant que li mostor corre; et vez ci la forme dou spatumile:	And I saw one child whose shoulder was full of water, and the head grew larger each day until he could not support it; and thought so much the moisture that he died, and this moisture is assembled below the bone on the scapula, between the heart and the bone; and the work is such if the moisture is between the heart and the bone, and the abscess is small, that you open a cut in the middle of the head wide; and as long as two fingers, as long as the moisture runs; and see here the shape of the spatula:
Se li moistor est plus creue, et li aposteme soit plus grans, si fai .ij. fendures en maniere d’une croix, selonc ceste forme:	If the moisture is thicker, and the abscess is larger, make two cuts in the shape of a cross, according to this form:
Et se li moistor est desoz l’os, et li signes que tu vois les commissures dou chief overtes de chescune partie, et li aigue saut fuer quant tu la presses de ta main au dedens, et ceu ne t’est mie reponut: si covient que tu fendes enmi lou chief .iij. fendures selonc ceste maniere:	And if the moisture is below the bone, and the signs that you see are the commissures of the head open on each side, and the water leaps out forcefully when you press it with your hand inward, and this is not returned to you: then you must make three cuts in the middle of the head according to this manner:
Et aprés l’incision estrai la moistor toute fuers. Aprés estraint les fendures de drapelz et de poudres, et i met vin et oile, et laisse ensi jusc’a cinquieme jor; puis le deslie, et cure la plaie par tentes et par oignemens, et laisse estraindre le chief egaument, et done mengier au malaide viande seche de poc de moistor tant que li membre soit confortez et sanez.	And after the incision, take out the moisture entirely. After that, insert bandages and powders, and put wine and oil in it, and leave it so until the fifth day; then undo it, and treat the wound with tents and ointments, and leave the chief bandage to remain, and then give the patient dry meat of poc of moisture as long as the limb is strengthened and healed.
Et une autre maniere d’incision est que tu regardes ou apert li grandor de l’aposteme, et li assemblé de l’aigue; car aucune fois est elle devant; aucune fois derrier; aucune fois en destre; et aucune fois en senestre.	And another way of incision is that you look where the abscess opens large and the assembly of liquid; for sometimes it is in front; sometimes behind; sometimes on the right; and sometimes on the left.
Taille donques lai ou li aposteme apert, et l’emplissement de l’aigue, et lou fent selonc ce que tu en as le pooir; et warde que tu ne coper l’artere; et veigne flun de sanc, si que li malaides muere dou decorrement de sanc et de l’evacuation de moistor.	Therefore, take it where the abscess opens and the filling of liquid, and make the incision according to what you are able; and beware that you do not cut the artery; and vein flow of blood, so that the patient dies from the loss of blood and the evacuation of moisture.
de reume	of sum
Quant il avient a aucun une maladie qui est apelee «catarre» as eulz ou au pis, et li maladie est anciainne, et li cure de medicine ne profite mie, adonques li derraine cure si est li cauteres avec ceu c’on li copera les .ij. arteres.	When it happens to anyone a disease which is called «catarre» in the eyes or at the breast, and the patient is old, and the medicine cure does not help, then the last cure is cauterizing with those one covers the two arteries.
Il covient donques, cant tu les vues coper, que li malaides faice rere son chief; aprés li frotte lou leu d’un drapel aspre tant que les arteres aperent, puis estraingne li malaides son col a tout .i. drapel; puis regarde ou li voine bait, et li leus de l’une et de l’autre sont aprés les oreilles, et poc sont reponues; puis signe les leus d’enche, puis cope l’une et l’autre d’un spatumile agut de .ij. pars. tant que li taille veigne jusc’a l’os, et ceu soit par lou large dou chief.	It is therefore necessary, when you see them to cover, that the patient make back his head; after rub their place with a rough cloth until the arteries appear, then constrict the patient his neck with one cloth; then look where the vein beats, and the places of one and the other are after the ears, and so they are returned; then sign their places with ink, then cut one and the other with a sharp spatula of two parts. As long as the width comes up to the bone, and that be by the wide part of the head.
Et se tu vues, boute le spatumile desoz l’artere et la cope au desus, en taillant ausi com .ij. dois au traver.	And if you see, thrust the spatula below the artery and cut it above, cutting also like two fingers across.
Et quant li voinne est copee, si saut li sans en haut continuelment fuers.	And when the vein is cut, blood jumps out continuously upwards.
Et se li artere n’apert au sentir, si covient que tu mesures la quantiteit de l’espaice de .iij. dois, puis seigne d’enche et fent jusc’a l’os; et ceu qu’il covient dou sanc mettre fuers si est .vj. c/, et par aventure un poc plus ou moins. selonc ce que li malaides puet soffrir, et la repletion de l’artere; puis regarde la plaie: s’il remaint sus l’os point dou syphac, si le cope que apostemes chaus n’i veigne, puis estrain la plaie et lie, et la cure d’oignement tant qu’ele soit sanee.	And if the artery does not open at the feeling, it is necessary that you measure the quantity of space of three fingers, then rule by drawing a line until the bone; and what it is necessary to put out of blood is six ounces, and perhaps a little more or less according to what the patient can suffer, and the fullness of the artery; then look at the wound: if it remains on the bone point without any sphagnum, cut it so that pus does not come, then strain the wound and tie it, and the cure of ointment until it is healed.
de emigrainne	of migraine
Quant emigrainne anciaine vient, et catarre agut, por les moistors des larmes et les chalors en temples et sode anciene forsenee et semblans choses, et il est medicinez par manieres de cures de medicine et tout ceu ne li profite mie, si estraions les arteres des temples et lou cauterizons, si com nos avons conteit.	When old migraine comes, and acute catarrh, because of the moisture of tears and heats in the temples and ancient soreness and similar things, and it is medicated by manners of cures of medicine and all that does not benefit them, then we strain the arteries of the temples and cauterize them, as we have counted.
Et li maniere de l’estraction d’elles si est que li malaides faice rere les poilz de ses temples, et entende a l’artere qui apert en la temple, car elle apert bien par son batement, et est poc reponue fuers que en aucuns homes qui sont trop froit; et s’elle est reponue, si estraigne son col li malaides d’aucuns drapelz, puis frote le leu d’aucun aspre drap, et arose le leu d’aigue chaude tant que li artere apere manifestement; puis pren le spatumile de coi ci est li forme:	And the manner of their extraction is that the patient makes back the hairs of his temples, and attends to the artery which opens in the temple, because it opens well by its beating, and is poorly returned outwards than in certain men who are too cold; and if it is returned, then restrain the neck of the patient with some cloths, then rub the place with some rough cloth, and raise the place with hot water until the artery appears manifestly; then take the spatula which here is the form:
puis escorche le cuir legierement tant que tu veignes a l’artere, puis la trai en haut as pinceures, et la depart bien des toiles que sont desoz li de chescune partie; et se li artere est subtilz, si la torne a la pointe de l’uncine, puis la cope de celle partie selonc la quantiteit des .ij. chiés. Car s’elle n’est copee, si ne saut mie li sans dou tout en tout.	then scrape the skin lightly until you come to the artery, then treat it upwards with pincers, and depart well from the tissues that are under each part; and if the artery is subtle, turn it back with the point of the forceps, then cut it on that part according to the quantity of two fingers. For if it isn’t cut, it doesn’t jump out the blood all at once.
Et trai dou sanc des .vj. c/, jusc’a .iij.; et se li artere est grans, si covient que tu la lies en .ij. leus d’un fil double fort de soie, que porriture n’i veigne devant le soudement de la plaie, et veigne decorremens de sanc; puis cope la superfluiteit qui est entre les .ij. liiens en celle houre meisme, et puis, se tu vues, si lou cauterize dou cautere cutellaire jusc’a l’os tant que li chiés soient copez; et c’est li muedre oevre, se li malaides n’a fievre et il est de chaude complexion.	And treat the blood from six to three fingers; and if the artery is large, it is necessary that you tie it in two leagues with a strong double thread of silk, so that putrefaction doesn't come before the closing of the wound, and there comes bleeding; then cut the superfluity which is between the two liens in the same hour, and then, if you wish, cauterize it with the cuticle cautery up to the bone until the fingers are cut; and this is the middle work, if the patient doesn't have fever and he is of a warm complexion.
Car li cauteres est aide por finir les moistors: por ceu est il de plus grant aide as moistors.	For the cautery is aid to finish the moistors: for this reason it is of more great aid against the moistors.
Ou il covient por l’estraction des arteres que om emplisse lou leu de viel coton et mette on sus tentes bien faites; et quant on les desliera, si soit curez de medicines seches que font naistre char, et de tentes, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se sans cort de l’artere tant dis com tu i oevres, si te haste dou coper par cautere, ou tu emple lou leu de vitriole et l’estrain a ta main que li sans soit estainchiez; et se tu n’as ceu present, si met sor le leu ton doit tant que li sans soit congelez, et arose le leu d’aigue froide tant que li sans cesse, et soit estraint si com il covient; et ceu qui est muedre et plus legier en l’estraction de l’artere est que tu cauterizes la voinne de cest cautere trenchant de .ij. pars, mais li trenchant soient bien espés por warder plus longement lor chalor.	Where it is necessary for the extraction of arteries that one fills their bed with old cotton and places on them well-made tents; and when one unbinds them, so be cared with dry medicines that cause flesh to rise, and with tents, until it is healed; and if without a splint of the artery as long as you work on it, so hasten to close it by cautery, or you put in its place vitriol and strain it in your hand that the wound is stitched; and if you do not have this present, so put on its bed your finger until the wound freezes, and raise the bed with cold water until the bleeding stops, and be constrained as is necessary; and what is more mature and lighter in the extraction of the artery is that you cauterize the vein of this cautery trenchant by .ij. parts, but the trenches be well spaced to keep longer their heat.
Car quant li estrumens est trop tenves, si tient moins sa chalor.	For when the instrument is too hard, it holds less its heat.
Et doit avoir entre les .ij. coutelz .i. doit de gros d’espaice, et puis quant tu as signiet d’enche les .ij. leus, et tu mes lou fer ardant sus tant qu’il viegne jusc’a l’os, et cope la voinne en .ij. leus; et soient esloigniet entre les .ij. chiés car il n’est mie soudez de cest cautere dou tout en tout; et c’est li forme dou cautere:	And must have between the two knives one should of great space, and then when you have signed in their two sides, and you place the red hot iron until it comes to the bone, and cut the vein in two lengths; and be separated between the two shoulders because it is not well joined by this cautery at all; and this is the form of the cautery:
des larmes	of tears
Quant les larmes des eulz sont dessendans des voinnes que sont sus lou test dou chief de fuer, et il ne profite mie cure de medicine c’on i faice, et tu vois la faice dou malaide enrougir, et sent ou front ambulation si com de fremis; et sui oil sont tenve et moiste si que li poil des papieres sont cheut, et sont eschaufees les papieres, et escorchies de l’ardor des larmes, si ait mestier de ceste cure.	When the tears of the eyes are descending from the veins that are on the forehead above the head of force, and it does not benefit any medicine to be done there, and you see the face of the patient turning in, and they feel pain in the front like a shivering; and where the eye is covered and moist so that the hair of the eyebrows falls, and the eyelids are chapped, and scorched by the ardor of tears, then this cure is necessary.
Et l’apelerent li ancien «cure contuse», et est que tu faices a rere au malaide qui a ceste maladie les poilz qu’il ait ou front, puis li fai .iij. fendures ou front igalment selonc la longesce dou front; et soit l’une des fendures ausi com .ij. doi tout emmi lou front en avalant aval jusc’a neif, et les autres .ij. as .ij. costelz par desus les papieres, et te garde de l’incision des arteres que sont as .ij. costez par desus les papieres; et aloigne ta main de la continuation des .ij. mandibules, et soit chescune plaie la quantiteit de .iij. dois au traver joins;	And they called it in the old days "contused cure," and that you do to the patient who has this illness the hairs that he has on his forehead, then he makes .iii. incisions on the forehead evenly according to the length of the forehead; and let one incision be as .ii. so as to completely remove the forehead, going down to the nose, and the other .ii. as .ii. ribs above the cheekbones, and keep yourself from the incision of the arteries that are as .ii. ribs above the cheekbones; and keep your hand away from the continuation of the .ii. jaws, and let each wound be the quantity of .iii. thumbs across joins.
et aies apparillie une piece d’esponge et mout de drapelz ses por essuer lou sanc, puis boute le spatumile agut de .ij. pars de coi ci est li forme:	And have prepared a piece of sponge and many cloths for wiping the blood, then put the spatula acute on two parts so that is the shape:
des l’incision qui est dever la temple jusc’a la seconde incision; et escorche tout le keur qui est entre les .ij. fendures a tot lou syfac qui est sus l’os, puis fai autreteil des la moiene incision jusc’a l’autre seconde, et puis estrai fuer cest spatumile.	from the incision that is under the temple up to the second incision; and scrape all the kernel that is between the two incisions to the whole syfac that is on the bone, then do another one from the middle incision up to the other second, and then extract further this spatula.
si boute en la premiere fendure l’estrument qui est apelez «cultellaire», et est tresbien trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part est souef, ne mie trenchans, et c’est li forme:	If it is inserted in the first crack the instrument which is called “cultellaire”, and is very sharp on one side, and on the other side is blunt, not sharp, and this is its form:
Et met le costeit taillant vers la char aerse au keur, et lou costeit souef vers l’os, et lou boute tant qu’il veigne a la moiene fendure. Et cope toz les vasselz que dessendent dou chief as eulz tant que l’incision soit continue jusc’a ceu qui apert dou keur, et puis autreteil fai en la moiene fendure jusc’a l’autre defuer; et puis estrai dou sanc igalment, et espresse lou leu por le sanc pris; puis met en chescune fendure une tente de viel coton, et met sus drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile et en aisil, et garde que apostemes chaus n’i veigne; et au tier jor deslie lou liien, et i amenistre grant planteit d’aigue tede, puis lou cure d’oignement basilicon avec oile roset, et d’autres cures dont on cure plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And put the sharp edge towards the flesh toward the heart, and the blunt edge toward the bone, and put it in until it comes to the middle crack. And cut all the vessels that descend from the head to the eyes as long as the incision is continuous until it reaches that which opens toward the heart, and then on the other side make in the middle crack until the other end; and then extract the blood equally, and express the wound for the blood taken; then put in each crack a tent of old cotton, and put above cloths moistened with wine and oil and aisil, and guard that an abscess does not come there; and on the third day untie the linen, and there administer abundant plant poultice, then the cure of basil ointment with rose oil, and other cures which one uses for wounds, as long as it is healed.
dou reume des eulz	of the eye's
Quant a aucun vienent catarre agut acostumeement, et tu vois les eulz tenves et petis, et afoiblir la veue, et les papieres brulees; et li poil chieent, et ou chief en parfont a dolor ague, et li malaides esternue; adonques saiches par ces accidens que celles matieres et cil catharre ne vient fuer que de maintes voines, et li muedre cure que i est, si est ceste.	When a certain catarrh comes acute by custom, and you see the eyes watery and small, and weaken the sight, and the papers burned; and the hair falls out, and where the chief partakes in a sharp pain, and the patient sneezes; therefore you know by these accidents that these matters and this catarrh come from many veins, and the cure that is there, if it is this.
Et est que tu comande au malaide a rere son front, puis fai une grant fendure emmi lou front, et une autre dou large. i. poc. Et comence des la fendure de la temple senestre a la temple destre, et soit li incision jusc’a l’os; et esloigne ta main des ners des temples que muevent au mengier; et quant li os est descovers, si essue tout le sanc a une esponge, et puis desevre entre les .ij. levres de la fendure et i met coton viel, et tentes de lin; puis lie desus drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile, et te garde d’aposteme chaut; quant il est ostez, si covient que tu frottes l’os tant que chars i comence a naistre, puis le cure de choses exiccatives, que font enjanrer char.	And it is that you command the patient to push back his forehead, then make a great incision in the middle of the forehead, and another wide one. And begin from the left temple incision to the right temple, and be the incision until the bone; and keep your hand away from the nerves of the temples which move at the touch; and when the bone is uncovered, wipe all the blood with a sponge, and then sew between the two lips of the incision and put old cotton there, and bandages of linen; then tie above cloth soaked in wine and oil, and guard against a hot abscess; when it is removed, you should rub the bone until pus begins to appear, then treat it with drying things that make pus dry.
En teil maniere: pren .ij. parties de flor de froment, et de colofoine .iiij. parties, et en fai emplaustre; et l’aministre en ces plaies por enjanrer char per tout.	In this manner: take 2 parts of wheat flower and 4 parts of colophony, and make a poultice with it; and administer it in these wounds to dry pus completely.
de l’estoupement des oreilles	of the plugging of the ears
Tout ceu que chiet ens oreilles est une des .iiij. choses: ou grains, ou beste, ou piere de mine ou semblans chose si com fer; ou semence, si com jaisses, feves, pois; ou chose defluans si com aigue et aisilz et semblans choses.	All that which falls into the ears is one of the four things: or grains, or beast, or stone of mine or similar thing like iron; or seed, as beans, lentils, peas; or flowing thing as water and such and similar things.
Quant il chiet en l’oreille piere ou autre maniere de chose que ne s’ajoste mie a l’oreille, ne ne croist en l’oreille, si met l’oreille au solel. Se tu vois la piere, si distille aucun poc d’oile violet ou oile de sisament, puis i amenistre extraction; et lou fai esternuer de condisi, et li estoupe les narines quant li esternuemens vient, et met entor l’oreille pieces de drapelz ou laine; et estent l’oreille au desus. Mout de fois vient fuer par ceste cure; et s’elle ne vient fuer, se li amenistre extraction as pinceures subtilz, de coi ci est li forme:	When it falls into the ear stone or another manner of thing that does not join to the ear, nor grows in the ear, put the ear to the sun. If you see the stone, instill a drop of violet oil or sesame oil, then administer extraction; and have him sneeze with condiment, and plug his nostrils when the sneezes come, and put around the ear pieces of cloth or wool; and keep the ear upward. Many times it comes out by this cure; and if it does not come out, administer extraction with fine pincers, of which this is the form:
S’elle saut fuer as pinceures, c’est boin; se ceu non, si amenistre extraction a l’oncine subtil de petite doubleure; et s’elle ne saut par ceu, si fai une caine d’arain et boute lou chief de la cainne ou pertuis de l’oreille fort, et estoupe ceu qui est entor la cainne de cire mole si que li vens n’i puisse entrer avec la cainne; puis le trai fuer forment, car mout de fois vient fuer si com nos avons dit; et s’elle ne vient fuer en teil maniere, si prent glut de coi en prent les oisiaus, et met en som aucun estrument qui soit a point por ceu faire, et met un poc de coton entor; puis presse le glut sus la piere ou quel chose que ce soit, et trai fuer.	If it comes out with the pincers, it is good; if not, administer extraction with a fine instrument of small double curvature; and if it does not come out by this, make a chain of iron and insert the head of the chain or through the ear hole strongly, and plug what is around the chain with soft wax so that the liquid cannot enter with the chain; then pull it out forcefully, for many times it comes out as we have said; and if it does not come out in this manner, take a glue of what they use to catch birds, and put on some instrument that is pointed for this purpose, and put a little cotton around it; then press the glue on the stone or whatever thing it is, and pull it out.
Et s’elle ne saut fuer de toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si te haste de fendre l’oreille ainsois que aposteme chalz i veigne, et spasme; et li maniere de la fendure si est que tu faices premier sainier lou malaide de la cephalique, et estrai dou sanc selonc la mesure de sa vertu, puis fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains et li torne l’oreille au desus, et fent une petite fendure en la racine de l’oreille a la graisse ou leu dependant; et soit li fendure ausi com une lune, tant que tu viegnes a la piere, puis l’oste selonc ton pooir, et la suce hastanment a ta bouche; et la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it does not leave all these things that we have said, then hasten to cut open the ear so that an abscess comes out, and spasms; and the manner of cutting is that you first make the patient bleed from the head, and extract blood according to the measure of his virtue, then make the patient sit between your hands and turn the ear upwards, and make a small cut at the root of the ear in the fat or where it depends; and let the cut be like a crescent moon, until you come to the bone, then the bone according to your power, and suck it diligently with your mouth; and the cure as long as it is healed.
Et se c’est grains qui est ens et il enfle, si aministre extraction; et si’il ne puet issir, si amenistre .i. spatumile tenve subtil selonc ceste forme:	And if it is grains that are inside and it swells, then administer extraction; and if it cannot exit, then administer i. spatula thin according to this form:
et amenistre incision de celui grain. Mais ne faire mie ceu quant tu penses que li grains est moistes por la moistor de l’oreille, tant que tu en aies fait maintes pieces; puis l’estrai as pinceures subtilz et au succier, si com nos avons dit, si que li estractions soit aligie.	and administer an incision to that grain. But do not do this when you think that the grain is moist due to the moisture of the ear, until you have made many pieces of it; then extract with fine pincers and suction, as we have said, so that the extraction be aligned.
En l’aigue donques que chiet en l’oreille covient que li malaides use d’esternuement de condisi premiers, et ample l’oreille de viel coton. Et soit gisans sus celle oreille meisme ou li aigue est. s’elle saut fuer per ceu, c’est boin. se ceu non, si prent maintes pieres selonc li longesce de ton doit tenves et legieres, et les eschaufe un poc au feu; et em mette li malaides une ou pertus de son oreille, et saille sus i. de ses piez d’autre part, et fiere d’une autre piere sus la piere qui est en l’oreille; et ne cesse de faire ceu de piere em piere tant que li aigue isse toute fuer, et ensi saut elle toute fuer; et se tu vues, si prent .i. jonc, et boute l’un des chiés en l’oreille, et l’autre chief emprent de feu tant que li plus dou jonc soit ars; puis refai autreteil d’autres jons tant que li aigue isse toute, si com nos avons dit en la piere.	In the ear water therefore that falls, it befits the patient to use the external of conditions first, and widen the ear with old cotton. And let him lie on that same ear where the water is. If it comes out by this means, that's good.
