If not, then take many stones according to the length of your finger tenuous and light, and heat them a bit at the fire; and put them in the patient's ear one pierced, and let it rise up on it. from his feet of another part, and fire from one stone upon the stone that is in the ear; and do not cease to do this of stone after stone until the water comes out entirely, and thus it shall come out entirely; and if you see, take .i. reed, and put one end in the ear, and the other end catch on fire until the more tender reed burns; then redo the other part with other reeds until the water comes out entirely, as we have said in the stone.
En l’estraction de la beste, s’elle est de petit cors, si com puce et semblans chose, cure la si com nos avons dit en la division; mais s’elle est de grant cors c’on la puisse sentir, si amenistre extraction de pinceures; et c’est li chose plus legiere a oster qui soit en l’oreille.	In the extraction of the beast, if it is of small body, as a flea and similar thing, cure it as we have said in the division; but if it is of great body which one can feel, administer extraction of pincers; and that is the lightest thing to remove that is in the ear.
En l’estraction des vers enjanrez as oreilles, quant tu lou cures si com nos avons dit en la division et ou traitier des distillations, et li cure ne profite mie, si covient que tu regardes l’oreille au soleil: s’il i apert nulz vers, si les trai as pinceures subtilz, et s’il n’aperent, si prent la cainne de coi ci est li forme:	In the extraction of worms in the ears, when you cure it as we have said in the division and where we treat distillations, and the cure does not benefit, then it befits that you look at the ear to the sun: if there appears any worm, then you treat them with subtle pincers, and if they do not appear, then take the cane of which this is the form:
Et soit estroite desoz et large desus. Et boute lou plus subtil chief en l’oreille selonc la quantiteit de la soffrance dou malaide, puis succe forment a tot la caine; fai ceu sovent tant que tuit li ver issent. Et s’il n’obeissent a issir, si estoupe entor la cainne de coton si com j’ai dit en la piere; et s’il ne saillent fuer si com nos avons dit, si aministre distillations que li ancien ont esprovees en l’ocision des vers, et tu les troveras ou traitier des distillations; et si distille tes oiles et tes medicines en l’oreille a tout cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme si com tu vois:	And it should be narrow below and wide above. And put the most subtle chief in the ear according to the quantity of the suffering of the patient, then succeed form to all the cane; do this often until all the worms come out. And if they do not obey to come out, then stop around the cane with cotton as I said in the stone; and if they do not come out further as we have said, then administer distillations that the ancients have proven in the excision of worms, and you will find them or treat with distillations; and if you distill your oils and medicines in the ear to all this instrument, of which this is the form as you see:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain estrois desoz a .i. petis pertuis, et desus overs por distiller; et por presser dedens la distillation a .i. estrument d’arain bien fait por ceu, et se tu vues pren .i. raseur et envoloupe entor la pointe avenanment coton; puis i giete ton oile ou ton jus, et ceu que tu vues de tes medicines en la cainne, et li caine soit en l’oreille; puis boute dedens lou raseur a tout lou coton, et presse ta main tempreement tant que li oile soit distilleit ou chevement de l’oreille; et lou sente li malaides dedens, et soit li distillations .i. poc eschaufee au feu ainsois c’on la distille en l’oreille; et garde qu’elle ne soit trop froide, car li medicine ne seroit mie si bone.	And let it be of silver or iron, narrowed below at one small hole, and wide above for distilling; and for pressing inside the distillation, one instrument of iron well made for this, and if you see take one razor and wrap around the tip evenly cotton; then put your oil or your juice, and what you want of your medicines in the cane, and the cane in the ear; then put inside the razor to all the cotton, and press your hand temperately until the oil is distilled or finished at the end of the ear; and let the patient feel it inside, and be the distillations one pock heated at the fire so that once distilled into the ear; and guard that it be not too cold, for the medicine would not be so good.
de l’estoupement des oreilles	Of the stopping of ears
Aucun enfant naissent qui n’ont nul pertus ens oreilles; et ceste meisme chose avient as homes par estoupement de plaie, ou de char nee dedens l’oreille, et cist estoupemens vient aucune fois em parfont en l’oreille, si c’on ne lou puet veoir; et aucune fois avient .i. poc defuer lou pertus, et lou voit om bien.	No child is born who does not have a hole in their ears; and this same thing happens to men by the swelling of a wound, or of flesh born inside the ear, and this swelling comes sometimes from within the ear, so that one cannot see it; and sometimes it happens i.e., point of fire, and one sees it well.
Celle donques que vient em parfont, si c’on ne la puet veoir, est de grief sanation em plusors dispositions, et en cele c’on voit covient que tu mettes l’oreille dou malaide au soleil; et regarde dedens: se tu vois l’opilation apparent, si la oevre a tot cest spatumile de coi ci est li forme:	That which comes from within so that one cannot see it, is of grievous healing in more dispositions, and in this one ought to put the ear of the sick person in the sun; and look inside: if you see the opening apparent, then the work has all this spatula-like thing of this kind:
Et soit agus et trenchans devant et derrier tout plain, si qu’il ne blece l’oreille; se li opilation est de char nee ou cors de l’oreille, si la tien as pinceures subtilz, et la cope legierement, tant que celle chars soit toute ostee.	And be straight and trenchant in front and behind all plain so that it does not blister the ear; if the opening is of flesh born or a body of the ear, then hold it with subtle pincers, and scoop it lightly, as long as that flesh is completely removed.
Et se li opilations est em parfont en l’oreille, si pren .i. raseur subtil legier et l’eschaufe un petit au feu, puis li met ou cors de l’oreille. Se tu sens l’opilation dont li malaides sent grieteit a l’oïr, perce legierement, et garde que tu ne grever les ners de l’oreille; puis met en l’oreille une tente selonc la largesce dou pertus, et la moille en l’oignement egyptien.	And if the opilation is in the ear, then take one razor subtle light and heat it a little in the fire, then put it into the flesh of the ear. If you feel the opilation that the patient feels greatly in the ear, pierce lightly, and keep that you do not wound the nerves of the ear; then put in the ear a tent according to the width of the hole, and moisten it in Egyptian ointment.
Fai ceu aucun jor tant que li plaie soit soudee, ou tu pren une tente et la moille en aigue rose, et poudre sus vitriole broiet; et se tu vois enflee l’oreille, si couvient que tu traies la tente et remue une autre tente moillie en cerote qui soit fait d’oile roset et de cire, tant que li enfleure soit ostee; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Do this until the wound is healed, or you take a tent and moisten it in rose water, and powder on powdered vitriol; and if you see the ear inflamed, then it is necessary that you withdraw the tent and move another tent moistened in cerote which is made of rose oil and wax, until the inflammation is removed; then cure it until it is healed.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si plonge une esponge et drapelz en aigue froide, et le met sus l’oreille, et use d’autres cures qui oste lou decorrement de sanc qui sont ou traitier des destillations.	And if bleeding comes, then dip a sponge and drape it in cold water, and put it on the ear, and use other cures that remove the bleeding which are or treat distillations.
de la char des papieres	of the sheet of paper
Cist althelul que vienent em papieres des eulz quant ils sont moiste et sont sec, si covient que tu les estendes de tenailles et de pinceures, et le cope d’un spatumile de ses racines; puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet.	This althule that comes from the papers of the eyes when they are moist and are dry, then you should extend them with tweezers and pincers, and the root of a spatula; then put on their place ground vitriol.
Et se sans en decort, si le cauterize dou cautere lenticulaire subtil, et li cauterizeir aprés l’incision vaut mues; et maintes fois repairent, cant aucune chose demoure de lor racines; et quant elles sont cauterizees par feu, si sont arses celles racines et ne revienent mie.	And if without it decored, then cauterize with a subtle lentile cautery, and after the incision the cauterization is worth to use; and many times they are repaireed, because nothing remains of their roots; and when they are cauterized by fire, those roots are burned and do not come back.
de la gresle	of the  grease
Maintes fois vienent em papieres des eulz unes choses que semblent gresle en sa forme et en sa duresce, et por ceu est ceste maladie apelee «grandine», et est une assemblee de moistor grosse en la papiere desus et desoz; li ovraiges est telz: pren warde se li grandine se muet d’une part et d’autre, et c’est legiere chose a savoir; fent la donques dou large, puis l’escorche de chescune partie legierement, puis la prent as pinceures, et la cope. se tu ne la pues coper sens percier un poc la papiere, si ne grieve rien au malaide; et se li fendure est grans, si l’assemble a une costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee; et s’elle est petite, si n’i faire point de force, car li oignemens la restoure tantost et enjanre char.	Many times come in papers the eyes some things that seem brittle in its form and in its hardness, and for these is this disease called "hail", and is a gathering of moisture large in the paper above and below; the works are such: take heed if the hail moves from one part and the other, and it's a light thing to know; then make the wide, then the skin of each part lightly, then take with the pliers, and the cut. If you cannot cut without piercing a bit the paper, so do not grieve the patient; and if the fissure is great, so assemble a suture, and cure until it is healed; and if it is small, do not make any force, for the ointment restore it soon and creates flesh.
Et se li grandine est dessendans au dedens de l’oreille vers la partie desus, si enverse la papiere, et estent la grandine a unes pinceures, et la cope et presse d’une part et d’autre; et se li papiere est esloignie par l’incision, ce ne grieve rien; et quant li grandine est copee, si leive l’oil d’aigue salee, et cure le leu de ceu qui enjanre char tant que li malaides soit sanez.	And if the hail is descending into the ear towards the upper part, so reverse the paper, and being the hail to pliers, and the cut and press from one side and the other; and if the paper is separated by the incision, it grieves nothing; and when the hail is cut, leave the eye of salt water, and cure the place of that which creates flesh until the patient be healed.
de la graisse des eulz	of the fat of the eyes
Exinach est une graisse qui est enjanree en toiles des papieres desus, et ce avient plus as enfans c’a nules gens, et grieve mout a lor eulz, et li vienent li catharre as matinees, et ne pueent regardeir la lumiere dou soleil por ceu que les larmes se hastent a lor eulz; et por ceu se couchent il sor lor faices adés, et dorment sus, et sont lor papieres desoz lor sorcilz moistes que li enfleure et li apparance ont covert de l’exinach qui apert en l’oil. Et quant tu presses lou leu a tes dois et sent l’exirnach entr’ous.	This is grease that is engendered in the fabrics of papers above, and this happens more to children than anyone else, and grieves their eyes much, and they come the catarrh in the mornings, and cannot look at the light of the sun because the tears hasten to their eyes; and because of this they lie down on their faces sideways, and sleep on top, and are their fabrics under their eyebrows moist that the swelling and appearance have covered with the exinach which opens in the eye. And when you press it with your fingers and feel the exinarch between them.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain; et puis pren .i. drapeil de lin, et appareille une tente em maniere d’un cercle selonc la quantiteit que conteigne exirnach de chescune partie, puis le met sus li; et presse a tes dois d’une part et d’autre, si que li exirnach soit assemblez emmi le cercle; puis fent em mileu de la moistor au spatumile trenchant une fendure dou large, et ne soit mie plus grans que li plaie c’on fait a la sainie de voinne; et fent le cuir em parfont tant que tu veignes a l’exirnach; et em plusors dispositions vient exirnach de la fendure, selonc la forme d’une piece de graisse blainche.	And the manner of the work is that the patient puts his head in your breast; and then take one draping of linen, and prepare a tent in the manner of a circle according to the quantity that contains exinarch from each part, then put it on top; and press with your fingers on one side and the other, so that the exinarch is assembled within the circle; then make in the middle of the moisture with the spatula cutting a fissure of wide, and not be more than the wound one makes in the vein; and make the leather in full force until you come to the exinarch; and in more dispositions comes exinarch from the fissure, according to the form of a piece of white fat.
Estrai la donques a tout une piece de drap charpit entre tes dois au defuer, et torne ta main a destre et a senestre tant qu’il soit espars; et garde que tu n’ajoster en la fendure, que tu ne viegnes a tout le spatumile jusc’a l’oil, que tu ne le bleces.	Extract then with one piece of cloth charpit between your fingers at the outer edge, and turn your hand to right and left until it is spread; and guard that you do not add in the fissure, that you do not come to the whole spatula up to the eye, that you do not bleach it.
Et se li exirnach n’apert en l’encomencement de la fendure, si acroi un poc la fendure legierement tant qu’il apere; puis l’estrai si com nos avons dit, puis moille drapelz en aisil et en aigue, et met sus le leu, et estrain de bendelz.	And if the incision does not open at the beginning of the split, then widen the split slightly until it opens; then extract as we have said, then moisten drapes in water and wine, and put them on top, and bind with bandages.
Et si a de tels homes qui broient seil et mettent sus por corrompre cele moistor qui est demoree. Puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez. Et s’il vient au leu aposteme chaut, si lou cure d’emplaustres assouajant tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if there are such men who grind flax and put it on top to corrupt that moisture that remains. Then treat it until it is healed. And if it comes back to the place as a hot abscess, then treat it with soothing plasters until it is healed.
des poilz des papieres	of hairs of papers
Quant em papieres naissent poilz ajostez autre que li naturez, et sont enveillit, si nuisent as eulz, et font venir manieres de maladies si com larmes acostumees et mollifications des papieres et albugine, tant que c’est cause de la destruction des eulz; et est li cure selonc .iiij. manieres: ou par cautere ensamble feu, ou par medicine ague selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre de cautere, et est fais ou par incision et costure ou par caines, selonc ceu que je dirai.	When hairs on the papers are born adjusted other than nature's, and they become old, they harm the eyes, and bring manner of maladies as tears accustomed and softening of the papers and albuginea, until it is cause of the destruction of the eyes; and it is cure according to .iiij. manners: or by cautery altogether fire, or by medicine ague according to what it is before or chapter of cautery, and it is done by incision and suture or by canes, according to what I will say.
Il covient que tu mettes lou chief dou malaide en ton sain, puis torne la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre; s’elle est convertie, c’est boin; se ceu non, si i boute une aguille a tout .i. fil desus; et soit ce delez la marge de la papiere ou li poil naissent delez ces poilz, et trai .i. fil au desus a tout la papiere, et la torne au raseur; puis fent en la partie desoz la papiere, desoz les poilz ajostez, a tout le spatumile copant, des le grant larmier jusc’au petit; puis estrai .i. fil, et met desoz la papiere une petite tente de couton et de drapeil, puis seigne sus la papiere une figure d’enche, si com la fuelle de mirte, et toutevoie il covient que li figure soit selonc la quantiteit que tu vues eslever la papiere qui est devisez a toz.	It behooves you to put the head of the patient in your breast, then turn the paper of the eye to your left hand; if it is turned, it is good; if not, there puts an needle at all .i. thread above; and let it be by the edge of the paper where the hair grows near these hairs, and treat .i. thread up to the whole paper, and turn it to the razor; then make in the part below the paper, below the hairs adjusted, to the entire spatula copant, from the great tearer to the small; then extract .i. thread, and put under the paper a small tent of cotton and drapery, then place on top of the paper a figure of an enche, like the leaf of myrtle, and nonetheless it behooves that the figure be according to the quantity that you see raise the paper which is divided to all.
Et si a teil qui a mestier c’on cope grant quantiteit de la papiere selonc ceu que li papiere est mollifie; puis fent a tout le spatumile sus les .ij. lignes que tu as signiet, et comence des lou grant larmier jusc’a petit; et soit li une des fendures pres des poilz naturez en la groissece d’un raiz, puis boute l’oncine en l’un des .ij. angles dou keur, puis l’escorche toute; puis assemble les .ij. levres a une costure d’une aguille a tout .i. fil de laine subtil, et essue le sanc, et fai aerdre la superfluiteit des filz sus les .ij. sorcilz a tout aucunes choses gluans, se tu vues faire ce; et se ce non, si n’en aies cure, puis laisse la costure et les filz jusc’a .iij. jors ou .iiij.; puis cure la plaie sens costure de choses sechans et constrignans, car li papiere se relive au soudement de la plaie et l’assemblement de li, mais li costure est muedre (si com dirent li ancien), et c’est ovraiges sens paor;	And if to him who needs it one cuts a great quantity of the paper according to what the paper is softened; then make at the entire spatula above the .ij. lines that you have signed, and commence from the great tearer to the small; and let it be one of the cleavages near the natural hairs in the thickness of a root, then put the oncine in one of the .ij. angles of the heart, then exfoliate all of it; then assemble the .ij. lips with a suture of a needle at all .i. thread of fine wool, and wipe the blood, and make airdré the superfluity of threads on the .ij. eyebrows to nothing sticky, if you wish to do this; and if not, have no care, then leave the suture and the threads until .iij. days or .iiij.; then cure the wound without a suture with things drying and constricting, because the paper revives at the closing of the wound and the assembling of it, but the suture is muedre (as they say the ancients), and this work without fear;
et si a une autre maniere: et est que tu seignes la papiere d’une figure qui soit ausi com li fuelle de mirte, si com nos avons conteit, a .iij. oncines desevrez selonc la forme qui est ci:	and if in another manner: and is that you mark the paper with a figure which is as well as the leaf of myrtle, as we have counted, at iii. ounces separated according to the form which is here:
puis cope ceu qui sormonte as petites forces igalment selonc la forme qui est ci:	then cut what rises above the small forces equally according to the form which is here:
Et se tu n’as pooir de tenir les tenailles, et li chose n’est mie igalz, si prent une aguille ou il ait .i. fil, et la boute emmi la figure; et boute .i. autre fil delez lou grant larmier, et lou secont fil delez lou petit, et assemble entre tes dois les filz igalment; puis lieve ta main igalment, et lieve tout le cuir sus coi tu as signiet, si com nos avons conteit, puis assemble les .ij. levres de la plaie par costure, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et se aposteme vient a ton incision, si l’apaise de cerote et de semblans oignement assouajans;	And if you do not have the power to hold the pliers, and the thing is not equal, then take a needle which has i. thread, and put it in the middle of the figure; and put one other thread near the large tear, and the second thread near the small one, and assemble between your two threads equally; then lift your hand equally, and lift all the skin above what you have marked, as we have counted, then assemble the two lips of the wound with stitching, and cure it until it is healed; and if an abscess comes to your incision, then soothe it with cerote and similar soothing ointments;
et aucune fois avient que li poil de la papiere sont convertit: si covient que tu uses ceu que nos avons dit de l’incision; mais li costure en l’une et en l’autre est plus artificialz.	and sometimes it happens that the hair of the paper are converted: so it is necessary that you use those that we have said of the incision; but the suture on one and on the other is more artificial.
Li cure des caines si est selonc ceste forme: et est que tu convertisses la papiere et la fent dedens selonc ceu que j’ai dit, et puis fai .ij. caines par art, et .ij. liiens subtilz ausi lonc com li papiere et li largesce dou spatumile est; et cope as .ij. chiés de .ij. pars ou tu tiens les filz; puis assemble l’un et l’autre subtilment sus ceu que sormonte de la papiere de l’oil, et estrain les .ij. cainnes des .ij. parties forment; et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, et li cuir qui iert estrainte morra et nercira et porrira, tant qu’il cherra par lui.	The cure of the cauteries is in this form: and that you convert the paper and the felt inside according to those that I have said, and then make two cautery by art, and two subtle ligatures as long as the paper and the width of the spatula are; and cut the two handles of two parts where you hold the threads; then assemble one and the other subtly on what surmounts the paper of the eye, and strain the two cauteries of the two parts forming; and leave it thus for some days, and the skin which is strained will die and shrink and carry, until it comes away by itself.
S’il tarde, si le cope aunes forces, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et quant li plaie iert soudee, et si ert levee li papiere, et ne poindront plus li poil; et c’est li forme des .ij. cainnes que tu feras selonc ceste figure, et selonc ceste quantiteit de lonc et de large:	If it tarries, then cut it with more force, then cure it until it is healed; and when the wound is soldered, and if it has been raised the paper, and they will no longer prick the hairs; and this is the form of the two cauteries that you will make according to this figure, and according to this quantity of length and width:
li ovraiges est telz que tu preignes une aguille subtil, et i boute .i. fil de soie souef et subtil; puis assemble les chiés et noe l’un et l’autre subtilment, et soit li longesce des filz une palme de lonc; puis ordene en la chasse .i. autre fil subtil de soie briément, et noe les chief dou fil; puis mette li malaides son chief en ton sain; et soit delez lou soleil si que li ovraiges soit declairiez, car c’est uns ovraiges subtilz et menus, puis boute l’aguille a tout la chasse en la racine dou poil ajosteit, et la fai percier en la papiere hastanment tant que tu la traies desus lou poil natureil; puis estrai le poil jusque sus la chasse, et boute en la chasse celui poil, s’il en i a .i. ou .ij. ou .iij. ou plusors; puis estrai ta main tant que li poilz veigne fuers a tout la chasse en la papiere avec lou poil natureil.	The work is such that you prick an awl, fine and I put one thread of silk, thin and fine; then assemble the shoulders and knot them together subtly, and let the length of the threads be a palm long; then arrange in the chase another fine thread of silk short, and knot its ends together; then put the patient's head on your shoulder; and be facing the sun so that the work is clarified, for it is a subtle and delicate work; then put the awl into the entire chase in the root of the hair just above, and make it pierce through the paper gently as long as you draw it from above the natural hair; then extract the hair up to the chase and put in the chase that hair, if there are one or two or three or more; then extract your hand so that the hairs come out through all the chase into the paper with the natural hair.
Et se li chasse est traite et li poilz ne vient fuer avec li, si trairas la chasse au desoz a tout le fil que tu i as ordeneit, tant que li chasse veigne fuer dou pertus desus et que tu la voies par la vision de l’oil; adonques si trairas la chasse et le fil, et clo l’oil et lou laisse clo .ij. jors ou .iij., tant que li poil s’aerde en son leu et naisse li char sus; et se li poilz est petis, si acompaigne .i. poil lonc des chevoulz naturez, et soit alevez avec celui ou tu le laisse, tant qu’il soit eslongiez et puis le lieve.	And if the chase is treated and the hairs do not come out with it, then you will draw the chase down to all the thread that you have arranged in it, until the chase comes out through the hole above and you see it by the eye; then you will draw the chase and the thread, and close the eye and let it be closed for two or three days, until the hair hardens in its place and grows the flesh above; and if the hairs are small, accompany one long hair from the natural ones, and leave it raised with that one as long as it is elongated and then raise it.
de la porriture de l’oil	of the rotting of the eye
Quant ceste maladie qui est apelee «aleacrati» ou li porriture vient en l’oil, si en i a de .ij. manieres: l’une natureil, et l’autre innatureil.  Et avient par soudement de plaie, ou de tailleure ou de cautere, et par semblans choses.	When this sickness which is called «aleacrati» or the rot comes to the eye, if there are two manners: one natural, and the other unnatural. And happens by suddenness of wound, or cutting or cautery, and by similar things.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige en li est que tu fendes celle soudure, et dessevre les levres de li, et met dedens tentes de lin, et la lie tant qu’elle soit sanee; et ne covient mie que tu uses en la cure de li de choses que sechent et restraignent. Car se tu fais ceu, si revient li maladie pire que li premiere; mais i oevre de choses amollissans, si com fenugreic; et l’arose d’aigue ou altee et semence de lin soient cuites, et oignemens dyaquilon fondut en aucun des oiles, et i envoloupe une tente, et le cure de ceu.	And the manner of working on it is that you split that suture, and loosen the lips of it, and put inside tents of linen, and let it be until it is healed; and it does not behoove that you use in the cure of it things that dry and restrain. For if you do this, so returns the illness worse than the first; but work of softening things, such as fenugreek; and the rose of water or aloe and seed of flax are cooked, and oil of diaquilon melted in any of the oils, and envelop a tent, and cure with that.
Et li tresors de ta cure si est que tu te dones en garde qu’ele ne soude mie selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant; et cist ovraiges que nos avons dit nen est fuers que adresemens de ceste maladie, qu’elle ne reviegne selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant.	And the treasures of your cure is that you take care that it does not close again according to the form that it was before; and this work that we have said is nothing but the addressing of this illness, so that it does not return according to the form that it was before.
de la char qui vient en l’oil	of the matter that comes into the eye
Ceste maladie que est desoz qui vraiement est apelee «axacrati», et est naturelz et accidens. Li accidens vient de plaie et de fendure et de cautere et de choses semblans; et li voie de l’ovraige en li si est que tu preignes un aguille, en coi il ait .i. fil double, et la fiche en la char, et li fai percier des le senestre larmier tant c’a destre, si que li filz veigne en .ij. chiés de la char; puis estent la char au desus a tout l’aguille, et la cope a .i. spatumile large.	This disease that is  dislocation which is truly called “axacrati,” and it is natural and accidental. The accident comes from wound and cut and cautery and similar things; and the way of the work in this is that you prick a needle, in which there is one double thread, and you put it into the matter, and you make it pierce from the left tear duct to the right, so that the threads come into two channels of the matter; then you raise the matter above the whole needle, and the cut at one spatula wide.
Et se li figure de la papiere revient selonc ceu qu’il covient, c’est boin; se ceu non, si pren .i. raseur et le met en la fendure, et torne la papiere, et fent .ij. fendures ou costeit dedens la papiere; et soient li chiés des .ij. fendures des .ij. angles de l’incision que tu as copeit, et soit fais uns angles si que quant elles sont assemblees, que li figure soit ausi com li figure d’une lettre qui a non «.j. griesche»; puis oste celle char, selonc la quantiteit que ses costez est agus desoz, de ceu qui enseut la papiere, puis ajoste les .ij. parties desevrees, et les cout d’un fil de lainne; puis lou cure de ceu que nos avons dit des medicines mollifians, et de tentes, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the figure of the matter returns according to what is right, it is good; if not, then you take one razor and put it in the split, and turn the paper, and make two splits where the cost inside the paper; and let the channels of the two splits be at the two angles of the incision that you have cut, and make two angles so that when they are assembled, the figure is as the figure of a letter which has no “j” griesche”; then remove that matter, according to the quantity that its cost is pulled out from below, of those who follow the paper, then join the two separated parts, and sew them with a thread of linen; then cure it with those that we have said about softening medicines, and bandages, until it is healed.
Et se li maladie vient de fendure ou de costure ou de cautere, si covient que tu fendes une fendure plainne desoz les poilz des papieres, et selonc ceu qui est ci devant; puis desevre entre les .ij. leivres d’une tente, si com j’ai dit; et doit on faire l’ovraige selonc la forme de la maladie, car elle est mout diverse en forme, et li saiges maistres appareille engien de tout som pooir coment il faice revenir la figure a sa forme natureil; et li malaides meisme, selonc ceu qu’il i covient d’ovraige et d’estrumens em plusors dispositions.	And if the ailment comes from a cut or suture or cautery, then it is necessary that you make a plain incision below the hairs of the papers, and according to what is before; then sew between the two leaves of a tent, as I have said; and one must do the work according to the form of the malady, because it is very diverse in form, and the wise masters equip everything of all their power how it makes return the figure to its natural form; and the patients themselves, according to what is necessary for the operation and instruments in more dispositions.
dou soudement de la papiere	Of the padding of the paper
Quant ceste soudure avient a mains homes en teil maniere que li papiere desus est sodee avec le blanc de l’oil, et ne puet movoir ne faire ses ovraiges naturez, si covient donques que tu i boutes la pointe d’un raseur desoz la papiere, et la lieve en haut; et l’estent as pinceures, tant que tu copes ceu qui est aert au spatumile subtil, qui ne soit mie trop agus ne trop trenchans, si que li malaides ne puisse soffrir que li spatumile trop agus ne blecent l’oil; et soit ton incision, dont tu escorche celle assemblee, legierement, si que li papiere reviegne selonc sa forme natureil; et est sanee toute celle assemblee, et font aucune fois en l’oil aigue salee, et le leve d’aigue douce, et de coliere; puis met entre la papiere et l’oil une tente de lin, et met sus l’oil laine moillie en abun d’uef; et aprés le tier jor use dou coliere et des choses soudans tant qu’il soit sanez.	When this suturing happens to a human hand in such a manner that the paper above is sutured with the white of the eye, and it cannot move or do its natural workings, then it is necessary that you put the tip of a razor under the paper, and lift it up; and keep it as pins, until you cut what is adherent to the spatula, which should not be too blunt nor too sharp, so that the patient does not suffer because the spatula is too blunt or bleaches the eye; and let your incision, from which you have excised that assembly, be gentle, so that the paper returns according to its natural form; and it is healed all of that assembly, and no time in salt water for the eye, and the rise of fresh water, and of collyrium; then put between the paper and the eye a tent of linen, and put on top of the eye moistened wool in abundance of an egg; and after the third day use collyrium and things soothing until it is healed.
de l’ungle de l’oil	of the angle of the eye
Saiches que li ungle est selonc .ij. manieres: elle est nervouse et semblans a .i. dur syfac, et une autre qui n’est mie nervouse, mais est semblans a blainche moistor congelee, que quant on la touche de fer et on la cuide panre as pinceures, si ne puet om; et l’une et l’autre semblance encomence devers le grant larmier, et croist poc et poc tant qu’ele cuevre toute la veue et toute la lumiere et le movement de l’oil.	Know that the angle is in .ii. manners: it is nervous and seeming to .i. hard syfac, and another which is not nervous, but is seeming to white moistor congelee, that when one touches it with iron and one bakes it panre as pincers, one cannot; and the one and the other semblance commences toward the great tear, and crosses poc and poc until it covers all the view and all the light and the movement of the eye.
Et li maniere de l’incision si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, puis li oevre les eulz; et lieve la papiere a ta main, puis coil l’ungle as pinceures de petite doubleure, et l’estent au desus; puis pren une aguille, et i met .i. poil de cheval, ou de vaiche, ou de buef, et .i. fil fort; et double la pointe de l’aguille un poc et la fiche emmi l’ungle, et la perce a tout l’aguille, et lie l’ungle d’un fil et l’estent au desus, et escorche a tout lou poil le costeit de l’ungle qui enseut la prunele et la soie au poil jusc’au chief, puis cope lou remanant en la racine dou larmier a tout lou spatumile subtil et as petites forces, et laisse la char natureil ou larmier, si que par l’incision ne veigne li cors des larmes acostumeement; et aucune fois s’estent li ungle a l’oncine soulement, et au fil, si com nos avons dit; puis l’escorche on a tout le spatumile souef de coi ci est li forme:	And the manner of incision is that the patient puts his head in your hand, then opens his eyes; and raise the paper with your hand, then coil the angle as pincers with a small doubleure, and lift it up; then take a needle, and put on it .i. hair of horse, or of calf, or of ox, and .i. strong thread; and double the point of the needle a poc and stick it into the angle, and pierce it all the way with the needle, and bind the angle with a thread and lift it up, and scrape all the hair on the side of the angle that follows the prunele and silk to the hair until the head, then cut off the remaining in the root of the tear all over the spatumile subtle and as small forces, and leave the char natureil or tear, so that by the incision does not come the body of tears acostumeement; and no times have the angle at the oncine alone, and to the thread, as we have said; then the scrape on all the spatumile souef of this is the form:
Et garde que li spatumile ne touche la toile charnue et la rompe, et que li prunele ne soit percie; et aprés l’incision giete en l’oil un poc de seil broiet, et dou coliere fait de litargire, et le laisse jusc’a l’autre jor; puis le cure de ceu qu’il i covient tant qu’il soit sanez.	And guard that the spatula does not touch the fleshy tissue and tear it, and that the needle is not pierced; and after the incision place in the eye a bit of silk ground, and of the collar made of litharge, and let it stay until the next day; then cure it as much as is needed until it is healed.
Et se li ungle n’est mie nervouse, et tu ne pues bouter l’aguille, et li uncines n’i puet entrer, maintes fois est curee ceste semblance d’ungle de medicines; et naissent sicom j’ai conteit en la division, et se tu la vues coper, si oevre l’oil dou malaide, et pren le spatumile legier poc agut selonc ceste forme:	And if the nail is not nerved, and you cannot put in the needle, and the tweezers cannot enter, many times this semblance of a nail is cured with medicines; and they grow as I have recounted in the division, and if you see it covered, work the eye of the patient, and take the spatula lightly pointed according to this form:
Et reis l’ungle desus subtilment, et se tu vois qu’elle amenuise point et li rasion i apresse, si distille de ta bouche en l’oil coliere fait de litargire et dou coliere rouge et seil broiet, et estoupe l’oil jusc’a l’autre jor; puis rencomence l’autre ovraige selonc ceste meisme oevre, tant qu’elle soit toute ostee.	And remove the nail carefully, and if you see that it does not diminish and the root is rapid, then distill from your mouth into the eye a collar made of litharge and red lead and silk ground, and plug the eye until the next day; then begin the other work according to this same operation, until it is completely removed.
Se aucune chose ne t’est contraire en l’oil, si com aposteme chaus, adonques la lait, et cure premier l’aposteme chaut tant qu’il soit sanez, puis rencomence l’ovraige si com devant, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If nothing is contrary to you in the eye, as a pustule, then milk it, and first cure the pustule hot until it is healed, then resume the work as before, until it is healed.
Et se li apparance de la chair dou larmier nuit en l’oil par grant nuisement, si la sospent a l’oncine, et en cope une partie et non mie tot, que cors de larmes n’i viegne; puis distille en l’oil coliere rouge qui est fais de litargire.	And if the appearance of the flesh due to the tear hurts in the eye by great annoyance, then suspend it with a bandage, and cut a part and not half entirely, that body of tears does not come; then distill into the eye red colic which is made of litharge.
de la char qui naist sus la prunelle	Of the flesh which arises on the pupil
Es eulz d’aucuns homes naist aucune fois char rouge, et cuevre la prunele et restraint sus les papieres et les torne au defuer, et semble une rose de balauste; et li ovraiges si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, puis li oevre les eulz, et coil toute celle char as uncines convenaubles a ceu, et la sostien a la force; puis cope la premiere char, et vai tout copant au raseur jusc’a la fin, et te garde que tune bleces l’oil a l’ovraige; et soit li incision dou spatumile que nos avons dit en l’incision de l’ungle et as petites forces de coi on oste lou sebel, si com li forme aprés cest chapistre lou demostre;	The eyes of some men are born at times with red flesh, and it covers the pupil and restrains upon the eyelids and turns them outward, and seems like a rosebud; and the work is that the patient puts his head in your hand, then you open their eyes, and coil all that flesh with suitable tweezers to this, and sustain it with force; then cut the first flesh, and go cutting all the way down to the end, and guard that you do not blind the eye during the work; and let the incision of the spatula be as we have said in the incision of the angle and the small forces from which we remove the sebum, as the form after this chapter demonstrates.
et quant li incision est acomplie et ostee toute li char, si emple l’oil de seil broiet ou tu i distille coliere rouge et semblans medicines corrosives, et met sus l’oil defuer coton avec abin d’uef, si qu’il soit asseurez d’aposteme chaut; et s’il i demore rien, et li sans chaus te sormonte, et tu doutes aposteme chaut, si laisse l’oil et cure l’aposteme de choses apaisant aposteme chaut; puis revien a ton ovraige tant qu’il soit sanez, et ensi fai cant chars est ajostee en l’oil par ceste semblance.	and when the incision is complete and all the flesh is removed, then apply the oil of silkworm crushed or distill there red coral and similar corrosive medicines, and put on top of the oil of fire cotton with yolk of egg, so that it be assured of a hot abscess; and if it remains nothing, and the skin covers over, and you doubt a hot abscess, then leave the oil and cure the abscess with things soothing a hot abscess; then return to your work as long as it is healed, and thus do until flesh is joined in the eye by this manner.
Mais toutevoie il covient que tu aliges la cure de chescun oil foible de la voie natureil; et de la voie accident, en ovraige de fer; et ne bouter mie ta main en aucun de ces ovraiges tant que tu voies que cist membres soit soffrans celui ovraige.	But nonetheless it is necessary that you follow the cure of each weak eye of the natural way; and of the accidental way, in work of iron; and do not put your hand into any of these works as long as you see that this limb suffers from that work.
des voines des eulz	of the veins of the eyes
Sebel sont voinnes rouges que sont covertes sus l’oil, et tolent a la veue son ovraige et afoiblissent l’oil toz jors. Mestier est donques au premier que tu regardes se li oil, en coi sebel est, est fors, et n’i a autre maladie fuers que lou sebel; adonques le coil en teil maniere: comande au malaide qu’il mette son chief en ton sain, puis sospent celles voines a tout l’oncine selonc sa sapience, et soit li oncines subtilz double selonc ceste forme:	Veins are red that are covered over the eye, and they take from the sight their work and weaken the eye every day.
Et soient dui oncine par degrez en .i. cors selonc ceste forme:	And let two threads by degrees in one body according to this form:
puis c’on coil as forces celles voinnes subtilment, et essue lou sanc houre aprés autre, tant que tu voies removoir celles voines fuers de l’oil; et garde que tu ne blecier l’oil as pointes des spatumiles, et fai cest ovraige a houre de midi devant lou soleil, et soies mout fervans en ton ovraige si que tu ne copes fuer que celles voinnes; et quant tu avras ce fait, si distille en l’oil coliere vert et rouge por corrumpre ceu qui est demorez dou sebel.	then coil as forces those veins subtly, and wipe the blood hour after another, until you see removing those veins from the eye; and guard that you do not prick the eye with the points of spatulas, and make this work at the hour of noon in front of the sun, and be very fervent in your work so that you do not cut further than those veins; and when you will have done this, then distill into the eye collyrium green and red to corrode what remains of the veil.
Et se tu n’as pooir de coillir tout ceu en celle houre, si fai emplastre sus l’oil de choses apaisans la dolor des eulz, et le laisse aucuns jors tant que li dolors soit apaisie et soit asseurez d’aposteme chaut, puis rencomence selonc ceste maniere qui est devant tant qu’il soit sanez; et c’est li forme des forces:	And if you have not the power to collect all these in this hour, make a poultice on the eye of things that soothe the pain of the eyes, and let it lie for several days until the pain is appeased and there is assurance of a hot abscess, then recommence according to this manner which is before as long as it is healed; and this is the form of forces:
de la fistule de l’oil	of the fistula of the eye
Li mire si nomment «arissati» fistule: quant tu la cures per cautere et par medicine ague ardant selonc ceu que j’ai devant dit, et elle n’est mie sanee, si est engien en li que tu fendes sus l’aposteme, lai ou il doit meurer, et trai toute la moistor que i est, tant que li os soit descovers.	The mire are called "arissati" fistula: when you cure it by cautery and by medicine burning according to those that I have before said, and it is not healed, then there is something in it that you cut on the abscess, where it must die, and treat all the moisture that is there, until the bone is uncovered.
Et quant li os iert descovers, et tu verras la corruption et la noiror, si la reis a tout l’estrument de coi ci est li forme; et est apelez «aspre chief», et soit fait de feir inde a .i. chief reont, et soit pointoiez si com une lime si com il est en la presente forme:	And when the bone is uncovered, and you will see the corruption and blackness, then the king has all the tools of this one form; and it is called "asper chief", and it is made from iron at one head rounded, and it is pointed like a file as it is in this present form:
Et met sus lou leu de l’os corrumput, puis le torne entre tes dois, et presse ta main un poc tant que tu saiches que celle corruption est rese; et fai ceu aucune fois, puis restoure lou leu de medicines exiccatives.	And place it on the place of the corrupted bone, then turn it between your two hands, and press your hand a bit until you know that that corruption is reset; and do this several times, then restore the place with medicinal drying agents.
se li leus est soudez, et char i naist, et li cors de la bowe est soudez, et remaint ensi xl. jors, et il ne renovele et n’est mie apostemez, et accidens mavais n’i vient, saiches qu’il est sanez; se ceu non, si n’i a autre engien que de ramener la fistule au pertus dou neif selonc ceste forme: et est que tu descuevre de l’os la seconde fois par fer, et par medicines agues, et quant il iert descovers si prent .i. foret selonc ceste forme, et soit li chiés de fer a .iij. angles, et li fust soit atenuis jusc’a chief si com tu vois ci:	If the bones are joined, and flesh grows, and the body of the bone is joined, and remains like this for 40 days, and it does not renew and is not inflamed, then know that it is healed; if this is not so, there is no other way than to bring the fistula back to the opening according to this form: and it is that you uncover the bone a second time by iron, and by sharp medicines, and when it is uncovered take one forest according to this form, and let the head of iron be at three angles, and the shaft be tapered up to the head as you see here.
puis le met sus l’os delez lou larmier, et esloigne ta main de l’oil .i. poc, puis torne a tot le foret tant qu’il perce l’os et le sent li malaides par ceu que li vens en ist s’il tient sa main sus son neif; et puis restoure lou leu de medicines seches, si com je t’ai ensigniet, et quant li char naist et endurcist li leus, si vait li matiere au neif; si est plus legiere chose au malaide.	Then place it upon the bone beside the tear duct, and move your hand away from the eye one finger's width, then turn to all the forest until it pierces the bone and the patient feels it through what comes in this if he holds his hand on his nose; and then return the place of dry medicines, as I have taught you, and when the flesh is born and hardens the joints, so goes the matter into the nose; thus is it a lighter thing for the patient.
de l’issue de l’oil	from the exit of the eye
Quant li eulz apert fuer dou tout en tout, et il ne vient point de destorbier au nef, ne amenuisement, si covient que tu lies lou malaide; puis le saine, puis li met ventouses ou haterel sens ferir por succier, puis met sus l’oil .i. liien fait d’acaice et de aloe et d’encens et de sarcocolle, et puis estrain l’oil, et l’emplaustre sus de bendes et de drapelz; et li maniere des drapelz si est que tu preignes drapelz assez molz, et double chescun en .iiij., et puis met l’un sus l’autre selonc la quantiteit que li eulz en ait mestier; puis l’estrain par desus d’un bendeil dur forment, et rencomence les ventouses por succier sens ferir; puis oste les ventouses et laisse l’oil estraint jor et nuit, et se li liiens amolist, si covient que tu l’estraignes mout; puis oste lou liien aprés le jor et la nut, et se tu vois l’oil repairier, c’est boin; se ce non; si rencomence l’emplaustre et les drapelz et lou liien et les ventouses tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the eyes are open and throughout, and there is no disturbance in the nose or decrease, then you must bind the patient; then heal, then place suction cups or aaterel without harming to suck, then put on the eye one linen made of acacia and aloe and frankincense and sarcocolla, and then strain the eye, and embalm it with bandages and cloths; and the manner of the cloths is that you take cloths soft enough, and double each in four, and then put one upon the other according to the quantity that the eye has need for; then strain it from above with a hard bandage-shaped, and reapply the suction cups to suck without harming; then remove the suction cups and leave the eye strained day and night, and if the linen softens, then you must strain it much; then remove the linen after the day and night, and if you see the eye healing, it is good; if not, then repeat the embalmment and bandages and linen and suction cups until it is healed.
dou derrompement de toile uvee	of the displacement of cloth woven
Quant disruptions vient en la toile uvee, puis apert, et vient fuer des papieres si com .i. grain de resins, et est espoantauble a veoir; adonques se tu la vues coper, li ovraiges est telz que tu boutes une aguille en la racine des la partie desoz jusc’a celi desus, puis boute une autre aguille ou il ait .i. fil double des la partie dou larmier; et la fai percier, et laisse la premiere aguille selonc la disposition; puis cope lou leu dou fil double et lie une partie de l’uve entor, et l’estraint bien, puis estrai l’aguille et met sus l’oil lainne moillie en abun d’uef; et le laisse tant que li filz chiece avec l’uve, puis cure l’oil de choses confortans tant que li plaie soit sanee; et aucune fois li plaie est restrainte par l’uve chescune part d’un cercle de drap, tant qu’elle soit sanee.	When a disruption comes in the woven cloth, then it opens, and comes forth like pieces of resin, and it is astonishing to see; therefore if you see this covered, the work is such that you push a needle into the root of the lower part until the upper one, then push another needle where there is one double thread from the part of the winder; and make it pierce, and leave the first needle according to its disposition; then cut the place of the double thread and tie one part of the vine around, and restrain it well, then extract the needle and put on the other half-eye oil in abundance of an egg; and let it remain as long as the threads fall with the vine, then cure the eye with comforting things until the wound is healed; and sometimes the wound is restrained by the vine each side of a circle of cloth, until it is healed.
Et se li eulz done grant apparance, si le perce au spatumile subtil qui viegne em parfont de l’oil, et corre la moistor albuginé et dessende li eulz, et entre ens tantost; puis l’estrai tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the eyes show a great appearance, then pierce it with a subtle spatula that comes from the eye, and correct the albuminous moisture and descend the eyes, and enter in forthwith; then extract it as long as it is healed.
de la bowe de l’oil	of the eye’s socket
Ceste maladie qui est apelee «alcunnati» nen est fuers que bowe qui est assemblee en l’oil, semblant a aigue dessendant, et ce n’est mie aigue; et li maniere de l’apparance de l’ovraige si est que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus .i. siege appareilliet et droit, puis prent le chief entre tes mains de .ij. pars, et lou muef tant que tu voies la bowe venir au desus a tes eulz; puis soit ens fichie, et ne dessende et soit descombree li lumiere, et voie li malaides les choses si com il soloit; et s’elle ne dessent desoz, saiches que c’est aigue, et se li dessendemens de la bowe n’est appareilliez si com nos avons dit. si fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, puis prent le spatumile subtil et fent sus la toile cornee .i. poc par la continuation de la conjunctive avec la toile cornee et la corone, tant que li bowe isse; et quant elle ert issue, si distille en l’oil aigue chaude mellee a miel, ou aigue ou fenugreic est boillis et miel, puis soit curee d’autre cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	This disease which is called "alcunnati" is nothing but the socket of the eye being assembled in the eye, resembling water descending, and it is not water; and the manner of appearance of the work is that you make the patient sit on a .i. well-prepared and straight seat, then take the head between your hands from .ii. parts, and move it until you see the socket coming up to your eyes; then be it fixed, and do not descend and let the light be dispersed, and the patient sees things as he used to; and if it does not descend below, know that it is water, and if the descent of the socket is not well prepared as we have said. So make the patient sit between your hands, then take the subtle spatula and make on the cornea .i. pock by the continuation of the conjunctiva with the cornea and the crown, until the socket is issued; and when it is issued, so distill into the eye hot water mixed with honey, or water or fenugreek is boiled and honey, then be cured of other cures until it is healed.
des aigues de l’oil	of the waters of the eye
Nos avons jai les semblances des aigues en la division, et ceu qu’il covient por percier; si en oevre selonc la santeit. Il covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains croisiet, fuers de la lumiere por le soleil, et li lie l’oil sain et estreint mout fort; puis met la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre se li eulz est senestres, ou a ta main destre se li eulz est destres; puis prent en ta main destre, se li eulz est senestres, l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda», ou a ta main senestre, se li eulz est destre; puis met la pointe de l’estrument delez la corone par la groissece d’un rait en celle blenchor de l’oil a la partie dou menor larmier, puis boute l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda» vertuousement, et trestorne ta main tant qu’il perce en la blenchor de l’oil, et sente que almagda viegne a la chose vuide; et covient que li mesure de la voie almagda soit au parfont de la mesure des l’espaice qui est des la prunele jusc’a la fin de la noirour; et c’est li corone de l’oil; si verras l’os en celle papiere por la clarteit de la toile cornee, et pues met l’estrument jusc’a leu ou li aigue est, puis l’espresse desoz une voie aprés autre. se li aigue dessent maintenant, si voit li malaides devant lui et l’estrument en son oil.	We have seen the appearances of the eyes in division, and what is required to examine; so in work according to the health. It is necessary that you make the patient sit between your hands crossed, far from the light of the sun, and tie the healthy eye and restrain it very strongly; then put the paper of the eye to your left hand if the eyes are left, or to your right hand if the eyes are right; then take in your right hand, if the eyes are left, the instrument which is called "almagda," or to your left hand, if the eyes are right; then put the point of the instrument beside the crown by the width of a fingernail in that whiteness of the eye at the part of the smallest tear, then push the instrument which is called "almagda" virtuously, and withdraw your hand until it pierces into the whiteness of the eye, and feel that almagda comes to the empty thing; and it is necessary that the measure of the way almagda is at the end of the measure of the space which is from the pupil to the end of the blackness; and this is the crown of the eye; so you will see the bone in that paper for the clarity of the corneal fabric, and then put the instrument until it reaches where the eye is, then express it under one way after another. If the eye comes now out, if the patient sees before him and the instrument in his eye.
Aprés repose .i. petit, et se li aigue remonte la seconde voie, met la fuer avec l’estrument, et quant elle est ens fichie et ele ne monte, si estrai almagda legierement en tornoiant ta main poc et poc; et puis remette en aigue un poc de seil gemme, et leive de ceu l’oil dedens. Puis met par defuer l’oil estoupes ou lainne moillie en oile roset et en abun d’uef, et lie avec l’oil sain.  Nos, et cil qui sont de nostre tens, mettons sus comin broiet avec abun d’uef.	After rest i. little, and if the eye returns the second way, put the force with the instrument, and when it is ens fixed and it does not rise, extract almagda gently by turning your hand back and forth; and then put in eye a bit of silk gem, and leave from that the oil inside. Then put outside the eye stopper or cloth moistened in rose oil and in abundance of egg white, and tie with the healthy eye. We, and those who are of our time, put on top as coming ground with abundance of egg white.
Et se almagda n’i puet entrer en l’oil par sa duresce, car il i a de teilz homes qui ont trop durs les eulz, si covient que tu preignes l’estrument qui est apelez «alberit», de coi ci est li forme:	And if almagda cannot enter the eye because of its hardness, for there are some men who have eyes too hard, it is necessary that you take the instrument which is called "alberit," from which this is the form:
Et perce donques la conjunctive soulement, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, mais fai .i. leu subtil, puis i boute almagda, si com nos avons dit; et au complissement de l’uevre appareille au malaide .i. dorteur avenant, en coi il dorme sus son dos en .j. leu tenebrous; et soit deveez de toz movemens, et preigne legieres viandes, et ne mueve son chief ne a destre ne a senestre, et soit liiez selonc sa disposition jusc’a tier jor; puis le deslie en cele maison meisme tenebrouse, et esprueve sa veue, et lou fai veoir aucunes choses, et puis li remet lou lien jusc’a septime jor; et ne covient mie que tu faices ceu en l’oure de la cure ou aprés l’incision maintenant, mais il covient que tu aliges ceu, por ceu que li aigue monte hastanment.	And pierce therefore the conjunctive alone, and do not pierce too deep in it, but make .i. small, then put almond, as we have said; and at the completion of the work, equip the patient .i. dorteur forward, in which he sleeps on his back in .j. dark place; and be free from all movements, and take light meats, and do not move his head neither to the right nor to the left, and be tied according to his disposition until the third day; then untie it in that same dark house, and examine his sight, and let him see some things, and then put back the bandage until the seventh day; and it is not necessary that you do this during the hour of the cure or after the incision now, but it is necessary that you do this, for that reason that the water rises hastily.
se apostemes chaus vient, que tu desliies l’oil devant le septime jor, et l’adrece de ceu qui assouaige aposteme; et quant il est apaisiez, si deslie la veue et met sus sa faice .i. orilliet por covrir aucun jor, et soit adés en celle maison tenebrouse. Et puis isse de la maison poc et poc, et se convertisse en ses cas; et saiches que nulz deciples ne se doit entremettre en cest cas.	And if the abscess comes, that you untie the eye before the seventh day, and the address of this who soothes the abscess; and when it is appeased, then untie the sight and put on his face .i. orilliet to cover any day, and be in that same dark house. And then go out of the house little by little, and convert into your cases; and know that no disciples should interfere in this case.
Et uns vint a nos qui estoit de la Yrach, qui nos dist que en som pais faisoit om almagda perciet, a coi on succe l’aigue, mais toutevoie je n’en vis onques nul en nostre terre, ne je ne lou lis onques en livres des anciens; et par aventure c’est une novele chose.	And one came to us who was from the Yrach, who told us that in their country they did almond pierced, so that one sucks the water, but nonetheless I have never seen any in our land, nor have I ever read it in books of the ancients; and by chance it is a new thing.
Et ce sont les semblances des formes de almagda, por ceu que cil qui ne les conoit les voie; et soient d’arain proprement:	And these are the resemblances of the forms of almonds, because those who do not know them see them; and be from properly grain.
Et soient li chief d’aus de ceste meisme subtiliteit, et li derriene en .iij. angles ague.	And let the head of these same subtlety, and the rear in three angles acute.
de la char sor le neis	of the flesh upon the knee
Aucune fois naissent ou neis chars ajostees diverses, de coi il i a aucunes qui semblent scorpions a mout de piez; et si i a de telz ou il ait char enchancree de fuxe color, et si a char souef de bone color. En celle donques de ces chars qui est souef, et ne mie enchancree, covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains encontre lou soleil; et oevre ses narines, et giete l’oncine a celles chars, et les trai fuers; puis cope ceu que tu em pues sostenir au spatumile subtil agut d’une part, tant que tu saiches que celle char est toute ostee.	Sometimes knees are born or grow with diverse flesh attached, because of which some appear like scorpions with many legs; and if there are such ones where the flesh is cracked a dark color, and some with flesh soft of good color.  In that one then of these fleshy parts which is soft and not cracked, it behooves you to make the patient sit between your hands against the sun; and open their nostrils, and blow into those fleshy parts, and rub them hard; then cut what you can sustain with a subtle sharp spatula on one side, until you know that the flesh is completely removed.
Et s’il en remaint aucune chose c’on ne puisse coper, si l’ovrez a tout .i. des estrumens subtil legierement, si qu’il n’i demoure rien; et se sans te sormonte, ou aposteme chaus, si lou secort si com il covient; et se c’est apostemes malignes, si te haste et lou cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez et soient ostees toutes les chars, puis giete ou neis aisil et aigue ou vin.	And if any thing remains that one cannot cover, then open it all, i.e., with instruments subtle and light, so that nothing remains; and if there are no sores, or abscesses, cleanse them as it is fitting; and if it is malignant abscesses, then hasten and cauterize it until the blood is extinguished and all the pus is removed, then giete or new oil or wine.
Se li neis oevre, et moistors en vient jusc’a palais, saiches qu’il est sanez; et se moistors ne perce si com il covient, saiches qu’il i a char nee en l’os desus, acoi li estrumens ne vient mie por taillier: adonques covient il que tu i boutes .i. fil de lin un poc gros, et soit noez de mains nous, et ait entre chescun nout d’espaice .i. doit ou moins; et mette li malaides lou chiés dou fil en son neif a som pooir, et traie en odorant tant qu’il viegne par lou neif dedens la bouche; et maintes fois font ensi li enfant as escoles, et c’est legiere chose a celui qui le vuet faire; puis tien le chief qui vient par lou neif a une main, et l’autre chief qui vient par la bouche a l’autre main, et saiche l’un aprés l’autre en soiant as nous qui sont ou fil. Fai ceu tant que tu saiches que li nout ont corrompue celle char, puis trai lou filz, essue le sanc, et moille lou fil en oignement egiptien, et le remet derechief au neis si com devant; fai ceu .iij. jors ou plus, tant que li oignemens corrode tout ceu qui est demorez de char; et puis met ou neis une caine de plonc aucuns jors tant qu’il soit sanez, et s’il a mestier de medicines sechans, si en use; et c’est li forme de l’estrument por purgier lou chief, a coi on distille les oiles et les medicines ou neis:	If the nose works and moisture comes as far as the palate, know that it is clear; and if the moisture does not pierce as it should, know that there is new flesh in the bone above, so the instruments cannot come to cut: therefore, you must put into it i.e., a thread of linen a bit thick, and be knotted by hands ours, and have between each knot a space i.e. an inch or less; and place the patient's head of the thread in his nose at its root, and pull gently until it comes through the nostril inside the mouth; and many times do children in school this, and it is a light thing to him who wants to do it; then hold the head which comes through the nostril with one hand, and the other head which comes through the mouth with the other hand, and feel each one after the other while you are at us who are or thread. Do this until you know that the knots have corrupted that flesh, then pull out the thread, wipe the blood, and moisten the thread in Egyptian ointment, and put it back in the nose as before; do this for three days or more, until the ointment corrodes all that remains of flesh; and then put on the nostril a poultice of wool for some days until it is healed, and if it needs drying medicines, use them; and this is the form of the instrument for purging the head, to which one distills the oils and medicines in the nose:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, semblant a une lampe overte, si com une cainne, et li conduis ausi; et se tu vues, si fai une cainne close, et soit li estrumens plains por espurgier lou chief; et ait .i. mainche au chief por lou tenir quant on chaufe l’oile ou aucune liquor.	And let it be of silver or iron, resembling an open lamp, like a basin, and conduct it so also; and if you see fit, make a closed basin, and let the instruments be full for purging the head; and have one handle at the top for holding it when one heats the oil or any liquor.
de la char sor le neis	of the bone upon the joint
Maintes fois naist au chief dou neis une maladie qui est apelee «telul», et croist et devient grans adés, tant qu’il est vis chose au regarder; et por ceu covient que tu lou copes au comencement, et l’oste tout fuer, puis met sor leu lou cautere ou la medicine ardant; et s’on le tarde a coper tant qu’il soit grans, si pren warde s’il est durs, de fuxe color, de povre sens: si ne lou touchier mie de fer car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, car quant on le cope aucune fois, si en vient grant malice au malaide; et se li apostemes est de soef touchement, non mie de fuxe color, et tu vois c’on le puisse tout coper, si vuide le malaide et lou cope sens paor, et cure le leu de choses sechans et restraignans.	Many times a disease named “telul” is born upon the joint, and it grows and becomes great, so much that it is a frightening sight to look at; and for this reason it behooves you to cut it from the beginning, and remove all the bone, then place upon its spot the cautery or burning medicine; and if one delays in cutting until it is large, beware if it is hard, of dark color, without feeling; do not touch it with iron because it is a festering abscess, for when one cuts it even once, great harm comes to the patient; and if the abscess is soft to the touch, not of dark color, and you see that one can cut it completely, then reassure the patient and cut it without fear, and treat the spot with things drying and constricting.
quant li neis est copez et cosus	when the joint is cut and closed
Saiches que quant solutions de continuation vient en une de ces cartillagines ovraiges, i profite poc, fuer que en aucuns homes. Il covient donques cant ceu avient a aucun, si regarde se li plaie est fresche a tout son sanc; et adonques ajoste les .ij. levres a une costure, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et se les levres sont ja desevrees d’une part et d’autre, si covient que tu escorches toutes les parties de lor keur tant qu’elles sainent, puis assemble les .ij. levres a une costure, et l’estraint, et poudre sus poudre de sanc de dragon, et encens broiet; et met sus les poudres une piece d’emplaustre de fort ou d’autre emplaustre soudant, et le laisse tant qu’il chiece par lui, puis le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Know that when a solution of continuation comes in one of these worked cartilages, it benefits little, because in no men. Therefore, when this happens to any man, see if the wound is fresh with all its blood; and then join the two lips with a stitch, then cure it until it is healed; and if the lips are already separated on both sides, then you must scrape all parts of their core until they heal, then bring the two lips together with a stitch, and restrain them, and powder on top of each other dragon's blood powder, and incense ground; and put on top of the powders a piece of strong plaster or another plasters binding, and let it remain until it dries by itself, then cure it with ointment until it is healed.
Li maniere de la costure si est que tu assembles la solution: ou par aguilles, si com nos avons dit en la costure dou ventre; ou par fil, si com je le t’ai fait savoir.	The manner of stitching is that you assemble the solution: either by needles, as we have said in the stitch of the belly; or by thread, as I have told you.
des apostemes des levres	of abscesses of the lips
A mains homes avient dedens les levres aposteme dur, semblans a grains de veces, et menor et plus grant; adonques couvient que tu tornes les levres, et fendes sus chescun nout, et le prent as pinceures et le cope en chescune partie; puis emple lou leu aprés l’incision de vitriole broiet, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; et puis lou leive d’aisil, et cure lou leu de choses seches tant qu’il soit sanez.	To men's mouths happen inside the lips abscess hard, seeming to grains of grapes, and smaller and larger; therefore it is necessary that you turn the lips, and fends upon each knot, and take with tweezers and cut in each part; then apply there after the incision of vitriol ground, as long as the blood is stained; and then the leave of air, and cure the place of dry things until it is healed.
de la char des gencives	of the flesh of the gums
Maintes fois naist sus les gencives char ajostee, que li ancien apelent «albulus»; si covient que tu la sostienes as tenailles, et la cope a sa racine, et laisse corre la bowe ou le sanc; puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet, ou autres poudres restraignans et desiccatives; et se celle char revient aprés l’incision, et maintes fois avient, si la cope la seconde fois, et la cauterize: si ne revient mie aprés le cautere; et ce sont les formes des estrumens por coper.	Many times flesh grows on the gums, which the ancients call "albulus"; therefore it is necessary that you hold it with tweezers and cut it at its root, and let the blood flow out; then put on the place vitriol ground, or other restraining and drying powders; and if that flesh returns after the incision, and this happens many times, so cut it a second time, and cauterize it: if it does not return after cautery; and these are the forms of instruments for cutting.
des sordens	of deafness
Aucunes fois sont assemblees au chief des dens, dedens la bouche entre les gencives, escorces qui sont laides et aspres; et aucune fois sont li dent noir et citrin et vers, tant que li corruption vient a la gencive, et sont li dent puant; si covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, et ses chiés soit en ton saint, et reis les dens ou les escorces aperent, tant qu’il n’i demore rien; et ensi fai de la noiror et de la verdor, et de la jaunice et des autres taiches, tant qu’elles soient mondees; et s’on oste ceu que i est a la premiere rasion, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence a rere le secont jor et lou tier, tant que tu aies tout reis; et saiches que li dent ont mestier de diverses formes d’estrumens por reire, selonc ceu que li oevre lou demoustre, por ceu que li raseur dont on reit defuer les dens ont autres formes que cil dont on reit entre les dens; et cestes formes et autres soient avec toi appareillies.	Sometimes are assembled at the head of the teeth, inside the mouth between the gums, scabs that are ugly and rough; and sometimes the tooth is black and yellow and toward, as long as corruption comes to the gum, and the teeth stink; so you must make the patient sit between your hands, and his jaws be in your saint, and remove the teeth or scabs appear, as long as nothing remains there; and thus do of blackness and verdancy, and jaundice and other spots, as long as they are cleansed; and if one removes that which is at the first reason, it is good; if those no, then starts again on the second day and the third, until you have all removed; and know that teeth need diverse forms of tools to remove, according to what the work shows, because the scraper with which one removes outside the teeth have other forms than those with which one removes between the teeth; and these forms and others be with you equipped.
Il covient quant tu cures lou dent de sa dolor que tu tardes dou traire tant com tu pues, car ce ne doit om mie faire; car c’est une substance mout haute jusc’a donc c’on n’ait point d’excusation dou raier.	It is necessary when you cure the tooth of its pain that you take care to draw as little as possible, because one must not do otherwise; for it is a very high substance until one has no excuse for scraping.
Adonques quant li malaides est constrains dou traire, si covient que tu soies certains dou dent doillant. Maintes fois desoit li dolor lou malaide, et cuide qu’elle soit ou dent saint, et fait traire le boin dent; et toutevoie ne se depart mie li dolor per ceu, tant que li malvais estrais, car nos l’avons ja veut faire a ces sainors; et quant tu es bien certains dou dent doillant, si covient que tu escorches entor lou dent a tout i. spatumile fort por warder la gencive de toutes pars; puis le mues a tes dois ou as tenailles subtilz au premier poc et poc, tant qu’il soit bien eslochiés, puis i afferme bien les tenailles; et soit li chiés dou malaide en ton saint entre tes genous, et lou tien bien si qu’il ne se mueve.	Therefore when the patient is constrained to be treated, it behoves you to be certain about the tooth aching. Many times the pain of the patient deceives, and he thinks that it is a tooth of saint, and makes treat the good tooth; and nevertheless it departs not the pain because of this, as long as the bad remains, for we have already seen it with our own kin; and when you are well certain about the aching tooth, it behoves you to scrape around the tooth to all its. spatula firm in order to ward the gum from all parts; then moves it to your two or pliers subtle to the first point and point, until it is well dislodged, then firmly affirms the pliers; and be the chin of the patient in your saint between your knees, and hold it well so that it does not move.
Aprés estrai lou dent droitement sens brisier, et s’il ne saut fuer, si prent aucun de ces estrumens et le boute dedens de chescune part legierement, et lou remuef si com tu as fait premier. Et se li dens est perciez et mengiez, si covient que tu l’emplisses de drapelz, lai ou li pertus sont; et si l’estraint subtilment as tenailles, que il ne brise a l’estraindre; et covient mout saigement ovrer entor la gencive por deschaucier lou dent.	After having extracted the tooth straight without breaking it, and if it does not come out for sure, take any of these instruments and put it inside each part gently, and move it as you have done first. And if the tooth is pierced and broken, it behoves you to fill it with drapes, where the perforations are; and if it is extracted subtly with pliers, that it does not break when extracting; and it behoves very sagely to work around the gum in order to dislodge the tooth.
Et te done bien en warde que tu ne le brises, et en remaigne une partie, et reveigne au malaide par la malice de la racine plus grans dolors de la premiere. Et te warde que tu ne faices mie ensi com font li ignorant sainor, qui par lor haste et par lor hardiesce brisent aucune fois le charreit, et n’i amenistrent mie ceu que nos avons conteit; mais font venir aucune fois par l’oquison de ceu grant maladie por les racines que i demorent, ou por lou charreit qu’il brisent, si com nos avons sovent veut; et quant li dens est trais, si lavez lou leu de vin ou d’aisil et de seil; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, que sovent avient, si emple lou leu de vitriole broiet; et se ceu ne vaut, si le cauterize.	And be well guarded that you do not break it, and remain a part of it, and return to the patient by the malice of the root greater pains than the first. And guard yourself that you do not act as the ignorant kin do, who by their haste and boldness break sometimes the tooth, and do not bring about what we have recounted; but often bring about by the consequence of these great illness for the roots that remain, or for the tooth that they break, as we have often seen; and when the tooth is pulled, wash the place with wine or oil and salt; and if there comes a discharge of blood, which often happens, put on the place vitriol ground; and if this does not suffice, cauterize it.
Les formes des estrumens, a coi om muet les dens premier, soient a longes pointes et a gros mainches, qu’il ne doublent mie quant tu trairas le dent; et ce sont les formes:	The forms of the instruments, as to which one moves the teeth first, should have long points and large handles so that they do not double when you pull the tooth; and these are the forms:
Et soient de gros membres si qu’il ne ploient mie au traire, et soient de fer inde bien fait, et soient dentez por mues tenir.	And be of thick members so that they do not bend when pulling, and be made of well-made iron, and be toothed for good hold.
de la racine des dens	from the root of the teeth
Quant li racine demoure au traire, si covient que tu mettes sor le leu coton moilliet em burre .i. jor ou ij., tant que li leus soit amolis, puis i boute les tenailles qui sont apelees «algefri», de coi li chiés semblet bec de soigne; et soient dedens faites ausi com une lime et c’est li forme:	When the root remains in the tooth, then it is necessary that you put on top of it cotton moistened in butter, for one or two days, until the gum is softened, then put the pliers which are called "algefri," because the jaw seems like a beak of care; and be inside made as well as a file and this is the form:
Et se les racines ne vuellent issir a tout ces tenailles, si covient que tu descuevre la char tot entor la racine, et i met l’estrument qui est apelez «althali», c’est a savoir palainche, de coi ci est li forme:	And if the roots do not want to come out with all these tweezers, it is necessary that you uncover the flesh all around the root, and put in the instrument called "althali", which is to say a chisel, because this is its form:
Et soit fors et gros si qu’il ne brise mie, et se li racine saut par ceu, c’est boin; se ceu non, si t’aide de toz les estrumens, de coi les formes vienent ci aprés:	And let it be strong and thick so that it does not break, and if the root jumps out with these, it is good; if these do not, then help yourself with all the instruments, of which the forms come after:
Et si s’aide on de cest estrument qui ait .ij. rains, de coi ci est li forme:	And if one helps oneself with this instrument that has two prongs, of which this is the form:
