et d’autres ferremens qui sont devant en la rasion des dens, et de cest estrument qui semble unes grans tenailles, dont ci est li forme:	and other iron instruments that are in front in the ratio of teeth, and of this instrument that resembles large tweezers, of which here is the form:
Et soit cist estrumens fors qu’il ne puisse brisier, et saiches que mout d’estrumens de dens sont; et ausi d’autres estrumens, qui ne sont mie contez; et li saiges maistres subtilz trueve par soi meisme son estrument, selonc ceu que ses ovraiges et li maladie li demoustre, car il i a de teilz maladies ou li ancien n’enseignerent point d’estrument por la diversiteit d’au;s et s’om brise point dou charreit ou des autres os, ou il porrit, si i cerche as estrumens qu’il i covient, que je t’ai dit, et t’aide des gestes, de coi ci est li forme:	And be this instrument so that it cannot break, and know that many instruments of teeth are; and also other instruments, which are not mentioned; and the wise masters subtle find by himself his instrument, according to what his works and the disease show him, for there are such diseases where the ancient do not teach any instrument for the diversity of others; and if one breaks not the bone or other bones, or it is possible, then seek the instruments that it befits, which I have told you, and help with gestures, for this is the form:
Et soient gros et bien tenant por tenir l’os, qu’il n’eschaipe, mais le puisse tenir et oster; et puis restoure lou leu de medicines convenant a ceu, et s’il ait en l’os porriture, et elle est petite, si la reis a tout cest estrument:	And let them be thick and well-fitting to hold the bone, so that it does not escape, but it can hold and remove; and then restore its place with medicines suited to this, and if there is in the bone rot, and it is small, then use all this instrument:
Quant li dent apperent ne mie selonc lou cors natureil, et li forme est laide, et meismement en femmes puceles, si covient que tu saiches se li dens est neis aprés lou dent, et n’est mie en droit leu, et on ne lou puet soier ne limer: adonques lou raie; et s’il est aers avec lou dent, si prent cest estrument dont ci est li forme, et est semblans a .i. petit bec, et soit de fer inde agut en som:	When the tooth appears not according to the body's natural form, and the shape is ugly, and even in virgins, it befits that you know if the tooth is newly grown after the tooth, and is not in its right place, and it cannot be filed or shaped; then use a file; and if it is stuck with the tooth, then take this instrument whose form is here, and is similar to one small beak, and let it be of sharp iron at its summit:
Et lou cope poc et poc em mains jors por la duresce dou dent, et por ceu que tu ne mueves les autres, et s’il est apparans c’on le puisse limer, si lou lime d’une teil lime com ci est li forme:	And the coping little by little in hands days for the hardness of the tooth, and because you do not move the others, and if it appears that one can be filed, if the file of a piece of file as this is the form:
et est ausi com li lime de coi on fait les aguilles; et en lime lou dent poc et poc em mains jors legierement, si qu’il ne se mueve tant qu’il chiece; puis la plaine en la fin a tout aucun raseur, et se li dens est trop trenchans et il blece la lengue, si covient limer l’aspreteit tant qu’il soit igalz, si qu’il ne blece la lengue ne ne corrompe la parole.	and is also like the file of which one makes the needles; and in file the tooth little by little in hands days lightly, so that it does not move until it falls; then the plain at the end to all any shavings, and if the teeth are too sharp and it bleaches the tongue, then it is necessary to file the sharpness until it be equal, so that it does not bleach the tongue nor corrupt the speech.
quant li dent lochent	when the tooth loosens
Quant li dent devant lochent, ou par percussion ou par cheoir, et li malaides ne puet presser sus ceu qu’il menjue qu’il ne chient, et tu les as curez de medicines restrignans, et ceu ne vaut; si les covient restraindre d’un fil d’or, car li filz d’argent devient vert et porrit, mais li ors ne se mue onques; et soit li filz moiens ne trop gros ne trop menus, selonc la quantiteit de l’espaice entre les dens; et se tu vues adrecier les dens, si pren lou fil et lou boute double entre les .ij. dens sains, puis met les chiés entre les dens meus, s’il en i a .i. ou plusors, tant que tu veignes saigement jusc’au dent sain d’autre part; puis rencomence la coverture jusc’a la partie ou tu encomensas, et estrains ta main subtilment et saigement, tant qu’il ne se mueve point; et soit ta lieeure a la racine dou dent si qu’il ne puist eschaper. Puis cope les chiés dou fil a unes tenailles, et les assemble, et les repont entre le dent sain, et le met ensi qu’il ne blece la lengue; et puis le laisse ensi estroit tant com il puet demorer, et s’il deslie, ou li filz ront, si l’estraint d’un autre fil; si demorrait et servira ensi tout son tens, et c’est li forme des dens et li figure de l’adrecement des .ij. dens sains, et des .ij. meus, si com tu vois:	When the tooth in front is loosened, either by percussion or by falling, and the patient cannot press on it so that it moves without paining him, and you have cured them with constricting medicines, and this does not help; then it is necessary to restrain it with a gold thread, because the silver thread becomes green and rots, but gold never changes; and let the thread be neither too thick nor too thin, according to the quantity of space between the teeth; and if you see the teeth are misaligned, take the thread and pass it double between the two healthy teeth, then put the jaws between the teeth, if there is one or more, until you come cleverly to the healthy tooth on the other side; then begin again the covering up to the part where you began, and strain your hand subtly and wisely, so that it does not move at all; and let the ligature be at the root of the tooth so that it cannot escape. Then cut the ends of the thread with pliers, and join them together, and place them between the healthy teeth, and set it so that it does not touch the tongue; and then leave it as tight as it can remain, and if it unties, or the thread breaks, then bind it with another thread; let it remain and serve thus throughout its duration, and this is the form of the teeth and the figure of the alignment of the two healthy teeth, and the two loose ones, as you see:
Et quant li dent chiet, si lou remet on en son leu, de fres en fres, si com nos avons dit; et ne s’en entremette mie qui n’est saiges et soffrans, et aucune fois fait on la forme d’un dent d’os de vaiche, et lou met on au leu ou li defaute est, et l’estraint on si com nos avons dit, et demore et sert ensi lonc tens.	And when the tooth falls out, then it is replaced in its place, fresh against fresh, as we have said; and let no one interfere who is not wise and experienced, and sometimes one makes the form of a tooth from the bone of a calf, and puts it in the place where the deficiency is, and binds it as we have said, and it remains and serves thus for a long time.
de coper lou liien de la lengue	to cover the ligament of the tongue
Aucune fois est cist liiens qui vient desoz la lengue ou naturez, que on naist ensi; ou par accident de plaie soudee; et li ovraiges est telz que tu oevre la bouche dou malaide, et ait sa teste en ton sain, et li lieve la lengue; puis cope lou liien nervous dou large, tant que li lengue soit desloie de son tenement, et se il i a duresce ou nout, et c’est de soudement de plaie, si i boute l’uncine et cope dou large celui liement; et garde que li fendure ne soit mie trop em parfont, por l’artere qui est desoz; et quant tu as fait, si leve le leu d’aigue rose et d’aisil, ou d’aigue froide, puis met desoz la lengue une tente de lin; et la teigne li malaides chescune nuit, que li leus ne puisse soder. Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si met sor le leu vitriole broiet; et se li sans te vaint, si le cauterize au cautere lentiginout, qui est boin a ceu; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez,	At no time is this ligament which comes from under the tongue or nature, that one is born thus; or by accident of a wound joined; and the work is such that you operate the mouth of the sick person, and have his head in your hand, and raise the tongue; then cut the nervous ligament wide, until the tongue is displaced from its place, and if there is hardness or knot, and this is from the joining of a wound, so put the probe and cut the wide ligament; and guard that the cut is not too deep, for the artery which is below; and when you have done, raise the level of rose water and of easy, or of cold water, then put under the tongue a tent of linen; and bind the sick person each night, so that the wound may not be joined. And if hemorrhage occurs, so put on the site vitriol ground; and if the bleeding does not stop, so cauterize it with the lentiginous cautery, which is good for this; then cure it with another cure until it is healed,
et se tu lou vois de fusse color ou noir ou dur, si que li malaides ne lou sent, si n’i touchier point, car c’est chancre; et s’il est declinans a blenchor, et il i a moistor, si i giete l’oncine, et lou fent d’un spatumile subtil, et lou delivre d’une part et d’autre; et se li sans te vaint a ton ovraige, si met sus vitriole broiet tant qu’il soit estainchiez, puis revien a ton ovraige tant que tu traies tout fuer; puis leve lou leu d’aisil et de seil, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you see it of black or hard color, and the sick person does not feel it, so do not touch it, for it is a chancre; and if it is declining towards whiteness, and there is moisture, so put the probe, and cut it with a sharp spatula, and deliver it on one side and the other; and if the bleeding does not stop to your work, so put on top ground vitriol until it is bleached, then return to your work as long as you draw out everything; then raise the level of rose water and of sage, and cure it with other cures until it is healed.
des apostemes de la gorge	of abscesses of the throat
Aucune fois vient dedens la gorge boces qui sont apelees «godath», et les apele on proprement les .ij. amandres, et quant tu les cures, si com nos avons dit en la division, et elles ne sont sanees, si pren garde: se c’est apostemes dur de petit sens et de fusse color, si ne lou touchier mie de fer. Et s’il est rouges et li racine est grosse, si ne lou touchier mie de fer, ausi por lou decorrement de sanc; mais lou laisse tant qu’il soit meur, et adonques tu lou partiras, ou il rompirait par soi; et s’il est de blainche color reont, et li racine est subtilz, si aies apareilliet l’estrument por coper, mais regarde premierement se li apostemes chalz repose et est apaisiez. Adonques fai seoir lou malaide devant lou soleil, et ses chiés soit en ton sain, et li oevre la bouche et lou preigne li serjans entre ses mains, et presse la lengue desoz a tout l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme; et soit d’argent ou d’arain subtil ausi com uns coutelz:	Sometimes there come inside the throat boils which are called "godath," and they call them properly the two almonds, and when you cure them, as we have said in the division, and they are not healed, if take care: if it is abscesses hard of small sense and fusse color, if do not touch it with iron. And if it is red and the root is thick, if do not touch it with iron, also for the flow of blood; but leave it until it is dead, and then you will split it, or it would break by itself; and if it is of white color reont, and the root is subtle, have prepared the instrument to cover, but first look if the abscess calz rests and is appeased. Then make the patient sit in front of the sun, and his knees be in your health, and the work opens the mouth and the preigne the serjans between his hands, and press the tongue below all the instrument, of which is the form; and be of silver or arrain subtle as a knife:
Cant tu presses la lengue a tout cest estrument, et tu vois l’aposteme, si pren l’oncine et lou fiche en l’amandre, et la trai fuer au desus plus que tu pues; et trai aucune chose des toiles avec, puis la cope a l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme, que semble unes forces; et toutevoie li chief sont corbé, et l’un endroit l’autre, et sont molt agut, et est fait de fer inde ou d’andainne:	And you press the tongue to all this instrument, and you see the abscess, if take the oncine and put it in the almond, and the pull upwards more than you can; and pull nothing of the cloths with, then the cope to the instrument, of which is the form, that seems some forces; and although the chief are curved, and one place the other, and are very sharp, and is made of iron inde or d'andainne:
Et se tu n’as cest estrument present, si lou cope as tenailles, de coi ci est li forme:	And if you do not have this instrument present, if it is cope with pliers, of which is the form:
Et soit trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part nom; et quant tu as copeit l’une des amandres, si cope l’autre selonc cele meisme maniere, et aprés l’incision gargarize li malaides aigue chaude, et aigue et aisil, et se decorremens de sanc avient, si gargarize li malaides aigue, ou escorces de pomes grenates soient cuites, ou fuelles de mirte, et semblans choses, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois naissent en la gorge autres apostemes que les .ij. amandres, si les cope donques ensi com les .ij. amandres igament.	And be trenchant on one part, and the other part no; and when you have cut one of the almonds, cut the other according to the same manner, and after the incision gargle the patient with hot water, and water and vinegar, and if a decorremens of blood happens, gargle the patient with water, or peels of pomegranates that are cooked, or leaves of myrtle, and similar things, as long as the san is stained; then cure it until it is healed; and no times are born in the throat other abscesses than the two almonds, so cut them then as well as the two almonds equally.
Et je medicinai une femme d’un aposteme que li estoit neis dedens la gorge, c’est a savoir .i. aposteme de petit sens; et avoit jai bien pres close toute la gorge, si que li femme ne pooit expirer por le conduit qui estoit estoupez, et ne pooit ne mengier ne boivre, et fust morte s’elle demorast ensi .i. jor ou .ij. Et li apostemes estoit jai si montez qu’il avoit fuer mis .ij. rains par les .ij. pertuis dou neis. Je hastai donques tantost, et fichai en l’un .i. oncine, puis lou traï fuers, et en traï grant porcion de bowe; puis refis autreteil en l’autre pertus dou neis, et li ovrai la bouche et li pressai la lengue; aprés fichai l’oncine en ces apostemes, et en copai une partie, et n’en issit fuers que un poc de sanc; et ensi fut destoupez li conduis de la gorge la femme, et comensa maintenant a boivre aigue et puis vin, et ne cessai de taillier de cel aposteme par lonc tens; et li apostemes recroissoit adés, et remplissoit lou leu que je avoie vuidiet, tant qu’il refut mout gros; adonques je l’engignai et lou cauterizai dedens la gorge: ensi demora sens croistre; et me partis de ces parties, et ne soi que Deus fist de li aprés moi.	And I medicated a woman from an abscess that it was born inside the throat, that is to say one abscess of small sense; and I had well pressed closed all the throat, so that the woman could not expire through the conduit which was stopped up, and could neither eat nor drink, and would have died if she remained thus one day or two. And the abscess was to me so mounted that it had been put two reins by the two openings of birth. I then immediately, and fitted in one one incision, then pulled out the track and a large portion of pus; then refit another piece in the other opening of birth, and opened the mouth and pressed the tongue; after fitted the incision into these abscesses, and cut a part, and only a little bit of blood came out; and thus was unstopped the conduit of the throat to the woman, and she began now to drink water and then wine, and did not cease to cut from this abscess for a long time; and the abscess grew back again, and filled up the place that I had emptied, until it became very big; then I ignited it and cauterized it inside the throat: thus remained without growing; and I departed from these parts, and know only that God did of her after me.
de l’uve	of the grape
Quant reume dessent a l’uve, et elle est enflee et elle est longe, si est apelee «perpendiculaire»; et s’elle est desoz grosse et reonde, si est apelee «uve». Quant elle est curee si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, et tu vois que li chaus apostemes est apaisiez, et elle est subtilz, si covient que tu la copes; et celle qui est reonde assemblee et n’est mie longe; et elle est sanguine ou de fusse color ou noire, si covient que tu eschues l’incision de li. Car il i a grant peril sus lou malaide. Il covient donques, quant tu la vois, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit, de sa blenchor et de sa longesce, que tu faices seoir le malaide devant lou soleil, et li presse la lengue a l’estrument dont nos avons fait la remembrance ci devant; puis fiche l’oncine en l’uve, et la trai desoz, et la cope a .i. des .ij. estrumens que j’ai dit en l’incision des .ij. amandres. Et covient que tu ne coper mie fuer que la superfluiteit qui est outre le termine natureil; car se tu en copes plus, si grieves a la voix, et a la parolle; et aprés l’incision, use de ceu que nos avons dit en l’incision des .ij. amandres, et le cure tant qu’elle soit sanee. Et se li malaides a paor dou coper, si covient que tu i use d’engien a la cauterization de li sens paor. Et li maniere dou cautere si est aigue ague. Et est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, et puis li presse la lengue a l’estrument que nos avons dit ou chapistre de cautere, et confis avec aigue vive chaus, si qu’elle ne soit mie trop espesse ne trop clere; et en emple le chevement de cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme:	When the grape is ripe and it is long, it is called "perpendicular"; and if it is short and round, it is called "grape". When it is treated as we have said in the division, and the treatment does not help, and you see that the abscess is calmed, and it is subtle, then you should cut it; and the one which is rounded assembled and is not long; and it is sanguine or of fusse color or black, then you should avoid the incision of it. Because there is great peril on the patient. So therefore, when you see it, according to the manner that I have said, by its whiteness and its length, that you make the patient sit before the sun, and press the tongue to the instrument of which we have made remembrance before; then insert the needle into the grape, and remove it below, and cut it at .i. of .ij. instruments that I have said in the incision of the .ij. almonds. And it is necessary that you do not cut more than the superfluity which is beyond the natural limit; because if you cut more, it grieves the voice, and the speech; and after the incision, use what we have said in the incision of the .ij. almonds, and cure until it is healed. And if the patient has fear to be cut, then it is necessary that you use an engine for the cauterization of the sensitive fear. And the manner of the cautery is sharp and acute. And it is that the patient puts his head in your hand, and then presses the tongue to the instrument which we have said or chapter of cautery, and confis with live fire so that it is not too thick nor too clear; and in employing the point of this instrument, by which this is the form:
Et ait ou chief une cheveure ou om met la medecine, si com li chevemens d’une cuillier, et met l’estrument a tout la medicine sus l’uve; et li malaides soit gisans sus son costeit, si que li salive et li muscillaige corre de sa bouche de la medicine dedens, si qu’ele ne dessende a la gorge, et lou blece; puis tien ta main a tout la medicine et la presse sus l’uve, la quantiteit de la moitiet d’une houre, tant que tu la vois nercie et li mordications de la medicine soit apaisie; et se tu vues, pren coton et l’envoloupe sus aucun estrument, et moille lou coton en la medicine, et boute l’estrument a tout le couton en la cainne desus, tant que li coton s’aerde sus l’uve; et fai ceu sovent, tant que li cauteres soit parfais, puis la laisse elle seche, et chiet aprés .iiij. jors ou .v. Et se tu as mestier de rencomencier lou cautere de la medicine, si le rencomence, et aprés le cautere l’essue entor l’uve, de couton embut em burre, et mundifie ceu qui est entor de la medicine; et soit arosez d’aigue froide, et soit curez de gargarismes tant qu’il soit sanez.	And have or chief a hair or one puts the medicine in, as the handle of a spoon, and put the instrument to all the medicine on the grape; and the patient be lying on his side, so that the saliva and the muscle move from his mouth of the medicine within, so that it does not descend to the throat, and the neck; then hold your hand to all the medicine and press it on the grape, the quantity of half an hour, as long as you see it burn and the irritations of the medicine be calmed; and if you see, take cotton and envelop it on any instrument, and moisten the cotton in the medicine, and put the instrument to all the cotton in the canal above, as long as the cotton hardens on the grape; and do this often, as long as the cautery is perfect, then let it dry, and fall after .iiij. days or .v.. And if you have need to recommence the cautery of the medicine, so commence it again, and after the cautery wipe around the grape, with cotton smeared in butter, and purify what is around the medicine; and be rinsed with cold water, and be cured with gargles as long as it is healed.
Ceste cure est plus save de l’incision, ne que li cautere; s’elle est curee de fumigation selonc ceste maniere, pren calament et ysope et origanum et rue et camomille et avronne et semblans herbes, et les assemble toutes ou aucunes d’eles en .i. pot, et i met aisil, et fai bullir; et li potz soit bien gluez de fort terre, et enmi le pot ait .i. estrument cheveit selonc ceste maniere:	This cure is more safe than incision, nor the cautery; if it is cured by fumigation according to this manner, take calament and hyssop and oregano and rue and chamomile and wormwood and similar herbs, and put them all together or any of them in one pot, and put it inside, and make it boil; and the pot should be well glued with strong earth, and inside the pot have one instrument head according to this manner:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, et soit li uns des chiés boutez en la bouche dou malaide tant que li vapor monte a l’uve par la caine, tant que li uve soit mortifie; aprés lou rencomence sovent, tant que li uve seche, et garde que tu ne faices ceu au comencement de l’avenement de l’aposteme chaut, car plusors choses i avienent; et ne faire mie ceu fuer que a la declination d’aposteme chaut. Et se cist estrument n’est presens, si pren une caine et met dedens lou chief une craiffe d’uef, si que li bouche au malaide n’ait mie trop chaut; car li craiffe d’uef ne lait mie la vapor grever la bouche, et c’est bone cure ensamble salut.	And be it of silver or iron, and be the one of the heads put into the mouth of the sick person as long as the steam rises to the grape through the cane, until the grape is mortified; afterward he begins again, until the grape dries, and guard that you do not make this at the beginning of the coming of the hot abscess, for many things happen; and do not make this cure except at the declination of a hot abscess. And if this instrument is not present, then take a cane and put inside its head a piece of egg, so that the mouth of the sick person does not have too much heat; for the piece of egg does not let the steam weigh down the mouth, and it is a good cure altogether health.
Maintes fois s’aert a la gorge os ou espinee de poisson, ou aucune chose; si covient donc que tu traies ceu que tu pues veoir, et li presse la lengue au soleil a tout l’estrument, si que tu voies mues la chose; et ceu que ne t’apert mie et est reponus en la gorge, covient que tu faices vomir le malaide ainsois que li viande soit cuite en l’estomac; par aventure si istra li chose aerse par le vomissement; ou li malaides englutisse une piece d’esponge, ou une piece de navel, ou une racine de laitue, ou .i. morceil de pain sec; et lie a l’esponge .i. fil, et puis la transglutisse; et quant elle venra au leu, si s’aerdra, et puis trairas fuer; et s’elle ne vient fuer de ceu que nos avons dit, si pren .i. estrument de plonc selonc ceste forme:	Many times a thorn or fish spine gets stuck in the throat, or some other thing; so it behooves you to pull out what you can see, and press the tongue to the sun with all the instrument, so that you see move the thing; and what does not appear to you and is put back in the throat, it behoves you to make the sick person vomit as soon as the food is cooked in the stomach; perhaps if this will take the thing out by vomiting; or the sick person swallows a piece of sponge, or a piece of navel, or a root of lettuce, or one morsel of dry bread; and tie to the sponge one thread, and then swallow it; and when it comes to the place, it gets stuck, and then you pull further; and if it does not come out from what we have said, then take one instrument of wood according to this form:
Et soit li estrumens corbés au chief si qu’il puist plus legierement entrer en la gorge, et ait le chief en haut leveit; et warde que tu ne touchier l’epiglote, que li tous ne li viegne, ne ne bouter mie l’os dedens; et mues vaut que li malaides i boute l’estrument, por ceu qu’il seit mues ou li chose est aerse; si la boute aval, ou il la traie fuer a tout l’estrument igalment, tant qu’elle soit fuer.	And let the instruments be curved at the head so that it may more easily enter into the throat, and have the head held high lifted; and guard that you do not touch the epiglottis, lest it come to life, nor push in the bone; and it is better that the patient pushes the instrument, because he will know if it is well or the thing is difficult; so if he pushes down, or he draws it up all of the instrument equally, until it is pulled.
de la sansue de la gorge	of the cutting of the throat
Aucune fois est medicinee li sansue, si com j’ai dit en la division, par la cure de medicines; et quant ceu ne profite mie, adonques regarde en la gorge dou malaide au soleil, puis que tu li presses la lengue a l’estrument que je t’ai dit. Et se tu vois la sansue, si la trai a tout .i. petit uncine, ou as tenailles subtilz que valent a ceu. Et se ceu ne vaut, si pren une caine chevee, et la boute en la gorge dou malaide, puis boute ou chevement de la caine .i. fer chaut, et fai ce sovent. Et se teigne li malaides d’aigue toute jor. puis pren plein .i. voirre d’aigue froide, et oevre la bouche, et la giete ens sens englutir, et la mueve a sa main sovent; et si tost com li sansue sent l’aigue, si chiet.	At no time is medicine for the cutting of the throat, as I have said in the division, by the cure of medicines; and when those do not help, then look at the throat of the patient in the sun, after which you press his tongue to the instrument that I have told you. And if you see the cutting, then treat it with one small pin, or with fine tweezers that are suitable for this purpose. And if this does not work, then take a sheep's wool, and put it in the throat of the patient, then push in the end of the wool .i. hot iron, and do this often. And if the patient remains thirsty all day. Then take full .i. cup of cold water, and open his mouth, and pour it into the throat so that he does not swallow, and move it with your hand often; and as soon as the cutting feels the water, it will fall.
Et s’elle ne chiet si com nos avons dit, si subfumige lou malaide d’asefetide, a l’estrument que j’ai dit en la fumigation de l’uve; fai ceu maintes fois, car elle cherra sens targier. Et li maniere de la fumigation si est que tu preignes .i. pot ou il ait charbons vis, et soit li pos covert d’un coverseil perciet en mileu, et en celui pertus soit li chiés de l’estrument; puis i giete ta fumigation, et li malaides mette lou chief de la cainne en sa bouche, et cloie la bouche, si que li fumee n’en isse mie, mais viegne jusc’a la sansue; et la sansue cherra maintenant, et s’elle ne chiet, si rencomence la fumigation par maintes fois; et soffre li malaides soif, et menjuce choses salees et als, et ne boive point d’aigue; et adonques li iert mestier qu’elle isse fuer par cest governement.	And if it does not fall as we have said, so fumigate the patient with asafoetida, using the instrument that I have said in the fumigation of the grape; do this many times, because it will come out without failing. And the manner of the fumigation is that you take one pot or it has burning coals, and let the pot be covered with a coverlet pierced in the middle, and in that pierce the head of the instrument; then put your fumigation there, and the patient puts the head of the cane in his mouth, and closes his mouth, so that the smoke does not go out, but comes up to the sinus; and the sinus will now come out, and if it does not fall, so begin the fumigation again many times; and let the patient suffer thirst, and eat salty things and such like, and do not drink water; and then it is necessary that it is gone by this governance.
Et li forme de l’estrument a coi on trait la sansue, si est, quant on la puet veoir, semblans a tenailles corbés por mues entrer en la gorge; et ait semblance au bec de soigne, et i ait asperiteit de lime, si que ceu qu’elle prent, elle ne puet lassier; et vez ci la forme:	And the shape of the instrument with which one treats the sinus is, when you can see it, like tongs bent so that they can enter into the throat; and it has the appearance of a bird's beak, and there are asperities of lime so that what it takes, it cannot let go; and see here the form:
li chapistres des apostemes	The chapters of abscesses
Mout de semblances d’aposteme sont, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient ci aprés d’un et d’autre en cest livre, et sont diver en perforation et en taille; et c’est en .ij. manieres dont l’une est en sa semblance meisme, et de ceu qu’il tient moistor. Et li seconde maniere si est por les leus ou il sont au cors. car li apostemes dou chief est autres que cil dou fondement, et li apostemes dou leu charnut est autres que cil qui vient en jointures, et chescuns ait son jugement en l’uevre.	Many resemblances of abscesses are, according to those that remembrance comes after from one and the other in this book, and are diverse in perforation and in size; and this is in two ways, of which one is in its very semblance, and of those that it holds moisture. And the second manner is for the places where they are on the body. For the abscesses of the head are other than those of the foundation, and the abscesses of the fleshy part are other than those that come in joints, and each has its judgment in the work.
Et si a apostemes c’on ne doit mie percier, tant que li bowe est meure selonc son acomplissement; et si a de telz qu’il covient percier quant il sont crut, et ne meurent mie selonc lor acomplissement, si com aposteme qui sont delez jointures. Car quant apostemes vient delez jointures, et on le laisse tant qu’il est porris entor, par aventure si sont corrumput li liien et li nerf de la jointure, par coi ce est cause de contraction en celui membre. Ou li aposteme est delez lou membre principel, et se tu tardes la perforation tant qu’il soit meurez, si nuira au membre principeil; ou il est delez lou fondement, si le perce on ainsois qu’il soit meurs; et ne covient mie que tu perces aposteme crut sens digestion acomplie, fuers que celui qui est delez lou fondement, qu’il ne porrisse em parfont, et soit alongiez dedens, et i viegne fistule; et ne puisse saner en grant termine.	And if to abscesses one should not pierce, as long as the boil is mature according to its accomplishment; and if there are such that it is necessary to pierce when they are ripe, and do not die according to their accomplishment, such as abscesses that are near joints. For when abscesses come near joints, and one lets it stay as long as it is ripe inside, by chance the ligaments and nerve of the joint are corrupted, which is the cause of contraction in that limb. Or if the abscess is near the principal member, and you delay piercing until it is mature, it will harm the principal member; or if it is near the foundation, pierce it then as long as it is ripe; and it is not necessary that you pierce a ripe abscess without complete digestion, except that which is near the foundation, so that it does not pour out by force, and be lengthened inside, and there comes a fistula; and cannot heal in a long time.
Et covient que tu saiches l’oure de la perforation de l’aposteme qui est meur selonc l’acomplissement, et c’est quant li dolor est apaisie, et li departemens de la fievre, et l’amenuisement de la dolor et de la roujor, et dou debatement et de l’aguisement dou chief de l’aposteme, et les autres signes; et covient que tu faices seoir la perforation ou plus dependant leu de l’aposteme, et la ou il apert mues; et soit li perforation dou lonc dou cors, et se li apostemes est as mains ou as piez, ou en jointures et au ners et as arteres, et en toz leus igalz ou il n’a point de ploieure.	And it is necessary that you know the hour of piercing the abscess which is mature according to its accomplishment, and this is when the pain has subsided, and the fever departs, and the lessening of the pain and the redness, and the swelling and the softening of the head of the abscess, and the other signs; and it is necessary that you make the piercing where more dependent place of the abscess, and where it opens out pus; and be the piercing long in the body, and if the abscess is at the hands or feet, or in joints and nerves and arteries, and in all places equal where there is no puss.
En ces que ploient, par selonc celui membre. Et quant apostemes est en leu charnut, si vaut mues que tu laisses la perforation tant qu’il soit confermez en digestion acomplie, si com nos avons dit. Car se tu lou perces devant ceu, si iert alongiez li cors dou venim de lui, et est plains de mout d’ordure; et par aventure endurcissent les levres et li parfondetez de lui. Et si a aucun aposteme que sont perciet selonc le large dou cors, selonc ceu que li membres en ait mestier.  Et covient que tu amenistres em petis apostemes, petis pertus; et en grans apostemes, grans pertus, et maintes fendures selonc la semblance de la grandor de l’aposteme; et si a de tels apostemes ou il covient chever lou keur, et coper; quant il est jai devenus ausi com .i. drapelz, et est amortis, si covient faire ausi com on fait as bubes: et si a de telz que sont fendut en .iij. angles, et si a de telz dont on cope ausi com la fuelle de mirte, si com apostemes des angres; et si a de telz ou on fait une reonde taille, et autres tailles et semblant copeure.	In these that boil, according to the member. And when an abscess is in its flesh place, it is worth doing that you leave the perforation until it is confirmed in digestion accomplished, as we have said. For if you pierce it before then, the body of the venom will flow from it, and it is full of much filth; and by chance harden the lips and the depths of it. And in any abscess that are pierced according to the width of the body, according to what the member needs.
Cil qui n’ont point de chief, si com aposteme souef superficial, il covient que tu lou perces plainnement; et covient quant li apostemes est gros, et il a coillit grant bowe, et tu lou perces, si ne traire mie toute la bowe en celle houre, mais en trai une partie; puis estoupe l’aposteme jusc’a l’autre jor, puis en trai aucune chose derechief; fai ceu par maintes fois de greit en greit, tant que li bowe isse toute; meismement se li malaides est de foible vertut, ou femme portans, ou petis enfes, ou viez hons decrepites. Car li esperis tressaut aucune fois avec l’issue de la bowe, que par aventure muert li malaides, et tu ne t’en persois. Eschuez donques cest chapistre par grant cautele, et quant tu as perciet ton aposteme, si essue la plaie, et regarde se li plaie de l’aposteme est petite; et se c’est une tailleure plainne, si amenistre tentes de lin ou de viez coton; et se c’est uns grans apostemes, et il i a mout de pertus, si covient que tu boutes en chescun une tente si qu’ele viegne l’une contre l’autre; et se tu as copeit en l’aposteme une partie dou cuir, et tu l’as cheveit entor, si covient que tu l’emplisses de viel couton ou de rasure de dras de lin sens moistor, et le lie jusc’au tier jor; puis l’oste, et le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Those who have no chief, like a superficial abscess, it is necessary that you pierce it fully; and it is necessary when the abscess is large, and it has collected much pus, and you pierce it, then do not draw out all the pus in that hour, but drain a part; then plug the abscess until the next day, then drain nothing directly; do this many times, little by little, until all the pus is gone; likewise if the patient is of weak strength, or pregnant woman, or small child, or old man decrepit. For the spirit trembles at any time with the discharge of pus, that by chance kills the patient, and you do not take care of yourself. Therefore, escape this chapter with great caution, and when you have pierced your abscess, then wipe the wound, and look if the wound of the abscess is small; and if it is a flat cut, then put bandages of linen or old cotton; and if it is a large abscess, and there are many punctures, it is necessary that you put in each one a bandage so that it comes against the other; and if you have cut into the abscess part of the skin, and you have covered it around, then it is necessary that you fill it with old cotton or lint shred from linen without moisture, and tie it until the third day; then remove it, and cure it with ointment until it is healed.
Et se decorremens de sanc avient a ton ovraige, si amenistre aigue froide et aisil, et moille .i. drapeil, et met sor le leu decorrant par maintes fois.  Et se li decorremens de sanc persevere, se i amenistre governement et cure, et les poudres que j’ai dit em mains leus en cest livre, et se c’est ou tens d’iver, et li leus ou li apostemes est est mout nervous, si couvient que tu mettes sus tentes et drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile chaut; et se c’est en esteit, et li leus est charnus, si covient que tu mes sus drapelz moilliez en aigue et en oile, ou en vin et en oile froit, jusc’au tier jor, si com nos avons dit; et puis deslie l’aposteme et l’essue et le cure, si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if there is bleeding in your work, then administer cold water and so on, and moisten one drape, and put it over the bleeding place many times.  And if the bleeding persists, then administer governance and cure, and the powders that I have said in this book, and if it is in winter, and the place where the abscess is is very nervous, then it is necessary that you put on bandages and drapes moistened in wine and hot oil; and if it is in summer, and the place is fleshy, then it is necessary that you put on bandages moistened in water and oil, or in wine and cold oil, until the third day, as we have said; and then untie the abscess and wipe it and cure it, as it is fitting, until it is healed.
Et ceu covient il conoistre universement en cures des apostemes: or vos ai dit coment on doit aler avant as cures des apostemes, et vez ci le chapistre.	And this it is necessary to know universally in treatments of abscesses: which I have told you how one must go before the treatment of abscesses, and see here the chapter.
des soros	of ulcers
Ou keur dou chief vienent petis apostemes, et sont manieres de nous que sont en toiles, ausi com li josier d’une geline, et mout en i a de semblances. Il en i a de gras et de telz ou il a moistor ausi com poulz; et si a de telz qui sont dur et pierous au taillier, et n’i a point de doutance se li artere n’i fait contraire. Et li ovraiges de la taille si est que tu esprueve a tout .i. estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», de coi li forme vient ci aprés, quel chose il contient. Car s’il contient moistor, si lou fent par desus dou lonc. Et quant li moistor est vuidie, si escorche sens rien laissier la peil qui contient celle moistor, car il revient adés quant on i laisse rien; puis plonge coton en oignement egiptien, s’il est presens; se ceu non, en aigue et en seil, et en emple la plaie, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor; et ceu corront ceu qui est demorez dou nit. Et pues rencomence lou coton, si com devant, le second jor, et lou tier, tant que tu saiches bien qu’il ne demoure point dou nit; puis cure la plaie d’oignement a ceu convenauble, tant qu’il soit sanez. Et se li apostemes tient .i. nout gras, si le cope selonc ceste forme, dou lonc; et i giete tes oncines, et l’escorche de toutes pars, et met toute ta cure de traire fuer la cotte ou il gist; et se li artere te fait contraire, si fai ceu que je t’ai dit aprés. Et ausi fai de l’aposteme s’il est pierous, et dou taillier et dou curer si com je t’ai dit.	Of ulcers which are like those in the cloths, as well as the joiner's of a garment, and many resemble them. There are some fatty ones and such that have moisture like poultices; and there are some that are hard and stony to the touch, and there is no doubt if the artery does not go against it. And the work of the tailor is that you suspect all one instrument which is called "entromissoire," because its form comes later, what thing it contains. For if it contains moisture, then let it be driven from above through the long way. And when the moisture is emptied, it peels without leaving the skin that contains that moisture, for it returns to its place when you leave it alone; then dip cotton in Egyptian ointment, if it is present; if not, in water and wine, and apply it to the wound, and let it stay until the next day; and then continue doing this which remains of the night. And then begin again with the cotton, as before, on the second day, and the third, until you know well that it does not remain of the night; then cure the wound with ointment as is suitable, until it is healed. And if the abscess holds one greasy one, so cut it according to this form, through the long way; and lay your incisions, and peel it from all sides, and put all your care to draw out the cotte where it lies; and if the artery goes against you, then do what I told you after. And do also for the abscess if it is stony, and in shape and in curing as I have told you.
Et li taille sus l’aposteme pierous et le moiste, si est plus legiere, car il sont de poc de sanc. Et si a aucuns de ces apostemes ou chief ou il n’a point de moistor, et de ces fut .i. apostemes que je copai ou chief d’une vielle femme; et trovai l’aposteme ausi com une piere xourde, aspre et blainche, et ne pooit brisier; et s’on en eust ferut aucun, on li eust ausi bien fait plaie com d’une piere. En autres apostemes venans ou chief, fuer que ces qui vienent as chief des enfans et as racines des oreilles, li overture si soit toz jors au plus dependant leu, por mues issir la bowe; et les cure si com il covient.	And the boils on a pus-filled abscess are lighter because they have less blood. And some of these abscesses or chiefs where there is no moisture, and from these I had one chief from an old woman; and I found the abscess like a hard, rough, white stone, and could not break it; and if one had made any incision in it, one would have done as well with a wound. In other abscesses coming or chiefs, whether they come from the chiefs of children or the roots of the ears, the opening should always be at the lowest point, so that pus can flow out; and treat them as is necessary.
des scrophules	Of scrofulas
Maintes fois avienent cist aposteme au col, et desoz les asseles, et ens angres, et aucune fois vienent autre part ou cors, et sont mout, et sont enjanrees l’une avec l’autre. Et chescune scrophule est proprement dedens sa cote, si com li nout et li aposteme dou chief, si com nos avons dit; et les semblances de ces scrophules sont maintes. Il i a de teles que contienent moistor, et si a de malignes qui ne vuellent obeir a santeit. en celle donques que tu vois de bone disposition au tochier, et est semblans a la color dou cors, et muet de chescune part et n’est mie aerse as ners dou col ne a l’artere ne au conduit, et n’est mie parfonde; si covient que tu la copes par desus, et l’escorche de chescune partie, et estent les .ij. levres dou keur as oncines, se tu en as mestier, si com nos avons dit en apostemes dou chief; et la trai poc et poc, et soies seur que tu ne coper lou nerf ne la voine, et ne soit mie li spatumile agus ne trenchans, que li mains n’eschaipe, et ne voise trop avant, que tu ne coper mie ceu que tu ne dois.	Many times these abscesses occur on the neck, under the arms, and in the armpits, and sometimes they come from other parts or body parts, and are many, and are joined together. And each scrofulous boil is properly within its own skin, like the others and the boils of the head, as we have said; and the appearances of these scrofulas are many. There are some that contain moisture, and some that are malign that do not want to obey health. So in the one you see that has a good disposition, touching it lightly, and appears like the color of the body, and is flat on all sides, and does not irritate the nerves of the neck nor the artery nor the vein, and is not too deep; then it is necessary that you cut it from above, and scrape it on each side, and are the two lips of the key as we have said in boils of the head; and treat them little by little, and be sure that you do not cut the nerve or the vein, nor should the spatula be too sharp, lest your hand slip, and do not look too far ahead so that you do not cut what you should not.
Et se tu copes la voinne ou l’artere, et ceu ne te laisse ovrer, si met en la plaie vitriole broiet, ou aucunes poudres que restainchent sanc, et estraint la plaie; et la laisse tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et soit amollie li plaie, et encomence a porrir. Et quant li sans est estainchiez, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que tu l’acomplisses; puis quier a ton doit indice s’il i demoure nules petites scrophules, si les cope et les munde. Et s’il a en la racine de la scrophule voinne grant, si ne covient mie que tu copes celle scrophule en sa racine, mais la lie d’un fil double fort, et la laisse cheoir par li, sens nuisement; puis emple la plaie de viel coton plongiet en oignement egiptien, puis la cure.	And if you cut the vein or artery, and it will not let you work, put in the wound pounded vitriol, or any powders that restrain blood, and hold back the wound; and leave it until the abscesses are calmed, and the wound is softened, and begins to rot. And when the bleeding is stopped, return to your work, as long as you complete it; then look at your index finger if there remain any small pustules, cut them and heal them. And if it has in the root of the pustule a vein large, it is not necessary that you cut that pustule at its root, but tie it with a strong double thread, and let it hang by it, without hurting; then apply the wound to old cotton dipped in Egyptian ointment, then cure.
Et se tu copes toute la scrophule, si covient que tu assembles les .ij. levres de la plaie, et les cout maintenant, puis qu’il n’i a point demoreit de superfluiteit por la grandor de la scrophule. si covient que tu entendes a coper la racine de li, et traire fuer, et la cout si com nos avons dit. Celles scrophules que tienent superfluiteit, perce lai ou il apert meure; et la perce ensi com celle devant dite, en dependant, puis i amenistre tentes avec oignement et semblans choses, si qu’elle corrompe ceu qui est demorez de la corruption; et quant li plaie est bien mundee, si la cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you cut the whole pustule, it is necessary that you bring together the two lips of the wound, and sew them now, then as long as there remains no superfluity for the size of the pustule. It is necessary that you pay attention to cutting the root of it, and draw out pus, and sew it as we have said. Those pustules that hold superfluity, pierce where it appears more; and pierce it like the one before said, depending, then administer tents with ointment and similar things, so that it rots what remains of the corruption; and when the wound is well cleaned, cure it with ointment encouraging flesh, until it is healed.
de squinance	of squamous cell carcinoma
Li ancien dirent et parlerent de la tailleure de la gorge; mais je ne vis onques en nostre terre qui la feist, et c’est li escripture de lor parole.	The ancients said and spoke of cutting the throat; but I never saw anyone in our land who did it, and this is the writing of their word.
A ces qui ont squinance, il covient que li fendure de la gorge qui est apelee «epiglote» soit eschuee; et c’on ne faice aide par ceu, por ceu que toutes les voines et li pormon dou malaide sont a ces qui ont aposteme chaut en la bouche, ou en la gorge ou en .ij. amandres.	For those who have squinting (?), it is necessary that the throat cut which is called "epiglottis" be avoided; and do not help them because all the veins and the pores of the sick person are at those who have an abscess hot in the mouth, or in the throat, or in two almonds.
Quant li maladie est en la chenal dou pormon, il covient coper l’epiglote por fuir la perdition qui vient de l’estranglement.	When the illness is in the channel of the pore, it is necessary to cover the epiglottis to avoid the perdition that comes from strangulation.
Il covient donques, quant nos volons fendre l’epiglote, que nos le fendons desoz .iij. cercles ou .iiij. une petite fendure dou travers, entre les .ij. cercles ou par la quantiteit de la fendure dou syfac, ne mie en la cartillaige;	Therefore, when we want to cut the epiglottis, it is necessary to cut it below three circles or four with a small incision across, between the two circles or by the quantity of the incision of the syringe, not in the cartilage;
et cil leus si est covenaubles a la section de l’epiglote qu’il n’i a point de char, et li vasseil sont lonc d’enqui.	and those their are comparable to the section of the epiglottis that there is no flesh, and the vessels are long from it.
Et se li maistres est paourous, si covient qu’il estende le cuir de la gorge a tout l’oncine, puis fende lou keur tant qu’il viegne a la cheneil; et eschue les vasselz de sanc, se tu vois aucune chose, et puis cope lou syfac, si com nos avons dit;	And if the master is fearful, then it is necessary that he stretch the skin of the throat to all of the neck, then cleave the keel until it comes to the channel; and avoid the vessels of blood, if you see no thing, and then cut the syfac, as we have said.
et est demostrez par la section dou fleume de la cheneil ki saut fuer par le leu qui est rompus, et par la defaute de la voix;	and it is demonstrated by the section of the phlegm of the neck that leaps from the place that is broken, and by the lack of voice;
et laisse la plaie overte une piece.	and leave the wound open a piece.
Et quant li houre est passee de coi on doute l’estranglement, assemble les .ij. levres de la plaie dou keur, et la cout toute soule sens la cartillaige; puis aministre medicines qui font naistre char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when the hour has passed of which one doubts strangulation, assemble the .ij. lips of the wound of the heart, and cut all alone sense the cartilage; then administer medicines that make flesh grow, until it is whole.
Albucasim dist c’on ne faice ce jusc’a tant que li gorge est toute estoupee, et li malaides est jugiez a mort, et li defaut li alaine.	Albucasim says one should not do this until the throat is completely stopped up, and the patient is judged to be dead, and the fault lies with the wing.
Adonques cope on l’epiglote por ceu que li malaides ne puet alener, et il respire par la plaie, et ensi est gardez de mort;	Therefore cut open the epiglottis because the patient cannot breathe, and he breathes through the wound, and thus is kept from death;
et por ce commanderent li anciain a laissier la plaie overte tant que li malice de la maladie soit passee, et elle est passee en .iij. jors ou en .iiij.	and for this the ancients commanded to leave the wound open until the malice of the disease has passed, and it has passed in three days or four.
Et adonques il comanderent a coudre la plaie et curer, tant qu’elle fut curee;	And therefore they command to sew the wound and care for it, until it was healed.
et je vos dirai ceu que je vis.	And I will tell you what I saw.
Je vis que une damoisele prist .i. coutel, et le ficha en sa gorge, et copa partie des chenelz dou pormon;	I saw that a young lady took .i. knife, and plunged it into her throat, and cut part of the channels of the windpipe.
et je fui apelez por li curer, et la trovai ausi com morte.	And I was called by her to cure her, and I found her just as dead.
Je descovris la plaie, et trovai le sanc qui en estoit issus, et soi bien qu’elle n’avoit mie copeit voine ne conduit fuer que la gorge, et li vens issoit fuer par la plaie.	I discovered the wound, and found the blood that was issuing from it, and well that it had not pierced a vein nor been led except to the throat, and the veins were issuing through the wound.
Je me hastai, et cousi la plaie, et la curai tant qu’elle fut sanee;	I bandaged it, and thus I closed the wound, and I treated it until it was healed.
et n’avint a la damoisele fuer qu’elle fut roge de voix, et revint aprés a sa disposition;	and it happened to the young woman that she was hoarse of voice, and returned after that to her usual state.
por ceu di je que en la tailleure de l’epiglote n’ait mie paour.	for this reason I say that in the cutting of the epiglottis there is no fear.
de la grosse gorge	of the large throat
Cist apostemes est apelez «hernie de gorge», et est uns grans apostemes en color d’une jaisse, et est molt en femmes;	This abscess is called "throat hernia," and is a large abscess in the color of a boil, and is very common in women;
et est selonc .ij. manieres: naturez, et accidens; ou natureil n’a point d’engien.	and it is according to two manners: natural, and accidental; the natural one has no cause.
Et li accidens est selonc .ij. manieres, de coi l’une est semblans a gras nous, et li autre maniere est semblans a aposteme qui vient de nous d’artere;	And the accidental one is according to two manners, of which one is similar to a fatty lump, and the other manner is similar to an abscess that comes from our artery.
et il i ait paour, et ne covient mie ovrer de feir fuers que en celi qui est petite, et le prueve et cerche a tout l’intromissoire:	and there is fear, and it does not behoove to work of fire except in this which is small, and the prove and searches at all the introitor:
se tu le trueves ausi com .i. nout gras, et ne pent a nulle voine, si le cope, si com on cope les nous, et le trai a tout sa coife, s’il en i a point;	if you find it also as our fat, and cannot at any vein, if the cut, as we cut the ours, and the train to all its cap, if there is any of it;
et encerche bien tot, et le cure si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	and encircle well soon, and the cure as it behooveth, until it be perfectly healed.
des nous	of ours
Maintes manieres de nous sont, dont je dirai toutes les semblances;	Many ways are to us, of which I will say all the appearances;
et or covient que je die toute la difference qui est entre nout et issue.	and therefore it is necessary that I say all the difference that is between ours and theirs.
Je dis que issue est chalors et fievre tenans, tant que li ebulicions est passee, et est acomplie li porriture; adonques repose li fievre et li chalor.	I say that an issue is sometimes and fever-bearing, as long as the boiling is not passed, and the rotting is accomplished; therefore the fever and heat rest.
Avec lou nout n’a ne chalor ne fievre ne dolor, et contient .i. syfac, qui est ses propres sac et est selonc la color dou cors, et encomence ausi com une jaisse, et devient gros;	With ours there is neither heat nor fever nor pain, and it contains one issue, which is its own sac, and is according to the color of the body, and begins as a boil, and becomes swollen.
et sont selonc ij semblances, ou grais, ou moiste, et mout de color sont si com j’ai dit en la division.	and are according to two appearances, or greasy, or moist, and very colored as I have said in the division.
Il covient, quant tu viens a la cure dou nout, que tu esprueves et l’enquier premierement a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», selonc ce que sa forme venra ou chapistre qui est aprés.	It is necessary, when you come to the treatment of a new injury, that you first examine and inquire with all the instruments which are called "entroissoir," according to what its form comes from the chapter that is after.
Et li maniere de l’inquisicion des apostemes des nous est que tu preignes ou plus moiste leu que tu trueves en l’aposteme, et torne tes dois poc et poc, tant que tu saiches que li estrumens ait perciet le keur, puis que ce soit selonc la grandor de l’aposteme;	And the manner of examining abscesses is that you prick or moisten the most moist place that you find in the abscess, and turn your two points (poc) and point (poc), as long as you know that the instrument has pierced the core, then according to the size of the abscess.
puis estrai l’entromissoire, et pren garde en ceu que saut fuer.	Then withdraw the "entroissoir," and take care in those who jump out.
Se moistor corrans cort, queil color elle ait, si le fent si com j’ai dit des autres apostemes;	If moisture runs short, whatever color it has, treat it as I have said of other abscesses.
et se aprés l’entromissoire nen vient moistor, saiches qu’il est gras, si le fent donques en croix, et le prent as pinceures, et l’escorche legierement de chescune part et warde la cotte ou il gist que tu la traies saine avec le nout;	And if after the incision moisture comes out again, know that it is fatty, so treat it in a cross shape, and take it with forceps, and lightly scrape it on each side, and cover the wound where it lies so that you pull it clean with the thread.
et se tu ne la pues traire saine, si la trai par pieces si qu’il n’i demoure rien.	And if you cannot pull it clean, then remove it in pieces so that nothing remains there.
Car s’il i demoure rien, si revient li nous par maintes fois;	Because if anything remains there, it returns to us many times.
et s’il en demore un poc, et li sans te grieve, si emple la plaie d’aucunes poudres corrosives agues, et estraint la plaie, et met sus choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez;	And if it remains for a little while, and the pain does not trouble him, apply to the wound some sharp corrosive powders, and hold the wound closed, and put soothing things on the abscess hot, and cure it with other cures until it is healed.
et se li nous est grans, si cout les .ij. levres de la plaie, et le cure de ceu qui enjanre char.	And if it is large, then sew together the two lips of the wound, and cure it with those things that cause flesh to grow.
et se li voine batans t’est contraire ou autre si te haste et emple le leu de vitriole broiet, et lou laisse liiet .ij. jors ou .iij., tant que li plaie porrisse, et repose li ebulicion dou sanc; puis revien au coper ceu que i est demoreit dou nout.	And if the vein is beating against you or otherwise quickly, then apply the powder of vitriol to it, and let it lie for two or three days until the wound purges, and rests the boiling of blood; then return to cover those things that remain from it.
Vez ci les formes des estrumens entromissoires, et sont de .iij. manieres: grans et moien et petit; et s’en i a .iij. quarrez qui sont apelez «albaret», et .i. qui est apelez «breb», et s’en i a de .iij. manieres: grant, moien, et petit, por encerchier les apostemes de fistule;	See here the forms of the instruments for introducing, and they are in 3 manners: large, medium, and small; and there are 3 squares that are called "albaret," and 1 which is called "breb," and there are 3 manners: large, medium, and small, to surround the abscesses of fistulae.
et sont ausi com les aguilles dont on cout les sorceles, et sont d’arain citrin, ou de fer, ou d’argent, et mues valent cil qui sont jaune, et sont plus esprovez de plonc noir por encerchier les corbeures de fistule;	and they are also like the needles with which one sews sorceresses, and are of citrine iron, or silver, and those that are yellow are more valuable, and are more proven from black pitch to surround the curves of fistula.
et sont de .iij. manieres: grans, moiens, et petis, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce des pertus.	and they are in 3 manners: large, medium, and small, according to the quantity of the breadth of the openings.
Les formes des oncines sont de mout de semblances, si com tu vois ci: grans, moiens, et petis; et si a oncines qui ont .ij. corbeures de .iij. manieres ausi;	The forms of the pincers are of many resemblances, as you see here: large, medium, and small; and there are pincers that have two curves in three ways also;
et si a oncines qui ont .iij. corbeures, et sont ausi de .iij. manieres; et si a oncines qui ont .ij. corbeures, et oncines d’une corbeure soulement, et sont de .iij. manieres; et tuit cist sont necessaire en lor leu.	and there are pincers that have three curves, and are also in three ways; and there are pincers that have two curves, and pincers of a single curve, and are in three ways; and all these are necessary in their place.
Li chief de ces a coi on fent sont trenchant, et de telz i a qui ne taillent mie fuer que d’une part, dont on escorche les nous, por ceu c’on ne cope la voine ne le nerf;	The head of these is what one uses to cut, and there are some that do not cut further than one side, with which one scrapes the nerves, because this way one does not cut the vein nor the nerve;
et de ces intromissoires sont les alemeles reponues en mainches, si que li malaide ne s’en persoivent a l’overture des apostemes;	and of these there are also instruments with handles, so that the patient does not feel it when opening abscesses.
et sont de .iij. manieres: grant, petit, et moien, si com tu vois;	and there are of three kinds: great, small, and medium, as you see;
et n’en use on mie fuer que en leu charnut, si com jambes, et bras, et mameles, et as angres, et en semblans leus;	and one should not use it except in fleshy places, such as legs, arms, nipples, and genitals, and similar parts;
et aucune fois fait on .i. autre estrument petit, semblant a escorces de fistices, selonc ceste forme, a coi on estainche sanc:	and never is made one other instrument small, seeming to shavings of fists, according to this form, with which one stanches blood;
et le met on aucune fois au leu qui saine a copement des voines, et as arteres, et aucune fois reont selonc ceste grant forme:	and it is put never in the place which bleeds from a cut of veins, and arteries, and never returned according to this great form:
Aucune fois enflent les mameles d’aucuns homes quant cil encomencent estre corrumput, tant qu’eles semblent mameles de feme;	Sometimes the breasts of some men swell when they begin to rot, so that they seem like women's breasts.
et demorent laides et enflees, et qui les vuet curer, si le covient soier selonc ceste forme des ceste ligne b. jusques a .g.:	and remain disfigured and swollen, and whoever wants to cure them, he should follow this form according to these lines from... up to ...:
puis escorche la graisse, et emple la plaie de medicine enjanrant char, puis assemble les .ij. levres de la plaie a costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee;	then scrape the fat, and apply medicine to the wound preventing decay, then stitch together the two lips of the wound, and treat it until it is healed;
et se li mamele cline aval, et est amolie por sa grandor si com il avient as femmes, si la fent en .ij. costelz desus, par .ij. semblans fendures;	and if the breast leans down and is softened due to its size as women have, then make two incisions above, in two similar places;
de coi l’une soit tenans a l’autre a la fin de l’une et de l’autre, si que li plus grans ligne conteigne la menor selonc ceste forme, des ceste ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.;	of which one is holding the other at the end of one and the other, so that the larger line contains the smaller according to this form, from this line .b. until the line .g.
puis escorche le cuir qui est entre les .ij. levres, et oste la graisse, et i amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de costure et de poudres, et ceu qui est necessaire en la cure, tant qu’il soit sanez;	then scrape the skin that is between the .ij. lips, and remove the fat, and there administer those things that we have said of sewing and powders, and those which are necessary in the cure, until it is healed;
et s’il n’est sanez, ou li incision n’est mie toute faite, por ceu que li malaides ne vuet reposer, ou por le decorrement de sanc, si covient que tu emplisses la plaie de coton moilliet en oignement corrosif;	and if it is not healed, or the incision is not fully made, because the patient does not want to rest, or for the loss of blood, then it is necessary that you fill the wound with cotton moistened in corrosive ointment;
et le laisse tant qu’il menjuce le remenant et la graisse, puis le cure tant qu’il soit saneis.	and leave it until it absorbs the remaining and fat, then cure it until it is healed.
des apostemes des asselles	of abscesses of the buttocks
Cist apostemes que vienent desoz les asseles sont manieres de scrophules dures ou il ait cotes, et s’en i a que contienent moistor.	These abscesses that come from under the buttocks are kinds of hard scrofulas that have ribs, and there are some that contain moisture.
Cil donques qui contienent moistor covient qu’il soient copez selonc ceste forme, des la ligne b. jusc’a la ligne .g.:	Those therefore that contain moisture ought to be cut according to this form, from the line b. until the line g.:
Et quant toute li bowe qui est en l’aposteme est vuidie, si emple la plaie de viel coton, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor, puis oste tout le coton, et cure d’oignement avenant a ceu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when all the pus that is in the abscess is drained, then apply to the wound old cotton, and leave it until the next day, then remove all the cotton, and care with ointment appropriate to this until it is healed.
Et se li apostemes est de semblances de scrophules, si le fent si com nos avons dit en fendures des scrophules, et se li plaie rent bowe, si amenistre cautere si com nos avons dit devant.	And if the abscess is of the likeness of a scrofulous lesion, then treat it as we have said for incisions of scrofulous lesions, and if the wound is curved inwards, apply cautery as we have said before.
de la routure de l’artere	Of the rupture of the artery
Quant li artere est route, et li cuir est soudez qui est sus, si en vient maintes fois apostemes, et tout aussi avient il a la voine enflee et aposteme;	When the artery is ruptured and the skin above it is sewn together, abscesses often occur, and this also happens with an inflamed vein and abscess.
et si le conoist on ensi quant c’est por l’artere, si est li apostemes lons em parfont;	And if the expert knows that it is due to the artery, then the abscess grows long by making incisions into it.
et quant tu le sens a tes dois, si sens .i. estraignement; et quant c’est por la voine, si est reons defuer aparans;	and when you feel it at your wrists, that is to say, constriction; and when this is for the vein, then it is reason to defer appearance of fire;
et c’est folie de coper cest aposteme, et meismement quant il est desoz les asseles et as angres et ou col et em mout d’autres leus, et est mout grans.	and it is folly to cover this abscess, and even when it is below the armpits and around the groin and neck and in many other places, and is very large.
Il covient donques eschuir la cure de fer, et celui qui est a chief covient eschuir ausi, et en celui qui est d’enfleure d’artere fent par desus le cuir dou lonc;	It therefore becomes necessary to shun the treatment of iron, and whoever is at the head it also becomes necessary to shun, and in him who has an inflammation of artery made from above the skin down long.
puis oevre la taille as oncines, et depart bellement l’artere des toiles, tant qu’ele soit descoverte;	then work the opening in the intestines, and beautifully separate the artery from the tissues, as long as it is uncovered;
puis boute desoz li une aguille, et la fai percier jusc’a l’autre costeit, et estraint l’artere d’un fil double en .ij. leus, selonc ceu que je t’ai ensigniet en l’estraction des .ij. arteres qui sont en temples;	Then put under it a needle, and make it pass until the other side, and strain the artery with a double thread in 2 lengths, according to what I have taught you in the extraction of the 2 arteries that are in the temples.
puis point le leu qui est entre les .ij. liens d’un intromissoire tant que li sans en isse qui i est, et soit deliiez li aposteme;	Then point the place which is between the two links with an introducer until the pus that is there comes out, and let the abscess be drained.
puis amenistre la cure que enjanre bowe, tant que li liien chient;	Then administer the cure that bowe [or Boethius?] prescribes, as long as the link sticks.
puis cure ceu d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez;	Then cure those with ointment following this, as long as they are healed.
et se li apostemes est por la taille de la voinne, si covient que tu teignes a ta main ceu que tu pues de l’aposteme a tout le cuir,	and if the abscess is for the size of the vein, then it behooves you to seize with your hand as much as you can of the abscess to all the skin.
puis boute l’aguille desoz le leu que tu tiens a ta main, et la fai percier, et i ait .i. fil double, si que tu le trais de l’autre costeit;	then thrust the needle under the place that you hold in your hand, and have it pierced, and let there be one doubled thread, so that you draw it from the other side.
puis lie l’aposteme, si com je t’ai dit, ou liien de l’une de .ij. pars as .ij. chiés dou fil;	then tie the abscess, as I have told you, or bind it with one of two parts of the two ends of the thread;
et se tu doutes que li filz n’isse fuer, si i reboute une autre aguille a tout .i. fil desoz tout l’aposteme a l’incision de la premiere aguille, et estraint les filz en .iiij. leus;	and if you doubt that the thread is not strong enough, then put another needle through all one thread under the whole abscess at the incision of the first needle, and strain the threads in four places;
puis cope l’aposteme tant que li superfluitez en isse, puis cope la superfluiteit dou keur et laisse ceu qui est liiez;	Then cut the abscess until the superfluities issue from it, then cut the superfluity of the core and leave what is joined.
puis met sus .i. drapeil moilliet en vin et en oile, puis li amenistre cures de tentes et d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then put on one cloth moistened in wine and oil, then administer treatments of poultices and ointments until it is healed.
des apostemes des ners	Of abscesses of the nerves
Ausi com aposteme vienent en l’artere et en la voine, vienent aposteme as ners quant il sont ferut, ou par trop grant travail, et semblans choses.	Just as abscesses come in the artery and vein, abscesses also come to the nerves when they are chafed, or by too much work, and similar things.
Et ceu avient plus sovent as adjutoires et as dois et en toz leus ou il ait jointures, et c’est .i. grief apostemes, et sa color semble la color dou cors, et est em plusors dispositions sens dolor;	And this happens more often in the shoulders and hips and in all the places where there are joints, and that is to say abscesses, and its color seems like the color of the body, and is in many positions without pain.
et quant on l’estraint forment, si sent li malaides dolor, et n’est mie em parfont dou cors, mais desoz lou keur;	And when it is restrained forcibly, the patient feels pain, and it is not quite in the middle of the body, but below the heart;
et muet bien de toutes pars, et ne va ne avant ne arrier, ne desoz ne desus, et celui qui est en jointures ne covient mie coper par fer: par aventure i vanroit contraction;	and it moves well in all directions, and does not go forward or backward, nor down or up, and the one who is in joints should not be covered with iron: for fear it would go into contraction;
et cil qui est ou chief ou ou front, fent le cuir au spatumile.	And he who is on the head or on the forehead, makes the skin taut on the spatula.
Se li apostemes est petis, si le tien a unes tenailles, et le cope en sa racine;	If the abscess is small, then hold it with pliers and cut it at its root.
et s’il est grans, si le sospent a l’oncine, et l’escorche, puis l’oste et assemble la plaie a la costure, et lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it is large, then suspend it with a thread, and flay it, then purge it and close the wound with sutures, and treat it until it is healed.
des grosses boces pendans	Of large boils hanging
Aucune fois avient en ventres et ne mie autre part thelul, et est une maladie qui est apelee «funge» par la semblance d’aus, et est li racine subtilz, et li chiez gros; et en i a de petis et de mout grans;	At times they appear in the belly and nowhere else, and it is a disease which is called "fungus" because of its resemblance to ears, and it has fine roots, and a large head; and there are some small ones and some very large.
et je vis .i. home qui en avoit .ij. ou ventre qui estoient plus semblans a funges que ai autre chose, et n’i avoit point de difference, et estoient blanc, et avoient menue racine, et estoient jai fendut, et en corroit adés moistor.	and I saw one man who had two in his belly that were more like mushrooms than anything else, and there was no difference, and they were white, and they had a small root, and they were somewhat split, and some moisture came out of them.
Je les copai et trovai en l’un .xviij. onces pesant, et en l’autre .vj. З., et li ovraiges en l’incision si est que tu regardes se li malaides est moistes, et li color de l’artelul est blainche et moiste et de subtil racine;	I cut them open and found in one 18 ounces weighing, and in the other 6, and the work in incision is that you look to see if the patient is moist, and the color of the artelul is white and moist and of a subtle root.
si le cope au spatumile large, et soient en ta presence li cautere au feu. Car au taillier vient maintes fois trop grans decorremens de sanc, et se li sans te vaint, si te haste donques dou cauterizer;	if you cut with the spatula wide, and have the fire cautery in your presence. For when cutting there often comes too great a flow of blood, and if the blood does not stop, then hastily do cauterize;
et se tu vois le malaide espoanteit et paourous de l’incision dou fer, si prent .i. fil de plonc bien fait, et en lie l’artelul si com nos avons dit, et le laisse .ij. jors;	and if you see the patient frightened and fearful of the incision with iron, then take one thread of lead well made, and bind the joint as we have said, and leave it for two days;
et puis le restraint, et ne cesser d’estraindre lou fil de plonc tant qu’il cope l’artelul, et chiece par lui sens travail; et se les racines sont grosses, si a paour au coper meismement por le ventre, mais tu em pues bien coper la moitiet,	and then restrain it, and do not cease to restrain the lead thread until it covers the joint, and ceases by itself without effort; and if the roots are thick, fear to cut even for the belly, but you may well cover half.
puis le cauterize qu’il ne reviegne; puis cure la plaie, et garde que tu ne coper le thelul qui est de fuxe color et de povre sens et de lait regart.	then cauterize it so that it does not return; then cure the wound, and guard that you do not cut the part which is of fox color and poor sensation and with milky appearance.
Car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, et je venrai a la cure de chancre ci aprés.	For it is an abscess suppurating, and I will come to the treatment of chancres after this.
quant li boude ist fuer	when the head of the
Se li apparance de la boude vient par cautere de plaie ou de fendure de syfac, et est sus le ventre et en ist aucuns des bouez, si com il avient en autres routures, ou de sanc qui cort de voines ou d’arteres selonc ceu qui est devant, ou de ventositeit;	If the appearance of the head comes from a cautery wound or fissure of the skin, and is on the belly and has some of the bumps, as it happens in other injuries, or of blood which cuts veins or arteries according to what is before, or of windiness;
et se c’est par la routure dou syfac et par l’issue dou bouel, si est li color de l’aposteme semblans a la color dou cors, et est legiere chose sens dolor, et apert de diverse issue.	and if it is from the rupture of the skin and the discharge of the pus, then the color of the abscess is similar to the color of the body, and it is a light thing without pain, and opens from various exits.
Et se c’est por l’issue de l’intestine, adonques est il plus divers, et quant on le presse a ses dois si se repont, et puis revient, et par aventure si est sarrez, et agrandist mout a l’entree dou bain et por fort travail.	And if it is from the issue of the intestine, then it is more diverse, and when pressed at its two ends it rebounds, and then returns, and perhaps it is scarred, and grows much at the entrance of the bath and for strenuous work.
Et se c’est por moistor, c’est legiere chose, et apert bien quant tu le presses a ta main, ne ne constraint mie; et se c’est por sanc, si apert par ces signes li apostemes gros et dur, et est fichiez selonc une quantiteit;	And if it is due to moisture, it is a light thing, and it opens well when you press it with your hand, do not constrain it at all; and if it is due to blood, it opens by these signs the abscesses large and hard, and are filled according to a quantity;
et se c’est por ventositeit, si est souef au tochier, et li ovraiges si est que tu regarde se li apparance est por le sanc de l’artere, ou de la voine, ou ventositeit.	and if it is due to windiness, it is soft to the touch, and the work is that you look if its appearance is for the blood of the artery, or of the vein, or windiness.
Si covient que tu laisses la cure. Car il en a doutance et paor, si com je t’ai dit ou chapistre des apostemes, por l’artere et por la voine.	Then you must leave the cure. Because there is doubt and fear in it, as I have told you or chapter of abscesses, for the artery and for the vein.
Et se li apparance est por l’intestine ou lou boueil, si covient que tu comandes au malaide qu’il teigne son alaine, et soit estendus tout drois, puis seigne d’enche tout entor la boude;	And if the appearance is for the intestine or the boil, then it behooves you to command the patient to hold his arm, and be stretched straight, then seize it all around the boil;
puis le comande a gesir sovin entre tes mains,	then command him to squeeze often between your hands,
puis va entor le leu que tu as signiet a tout le spatumile,	then go around the place that you have marked with all the spatula,
