puis estent la moitiet de l’aposteme au desus a tout le grant uncine;	then extend half of the abscess upwards to the whole great incision;
puis le lie entor d’un fil fort, ou d’une corde de fort soie fermement, et soit li nous dou liien assolz;	Then tie it together with a strong thread, or a strong silk rope firmly, and let the ends of the thread be tied.
puis oevre la moitiet de l’aposteme estendut sus le liien, et i boute ton doit indice, et quier l’intestine;	Then work the middle of the abscess extended over the thread, and put your index finger in it, and seek the intestine.
se tu le trueves pris dou liien, si le deslie, et boute l’intestine au defuer dou ventre;	If you find it caught on the thread, untie it, and push the intestine out through the belly.
et se tu trueves le boueil, si le prent a l’oncine, et en cope la superfluiteit;	And if you find the boil, take it with the forceps and cut away the excess.
et se li artere te fait contraire, ou li voine, si vai belement entor, puis revien a ton ovraige et pren .ij. aguilles, et i boute .ij. fors filz, et boute les .ij. aguilles entor ceu que tu as fait en crois que tu feis percier;	and if the artery opposes you, or the vein, then go well around it, then return to your work and take 2 needles, and put 2 strong threads through them, and put the 2 needles around what you have done in the shape that you made visible.
puis estrain l’aposteme en .iiij. leus sus les aguilles, et se tu vues, oste les aguilles, et laisse lou leu tant qu’il porrisse, et chiece li char morte par soi;	then strain the abscess in 4 lengths on the needles, and if you see it, remove the needles, and leave the wound as long as it purrs, and let the dead flesh fall away by itself.
ou tu la cope quant elle iert subtiliie et porrie, puis le cure de ceu qu’il covient, et cheve l’aposteme si com nos avons dit;	or you cut it when it is subtle and purrs, then treat it as needed, and heal the abscess as we have said.
et estrai le sanc ou la moistor que tu trueves, puis cure le leu de ceu qu’il couvient, et soude le leu.	and draw out the blood or moisture that you find, then treat the place with what is fitting, and suture the place.
dou chancre	of the ulcer
Nos avons dit en la division les semblances de chancre, et coment on i doit ovrer par medicines, et coment on doit eschuer la cure de fer; et disons le chancre enjanreit en la marris, et grant cautele a en la cure, et dirent li ancien que quant chancres est en leu ou on le puet raier si com chancre qui est em mameles, et en la cuixe, et en semblans leus, et le doit tout oster quant il est en l’encomencement; et quant il est grans et anciens, si ne covient mie que tu l’aproches, car je n’en poi onques nul saner; ne nulz n’en sana onques devant moi.	We have said in the division the similarities of ulcers, and how one should work on them with medicines, and how one should avoid the cure of iron; and let us say that an ulcer arises in the marshes, and great caution is needed in its treatment, and they said the ancients that when an ulcer is in a place where it can be scraped like an ulcer that is in the breasts, and in the groin, and similar places, then one should take it all out when it is at the beginning; and when it is large and old, it is not fitting that you approach it, because I have never cured any of them; nor has anyone else ever cured any before me.
Et li ovraiges, quant il est en leu ou on le puet oster, si com nos avons dit, est que tu purge aucune fois le malaide de cole noire; puis le fai sainier s’il ait manifeste repletion, puis afaite le malaide .i. boin leu por faire l’ovraige; puis giete tes oncines ou chancre, et le cheve de toutes pars, et l’oste de toutes pars sens rien laissier; et laisse corre le sanc tout fuer, et espreint bien le leu a ta main ou a aucune chose, et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire de l’incision de l’artere ou de la voine, si le cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the work, when it is in a place where it can be taken out, as we have said, is that you purge the patient once of black bile; then let him bleed if he has a clear repletion, then make the patient's  good place to perform the operation; then cut your incisions or ulcer, and shave it from all sides, and the bone from all sides without leaving anything; and let the blood flow out completely, and press well the place with your hand or any thing, and if the bleeding counteracts the incision of the artery or vein, then cauterize it as long as the bleeding is stanched; then cure it with other remedies until it is healed.
de ydropisie	of dropsy
Nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’idropisie, et en queil maniere li assemblee de l’aigue est faite, et les signes de chescune semblance, et la cure qui est faite par medicines, et cele qui est curee par fer: si est eclites soulement; et ne doit on touchier de fer en ces .ij. semblances: c’est a savoir, tympanites et yposarche, car c’est mortelz chose; donques quant tu medicines ceste semblance de ydropisie qui est apelee «eclites» de medicines, et li cure ne profite, si regarde se li malaides est foibles, ou s’il ait autre maladie que ydropisie, si com toust et solution de ventre et semblans choses; si n’i touchier de fer, car il i a doutance; et se tu vois le malaide de fort vertut, et il n’a autre maladie que ydropisie soulement, et il n’est mie trop jones ne trop vielz, si dois ensi ovrer:	We have said in the division the appearances of dropsy, and in what manner the assembly of water is made, and the signs of each appearance, and the cure which is done by medicines, and that which is cured by iron; thus it is only; and one must not touch iron in these 2 appearances: namely, tympanites and hyposarche, because it is a mortal thing; therefore when you medicate this appearance of dropsy which is called “eclites” by medicines, and the cure does not benefit, look if the patient is weak, or if he has another illness besides dropsy, such as coughs and solution of belly and similar things; if do not touch iron, because there is doubt; and if you see the patient of strong virtue, and he has no other illness but dropsy alone, and he is neither too young nor too old, then you must thus operate:
lieve le malaide droit sus tes mains, et li ministres presse le ventre em boutant l’aigue a la plus basse partie dou pis, puis pren le spatumile espinous selonc ceste forme: Et soit trenchans de .ij. pars. a pointe, et toutevoie ne soit mie si entrans qu’il puist venir jusc’a l’intestine quant on le fiche ens, et ne le puist blecier;	lift the patient right up on your hands, and the minister presses the belly pushing the water to the lowest part of the pelvis, then take the spinal spatula according to this form: And be sharp for 2 parts. at the point, and nonetheless do not be so deep that it can come to the intestine when you insert it, and you cannot pierce it;
puis regarde se li ydropisie est enjanree devers les intestines: si covient que tu fendes ensus de la boude .iij. dois droit desoz sus lou poignil; et se li ydropisie est por la maladie dou foie, si soit ta fendure au senestre de la boude .iij. dois; et se c’est por la miuce, si soit a destre, et ne covient mie que li malaides gise sus la fendure que les superfluitez ne corrent a celui foible leu;	then look if the dropsy is  towards the intestines: then it is necessary that you cut under the ribs three finger widths right above the nipple; and if the dropsy is due to the liver disease, then the incision should be on the left side of the ribs three fingers wide; and if it is due to the spleen, then it should be on the right side, and it is not necessary that the patient lie on the cut so that the superfluities do not run to that weak place.
puis perce tout le cuir a l’estrument, et le boute, et lieve ta main a tout le spatumile entre le cuir et le syfac ausi com en escorchant a la quantiteit d’une ungle ou enqui entor; puis perce lou syfac tant que li spatumile viegne au leu vuit, et c’est li leus de l’aigue, puis le trai fuer, et i boute cest estrument de coi ci est li forme: Et est semblans a une caine d’argent subtil, et est d’arain ou d’archaut legier, et a en la partie desoz .i. petit pertus; et ou costeit d’une part, .iij. pertus; et .ij. d’autre part, et .i. d’autre; et est li chiés tailliez si com une penne, et c’est li forme de l’incision dont li escrivains taille la penne:	then pierce the entire skin with the instrument, and push it, and lift your hand to all the spatula between the skin and the fascia as if in scraping a quantity of a fingernail or thorn; then pierce the fascia until the spatula reaches its depth, which is the place of the water, then extract the trail, and it puts this instrument that's this form: And it's similar to a subtle silver coin, and it is light iron or archaut, and on the underside there is one small hole; and on one side, three holes; and two on the other side, and one on the other; and the head is cut like a feather, and this is the form of the incision with which the scribes cut the feather:
au chief desus est li alemele, si que quant li estrumens vient a l’aigue, si dessent maintenant sus l’estrument; vuide la donques la moitiet ou la tierce part, car se tu en vuides plus qu’il ne covient en celle houre, par aventure si muert li malaides por la resolution de son esperit de l’arme, ou il chiet paumez, ou il aproche a la mort;	at the top is the alemel, so that when the instrument comes to the water, it draws now on top of the instrument; empty therefore half or the third part, because if you empty more than it is necessary in that hour, perhaps the patient will die for the resolution of his spirit from the weapon, or he will fall into a coma, or he will approach death;
mais en vuide selonc la quantiteit de sa vertut, et selonc ceu que les dispositions de la vertut dou malaide signifient, et ses poulz; puis trai l’estrument et retien l’aigue, et elle est retenue maintenant por le keur qui estoupe le pertus qui est sus le syfac, de coi j’ai parleit, que tu perces selonc ceste maniere; puis rencomence l’estrument l’autre jor, se tu vois le malaide soffrant ceu, et trai de l’aigue une petite quantiteit;	but in void according to the quantity of its virtue, and according to what the dispositions of the virtue of the patient signify, and his poults; then treat the instrument and hold the water, and it is retained now for the heart that stops the passage which is on the syfac, because of this I have spoken, that you pierce according to this manner; then begin again the instrument the other day, if you see the patient suffering those, and treat of the water a small quantity
fai ce aucun jor, et te garde de foloier tant qu’il ni demore mais c’un poc d’aigue. Et se tu doutes sus le malaide, et tu i lais mout d’aigue, si le cure de la sepulture ou sablon chaut, et par mout sueir ou bain et au soleil, et se teigne de boivre; et le cure de medicines desiccatives tant qu’il soit sanez, et cauterize sus l’estomac et sus lou foie et sus l’esplen aprés l’estraction de l’aigue, si com j’ai dit devant.	do this no day, and keep yourself from following until there remains but a little of the water. And if you doubt about the patient, and you put him much water, so the cure of the burial or hot sand, and by much sweat or bath and sun, and it stains to drink; and the cure of drying medicines as long as he is healed, and cauterize on the stomach and on the liver and on the spleen after the extraction of the water, as I have said before.
de l’estopement de la verge	of the stopping of the penis
Aucune fois naissent enfant qui n’ont point de pertus en la verge, ou li pertus est petis, ou il n’est mie en son leu. Si le covient tantost qu’il n’aist percier a tout .i. spatumile molt subtil selonc ceste forme: puis met ou pertus .i. clo subtil de plonc, et le lie et le tien ensi .iij. jors ou iiij. et quant il vuet faire urine, si soit ostez li clos, et faice urine, et puis li remet; et par aventure nen i couvient point, car li urine qui vient fuer ne lou laisse close.	Sometimes children are born who have no openings in the penis, or the opening is small, or it is not in its place. If this happens, it is necessary as soon as possible that he be able to pierce a whole i. spatumile very fine according to this form: then put on the opening i. clo subtle of lead, and tie it and hold it thus for three or four days and when he wants to urinate, have him remove the plug, and let him urinate, and then put it back; and by chance it is not necessary, because the urine that comes out does not leave it closed.
Cil de cui li pertus est petis, si est medicinez dou clo de plonc, si com nos avons dit, si s’eslargera. Cil qui n’ont mie le pertus en lor leu sont bleciet, car aucun naissent qui ont le pertus au chief de la verge, por coi il ne puient pissier avant s’il ne lievent lor verge en haut; et ne pueent enjanrer por ceu que li matiere ne puet venir jusc’a la marris, et c’est une male maladie.	Those whose opening is small, if they are medicated with the lead plug, as we have said, it will widen. Those who do not have the opening in their place are blueish because none are born who have the opening at the head of the penis, so that they cannot urinate before they raise their penis; and they cannot ejaculate for this reason because the matter cannot come to the glans, and this is a bad disease.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, puies estent le chief de la verge et le cope ausi com la taille d’une penne, si ke li pertus chiece em mileu, si com il covient; et te garde de decorrement de sanc qui i vient maintes fois, et s’il avient, si l’estainche de ceu qui estainche sanc, et cure la plaie tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the manner of the work is that the patient lies often on his back, then is extended the head of the penis and the scrotum as well as the waist of a feather, so that the opening falls in the middle, as it should; and guard against bleeding which comes many times, and if it happens, have the one who stanches blood stanch it, and cure the wound until it is healed.
des pustules de la verge	of the pimples of the penis
Maintes fois vienent cist albathe en la verge, et est une apparance de char laide; et en i a malignes et non malignes; si covient que tu les preignes a .i. oncine subtil, et les cope et munde toutes, puis met sus coton moilliet en oignement egiptien; puis le cure d’oignement diafinicon tant qu’il soit sanez.	Many times come these pimples to the penis, and it is a loathsome appearance of flesh; and there are malignant and non-malignant ones; so it behoves you to pick them at .i. one fine thorn, and to cut and cleanse all, then put cotton moistened in Egyptian ointment; then cure with diafinicon ointment until it be healed.
Et se li albathe est maligne, de pute color et depuant, si covient que tu i amenistres cautere. Quant tu l’as copeit, et se li albathe est en som la verge, et en ait partie dedens la peil et partie defuer, si covient que tu oste l’albathe qui est dedens premier; et quant il est soudez, si le cure defuer. Car quant tu le cures ensamble, si n’est mie asseurez li chiez de la verge qu’il ne soit perciez, et vient noiror et corruption en son la verge et ou coion; si covient chever tout ceu qui est noir et corrumput, puis lie sus l’emplaustre de miel et de farine qui soit fait d’escorce de poumes grenates et de veces, puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the pimple is malignant, of foul color and putrid, so it behoves you to cauterize it with fire. When you have cut it open, and if the pimple is within the penis, and has part inside the skin and part outside, then it behooves you to remove the pimple that is inside first; and when it is healed, cure the one outside. For when you cure them together, it is not sure that the head of the penis will not be pierced, and blackness and corruption come in its penis and scrotum; so it behoves to shave all that is black and corrupt, then apply a plaster of honey and flour made of powdered quince bark and vicks, then cure with other cures until it be healed.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si amenistre le cautere lunaire selonc ceste forme: Li cauteres si aide as .ij. dispositions ensamble: c’est asavoir, au decorrement de sanc, et a la corruption; et se li chiés de la verge est corrumpus et retrais, si covient que tu boutes ou conduit de la verge une cainne de plonc, et pisse li malaides parmi; et quant li pelz iert aerse au chief de la verge qui avient a ces qui n’ont mie esteit circoncis, ou il avient por plaie ou por aposteme, si covient donques que tu l’escorches a .i. estrument cheveit, tant que li liiens soit desliiez, et soit delivrez li chiez de la verge de toutes pars;	And if bleeding comes, so administer the lunar cautery according to this form: The cauteries helps with two dispositions together: namely, to stopping bleeding, and to corruption. And if the head of the penis is corrupted and retracts inward, then it behoves you to put or lead a chain of flax into the penis, and make the patient urinate amidst it; and when the skin is rough at the head of the penis which happens to those who have not been circumcised, or there is an ulcer or abscess, then it behoves you to scrape it with one sharp instrument, until the bonds are loosened, and the head of the penis be delivered from all sides;
et se c’est grief chose de deviser ceu, si covient que tu l’escorches a .i. spatumile aucun poc dou chief de la verge et de la peil; puis dessevre belement entre .ij., et i met .i. subtil drapeil de lin moilliet an aigue froide, qu’il n’aerse derechief.	and if it is a grievous thing to devise these, then you must scrape it with a spatula of the head of the rod and the peel; then sew carefully between two, and put one fine veil of linen moistened in cold water so that it does not dry.
de la circoncision	of circumcision
Circoncision n’est mie desliemens de continuation si com les autres plaies; toutevoie quant nos faison ceste oevre de nostre volenteit, et proprement as enfans, si est mestier que nos faisiens la millor oevre, et la plus legiere a salut.	Circumcision is not a wound that heals like others; nonetheless, when we perform this work by our own will, and especially on children, it is necessary that we make the best work and the lightest to heal.
Je dis que li ancien ne dirent mie la circoncision de lor enfans, car il n’en usent mie en lor loi, et n’en avons mais que ceu que nos avons aquis par experiment.	I say that the ancients did not speak of circumcision for their children because they did not practice it in their law, and we have only what we have acquired through experience.
Car j’ai veut la plus grant partie des maistres et des sainors qui faisoient circumcision entor .i. dal, et as forces, et a tout une novacule; si fuioit li keurs car il i a .ij. toiles, et par aventure si cope on celi desus et demore celle desoz.	Because I have wanted the most part of the masters and of the healers who made circumcision under i.e., dal, and forces, and at all a new knife; so it was the keurs because there are .ij. cloths, and by adventure if one cuts that above and remains that below.
Or la recovient coper, et est li dolor double, et a la mundification qui est dou dal n’est mie asseuree li pointe dou membre; et a la mundification de l’ungle par aventure eschaipe li fer, et corront l’uevre, et maintes fois naissent ensi qu’il n’ont mestier de mundification et je l’ai veut.	Or it is convenient to cut, and is the pain double, and at the purification which is from dal there isn't assured the point of the limb; and at the purification of the angle by adventure escapes the iron, and runs the work, and many times they are born as if they don't have need of purification and I have wanted it.
De la mondification qui est faite as forces a tout le liien de fil ai je troveit la bonteit de l’experiment, car les forces taillent justement ausi bien desus com desoz.	Of the purification which is done with forces to all the linen of thread I have found the goodness of the experiment, because the forces cut justly as well above as below.
Car quant tu presses ta main, si tailles igalment en .i. tout soul tens; mais que li filz soit bien estrois entor lou cuir; et soit li maniere dou premier ovraige si est que tu faices penser l’enfant, s’il entent, que tu ne li fais fuer que liier le fil entor la verge tant soulement, et pues le fai esjoir en toutes les manieres que tu pues;	For when you press your hand, so equally in one, all soul tense; but that the threads be well stretched around the skin; and let the manner of the first work be such that you make the child think, if he understands, that you only tie the thread around the member as much, and then allow him to enjoy himself in all the ways that you can;
puis le fai ester entre tes mains tout droit, et repont les forces entre tes mains ou desoz tes piez que li enfes ne les voie, ne aucun des estrumens; puis boute ta main a la verge et souffle ou keur, et la trai en haut tant que li chiés de la verge soit ens; puis la mundifie bien de l’ordure qui i est assemblee, puis lie le leu signiet d’un fil double, puis la lie desoz .i. poc a .i. autre liien; et la tien as .ij. dois par la seconde lieeure au pouchet et au doit indice, et cope entre les .ij. liiens, puis lieve le keur desus hastanment et trai le chief de la verge;	Then make him straight between your hands, and respond the forces between your hands or under your feet that the child does not see them, nor any of the instruments; then put your hand on the member and blow on it, and pull it up until the head of the member is inside; then cleanse it well of the filth that has accumulated there, then tie the place with a double thread, then tie it under one pock to another lien; and hold it as two digits by the second lieneure at the pouch and at the index finger, and cut between the two liens, then lift the head upward carefully and pull the head of the member.
puis laisse corre le sanc poc et poc, car c’est li muedres; et met poudre sus et sus la poudre .i. drapeil glueit d’un moieuf d’uef cuit destempreit d’aigue rose, confit avec oile roset boin et fres, et lou laisse sus jusc’a l’autre jor, et le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then let it clot blood piece by piece, for that is the way; and put powder on top and on top of the powder one drape made from a yolk of an egg cooked in water tempered with rosewater, mixed with good and fresh rose oil, and leave it there until the next day, and treat it with another cure as long as he is healed.
Li forme des forces a la mundification si est ceste: li dui chiés soient tenves et soient trenchans, et soient li chiés ausi grant com li mainche igalment:	The form of the forces for the mundification is this: the two shoulders be raised and pointed, and the shoulders also be as large as the hands equally.
li error de la mundification si est quant li keurs dedens fuit a l’incision; donques il covient que tu l’estendes a ton ungle, ainsois que li leus faice aposteme; et le cope igalment, et se tu ne lou pues tenir a ton ungle, si le tien as tenailles, et puis le cope.	The error of the mundification is when the kernel within is at the incision; therefore it is necessary that you extend it to your finger, so that the lesion makes an abscess; and cut it equally, and if you cannot hold it with your finger, then hold it with pliers, and then cut it.
Et s’il trespassent .iij. jors, et ceu qui est desoz la verge est enflez, si le laisse tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et l’escorche legierement; si le cope si com tu pues mues, et te garde de la partie de la verge, ce ne li nuira niant.	And if it trespasses three days, and that which is below the shaft is swollen, let it alone until the abscess heals, and the scab lightly peels; then cut it as much as you can move, and guard the part of the shaft, it will do it no harm.
Cure donques le leu de choses soudans plaie de poudre, que nos avons dit ou traitier des poudres, et s’on cope dou keur outre mesure, et il va au desus, si ne nuira point; cure le donques, si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Cure therefore the place with some powder wound, which we have said or treated of powders, and if one cuts the kernel beyond measure, and it goes upwards, it will do no harm; cure it therefore, as we have said, until it is healed.
dou retenement de l’urine	Of the retention of urine
Li retenue de l’urine si est d’opilation de piere, ou de sanc congeleit, ou de bowe, ou de char nee, ou de semblans choses, que nos avons dit en la division;	The retention of urine is from an obstruction in the bladder, or of blood clotted, or of a tumor, or of new flesh, or similar things that we have said in the division.
et se li urine n’est desliie, et tu vois estre la retenue por la piere qui est jai ou col de la vessie, si covient que li malaides soit corbés sus ses genoulz; et li soient mis li piez sor le dos, et estende son ventre de la partie desus lou dos, et restraigne li malaides s’alainne tant com il puet; et adonques est constrains li colz de la vessie a l’expression de la piere au desus, por coi li urine est desliie e;	and if the urine is not released, and you see that the retention is due to the stone being in the urethra or neck of the bladder, then it is necessary for the patient to be bent on their knees; and his feet are placed on his back, and his belly is extended from the upper part towards his back, and restrain the patient's legs as much as he can; and thus the neck of the bladder is constrained to express the stone upwards, so that the urine is released.
et s’elle ne vient, si com nos avons dit, et li malaides sent grant dolor, si covient que tu i aministres extraction a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «siringue», de coi ci est li forme: et soit d’argent subtilz legiere chevee, si com li penne d’un oiseil; et soit li caine d’une palme de lonc et demie, et soit subtilz au chief.	and if it does not come, as we have said, and the patient feels great pain, then it is necessary for you to administer extraction with all the instrument that is called a "syringe," of which this is the form: it should be a finely crafted light silver one, like the feather of a bird; and its shaft should be a palm long and half, and be fine at the tip.
Et li maniere de l’issue de l’urine si est que tu pren .i. fil double, et lie au chief .i. poc de laine ou de couton, et boute le chief dou fil dedens la siringue; et cope la superfluiteit de la lainne et le boute jusc’au chief de la siringue, puis oint la siringue d’oile ou de burre et d’aubin d’uef, et fai seoir le malaide sus .i. siege, et li arose la vessie et la verge d’oile moiste et d’oile d’olive et d’aigue tede;	And the manner of the issue of urine is that you take one double thread, and tie to the head one piece of wool or cotton, and put the head of the thread inside the syringe; and cut the superfluity of the wool and put it up to the head of the syringe, then anoint the syringe with oil or butter and aubin of egg, and make the patient sit on one seat, and raise his bladder and penis with moist oil and oil of olive and tepid water.
puis met legierement la siringue en la verge, tant qu’elle viegne a la racine de la verge, puis double la verge desus devers la boude; puis boute la siringue avant jusc’a la vessie, et la sente li malaides venir jusc’a la chose vuide, et ceu n’est mie fait selonc cest ordre fuer que por ceu que li conduis ou elle vait est tors; puis estent le fil a tout la laine poc et poc, et li urine en suit la laine, puis l’estrai fuer, et fai corre l’urine;	then put gently the syringe in the penis, until it comes to the root of the penis, then double the penis upwards towards the pubis; then put the syringe forward up to the bladder, and let the patient feel it coming up to the empty thing, and this is not done according to this order for those who lead or where it goes is twisted; then is the thread at all the wool piece by piece, and the urine follows the wool, then extract it further, and do correct the urine;
et rencomence la siringue tant que li vessie soit vuidie, et soit aligiez li malaides.	and recommence the syringe until the bladder is emptied, and the patient is aligned.
des maladies de la vessie	of the bladder diseases
Quant escorcheures ou sanc vient en la vessie, ou porriture i est assemblee, et tu i vues distiller aigues et medicines, si fai a tout l’estrument qui est apellé «clepsedre», et c’est li forme:	When scabs or blood comes in the bladder, or there is rottenness assembled, and you see it distilling sharp waters and medicines, so do to all the instrument that is called "clepsedre", and this is its form:
Elle est close, et si a .iij. pertus: .ij. d’une part, et .i. d’autre, si com tu vois; et li leus chevez par coi li medicine cort soit telz qu’il estoupe bien la verge sens adition, si c’on em puisse traire la moistor, et bouter quant mestier est;	It is closed, and has .iij. openings: .ij. on one side, and .i. on the other, as you see; and the leus chevez by which the medicine is poured so that it stops well the penis without addition, so that if one can draw out the moisture, and expulse when necessary;
et quant tu vues giter tes medicines en la vessie, met le chief dou keusteur en la moistor, et trai au traiant qui est ens; si trairas la moistor au kesteur, et puis reboute fort le traiant ens; si entrera li moistors ens, et venra a la vessie maintenant, si que li malaides la sentira;	and when you want to pour your medicines into the bladder, put the chief of the keuster in the moisture, and draw with the tube that is inside; so you will draw the moisture into the keuster, and then firmly replace the tube inside; so the moisture will enter inside, and come to the bladder now, so that the patient will feel it;
et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil dont on clisterize la vessie: si est ci:	and this is the form of the subtle clyster by which one enemas the bladder: it is here:
Et est d’argent ou d’archaut, et est li chiés plus haut; et desoz a .i. sein ou li liiens chiet; puis pren une vessie de mouton et i met la moistor dont tu vues clisterizer la vessie, puis la lie entre les .ij. seins forment d’un boin fil double, et chaufe .i. poc celle moistor sus le feu; puis boute le chief dou clistere en la verge, puis estrain ta main sus la vessie a tout la moistor avenanment, tant que li malaides sente que celle moistor est jai venue a la vessie;	And it is of silver or of argentium, and the head is higher; and below to one breast or where the shoulder falls; then take a sheep's bladder and put in the moisture which you wish to enemas the bladder, then tie it between the two breasts formed of a double fine thread, and heat one part of the moisture on the fire; then put the head of the clyster into the penis, then strain your hand on the bladder throughout the entire administration of the moisture, until the patient feels that the moisture has come to the bladder.
et se tu n’as la vessie, si pren une piece de parchemin, et en fai .i. cercle, et le perce rondement entor; puis boute .i. fil fort en ces pertus, puis assemble le cercle si com on assemble .i. dal, et met dedens ceu que tu vues d’oile et de moistor et d’aigue, et le lie en l’estrument; et fai si com tu as fait de la vessie, de presser a ta main tant que li moistor veigne a la vessie.	And if you do not have the bladder, then take a piece of parchment, and make one circle, and pierce it roundly throughout; then put one strong thread into these holes, then assemble the circle as one assembles a dial, and put inside this what you wish of oil and moisture and water, and tie it to the instrument; and do as you have done with the bladder, pressing with your hand until the moisture comes to the bladder.
de la piere	of the stone
Nos avons jai dit en la division les manieres de piere, et l’estraction ensamble medicines; et ai dit la difference entre la piere enjanree as rains, et toz les signes, et en queil piere on doit ovrer de taille; et en la vessie, et en la verge; et je le vos dirai apertement et briément.	We have said in the division the manners of stone, and the extraction together medicines; and I have said the difference between the stone engendered as rains, and all the signs, and in what stone one must work with a size; and in the bladder, and in the member; and I will tell you it clearly and briefly.
Je dis que li piere qui est enjanree en la vessie si avient plus sovent as enfans, et c’est signe que li aigue saut de la vessie semblans a aigue en sa subtiliteit; et i apert harene, et graite li malaides sa verge, et li pent maintes fois, et puis enroidist; et a mout de ces saut li fondemens; et est legiere li sanation des enfans jusqu’il ont .iiij. ans, et est mout grief en viellars, et est as jones moiene, a ces qui sont entre jonesce et viellece; et est li cure plus legiere de ces qui ont la piere grans, que de ces qui l’ont petite.	I say that the stone which is engendered in the bladder happens more often as children, and it is a sign that the water leaps from the bladder seeming like water in its subtlety; and it appears hare-like, and grieves the patient his member, and he bends many times, and then urinates; and after many of these leaps it founds the foundations; and it is light the cure of children until they have four years, and it is very grievous in the old, and is to the middle ones, those who are between youth and old age; and the cure is lighter for those who have large stones than for those who have small ones.
Et quant nos venons a la cure, si couvient premier mundifier le malaide per clistere, por traire tout le fiens qui est as intestines. Car il encombre aucune fois a querir la piere.	And when we come to the cure, it is convenient first to purify the patient by clyster, in order to draw out all the filth that is in the intestines. For it often hinders the searching for the stone.
Puis prenez le malaide par les piez, et lou deboutez et movez au desoz, si que li piere dessende au parfont de la vessie, et saille aucune fois dou leu haut; puis le fai seoir entre tes mains appareilliet, et ses mains soient desoz ses cuisses, si que li vessie soit toute declinans aval; puis la quier et la touche ded ens;	Then take the patient by the feet, and loosen and move them downwards, so that the stone descends to the entrance of the bladder, and sometimes comes out from its high place; then make him sit between your hands equipped, and his hands be below his hips, so that the bladder is entirely sloping downwards; then the quiver and touch it from within.
se tu sens la piere en l’espaice, si te haste maintenant de taillier sus la piere. Et s’elle ne chiet au touchier dou tout, si moille ton doi indice d’oile de la main senestre, se li malaides est enfes, ou ton doi moien, se li malaides est jovencelz acomplis; et le boute en son fondement, et quier la piere, et quant tu la sens a ton doi, si l’amoine au col de la vessie; puis presse sus a ton doi, et la boute au defuer lai ou tu vues taillier.	If you feel the stone in the space, then hasten now to cut above the stone. And if it does not fall at the touch of all, then moisten your index finger with oil from the left hand, if the patient is a boy, or your middle finger, if the patient is an adult; and put it into its foundation, and feel for the stone, and when you feel it on your finger, pull it to the neck of the bladder; then press upwards on your finger, and push it outwards where you wish to cut.
Et comande au ministre qu’il presse la vessie a sa main, et li comande qu’il estende a sa main destre les coions en haut, et a sa main senestre oste le cuir qui est desoz les coions en la partie ou on fait la taille; puis i boute le spatumile copant, de coi ce est li forme:	And command the minister to press the bladder with his hand, and command him to extend with his right hand the testicles upwards, and with his left hand remove the skin which is below the testicles in the part where one makes the cut; then put the spatula cutting, of which this is the form:
Et fent entre ceu qui est entre les coions et le fondement, ne mie em mileu mais au costeit de la naige senestre; et soit drois sus la piere, et tes dois soit adés ou fondement, et soit li taille dou traver si qu’ele soit large par defuer, et dedens estroite, selonc la quantiteit de la piere, ne mie trop grans;	And make between what is between the hips and the foundation, not in the middle but at the side of the left hip; and be straight over the stone, and the two sides be either foundation or top, and let the waist be travers so that it is wide outside, and inside narrow, according to the quantity of the stone, nor too large;
par aventure la presse si li dois qui est ou fondement, qu’elle saut fuer sens travail; et saiches qu’il i a teil piere ou il a angles, et marges: si est griés a issir; et si a teil qui est souez, semblans a une glant, et reonde, dont li issue est legiere.	By chance the press if the sides which is either foundation, that it leap outward without work; and know that there are such stones which have angles, and margins: if so it is grieved to move; and if there are those which are below, seeming like a glant, and round, whose issue is light.
A celi donques ou il a angles et marge, fai la taille plus grant; et s’elle ne saut, si covient que tu estraignes sus as tenailles qui sont ausi com une lime au chief, por mues estraindre la piere si qu’elle n’eschaipe; ou tu boute desoz li .i. estrument subtil corbé au chief; et se tu ne la pues engignier ensi, si eslarge .i. poc lou pertus, et se li sans decort, si l’estrainche de vitriole;	To those then where there are angles and margins, make the waist larger; and if it does not leap, then it is necessary that you extract with tongs which are also like a file at the chief, in order to move the stone so that it does not escape; or you put under it one instrument subtle curved at the chief; and if you cannot engineer it thus, enlarge one pock the opening, and if the without decortication, then strain the vitriol;
et s’il i a plus d’une piere, si boute premier la plus grant au col de la vessie, puis cope sus, puis le trai fuer, et les petites aprés s’il en i a plusors. Et s’elle est mout grans, si la covient soier, et faire plus grant plaie. Car .ij. choses avienent au malaide: ou il muert, ou li urine vient adés par lai que li leus ne puet souder; mais toutevoie t’efforce dou traire, ou dou debrisier as tenailles, tant que tu la traies par pieces;	and if there is more than one stone, first bring the largest to the neck of the bladder, then cut above, then the drive it down, and the small ones afterward if there are more. And if she is very large, it should be removed, and make a larger wound. For two things happen to the patient: either he dies, or urine comes back through where the flesh cannot close; but nonetheless you force to drain it, or to break it with pliers, until you draw it in pieces;
et quant tu as acomplit ton oevre, si emple la plaie d’encens et d’aloe et de sanc de dragon, et l’estraint, et met par sus .i. drapeil moilliet en oile et en vin, ou en oile et en aigue rose et aigue froide, por apaisier l’aposteme chaut; puis resovine le malaide sus son col, et ne desliier lou lien jusc’au tier jor.	and when you have completed your work, apply the wound with incense and aloe and dragon's blood, and hold it together, and put on top one cloth soaked in oil and wine, or in oil and rose water and cold water, to soothe the hot abscess; then bandage the patient on his neck, and do not loosen the bandage until the third day.
Et quant tu le desliies, si arose mout bien lou leu d’oile et d’aigue, puis le cure d’oignement dyafinicon et d’oignement basilicon, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you unwrap it, moisten the place well with oil and water, then cure it with diaphoni ointment and basil ointment, until it is healed.
Et se apostemes chaus vient en la plaie et corrosions, et congelemens de sanc en la vessie, et soit par ceu retenue li urine, qui est conue en teil maniere que sans saut avec l’urine: boutes donques ton doi en la plaie, et estrai celui sanc, car s’il i remaint, si corront la vessie, et la porrit;	And if abscesses come in the wound and corrosions, and congealings of blood in the bladder, and by this is retained urine, which is known in such manner that without jumping with the urine: therefore you must put it into the wound, and extract that blood, for if it remains, they will corrupt the bladder, and it will rot.
puis leve la plaie d’aigue et d’aisil et de seil, et li aide en toutes les manieres que tu seis, tant qu’il soit sanez; et covient que toutes les oures que tu le cures, que tu li lie les .ij. cuisses, et assemble les medicines sus le leu.	Then raise the wound of sharp and smooth and fine, and help him in all the ways that you know, until it is healed; and it is necessary that all the hours that you cure him, that you tie his two thighs together, and assemble the medicines on the place.
Et se li piere est petite, et ele est ou conduit de la verge, et fichie ens, et li urine ne puet issir; si le cure de ceu que je dis ainsois, que tu lou tailles maintes fois, est on escusez de la taille per ceste cure. Je ai ja ce proveit ensi.	And if the stone is small, and it is where the penis leads to, and stuck inside, and urine cannot issue; then cure by what I say also, that you cut it many times, is excused of the cutting through this cure. I have already proved this thus.
Pren .i. foret de fer selonc ceste forme et soit a .iij. angles fichiees en .i. tison:	Take one piece of iron forest according to this form and have it with three angles attached to one coal:
puis pren .i. fil et lou lie entor la verge desoz la piere, si qu’ele ne puist venir arrier en la vessie; puis boute le foret en la verge legierement, tant qu’il viegne a la piere; et torne le foret a ta main en la piere poc et poc, tant que tu puisses percier la piere d’autre part; si venra tantost li urine, puis presse ta main sus ceu qui est demorez de la piere qui est dedens la verge. Si est tantost brisie, et saut fuer avec l’urine, et est garis li malaides;	Then take a thread and tie it around the shaft below the stone, so that it cannot come back into the bladder; then put the forest into the shaft lightly, until it comes to the stone; and turn the forest in your hand on the stone, poke and poke, until you can feel the stone from the other side; then soon the urine will come, then press your hand on what remains of the stone which is inside the shaft. It is then broken, and jumps out with the urine, and the patient is healed;
et se tu ne pues ce faire por aucune chose qui le deffent, si lie .i. fil desoz la piere et .i. autre desus, puis fent la verge endroit la piere entre les .ij. liiens, puis l’estrai fuer, et deslie lou liien, et mundifie lou sanc congeleit qui est en la plaie; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	and if you cannot do this for any reason that prevents it, then tie one thread below the stone and another above, then make the shaft straight against the stone between the two threads, then extract it, and untie the thread, and clean the congealed blood that is in the wound; and cure it until it is healed.
de la piere des femmes	of the stones of women
Poc avient que piere soit enjanree en femmes, et s’il avient aucune fois, si est li cure grief, et est deffendut por .iij. choses: l’une est que per aventure li femme est vierge; et li seconde est c’on ne puet trover femme bien saichant qui se descuevre as mires, meismement quant elle est caste.	It happens that stones are found in women, and if it happens at any time, the cure is difficult, and it is forbidden for three things: one is that perhaps the woman is a virgin; and the second is that one cannot find a well-knowing woman who unveils the privy parts, especially when she is chaste.
Et li tierce maniere si est que par aventure on ne puet trover femme bien saichant en cest art de mains; et li quarte maniere si est que li piere de la femme si est plus em parfont que li piere de l’ome, por coi il i couvient faire plus parfonde taille, et grant paour i a.	And the third way is that perhaps one cannot find a woman well-knowing in this art of hands; and the fourth manner is that the stone of the woman is more profound than the stone of the man, for which it is necessary to make a deeper incision, and there is great fear.
Et se necessitez semont a ceu, si covient que tu preignes une mieresse bien sachant, et a poines la trueve on, et se tu n’en trueves, point si quier .i. caste mire subtil; et li presente une baile bien saige en la vie des femmes, ou une femme qui saiche une partie de l’art, et li comande qu’ele faice ceu que tu li comandes de l’inquisicion de la piere;	And if necessity arises to this, it is necessary that you seek a midwife well-knowing, and if you cannot find one, then do not seek a single chaste woman subtle; and present her with a wise woman in the life of women, or a woman who knows part of the art, and command her to do what you command her from the inquiry of the stone;
et regarde mout bien se li femme est vierge: adonques li covient bouter son doit ou fondement et querir la piere; et s’ele la trueve, si la constraigne desoz son doit, et li recomande qu’elle boute son doit ou con la malaide, et quiere et presse sa main senestre sus la vessie forment.	And look well if the woman is a virgin: then it behooves her to put her buttock or foundation and seek the stone; and if she finds it, constrain it under her buttocks, and recommend that she puts her buttock on the sick person, and seeks and presses her left hand on the bladder.
S’elle la trueve, si covient qu’elle la mueve de greit en greit des l’entree de la vessie jusque desoz, tant qu’elle viegne a la racine de la cuisse; puis cope sus la piere en la racine de la cuisse encontre le mileu dou con, lai ou il est mues apparilliet, et sent la piere en celle partie; et ne mueve son doi desus la piere ou desoz, et soit li taille au premier petite;	If she finds it, then it behooves her to move it from great to little from the entrance of the bladder until it comes to the root of the thigh; then cut on the stone at the root of the thigh opposite the middle of the buttocks, where it is seen appearing, and feel the stone in that part; and do not move her buttock on the stone or under, and let the waist be initially a little.
puis boute lou rait en la taille, se tu sens la piere si acroi la plaie tant que li piere puisse issir fuer, et saiches que maintes manieres de pieres sont: c’est a savoir, petites et grans et aspres et souez, longes et reondes, et qui ont rains. si saiches les semblances por savoir l’issue.	Then put the root in the waist, if you feel the stone so near the wound until the stone can possibly issue forth, and know that many kinds of stones are: namely, small and large and rough and smooth, long and round, and which have veins. Know these similarities to know the outcome.
Et se li sans te vaint, si met au leu vitriole broiet, et li tien une houre tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis revien a ton ovraige, tant que li piere soit fuer, et aies des estrumens que je t’ai dit en l’estraction de la piere as homes por toi aidier en ton oevre;	And if the stone does not want to come out, put vitriol ground at its place, and hold it for an hour until the stone is softened; then return to your work, as long as the stone is removed, and have the instruments that I told you about in the extraction of stones for men to help you in your work.
et se li sans te vaint, et c’est de l’artere qui est copee, si met la poudre sus le leu et l’estrain de tentes et de bendelz, et ne rencomencier plus ceu, et laisse la piere et ne la traire mie, que par aventure morroit li malaide; puis cure la plaie.	And if the stone does not want to come out, and it is the artery that is cut, put the powder on the place and strain it with bandages and strips, and do not begin again those, and leave the stone and do not try it any more, for fear of death; then cure the wound.
Et quant li chalor dou sanc est apaisie, et li leus porrist, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que li piere soit fuer.	And when the heat of the blood is appeased, and the area is dry, then return to your work as long as the stone is removed.
de hernie carnouse	of fleshy hernia
Ramice aquouse n’est autre chose que assemblee de moistor ou blanc syfac, qui est desoz lou keur des coions, que contient l’uef; et est apelez «syfac», et aucune fois est proprement en la toile de l’uef, si c’on cuide que ce soit .i. autre oef; et c’est li cuir dou coion entre lou blanc syfac que nos avons dit; et ceu n’avient se poc non.	Ramice aquouse is nothing else than an assembly of moisture or white syfac, which is below the heart of the testicles, which contains the egg; and it is called "syfac," and sometimes it is properly in the membrane of the egg, if one thinks that it is i.e., another egg; and it is the skin of the testicle between the white syfac that we have said; and those did not have this pox no.
Et li generation de cest ramice si est de foibleteit que vient as coions, et est espandue celle matiere.	And the generation of this ramice is so weak that it comes to the testicles, and that matter is spread out.
Et aucune fois si vient de percussion sus les coions, et ceste moistor si a maintes colors: ou c’est color declinans a jaunice, ou c’est sans rouge, ou noir, ou aquous blans, et ce avient plus;	And sometimes it comes from a blow on the testicles, and this moisture has many colors: either it is declining towards yellow, or it is without red, or black, or aqueous white, and this happens more;
et ce sont li signe de conoistre ceste assemblee, car s’elle est ou blanc syfac que nos avons dit, si est li apostemes reons, .i. poc lonc si com li figure d’un oef, et n’apert mie li coions, car il a moistor tout entor.	and these are the signs to know this assembly, because if it is or white such as we have said, then the abscesses are ripe, that is, about long as the figure of an egg, and does not open the corners, because it has moisture all around.
Et s’il a moistor en la propre toile, si est li apostemes reons avec une partie de l’uef, et por ceu pense on que c’est uns autres oef;	And if it has moisture in the proper cloth, then the abscess is ripe with a part of the egg, and for this reason one thinks that it's another egg;
et se li moistor est entre le cuir des coions et le blanc syfac, si le sent om bien; donques quant tu vues savoir la color de la moistor, si esprueve a tout l’intromissoire quarreit, de coi li forme est ci devant.	and if the moisture is between the skin of the corners and the white such as, then one feels it well; therefore when you want to know the color of the moisture, one probes at all the intromissoire quarrelit, because its form is as before.
Selonc ceu donques qui vient aprés l’intromissoire, juge de ceu qui est dedens.	According to this therefore which comes after the introducer, judge of that which is within.
Et quant nos la curons par fer, si covient que li malaides soit sainiez selonc som pooir et la repletion de son cors; puis le sovine sus son dos, sus une chose un poc haute, et met desoz lui mout de drapelz;	And when we cure it with iron, it is necessary that the patient be healthy according to his power and the fullness of his body; then lay him on his back, on a thing a little high, and put under him much of blankets;
puis sié sus sa senestre, et comande au ministre qu’il sié a destre, et estende la verge a l’un des .ij. costelz dou keur des coions;	then sit on his left, and command the minister that he sit on the right, and extend the rod to one of the two ribs near the heart of the bones;
puis pren le spatumile leit, et cope le cuir des coions parmi leu dou lonc jusque delez lou poignil, et soit ta fendure toute droite en devisant le cuir des coions jusc’a syfac blanc, et l’escorche subtilment selonc tom pooir;	then take the pointed knife, and cut the skin of the bones among them from the long one to near the armpit, and let your incision be straight dividing the skin of the bones until the white fat, and the peel it carefully according to your power;
puis perce lou syfac plain d’aigue a .i. large pertus, et estrai toute l’aigue, et puis met tes oncines, et estent lou syfac amont; et ne touchier le keur des coions, mais que le syfac soulement; cope tout ou par pieces meismement le costeit de lui subtil, que se tu ne le copes bien saigement, si revenra li aigue;	Then pierce the abscess with clean water to 1 inch wide opening, and draw out all the water, and then put your bandages on, and raise the abscess; and do not touch the root of the boils, but only the abscess; cut everything or in pieces carefully the side of it subtly, that if you do not cut it wisely, it will return the water.
et se l’uef saut fuer a ton oevre, si le ramoinne en son leu quant tu avras acomplit l’uevre dou syfac; puis assemble les .ij. leivres dou keur des coions a une costure, puis le cure si com les autres plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the boil is healed after your work, then set it in its place when you have completed the work of the abscess; then join the two leaves of the root of the boils with a stitch, then cure it like other wounds until it is healed.
Et se tu trueves l’uef corromput d’autre maladie, si covient que tu lies les vasselz que sont suspensoire, en doutant le decorrement de sanc; puis cope le coion a tout le suspensoire, et estrai l’uef, et le cure si com nos avons dit.	And if you find the boil corrupted by another illness, then it is necessary that you bind the vessels that are suspended, fearing the flow of blood; then cut the boil all the way to the suspension, and draw out the boil, and cure it as we have said.
Et se aigue est assemblee en .ij. parties ensamble, saiches que ce sont .ij. ramices; si cope l’autre partie si com tu as fait la premiere igalment, puis essue lou sanc, et met en la plaie lainne moillie en oile roset;	And if the fluid is assembled into two parts together, know that these are two roots; so cut the other part as you have done the first equally, then wipe away the blood, and put in the wound a cloth moistened with rose oil.
et met defuer autre laine moillie en vin et en oile, et met sus les .ij. coions, et met desus drapelz doublés, et le lie sus a tout le liien qui est selonc ceste forme:	and put on top another piece of cloth moistened with wine and oil, and place the two cushions on top, and put doubled cloths above, and tie it over the entire length which is according to this form:
Puis pren .ij. drapelz, et les emple de laine charpie selonc ceste semblance et soient assemblez par cousture en la gorle des braies, et li uns des chiés preigne sus le fondement jusc’au dos, et li autres a la partie dou poignil; et li autre dui chief sus les .ij. angres, et soit toute assemblee li restreinture en la boucle dou braier;	Then take two cloths, and make them into a lamb's wool padding according to this appearance, and be assembled by stitching at the waist of the breeches, and one of the shoulders rests on the foundation until the back, and the other on the armpit side; and the other two on the two angles, and let the entire restraint be assembled in the loop of the breeches;
et aucune fois est medicinee ceste ramice de cautere en leu de taille de fer, et est que tu preignes .i. cautere cultellaire subtil, et cope le cuir des coions, et soit eschaufez si com nos avons dit, si que li syfac blanc que contient l’aigue est descovers;	And sometimes this ram's horn cautery is used in place of a steel scalpel, and you should take one subtle cuttlefish cautery, and cut the skin of the scrotum, and be heated as we have said, so that the white syfac which contains the fluid is uncovered;
si pren lou cautere selonc ceste forme, et perce celui syfac as oncines, et l’escorche a cest subtil cautere chaut:	If you take the cautery according to this form, and pierce that syfac with one quickness, and scrape it with this subtle heated cautery:
Et lou cope en toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que tu esraiches tout; et garde que li feus ne touche l’uef; et saiches que ceste oevre est plus salve; et mues gardans de decorrement de sanc, et muedres que li ovraiges de taille;	And the scrape in all ways that you can, as long as you scrape everything; and keep that the fire does not touch the egg; and know that this work is more safe; and moves guarding of blood loss, and moves that the works of scalpel;
et se nulle chose te fait contraire, ou aposteme chaus ou decorremens de sanc ou autre chose, si cure ce qui te fait contraire, selonc ceu qui est devant dit.	and if nothing goes against you, or abscess or discharge of blood or other thing, so treat what is going against you, according to what is said before.
Et se li malaides est paourous, et ne vuet atendre cest ovraige por son horribleteit, si amenistre perforation, si com je te di, et est que quant tu es bien certains par les significations que nos avons dit que ramice aquouse est lai,	And if the patient is fearful, and does not want to endure this work because of its horror, then administer the perforation as I have told you, and it is that when you are certain by the signs we have said that the watery root is there,
si fai seoir le malaide sus .i. siege leveit; puis perce l’aposteme an la partie desoz a tout le spatumile large, et met la perforation dou lonc dou cors; et soit larges li pertus, si que toute li aigue corre fuer;	if you make the patient sit on a raised seat; then pierce the abscess in the lower part to all the breadth of the spatula, and put the perforation deep into the body; and let the opening be wide so that all the water flows out;
puis met coton sus le leu, et le lie, et laisse por corre le remenant de l’aigue, puis le cure tant que li plaie soit sanee;	then put cotton on the spot, and bind it, and let the remaining water run out, then treat it until the wound is healed;
et se li blainche toile ne laisse issir l’aigue en la bouche de la plaie, si covient que tu i boutes une penne ou l’estrument dont on trait l’aigue des ydropiques, de coi li forme est ci devant; et eslarge .i. poc la plaie, et saiches que li aigue revient, et est assemblee aprés .vj. mois ou enqui entor, et quant elle est assemblee si com devant, et ensi passera li malaides ses jors.	And if the white cloth does not let the water go out of the mouth of the wound, then it is necessary to put in a pen or the instrument with which one treats the water of the dropsy, for whose form is before; and enlarge i. poc the wound, and know that the water returns, and is assembled after six months or until later, and when it is assembled like before, and thus will pass the patient his days.
de l’aposteme des coions	of the abscess of the testicles
Saiches que en la section de ceste ramice a paor em plusors dispositions, por coi il me semble que mues vaut c’on la laisse;	Know that in the section of this branch there is fear in many dispositions, for which I think it is better to leave it.
et je vos dirai l’ovraige et les semblances de l’aposteme.	and I will tell you the work and likenesses of the abscess.
Je dis donques que maint aposteme vienent ou cors, et meismement as coions; et c’est par mout de cas.	I say therefore that many abscesses come to the body, and even to the testicles; and this is by many causes.
C’est a savoir par superfluiteit aigre et ague, qui est espandue as coions, ou de percussion;	That is to say by excess of sour and acrid, which is spread to the testicles, or from percussion;
et est li color de l’aposteme selonc la color dou cors; et ne trueve point de dolor, et est aposteme grief;	and the color of the abscess is according to the color of the body; and it finds no pain, and it is a grievous abscess;
et par aventure est uns apostemes griés paourous et pierous, et de fuxe color, et aucune fois vient de nout d’artere, ou d’enfleure de voine.	And by adventure is one abscess grievously and terribly painful, and of dark colour, and sometimes comes from our artery, or an inflammation of a vein.
Quant c’est par nout d’artere, si est conus par la disposition d’aposteme chaut, quant tu la presses a tes dois;	When it is by an artery, then it is known by the disposition of the hot abscess, when you press it with your fingers.
et ne covient mie que tu i touches.	and it does not behoove you to touch it at all.
Cil qui est fais d’enfleure de voine est conus par sa disposition a l’expression dou touchement des dois,	He who is made from an inflammation of a vein is known by its disposition at the expression of touching with fingers
et puet om bien faire la taille sus ceste semblance, et sus les autres chars;	and one can well do this operation on these kinds of things, and on other similar things.
et est que tu cope lou keur des coions, puis estent l’uef en haut, et le trai fuer dou blanc syfac, et delivre lou suspensoire de toutes pars de l’uef.	and it is that you cut the heart of the onions, then being the head up, and the body toward white side, and deliver the suspension from all sides of the head.
Se li uef est ja sodez avec ces chars nees, si covient donques que tu traies l’uef, et lou cope;	If the onion is already cut with these kinds of cuts, then it is necessary that you pull out the onion, and cut it.
et s’il est aers au syfac, ou en ceu qui est dedens les vasselz, si covient que tu delivre toute celle tenve, et la cope reondement.	and if it is adhered to the white side, or in those who are inside the vessels, then it is necessary that you deliver all of that part, and cut it roundly.
Et se li naissance de la char est ou leu derrier, si covient que tu la copes toute, et estrai l’uef, si com nous avons dit.	And if the birth of the bone is or its rear, it behooves you to cut it all and extract the egg, as we have said.
Et quant tes ovraiges est acomplis, si emple la plaie de laine moillie en oile roset et en vin, puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when your works are accomplished, smear the wound with wool moistened in rose oil and wine, then dress it with other dressings until it is healed.
de l’aposteme des coions	of the boils of the privy parts
Cis est uns apostemes envoloupez d’un envoloupement semblant a .i. borjon, avec le mollifiement des coions,	This is one boil enclosed in an envelope resembling a certain kind of husk, along with the softening of the genitals.
et se muet li malaides griement quant il vait;	and the patient moves loudly when he walks;
et li cure de ceste maladie si est bien pres ausi paourouse com ceste ci devant,	and the cure of this disease is as well-prescribed as fearsome as the one before.
et toutevoie nos vos dirons l’ovraige de li, selonc ceu que li ancien firent.	and nevertheless, we will tell you the work of it, according to what the ancients did.
Il covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus .i. siege aleveit, puis li boute le suspensoire des coions aval a tes dois,	It is necessary that you make the patient sit on one elevated seat, then tie the suspensory of the testicles down to your two thighs,
a tout le vasseil qui sont prochien a la verge, et les teigne li maistres, et les estende forment;	To all the vessels which are near the penis, and the masters braid them, and the extenders form them;
puis cope au spatumile trenchant large dou traver endroit les vasselz, tant qu’il soient descovert,	then cut with a sharp trowel wide through the vessels, until they are uncovered,
et puis escorche de chescune part, si com nos avons dit en l’estraction des arteres qui sont en temples;	and then peel from each side, as we have said in the extraction of the arteries which are in the temples;
puis i fiche une aguille ou il ait .i. fil double, et le lie au premier leu ou li vis est venue, et le lie derechief a l’autre chief;	Then insert a needle where there is one double thread, and tie it at the first place where the vein came, and tie it straight to the other end;
puis les cope em mileu droitement, selonc la longesce dou cors, et en trai les moistors corrumpues;	then the blade is placed in the middle straightly, according to the length of the body, and in treating the corrupted moisture
puis cure la plaie si com les autres ou on enjanre bowe, si que aucun vassel chiecent que norrissent l’un des coions;	then heal the wound as with the others where one avoids bowe, so that no vessel is punctured that nourishes one of the corners;
car par ceu n’i vient point de mal, et se a toz les vasselz vient vis, si covient traire les coions a tout les vasselz;	for by these no harm comes, and to all vessels comes life, so it is necessary to treat the corners of all vessels;
si que li oes ne perde son norrissement por l’incision des vasselz, et sechent et ne se puient aidier.	so that the flesh does not lose its nourishment through the incision of the vessels, and dries up and cannot be helped.
de la routure dou syfac	of the rupture of the thigh
Li avenemens de ceste ramice si est par la section que vient ou syfac, ou l’estension sus le ventre en la partie des angres, por coi li intestine dessendent de celle routure a l’un des coions;	The events of this malady are by the section that comes to the thigh, or the extension upon the belly in the part of the groin, for which reason the intestines descend from that rupture to one of the groins.
et ceste routure est ou dou syfac, ou de l’estension de li, et vienent ces .ij. manieres de mout de causes: ou de percussion, ou de saut, ou de braire, ou de levement de grief faix, et par semblans choses;	And this rupture is in the thigh or from the extension of it, and these 2 manners of wounds come from many causes: either by percussion, or jumping, or wrestling, or lifting a heavy load, and similar things.
et li signes quant c’est de l’estension dou syfac, si est qu’il avient poc et poc, en lonc tens, et ne vient mie soudainnement;	And the signs when it is an extension of the thigh, are that it happens in little stages over a long time and does not come suddenly;
et est li apostemes igalz jusque vers le parfont, por ceu que li syfac apresse l’intestine.	and is the abscess even up to the root, because the sifac presses upon the intestine.
Et li signes est quant c’est de la section dou syfac, qu’elle fait venir a l’encomencement dolor soudaine, et est li apostemes divers apparans, desoz le cuir pres, et c’est por l’issue de l’intestine et le cors au defuer dou syfac.	And the signs are when it is of the section of the sifac, that it brings sudden pain at the beginning, and is the abscess various appearances, under the skin near, and this for the issue of the intestine and the body to the outside of the sifac.
Et aucune fois dessent li cirbes avec l’intestine, et est retenus enqui, et fait grant dolor soffrir au malaide, meismement quant il est pressez.	And at times they send the intestines with the sifac, and are retained within, and causes great pain to suffer the patient, even when it is pressed.
Et en ces cures de fer a paor, por coi il s’en covient eschuir.	And in these cures of iron there is fear, so one must avoid them.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que tu comande ou malaide qu’il ramoine l’intestine a sa main au dedens en la plaie, s’il i puet rentreir;	And the manner of the work is that you command the patient to put the intestine into his hand within the wound, if he can enter it.
puis soit sovinez sus son col. entre tes mains, et lieve les cuixes;	Then either support it on his neck between your hands, and raise the hips.
puis estent le keur au desus, et cope tout le cuir des coions dou lonc;	Then extend the core upwards, and cut all the skin of the scrotum along its length;
puis boute dedens les leivres de la taille uncines selonc ceu que tu en as mestier por ovrir la plaie, et soit telz que li oes em puist issir;	Then put inside the folds of the waist a pair of needles according to what you need to open the wound, and such that the entrails can issue forth;
puis escorche lou syfac que est desoz lou cuir des coions, tant que li blans syfac dur soit descovers de toutes pars;	Then scrape the substance that is under the skin of the groin, until the white substance hard be uncovered from all sides.
puis boute ton doi indice en ceu qui enseut lou coion, en ceu qui est entre lou blanc syfac qui est desoz lou cuir de l’uef, et entre lou secont syfac,	Then put your index finger into that which follows the groin, in that which is between the white substance which is under the skin of the buttock, and between the second substance.
et depart ceu qui est derrier l’uef, et entre lou secont syfac; et pues muef a la main destre dedens lou keur des coions, et estent lou blanc syfac en haut a ta main senestre, et lieve l’uef a tout lou syfac devers la taille;	And depart that which is behind the buttock, and between the second substance; and then move with your right hand into the heart of the groin, and keep the white substance on top in your left hand, and lift the buttock over all the substance towards the waist.
et comande au ministre qu’il estende l’uef en haut, et deslie ceu qui est aers derrier le liement;	And command to the minister that he extend the buttock upwards, and loosen that which is above behind the ligament.
et quier a tes dois s’il a point de l’intestine envoloupeit ou blanc syfac dur, et se tu en trueves aucune chose, si le boute au ventre desoz;	And if there is any piece of the intestine enveloped or white syfac hard, and if you find none of these things, then put it in the belly below;
puis pren une aguille ou il ait .i. gros fil fait de .x. filz, et la boute en la derriere partie dou syfac, qui est aprés lou cuir des coions; aprés la taille, puis cope les chiés qui apperent des filz, tant qu’il i ait .iiij. filz;	Then take a needle or it has one thick thread made of ten threads, and put it in the back part of the syfac, which is after the skin of the buttocks; after the waist, then cut the hairs that appear from the threads, until there are four threads;
puis les assemble l’un sus l’autre en maniere de croix, et en lie lou syfac, dont nos avons dit qui est desoz lou cuir des coions, d’un fort liien de .ij. pars;	Then assemble them one above the other in the manner of a cross, and bind the syfac, which we have said is below the skin of the buttocks, with a strong band of two parts;
puis envoloupe les chiés des filz, et les lie forment de .ij. pars, si que nuls des vasselz que les norrissent ne puissent entrer en ous, que aposteme chaus n’i viegne;	Then envelop the hairs of the threads, and bind them forming two parts, so that none of the vessels that nourish them can enter in, except for an abscess if it comes;
et met derechief le liien selonc le premier liien lonc .ij. dois de celui, et aprés ces .ij. liiens laisse dou syfac qui est desoz lou keur des coions le grant d’un doi;	and set straight the linen according to the first linen long two fingers of that one, and after these two linens leave about the space which is below the heart of the loins the width of a finger;
et aprés tout l’autre selonc la rondesce que li euf porte; puis cope en la partie qui est desoz le cuir des coions, tant qui li sans corre, et li bowe, si com nos avons dit ci devant;	and after all the other according to the roundness that the egg bears; then cut in the part which is below the skin of the loins, as much as the sinew, and the bone, as we have said before;
puis amenistre laine moillie en oile, et met em plaies, et i amenistre le liien que nos avons dit.	then administer wool moistened in oil, and put it into the wounds, and put in the linen that we have said.
Et aucune fois est cauterizez li blans syfac que nos avons dit, aprés l’incision, par doutance de decorrement de sanc.	And at no time is the white space that we have said cauterized after the incision, out of fear of bleeding.
Car ce avient maintes fois, et laisse le liien tant qu’il chiece per lui; et s’il tarde au cheoir, si soit arosez d’aigue chaude, et met sus ceu que nos avons dit, tant qu’il chiece;	For this happens many times, and let the thread as long as it falls through; and if it delays at falling, be raised with hot water, and put on what we have said, until it falls;
puis cure la plaie d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	then cure the wound with other cures, until it is perfectly healed.
de hernie carnouse	of fleshy hernia
En ceste ramice ne vis je onques nul qui osast faire la cure par fer.	In this branch I have never seen anyone who dared to make the cure with iron.
Et li ancien dirent qu’ele est faite si com li ramice qui est ensamble la vis, en teil maniere que tu lie les vasselz, aprés la taille sus ous legierement au desoz;	And the ancients said that it is made like the root which is assembled with the wood, in such a manner that you tie the vessels after the cut above or slightly below;
puis cope em mi, et cure l’aposteme de ceu qui oevre, tant que li vasselz chient; et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	then cut it in two, and cure the abscess of those who work on it, as long as the vessels bleed; and cure it as we have said, until it is healed.
Aucune fois vient routure ens angres, si com nos avons dit, et apert li leus; et ne dessent nulz des intestines as coions, et s’il en i dessent, c’est poc, et repaire toutes houres;	Sometimes a rupture comes in the bowels, as we have said, and open them; and do not pull any of the intestines out to the sides, and if any are pulled out, it is bad, and repair them immediately;
et toutevoie s’il demoure trop en cest point, si croit li plaie ou syphac, tant que li intestine dessent;	and nonetheless if they remain too long in this spot, the wound or ulcer grows, as long as the intestines are pulled out;
et ceu avient par l’estension dou syfac qui est as angres, si com nos avons dit, car il est estendus, puis est mollifiez et enflez li leus et apert;	and this happens by the extension of the sinew which is at the angles, as we have said, for it is extended, then softened and swollen its joints and open;
et li cure si est par cautere, si com nos avons devant dit; et aucune fois est curee par fer en ceste maniere:	and the cure of this is by cautery, as we have said before; and sometimes it is cured by iron in this manner:
et est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos entre tes mains, puis cope le leu de la routure enfleit dou large selonc la quantiteit de .iij. dois;	and it is that the patient lies soundly on his back between your hands, then cut the place of the rupture inflated by a breadth according to the quantity of three fingers;
et puis estrai le syfac qui est desoz le cuir que l’ensuet, puis pren lou rait et lou met sor le leu apparant dou syfac;	and then extract the sinew which is below the skin that the following, then take the root and place it on the apparent place of the sinew;
et lou presse au parfont dou ventre, puis cout les .ij. leus apparans dou syfac sus lou chief dou rait, et cout l’un et l’autre;	And he presses at the front of the belly, then counts two apparent limbs of the siphon upon the head of the waist, and counts one and the other.
puis estrai le chief dou rait, et ne coper point dou syfac ne n’estendre l’uef n’autre chose, si com je t’ai fait savoir en la cure de la ramice des intestines;	Then he removes the head of the waist, and does not cover the siphon nor extend any other thing, as I have made known to you in the cure of the intestine's root.
puis le cure par la cure des plaies. Et quant tu copes les filz, si le mundefie et cure la plaie, tant qu’elle soit sanee.	Then he cures by the cure of wounds. And when you cover the filaments, if it is purified and heals the wound, as long as it is healed.
Li syfac est constrains, et n’a point d’apparance en la routure, et li cauteres est muedres en cest leu, et plus prochiens a salut.	The siphon is constricted, and has no appearance in the rupture, and the cautery is moved in this place, and closer to salvation.
de l’amollissement dou cuir des coions	of the softening of the skin of the testicles
Maintes fois est amollis li cuirs des coions en aucuns homes, por ceu que les chars que sont dedens sont mollifiees, et est lait a veoir; et est mestier, quant on le vuet curer, c’on faice gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li cope le cuir qui est mollifiez sus le cuir natureil; puis assemble les .ij. levres a une costure, et se tu vues, cout premier la superfluiteit dou cuir mollifiiez a .iij. costures ou .iiij. fermement; puis cope entre les costures, et lou cure si com les autres plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez, et chient li fil.	Many times the skin of the testicles is softened in some men, because the sacs that are inside them are softened, and it is seen; and it is necessary, when one wants to heal it, that one make the patient lie on his back, and one cut the skin which is softened on the natural skin; then assemble the two lips with a seam, and if you see, sew first the superfluity of the softened skin with three or four stitches firmly; then cut between the stitches, and treat the wound as other wounds, until it is healed, and remove the thread.
dou chastrement	of the strapping
Saiches que chastremens est escomeniez en nostre loi, et por ceu il me plairoit que je n’en parlasse mie en cest livre; et n’est necessaires fuer que por .ij. manieres: dont l’une est que li mires en saiche respondre quant on li demandera, et en saiche la cure; et li autre, por ceu que nos avons sovent mestier de chastrement d’aucunes bestes por nos aidier, si com de bouc et de mouton et de chait et d’autres bestes. Je dis donques que chastremens est fais selonc .ij. manieres: ou par atraction, ou par fendure.  En celle que nos faisons par attraction, faisons nos seoir la beste en aigue chaude, tant que li coion soient mollifiez et pendant; puis les preing a ta main, tant qu’il soient remis et que tu ne les sentes plus.  Du chastrement de taille: covient que tu teignes la beste, et li presse le cuir des coions a ta main senestre, puis lie le suspensoire, et cope sus chescun oef a .i. cop, quant tu les avras bien escorchiez; et i laisse aucun poc dou syfac et lou subtil syfac qui est sor les vasselz; et ceste maniere de chastrement est muedre que cele qui est faite par attraction, por ceu que a l’atraction demoure par aventure aucune chose des coions, par coi li beste desire luxure; puis cure la plaie tant qu’ele soit sanee.	Know that strapping is common in our law, and for that reason I would like not to speak of it much in this book; and it is necessary only for two manners: one of which is that the wise respond when asked, and know the cure; and the other because we often need strapping of some animals to aid us, such as goats and sheep and calves and other beasts. I say therefore that strapping is done in two ways: either by attraction, or by cutting.  In that which we do by attraction, we make our sit the beast in hot water, until the testicles are softened and pliable; then take them in your hand, as long as they are put back and you no longer feel them.  As for strapping the tail: it is necessary to hold the beast, and press the skin of the testicles with your left hand, then tie the suspensory, and cut on each side one cut, when you have well scratched them; and leave no prick of the sheath and the fine sheath that is on the vessels; and this manner of strapping is more mature than that which is done by attraction, because in attraction remains perhaps some thing from the testicles, by which the beast desires lust; then cure the wound until it is healed.
des hermofrodites	Of the hermaphrodites
