Hermofrodie est selonc .ij. manieres as homes: l’une si est que entre les .ij. coions apert ausi com li figure de la nature d’une femme, ou il ait poil, et aucunes fois en cort li urine.  Et li autre maniere si est en femmes, et ait sus lou poignil ausi com une verge et .ij. coions.  Et li cure de l’ome et de la fame si est que tu copes les chars ajostees toutes, et les cure si com autres plaies; en la seconde maniere, des homes dont li urine saut par lou cuir des coions, si n’a point de cure.	Hermaphrodite is according to .ij. manners as men: one if it is that between the .ij.  parts appears also as the figure of nature of a woman, or it has hair, and sometimes in short the urine. And the other manner is in women, and has on the pubis also like a penis and .ij. parts. And the cure of the man and the woman is that you cauterize the joined parts all, and the cure them as other wounds; in the second manner, of men whose urine jumps out by the skin of the parts, there is no cure.
de la tentigene	Of the tenting
Tentigene est une chars ajostee sus la partie natureil, tant qu’elle est trop laide a veoir; et aucunes femmes l’ont ausi grant com une main, et c’est li cure. Il covient que tu teignes la superfluiteit de la tentigene a ta main ou as oncines, et la cope legierement; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et a une autre char que naist a la bouche de la marris, et l’emple, et par aventure saut fuer, et est selonc la semblance d’une kowe, et por ceu l’apelerent li ancien «maladie kowee». Si covient que tu la copes, si com nos avons dit la tentigene, et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	Tenting is a joined part on the natural part, as long as it is too ugly to see; and some women have it as large as a hand, and that is the cure. It behooves you to shave off the superfluity of the tenting with your hand or tweezers, and lightly cauterize; and don’t go too deep, so that bleeding doesn’t come out, then cure the other cure until it is healed; and to another part that is born at the mouth of the anus, and the temple, and perhaps jumps out, and is according to the resemblance of a cow, and for this they called it by the ancients “cow disease”. If it behooves you to cauterize it, as we have said about the tenting, and cure it until it is healed.
de erratique	of wandering
Erratique si est quant li nature de la femme n’est mie percie, ou li pertus est petis; et est naturez par naissance, ou accidens par maladie que venue i est; ou c’est par char ajostee, ou dou syfac subtil ou espés, et est fais em parfont en la marris, ou en costez, ou desoz, ou que soit; et deffent le concevoir, et l’enfantement, et par aventure les flors a avoir; et li connoissance de ceu si est par le regart de la baile. Se li estoupemens est prochiens apparans, si quier a tes dois ou au rait. S’il est dou syfac subtil, et il est prochiens as .ij. leivres, si te haste, et la ront ensi: met tes .ij. dois indices ensamble, et li femme soit sus son dos, espandues ses jambes; puis estent les .ij. leivres forment, tant que li subtilz syfac soit rons, et soit overs li estoupemens; puis pren laine, et la moille en oile, et la met sus le leu, et gise li femme a home chescun jor, si qu’il ne puist souder. Et se li syfac est dur et espés, si covient que tu lou copes au spatumile semblant a foille de mirte. Se li estoupemens est de char nee, si la sospent a l’oncine et la cope; et aies les medicines estainchans sanc, si com acaice, sanc de dragon, encens, ensamble abun d’uef; puis amenistre une caine de plonc large, si que li plaie ne puisse souder; et ensi soit longement, et li amenistre une tente de lin sec; puis soit curez d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.  Et quant en la marris vient char nee, si la covient coper selonc ceste maniere, se ce n’est apostemes enchancrez. Car a l’aposteme enchancreit qui est en la marris, ne doit on touchier de feir.	of wandering if it is when the nature of the woman is not perceived, or the opening is small; and is natural by birth, or accident by illness that has come to it; or it is by a charm joined, or by subtle or thick syrup, and is made in the belly, or in the ribs, or below, or wherever it may be; and prevents conception, and pregnancy, and by chance the flowers to have; and the knowledge of these is by the gaze of the bailiff. If the obstruction is near apparent, if you wish to its two sides or to the back. If it is subtle syrup, and it is near two fingers' breadth, hasten, and do thus: put your two fingers together, and let the woman be on her back, legs spread; then being the two fingers formed, as long as the subtle syrup is round, and is over the obstruction; then take wool, and moisten it in oil, and put it on top, and lie the woman to home each day, so that he may not sweat. And if the syrup is hard and thick, it is necessary that you chop it with a spatula similar to myrtle leaf. If the obstruction is of flesh born, suspend it at the armpit and cut it; and have the medicines stanching blood, as acaice, dragon's blood, incense, together with an abundance of egg; then administer a poultice of broad plantain, so that the wound may not close; and thus for a long time, and administer a poultice of dry linen; then cure it with other cures until it is healed. And when in the belly comes flesh born, it is necessary to cut it according to this manner, unless it is inflamed abscesses. For the inflamed abscess that is in the belly, one must not touch to make.
des emorroides	of hemorrhoids
Emorroydes sont overtures de voines dont sans cort acostumeement, et quant les emorroydes sont vielles si devienent thelul; et nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’aus, et les signes, et je dirai ci celles qui resoivent curation. Je di que les emorroides et li thelul, quant il sont em parfont en la marris, et il n’aperent au sentir, si n’est mie li cure par fer. Cil qui sont a la bouche de la marris, c’on puet sentir, sont cil c’on puet curer. Il covient donques que tu mettes la femme en une maison froide, puis estent l’altelul as tenailles, et le cope en ses racines, puis poudre sus medicines restraignans sanc, si com acaice et sanc de dragon et encens, et semblans choses; puis boute ses piez a la paroit une houre, puis la met en aigue froide; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, si la fai seoir en une decoction de sumac et d’escorce de pomes grenates et de gales et de semblans choses, et puis pren farine d’orge, et la confis avec miel et aisil, et en fai .i. emplaustre sus son dos. Et se il estainche, c’est boin. Se ceu non, se li fai aerdre ventouses au dos et as mameles sens ferir; puis pren lainne, et la moille en jus de plantain ou en jus d’aglentier avec vin viel, et fai aerdre au leu.  Et quant li aposteme repose, si cure lou leu d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et celle qui est apelee «albathir» est rouge, et est semblans a .i. chief aspre, si le covient coper si com j’ai dit le thelul; et puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Hemorrhoids are openings of veins which without custom, and when hemorrhoids are old they become hardened; and we have said in the division the resemblances of those, and the signs, and I will say here those which resolve healing. I say that hemorrhoids and the hardening, when they are cut within the marsh, and they do not appear to the touch, unless it is cured by iron. Those who are at the mouth of the marsh, one can feel them, are those one can cure. It behooves therefore that you put the woman in a cold house, then after the hardening is taken with tongs, and the cope at its roots, then powder on medicines restraining blood, such as acaice and dragon's blood and incense, and similar things; then put her feet to the air for one hour, then put her in cold water; and if bleeding comes from it, then have her sit in a decoction of sumac and bark of pomegranates and galangal and similar things, and then take barley flour, and bind it with honey and oil, and make one plaster on her back. And if it hardens, it is good. If this does not, then have her apply leeches to the back and breasts without iron; then take linen, and soak it in plantain juice or in elderberry juice with old wine, and apply it there. And when the abscess rests, cure its place with ointment until it is healed; and the one called "albathir" is red, and resembles one sharp chief, so it must be cut as I said the hardening; and then cure it until it is healed.
des apostemes de la marris	Abscesses of the marsh
Maintes manieres d’aposteme vienent en la marris, si com chancre et aposteme pierous et herpes et estiomenes et fistules et emorroides et aposteme chaut, et plusors autres maladies que j’ai dit en la division. Il covient donques que je die en cest traitier l’aposteme chaut qui vient en la marris, qui n’est mie des apostemes que coillent bowe; et se tu vues savoir l’ovraige de fer, si regarde se li apostemes est agus en l’encomencement de sa venue, et plain de chalor et de fievre, et s’il devient rouge se tu le pues veoir.  Adonques ne te haster mie de percier, mais lou fais meurer tant que li dolor soit apaisie; et puis fai seoir lou malaide sus .i. siege, et ait .ij. petis sieges ou il se cline, et apoie sus son dos et assemble ses piez as parties defuer la jambe; et soient ses cuixes espandues, et mette ses braz desoz ses genous, et les lie bien d’un boin liien; puis succe li baille devers lou destre costeit, et i amenistre l’estrument dont on oevre la bouche de la marris, de coi ci aprés vient li forme; et covient que quant tu i vues amenistrer cest estrument, que tu fiches le rait premier ens por savoir la parfondeté de la marris, si que ceu qui entre ens de l’estrument n’i viegne plus em parfont qu’il ne doit, et qu’il ne blece la malaide; et se li estrumens est plus grans, si covient covrir la parfondesce de la marris de drapelz, si que li estrumens ne li grieve; et covient qu’il mette le cornet de l’estrument au desus, et qu’il teigne l’estrument. Et quant li apostemes apert, et on lou fent a la main mol, si le covient coper au chief, au spatumile leit; et quant li bowe est vuidie, si covient que tu mettes en la plaie tentes moillies en oile roset, ou en oile vert sec; et met la tente fuer de la plaie au parfont de la marris, et met par defuer sus la marris et sus le poignil lainne nette moillie en aigue ou malves soient cuites; puis le cure aprés .ij. jors d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois leve on la marris et la plaie par clistere d’aigue et de miel, et puis d’aigue ou racines de lis et aristologe longe soient cuites; puis reveigne a l’oignement.  Et se li plaie est reponue en la marris, si covient que tu te gardes de cuire de fer, mais cure la si com nos avons dit en la division.	Many kinds of abscess come to the marsh, such as chancre and pus-filled abscesses, herpes, estiomenes, fistulas, hemorrhoids, and hot abscesses, and more diseases that I have said in the division. It behooves therefore that I say in this treatise the hot abscess that comes in the marsh, which is not of abscesses that boil; and if you want to know the work of iron, see if the abscess is agitated at the beginning of its arrival, and full of heat and fever, and if it becomes red you can see it.  Therefore do not hasten to pierce, but let him die until the pain is appeased; and then have the patient sit on one seat, and two small seats where he leans, and support his back and bring his legs together towards the outside of the leg; and be his thighs spread apart, and put his arms below his knees, and bind them well with a good linen cloth; then gently lift him to the right side, and administer the instrument with which one works the mouth of the marsh, from what comes after its form; and it is necessary that when you see to administer this instrument, that you first insert the point in order to know the depth of the marsh, so that what enters into the instrument does not go deeper than it should, and that it does not injure the patient; and if the instrument is larger, it is necessary to cover the depth of the marsh with cloths, so that the instrument does not hurt him; and it is necessary that he put the cone of the instrument on top, and hold the instrument. And when the abscess opens, and one helps it with a soft hand, it must be covered at the head, at the spatule; and when the boil is emptied, it is necessary to put into the wound tented moistened cloths in rose oil, or in green sec oil; and put the tent further from the wound to the bottom of the marsh, and put outside over the marsh and over the knife clean linen cloth moistened in water or malves are cooked; then cure it after two days of ointment coming before these, until it is healed; and at no time lift the marsh and the wound by clyster of water and honey, and then of water or roots of lilies and long aristolochia that are cooked; then return to the ointment. And if the wound is renewed in the marsh, it is necessary that you guard against cooking iron, but cure it as we have said in the division.
de l’enfantement	of childbirth
Mestier est premier a la baile qu’elle conoisse la figure de l’enfantement natureil, et li signes si est quant tu vois la femme apresser aval, et desire odorer l’ar: adonques se haste li enfes de fuer issir; adonc saiches que cil enfantemens est selonc la figure natureil, et est li issue soz son chief, et li secondine avec lui; et quant tu vois ces signes, si covient presser legierement son ventre, si que li enfes isse tost; car quant il dessent sus son chief, si ist li secondine avec lui, et est mondee li marris de ses superfluitez par bone mundification; et cist qui vient autrement ne vient mie naturelment. Car il vient aucune fois sus ses piez, et vient fuer li cors ou li chiés, et les mains, ou il vient sus son ventre, ou sovin, et est convertis par aventure sor son col, et par autres figures malvaises; si est mestier a la baile qu’elle soit saige et subtilz en ces choses, et se warse d’error et de decevement, et je vos mostrerai toutes les figures coment on li doit aidier.	It is the midwife's first duty to know the figure of natural childbirth, and the signs of it are when you see the woman press her abdomen and desire to smell the air: then she hastens for the child to come out; therefore you know that this birth is according to nature, and it is the head first, and the second after him; and when you see these signs, you must gently press her belly so that the child comes quickly; because when it comes out on its head, the second comes after it, and the world is cleansed of its superfluities by good purification; and this which comes otherwise does not come naturally.
Se li enfes vient sus son chief par issue natureil, et li femme enfante griement, et li vertus de li est foible, si la fai seoir sus une selle, ou les femmes la tienent; et arose sa nature d’oile ou fenugreic soit cuit, et puis boute li baile entre ses dois le petit spatumile dont ci est li forme:	If the child comes out on its head by natural birth, and the woman is giving birth loudly, and her strength is weak, then have her sit on a saddle, or the women hold her; and anoint her nature with oil or fenugreek that is cooked, and then put the midwife between her thighs the little spatula whose form is here:
et fende la secondine, et cope a son ungle tant que li moistors qui est ens corre fuers; et preint lou ventre de la femme tant que li enfes dessende, et s’il ne dessent, si covient clisterizer la femme de muscillaige de fenugrec avec oile de sisament; puis la fai preindre et esternuer de condisi, et tien sa bouche et son neis une houre: si istra maintenant l’enfes.Et se les .ij. mains issent fuer, si covient que tu les ramoinne legierement poc et poc; et s’elles n’i puent entrer, si met la femme sus .i. siege, et li lieve les piés en haut; puis deboute le siege sus terre, et teigne on la femme, qu’elle ne chiece au deboutement; et se li mains n’i puet entrer, et li enfes muert, si li cope les mains au couteil qui est ci devant mis, et estrai l’enfant, et ramoine igalment.	and cut the perineum, and chop at its nail until the moisture that is inside is gone; and grasp the belly of the woman as long as the child descends, and if it does not descend, then it is necessary to cleanse the woman with fenugreek mullein with sesame oil; then make her inhale and sneeze from condyment, and hold her mouth and nose for an hour: thus now the child will be delivered. And if the two hands come out, then you must gently reset them bit by bit; and if they cannot enter, then put the woman on one seat, and raise her feet up; then turn over the seat to the ground, and hold the woman so that she does not fall during the turning over; and if the hands cannot enter, and the child dies, then chop the hands at the knife which is before put, and extract the child, and reset them equally.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses piez	of the delivery of the child on its feet
Quant li enfes vient sus ses piez, si lou covient bouter en haut;	When the child comes on its feet, then it is necessary to push upwards;
et puis le torne poc et poc, tant qu’il soit igalz;	And then turn it back and forth, until it is even.
puis preigne .i. des piez et l’estende poc et poc.	Then prick one of the feet and extend it back and forth.
Cant il saut jusc’as cuixes, si la comande a preindre, et la fai esternuer de condisi;	Let him jump as far as his hips, if he is commanded to take it, and make him sneeze from the conditions.
si saut fuer, se Deus vuet.	If he jumps, God willing.
Et s’il n’ist fuer si com nos avons dit, si le torne poc et poc, tant qu’il soit selonc la figure natureil.	And if it is not as we have said, then turn it back and forth, until it is according to the natural figure.
Car adonques ist il legierement.	For therefore it is easily done.
Et s’il ne vient fuer si com nos avons dit, si pren muscillaige de altee, et oile de sisament, et gomme fondue, et broie tout en .i. mortier;	And if it does not come out as we have said, then take a mixture of alum, and sesame oil, and melted gum, and grind all in one mortar;
et met sus la nature de la femme dedens et defuer cest oignement,	and put upon the nature of the woman inside and outside this ointment,
puis la fai seoir en aigue tede jusque desoz les costelz;	Then make him sit straight upright until below the ribs;
et quant elle est moillifie desoz, se li fai .i. coliere de mirre, et li met desoz, et li laisse une houre;	and when it is softened below, give him one coil of myrrh, and place it below, and leave it for an hour;
puis la fai seoir sus .i. siege, puis la fai esternuer et estraint sa bouche et son neis, et li preint le ventre legierement, car li enfes saut maintenant.	then make him sit on one seat, then make him sneeze and restrain his mouth and nose, and take his belly lightly, for the child now leaps.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses genous	from the issue of the child on his knees
Quant li enfes vient en ceste forme, si i mette li baile ses mains poc et poc;	When the child comes in this form, he puts his hands hand over hand.
puis soit sovinee sus son col, et li pendent li piez aval, et soit gisans sor .i. lit;	then either support him on his neck, and hang his feet down, and let him lie on a bed;
et plie ses mains poc et poc, et puis li preint les mains sus lou ventre, et li oste les cussins desoz, tant qu’elle soit appareillie aval;	and fold his hands hand over hand, and then take his hands onto his belly, and remove the cushions from beneath him, until it is ready to go down;
et se li enfes ne saut, si pren ses piez et li muef forment, puis li muef lou ventre amont, puis i boute tes mains;	and if the child does not jump, take his feet and move them forcefully, then move his belly upwards, then push with your hands;
et ewe l’enfant poc et poc; et comande a la femme qu’elle se preigne tant que li enfes isse.	and poke the child here and there; and instruct the woman to prepare herself while the child is being born.
de l’issue de l’enfant qui vient dou large une main pendant	of the issue of the child who comes out with one hand wide open
I covient engignier a ramener la main:	it is necessary to contrive to bring back the hand:
s’on ne la puet ramener, si fai lever la femme, et aler;	if one cannot bring it back, then make the woman get up and leave;
s’elle ne puet aler, si la fai gesir sus .i. lit, et li deboute les jambes forment;	If she cannot walk, put her on a bed of straw and straighten her legs.
puis amenistre lou muscillaige que j’ai conteit;	Then administer the poultice that I have recounted.
et s’elle n’enfante, si la fai seoir sus .i. siege, puis estudie au rameneir la main;	And if she does not give birth, put her on a seat, then study to bring back the hand.
et ewe l’enfant selonc la figure natureil, et la fai esternuer, et li comande qu’elle se preigne tant que li enfes isse fuer.	And guide the child according to its natural form, and make her sneeze, and command her to strain until the child comes out.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus son col, et ait espandues ses mains, et sa faice tornee devers lou dos sa mere	of the issue of the child on its neck, and has spread its hands, and its face turned towards the back of its mother
I covient que li baile teigne sa main, puis le torne poc et poc, et l’ewe legierement;	It is proper that the midwife holds his hand, then turns it little by little, and the egg gently.
et quant il est igalz, si met sus la nature muscillaige de altee et oile, si com nos avons dit, puis li comande qu’elle se mueve poc et poc;	and when it is equal, it puts on the soft and oily cloth of the altar as we have said, then commands her to move little by little.
et quant tu avras ce fait, si la fai seoir sus .i. siege, et li comande k’elle se preigne; et la fai esternuer.	And when you have done this, make her sit on one seat and command her to sneeze; and let her sneeze.
de ceste meisme maniere a tout la secondine	in this same manner to all the secondine
Quant il vient fuer en ceste maniere a tout la secondine, si cope la secondine a ton ungle, tant que li moistors soit vuidie;	When it comes to be done in this manner to all the secondine, so cut the secondine at your fingernail, until the moisture is gone.
et se li enfes pent sus sa faice et sus son col, si la cope des la boude, qu’elle ne soit retenue, et muere li enfes;	and if the child can sit on its face and neck, so cut from the bud, that it is not held back, and die the child.
puis boute l’enfant dedens, tant que tu l’aies mis si com il covient, et comande a la femme qu’elle se preigne aucune fois:	then put the child inside, until you have placed it as is fitting, and command the woman that she refrain at all times.
adonques si istra legierement.	therefore it must be set gently.
de l’issue des gemelz	of the issue of twins
Saiches que gemeil naissent maintes fois, et aucune fois en naissent .iij. ou .iiij.; et ceu n’est mie estrainge chose, et poc avient.	Know that twins are born many times, and sometimes three or four; and this is not a strange thing, and it happens often.
Dui sont estrainge chose, et ne vivent mie, se poc nom;	Two are a strange thing, and they do not live, if at all.
je sai ceu, qu’il soient multipliiet, et sont desevrez par lou syfac qui les devise, qui est liiez a la boude;	I know these, that they are multiplied, and are loosened by the faculty which divides them, which is joined to the body.
et aucune fois issent ausi naturelment com uns tous sous, si com nos avons dit.	And at times they issue as naturally as one all underneath, as we have said.
Et s’il issent griement, si la cure si com nos avons dit, et soit li baile subtilz, et faice tost et legierement ceu qu’elle fait;	And if they issue violently, then the cure as we have said, and let the discharge be subtle, and do quickly and lightly what it does;
et faice ensi com il vaut mues a salut.	and thus do as it is worthy of healing.
de plusors enfans	of many children
Aucune fois sont formez en la marris .i. ou .ij. ou .iij. ou .iiij. ou .v. ou .vj. ou .vij., ou plusors jusc’a .xv., et sont tout formeit en forme d’enfant par le mesurement dou saige glorious,	Never are formed in the marsh i. or ii. or iii. or iv. or v. or vi. or vii., or more until xv., and they are all formed in the shape of a child by the measurement of his glorious sage,
et couvient que li baile saiche tout ceu, car par aventure semblans chose li avient;	and it is necessary that the bailiff knows all this, because by chance seeming things happen to him;
si faice selonc ceu qu’il covient.	so it is done according to what is fitting.
de l’enfant mort	of the dead child
Quant tu cures la femme de l’enfant mort ou ventre, si com j’ai dit en la division, et il ne vient fuers, et tu es constrains d’ovraige de mains;	When you cure the woman of the dead child or belly, as I said in the division, and it does not come out, and you are constrained to work with your hands;
si covient que tu saiches se li femme est de saine vertut, et n’ait accident ou elle ait paor de mort;	it is necessary that you know if the woman is of sound virtue, and has no accident or she has fear of death;
si covient que li femme soit sovinee sus son dos, et soit ses chiés enclins aval, et les jambes levees;	it is necessary that the woman be laid on her back, and her hips inclined downward, and her legs raised;
et li ministre la teigne de .ij. pars, ou elle soit liie au lit si qu’elle ne soit traite au dessendement de l’enfant;	And the minister lays the band of two parts, where it is tied to the bed so that it does not touch the descent of the child;
puis frotez la bouche de la marris d’oiles moistes avec muscillaige de altee et de fenugrec et semence de lin, puis oigne li baile ses mains de ces oiles et de ces muscillaiges;	Then rub the mouth of the mare with moist oils with mucus of althea and fenugreek and flax seed, then anoint the bale its hands with these oils and these mucus.
puis les boute en la marris legierement, puis quiere .i. leu ou elle boute les oncines que soient covenaubles a ceu,	Then put it in the mare lightly, then take one (measure) where she puts the oats that be suitable to those
et pren warde se li enfes est apparilliez qu’il dessende sus son chief;	And take heed if the child is appeared that it descends upon its head;
si fiche les oncines en ses eulz ou en son col ou en sa bouche ou en som palais ou desoz la barbe ou en la forcele ou pres des costez,	if he sets the pins in his eyes or in his neck or in his mouth or in his palate or under the beard or in the throat or near the ribs
et se li dessendemens est sus piez, se li fiche ou poignil et as costes moienes;	and if the descent is on feet, he sets it or pierces and at the sides;
et covient qu’il teigne l’oncine a sa main destre, et mette la corbeure entre ses dois de la senestre main, et li boute a tout sa main legierement, et fiche l’oncine en aucun de ces leus que nos avons dit, tant qu’il viegne a la chose vuide;	and it is necessary that he hold the pin in his right hand, and place the curve between his two fingers of the left hand, and he thrusts it with all his hand lightly, and sets the pin into any of these places that we have said, until it comes to the empty thing;
et c’est li forme de l’oncine:	and this is the form of the pin:
puis fiche encontre .i. autre oncine, ou le tier se tu en as mestier, si que li estractions soit igalz;	Then place against one another, or the third one if you need it, so that the extractions are equal
et puis l’estent igalment en movant d’une part et d’autre, por mues issir, et soit li oncines dentez por mues tenir, si com ci est li forme:	And then make them equal by moving from one side to the other, so that they may move easily, and let the edges of the bones be toothed so that they may hold, as it is in this form.
Et s’il en demoure une partie, si oigne li baile aucuns de ses dois d’oile, et les boute en celle partie, et traie l’autre partie;	And if a part remains, then oil the groin of some of its joints with oil and put it in that part, and pull the other part.
et s’il en i demoure point, si met cest oncine ou plus haut leu, et fai ceu tant qu’il s’en isse tout fuers.	And if none remain, then put this bone or higher up its place and do this until it all moves out.
Et se l’une mains vient devant l’autre, et il ne puet ramener por l’estreignement,	And if one hand comes before the other, and it cannot be brought back for constriction,
si covient que tu envoloupes sus .i. drapeil, tant qu’il isse tote;	then it is necessary that you envelop it in a cloth, until it is whole;
puis la cope en la jointure de la plante ou au coute, et ensi covient que tu faices en l’autre main, et as .ij. piés.	then wrap the bandage at the joint of the wrist or elbow, and in this way you should do for the other hand, and at two feet.
Et se li chiés de l’enfant est gros et il est estrois en l’issue, ou il ait ou chief aigue assemblee,	And if the child's shoulder is swollen and it is sticking out, or it has a sharp peak assembled,
si covient que tu boute le spatumile espinous entre tes dois, et fent le chief et estrai l’aigue;	if it is necessary that you put the pointed spatula between your two [parts], and make the head and extract the water.
ou tu la ront a l’estrument qui est apelez «almidach», de coi li forme vient avec les estrumens ou chapistre qui est aprés cestui;	or you take it to the instrument which is called "almidach," because its form comes with the instruments or chapter which is after this one.
et ensi meisme faice se li enfes a grant chief naturelment;	and in the same way, make it if the child has a large natural head;
et puis traie fuer les osses as tenailles,	and then draw out the bones with the forceps,
et se li chiés saut fuer et il estraint a la forcele, si soit fendus, tant que li moistors qui est ou pis issue fuer;	and if the head jumps out and is strained with force, it may be split, as long as the moisture that is or worse has come out.
et s’elle ne puet issir, si le cope par pieces au mues que tu pues;	and if it cannot be brought back in, cut it into pieces as much as you can.
et s’il est enflez au ventre ou desoz les costez, si covient que tu lou perces tant que li moistors corre.	and if it is swollen in the belly or below the ribs, then it is necessary that you pierce it until the moisture runs out.
Et se li enfes est sus ses piez, si est li attraction legiere, et li adrecemens a la bouche de la marris est legier.	And if the child is on its feet, the traction is light, and the pressure at the mouth of the birth canal is slight.
Et s’il est estrois au ventre ou au pis, si couvient que tu l’estraies a .i. drapeil envoloupeit sus la main;	And if it is outside in the belly or at the breast, then you should extract it with i.e., wrapped cloth placed above the hand;
et fent le ventre ou le pis, tant que li moistors qui i est corre;	and make the belly or breast, as long as the moisture that is there dries;
et se li autre membre sont osteit, et li chiez demoure,	and if the other members are removed, and the head remains,
si boute li baile sa main em parfont de la marris, et le traie jusc’a la bouche de la marris;	then bring the patient's hand with force out of the marrow, and draw it up to the mouth of the marrow;
puis i boute .i. oncine ou ij., et le trai fuer;	then he puts one or two, and the treatment is done;
et se li bouche de la marris est retrecie por aposteme chaut qui i est venus, si n’i covient mie travillier,	and if the mouth of the abscess is narrowed by the heat that came to it, then it does not need to be worked on;
ains covient amenistrer choses moistes et grasses;	otherwise moist and fatty things must be administered;
et li amenistre emplaustres, et siece en aigue mollifians et amoistans.	and administer plasters, and soak in softening and moisturizing water.
Et se li enfes est sus son costeit, et tu le pues mettre igal, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit en l’enfant vif;	And if the child is on his side, and you can put him straight, so administer what we have said in a living child.
et s’on nen ait pooir, si lou trai fuer par pieces, et n’i laissier rien de la secondine.	and if one has no power over it, then the body be treated by pieces, and leave nothing of the secondary part.
Et quant tu avras ce fait, se li amenistre ceu que nos avons dit ens apostemes chaus que vienent en la marris;	And when you have done this, if it comes to an abscess as we have said in the matter of boils.
et se decorremens de sanc vient, si soit mise en aigue restraignant, et li amenistre autres cures.	And if blood flow comes out, then put it in a cool restraining bandage, and administer other treatments to it.
Et je vis une femme en cui ventre uns enfes avoit esteit mors, puis consut .i. autre sus celui, et refut mors li autres.	And I saw a woman in whose belly one child had been stillborn, then conceived another on top of that, and refused to miscarry the other.
Aprés lonc tens li vint uns apostemes en la boude, et enfla tant qu’il ovrit, et comensa a grant porreture.	After a long time it came upon her an abscess in the abdomen, and it swelled so much that it opened, and began to drain with great pus.
je fui apelez a la cure, et i pensai lonc tens, et ne pot soder li plaie.	I was called to heal her, and I thought long about it, and could not sew up the wound.
Je mis sus emplaustre de fort attraction, et en issit uns os, et aprés aucuns jors uns autres.	I put on a plaster of strong attraction, and out came one bone, and after some days another.
Je me mervillai mout, por ceu c’ou ventre n’a point d’os.	I was much amazed, for this reason because the belly has no bones.
Si pensai que c’estoit des os d’un enfant mort.	If I thought that it was the bones of a dead child.
Je quis la plaie, et en traï mains os, tant que li femme fut em miglior point;	I examined the wound, and in treating the bone, until the woman was in better condition.
et vesquit li femme lonc tens ensi, et issoit adés un poc de bowe dou leu;	and I visited the woman for a long time thus, and it appeared to her a little bit of bowel from its place;
et je n’ai recordeit cest chapistre fuer que por ceu que, quant li maistres trueve une estrainge chose, qu’il i saiche mettre aide.	and I have recorded this chapter only for those who when the masters find a strange thing, that he knows how to help.
dou ramener la marris a son leu	how to bring the bone back to its place
Ci aprés vient li forme dou pressor, a coi on ewe les livres; et a .ij. tornans as .ij. chiés des .ij. liiens.	Here comes the form of the forceps, which is written in books; and two turns at two handles of the two arms.
Toutevoie, li cornes soit plus subtilz dou restrictoire, et soit fais de ebene ou de bux;	However, the horns should be more subtle of the restrictor, and made of ebony or boxwood;
et soit li bouche dou fust .i. doi de large, et li marge des arbres .i. doit, et de lonc une palme et demi;	and let the mouth of the staff be i.e., two wide, and the margin of the trees i.e., one, and in length one palm and a half
et enmi les .ij. liemens soient dui ajostemens de cest meisme fust, qui soient fermeit en l’un et en l’autre, de demi palme de lonc ou un poc plus;	and in the middle of the two limbs be two joints of this same staff, which be joined together and in one another, of half a palm in length or one jot more;
et cist dui ajostement sont bouteit en la bouche de la marris por ovrir quant on torne les .ij. cornes.	and these two joints be put into the mouth of the marrow to open when one turns the two horns.
Une autre forme, a sa semblance plus subtilz et plus legiere, soit faite de fust de ebene ou de bux, selonc la semblance des tenailles;	Another form, similar in appearance but more subtle and lighter, be made of ebony or boxwood staff, according to the likeness of pliers;
et ait as .ij. chiés .ij. ajostemens, si com tu vois, d’une palme de lonc, et .ij. dois de large;	and have as two bones two joints, as you see, of one palm long, and two digits wide;
et quant tu vues ovrir la marris a tout l’estrument, si fai seoir la femme sor .i. lit, les piez pendant et les jambes overtes,	and when you see to open the mare with all the instrument, so make the woman sit on one bed, the feet hanging and the legs open,
puis boute les .ij. ajostemens ajostez ensamble en la marris, et tien le chief de l’estrument desoz entre ses cuixes;	then put the two joints together in the mare, and hold the head of the instrument below between her hips;
puis oevre ta main a tout l’estrument, si com tu as fait as tenailles igalment, selonc la quantiteit que tu vues ovrir la bouche de la marris, tant que li baile faice ceu qu’elle vuet.	then work your hand on the instrument, as you have done with the pliers equally, according to the quantity that you see to open the mouth of the mare, until the bail does what she wants.
Cist estrument sont tuit sormontez, et sont multiplies lor semblances; et quant li mires les ait apareilliez, tant est plus hastans li oevre, et plus haute as homes por lor quantiteit.	This instrument are all mounted, and they multiply their likenesses; and when the eyes have appeared them, so much is more hasten the work, and more high to men for their quantity.
Si ne despire mie l’estrument que tu ne l’aies apparelliet, car lor necessitez n’est mie escusauble.	If you do not despise the instrument that you have not appeared it, because their necessities are not excusable.
Quant li secondine est retenue a l’enfantement, si covient que tu comandes a la malaide qu’ele reteigne son alaine, et puis la fai esternuer de condisi, et li estraint tes mains a la bouche et au neis;	When the secondine is held during childbirth, it is necessary that you command the woman to retain her breath, and then make her sneeze with condiment, and restrain her hands at her mouth and nose.
et s’elle saut per ceu, bien est.	And if she jumps because of this, well it is.
Se ceu non, si prent .i. pot, et fai .i. pertus ou cuvercle, et i met herbes que puissent ovrir la bouche de la marris, si com calament, rue, anis, camomille, cassialigne et centoire;	If this does not work, then take one pot and make one hole or cover, and put in herbs that can open the mouth of the marsh, such as calamint, rue, anise, chamomile, cassegrain, and centaury.
toutes ces herbes, ou aucunes d’eles, soient cuites ou pot en aigue sus le feu; puis met une caine ou pertus dou pot, et l’autre chief en la bouche de la marris,	All these herbs, or none of them, be cooked or put in water on the fire; then put one end of a rope or pierced hole into the pot, and the other end in the mouth of the marsh.
et la teigne tant que li vapors viegne dedens la marris; puis la fai esternuer, si com nos avons dit.	And hold it until the vapors come from within the marsh; then let it be blown out, as we have said.
Si saut li secondine hastanment.	If the secondine is thrown hastily.
Et s’elle remaint aprés ceste cure, et n’ist mie fuer, si comande a la baile qu’ele moille sa main senestre en oile de sesement ou en muscillaige de altee, et puis la boute en la nature,	And if it remains after this cure and there is no fever, command the midwife that she soak her left hand in oil of sesame or in liniment of arnica, and then put it into the womb.
et quiere la secondine; et quant elle l’avra trovee, si la preigne et l’estende poc et poc droitement, si que li marris ne chiece a l’estraction;	and she feels for the second one; and when she has found it, she seizes it and stretches it slightly back and forth so that the cord does not break off during extraction.
mais la covient movoir legierement a destre et a senestre, et puis traie; si venra et se desaerdra.	but she must move it gently to the right and left, and then pull; it will come out and unwind itself.
Et se li bouche de la marris est jai estrecie, nos avons dit la cure d’esternuer, et de fumigation des herbes;	And if the baby's mouth is too narrow, we have said the cure of sneezing and fumigating with herbs;
et s’elle n’ist de tout ceu que nos avons dit, si garde que tu ne foloies au traire;	and if it is not of all that we have said, so guard that you do not apply to the breast.
mais il couvient que ceu qui est a la bouche de la marris, que tu le lies a la cuixe de la femme, puis la clisterize d’oignement tetrafarmaçon;	but it is necessary that he who is at the mouth of the marsh, you tie him to the hip of the woman, then clysterize him with ointment tetra-pharmakon.
si la porrira et remettra, et venra fuer; mais toutevoie, quant elle porrist si en vient male odor au stomac et au chief, et blece la malaide.	if she will bear and return, and come back for more; but nonetheless, when she bears it comes ill-smelling to the stomach and head, and pales the patient.
Si covient donques fumigations covenaubles a ceu: aucun des anciens ont esproveit fumigation de cresson et de figues seches.	So it is necessary then for fumigations fitting to those: none of the ancients have experienced fumigation of watercress and dried figs.
Li forme de l’estrument a coi on fumige la femme a la retenue des flors et de la secondine si est ceste:	The form of the instrument for which one fumes the woman to retain the flowers and the afterbirth is this:
Et est de voirre semblant a une caine, et met on le chief subtil en la nature, et les chiés larges sus le feu;	And it is of glass resembling a dog, and one puts the tip subtle into the vagina, and the handles wide over the fire;
et soit li fumigations sus les charbons, et la teigne tant qu’elle soit gastee, et rencomence une autre.	and let the fumigation be over the embers, and the reed as long as it is burnt, and begin another one.
de percier lou fondement	to examine the foundation
Maint enfant naissent qui n’ont mie le fondement perciet, ains l’ait estoupeit uns subtilz syfac:	Many children are born who do not have the foundation perceived, but it is stopped by subtle artifices.
si covient donques a la baile qu’ele perce celui syfac a son doit, et ne lou perce mie de spatumile agut, et garse le lacement qu’elle ne le touche;	It therefore becomes necessary for the midwife that she pierce that artifice to its proper place, and does not pierce it with a sharp spatula, and guards the wound so that she does not touch it.
puis met sus lainne moillie en vin et en oile, puis la cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	then put on linen moistened in wine and oil, then the ointment dressing until it is healed.
Et se tu doutes qu’il ne restoupe, si met ou pertus une caine de plonc, et li laisse mains jors, et soit ostee quant li enfes vuet aler en chambres.	And if you doubt that it will not return, then put in the opening a piece of cloth, and leave it there for many days, and remove it when the child wants to go into the chambers.
Et aucune fois vient cist estoupemens de soudement de plaie ou d’aposteme; si covient coper celui soudement: si soit curez, si com nos avons dit de la caine de plonc.	And sometimes this stoppage comes from a wound or abscess; so it is necessary to cover that stoppage; if it be cured, as we have said of the cautery of iron.
de la fistule dou fondement	of the fistula of the foundation
Fistules qui vienent desoz le fondement sont nodation, et groissor que vienent delez lou fondement defuer, ou en l’espaice des .ij. parties,	Fistulas that come from under the foundation are nodules, and larger than those that come from near the outer foundation, or in the space of two parts,
si a une fistule ou plusors; et quant celle nodation est anciene, si aoeuvre, et encort moistor awouse blainche ou subtilz bowe,	If there is one fistula or more; and when that nodule is old, it works, and still moisture brings white or subtle boils,
et aucune fois sont ces fistule persans; et sont conues par ceu qu’il en ist ou egestion ou ventositeit quant li malaide fait egestion, et par aventure en saut uns vers.	and sometimes these fistulas are closed; and they are known by those who have them or by evacuation or venting when the patient defecates, and by chance some go out.
Et si a fistules que percent jusc’a la vessie, et jusc’a la moitiet de la verge; et parvienent jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, et jusc’a nout de la kowe.	And if fistulas that pierce to the bladder, and to half the penis; and reach to the junction of the hip, and to outside of the buttock.
Et ensi conoist on la fistule persant au fondement, et ne mie persant:	And thus one knows the fistula piercing to the base, and not piercing.
et est que tu boutes ton doi indice ou fondement, et boute une aguille subtil d’arain ou de fer en la fistule quant il n’i a tortuositeit.	and it is that you put your thumb or base, and put a subtle needle of iron or steel into the fistula when there is no twistiness.
Et s’il ait tortuositeit, si i boute une tente de plonc subtil, ou .i. poil de cheval, tant que tu sentes la tente ou le poil a ton doit;	And if there is a tortuosity, put a tent of fine sponge or a horsehair thread, as long as you feel the tent or hair at your finger;
et se tu ne le sens, et il ne vient dou pertus egestion ne ventositeit ne ver, si com nos avons dit:	and if you do not feel it, and it does not come out through the opening nor with a puff nor wind, as we have said:
saiches qu’elle ne perce mie; si te haste dou curer.	know that it does not pierce; so hasten to cure it.
Et quant li fistule est persans jusc’a la vessie ou jusc’a conduit de l’urine, si en saut li urine, et ne puet soudeir par medicines.	And when the fistula is pierced up to the bladder or up to the urinary duct, then urine leaks out, and it cannot be stopped by medicine.
S’elle est percie jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, si est li tente venans jusc’au leu;	If it is pierced up to the junction of the hip, then the tendon comes to the place.
s’il n’i a tortuositeit et li invention de la dolor entor, si est qu’il en ist adés bowe, et n’i vaut medicine ne soudement par oignement;	If there is no twisting and the pain is only in the surrounding area, then it is that it has a bend here, and there is no use of medicine or ointment.
et en ces fistules persans n’a point de cure fuer que labor, et vaniteit des folz mires qui s’en entremettent.	And in these fistulas, there is no cure other than labor, and vanity of the foolish mirrors that interfere with them.
En celle qui n’est mie persans et n’est mie anciene, a esperance de saniteit par fer, si com j’ai esproveit,	In the one that is neither pierced nor old, there is hope of healing by iron, as I have experienced.
et est que li malaides gise entre tes mains sus son dos; et li lieve les jambes jusque sus ses cuixes, et ait ses cuixes enclinees a son ventre;	And it is that the patient lies between your hands on his back; and lift his legs up to his hips, and have his hips inclined to his belly.
puis boute une tente d’arain, ou de plonc s’il i a tortuositeit, tant que tu saiches ou li tente vient.	Then put a tent of iron, or of lead if there is tortuosity, as long as you know where the tent comes from.
Se li malaides la sent entor le fondement, si covient que tu i boutes ton doi indice,	If the patient feels it around the base, then it behooves you to put your index finger on it.
se sens adonques que li tente l’ait perciet; et soit descoverte ou tu sens entre ton doit le syfac ou la char, adonques saiches qu’elle est persans;	And if you then feel that the tent has pierced it; and whether uncovered or you feel between your finger the skin or flesh, then you know it is through.
si n’i travillier mie c’on ne la puet saner.	if one does not work on it, it cannot be cured.
On dist toutevoie c’on em puet bien saner aucuns, mais ce avient poc;	It is said however that one can cure some well, but this rarely happens.
et li aide c’on i fait, si est c’on eschaufe le cautere subtil selonc la largesce de la fistule, si com il est devant dit;	and the help one gives is if one carefully applies the subtle cautery according to the width of the fistula, as it was said before.
et le boute tout chaut en la fistule, tant qu’il viegne delez le fondement; et faice ceu .ij. fois ou .iij., tant que tu saiches que ces chars fautrees soient arses, qui sont semblant a une penne d’oiseil;	and he sears the whole thing hot into the fistula until it reaches to the base; and do this two or three times, as long as you know that these charred bits are burned, which look like an eye feather.
et puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre, tant que celle chars isse fuer, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char et soudant.	and then the cure of damp tents in butter, until that it shall be healed, and then the cure of ointment comforting flesh and welding.
S’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien. Se ceu, nom autrement ne puet estre sanez;	If it is thus healed, it is well. If not, it cannot otherwise be healed.
et se li tente entre, et ne perce jusc’au doit qui est ou fondement, et a entre ton doi et la tente une coverture espesse de char ou de syfac, et tu vois la fistule a ceu qui enseut la coverture dou keur;	and if the tent goes in and does not reach to the point that is the foundation, and there is between your door and the tent a thick covering of flesh or of fat, and you see the fistula at what follows the covering of the heart.
si le cope des l’encomencement de la fistule, et boute adés avant la tente, et pues le cautere aprés, tant qu’il viegne au chief de la tente;	If you cut at the beginning of the fistula, and push ahead before the tent, and then cauterize after, as long as it reaches to the head of the tent.
et sera delivré li tente, et cherra; puis mondefie celles chars fautrees que semblent une penne d’oisel, et n’en remaigne niant.	And will be delivered the tent, and will shrink; then bind those hairs that seem like a feather of an owl, and do not leave any.
Et si li sans te vaint, et cort entre toi et l’uevre, si le cauterize de feu ou de medicine ague.	And if the blood goes out and comes between you and the work, then cauterize it with fire or with medicine sharp.
Car li cauteres de feu assemble .ij. bones choses: c’est a savoir, l’arsure de ces chars ajostees, et l’esteinchement de sanc et la sechor de la moistor;	For the fire cautery brings together two good things: that is to say, the burning of those hairs joined together, and the stopping of blood and the drying of moisture;
puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre ou en choz broiez, tant que li leus giete bowe, et isse fuer li chars arse en la bowe;	Then the cure with tents moistened in butter or in a thing ground, as long as the wound lies raw, and if the hairs are burned in the raw;
puis cure la plaie des oignemens soudans enjanrans dure char, et sont les medicines seches.	then cure the wound of the eyelids inside by inflaming hard flesh, and are the medicines dry.
Car quant il est restoree, si est sanee et ne revient mie.	For when it is restored, it is healed and does not return.
Et se fistule vient jusc’a parfont dou fondement, et est esloigniez dou cors, se li boute ton doi ou fondement, et enquier ceu.	And if a fistula comes all the way up to the bottom of the foundation, and is removed from the body, it is sealed with that opening or foundation, and inquire there.
Se tu sens la tente, et entre .ij. est li toile ou li syfac ou chars, ou il est pres a percier, si n’i ait fuers que voie de fiance et d’esperance, par l’aministrement de l’une des .iii. manieres:	If you feel the tent and between 2 is the cloth or silk or leather where it is about to pierce through, if there is no other way except by faith and hope, then by administering one of these three ways:
ou tu le cauterizes si com nos avons dit, ou tu le cope jusc’a fons, ou se tu pues si i met tentes et cure si com premier;	or you cauterize it as we have said, or you cut it to the bottom, or if you can put dressings there and treat it as first;
et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que tu ne coper le tenement qui tient le fondement, et viegne li egestions par lai sens volenteit;	and do not go too deep in by cutting, that you do not cut the tissue which holds the foundation, and let the excrement come out by its own will;
puis le cure, si com nos avons dit;	then treat it, as we have said;
par aventure si sera sanez, ou tu esloigne celle coverture et la munde puis qu’elle est copee delez lou fondement, ou par tente ou par autre estrument apointé;	perhaps then it will be healed, or you remove that covering and the wound since it is cut near its foundation, or by dressing or by some other pointed instrument;
puis mondefie cele char fautree qui est en la plaie, tant com tu pues;	Then remove carefully the flesh which is in the wound, as much as you can.
puis estudie a restorer la plaie, et a demorer la fistule en la partie defuers le fondement: si iert plus legiere chose au malaide.	Then study to restore the wound, and keep the fistula in the part outside the foundation: so it is lighter for the patient.
Et aucune fois sont fistules selonc ceste maniere: et est quant tu boutes la tente en la fistule, et elle est ou costeit dou fondement delez lou cuir desus,	And sometimes fistulas are like this: and it is when you put the tent in the fistula, and it is or rests against the foundation near the skin above,
si pren une tente percie au chief selonc ceste forme:	if you take a tent pierced at the top according to this form:
Et i boute .i. fil tort en .ij., et boute la tente a tout le fil en la fistule tant qu’il soit au chief.	And it puts one twist thread into two, and puts the tent to all the thread in the fistula until it is at the head.
S’elle est persans en la marge dou fondement dedens, adonc estrai lou fil de celui pertus, ensi que tu boutes ton doi ou fondement;	If it is pierced at the edge of the bottom inside, then extract the thread from that which is pierced, in this way that you put your two or foundation.
et trai le chief dou fil, et assemble les .ij. chiés ensamble, et estraint l’un a l’autre, et le laisse .i. jor ou .ij.;	And treat the head of the thread, and assemble the two ends together, and hold one to another, and let it be for one or two days;
et le restraint aucune fois, tant que li filz cope ces chars que sont entre dous, et chiecent;	and restrain it no time, until the thread's chops that are between them close, and stick together;
puis cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit soudee et sanee.	Then cure the wound until it is healed and sound.
Se li fistule ne perce, si la fai percier en toutes les manieres que tu pues, s’ele n’est trop em parfont.	If the fistula does not pierce, then make it pierce in all the ways that you can, if it is not too deeply embedded.
Car il ne covient mie faire por le lacement coper si em parfont, et puis le cure, si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	For it does not behoove to do for the lacing cover if too deeply embedded, and then cure it, as we have said, until it is healed.
Li forme dou spatumile espinous dont on fent la fistule si est mout agus d’une, part et trenchans;	The form of the pointed spatula with which one makes the fistula is very useful, in one part and sharp;
et d’autre part non, por ceu c’on ne cope mie ceu c’on ne doit mie copeir, si com tu vois ci:	and on the other hand no, because one does not cut what one should not cut, as you see here:
des emorroydes	of hemorrhoids
Emorrydes sont selonc ij. manieres: ou elles sont dedens le fondement, ausi com grain de resin, et s’en i a petites et grans, et en cort adés sanc,	Hemorrhoids are according to two manners: or they are within the foundation, as much as grains of resin, and some are small and large, and in short they bleed.
et s’en i a une ou plusors, et sont defuer le fondement et au chief dou fondement; mais celles qui sont defuer si ont poc de moistor,	and there are one or more, and they are outside the foundation and at the top of the foundation; but those that are outside have little moisture,
et encort adés ou un poc d’aigue citrine ou un poc de sanc, et ont la color dou cors;	and then again it is added with a bit of citrine water or a little blood, and has the color of the body.
et li cure de ces qui les ont dedens le fondement, si est que tu comandes au malaide qu’il s’espreigne por aleir en chambres, tant que li fondemens li isse fuer, et c’aperent li filz;	and the treatment of those who have them in the foundation, if it is that you command the patient to stretch so as to go into chambers, until the foundations are gone and the threads appear.
si te haste, et le pent as tenailles, ou tu le tien a ton ungle, puis le cope en ses racines;	if you hurry, and can hold it with pliers, or you hold it with your finger, then cut it at its roots;
et se li uncine ne les pueent tenir por ses moistors, si les prent a .i. drapeil, ou a couton, ou d’une piece de chamelot;	and if the tweezers cannot hold them because of their moisture, then take them with one drapery, or with cotton, or with a piece of felt.
et les estrai a tes dois, puis les cope, et poudre desus aucunes chaudes poudres que soient en leu de cautere;	and restrain them to your hands, then cut them, and powder above any hot powders that be in their place of cautery;
ou tu les cauterize si com il est dit ou chapistre de cautere, puis les cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez;	or you cauterize them as is said in the chapter of cautery, then cure them with other cures until they are healed;
et se li fondemens ne puet issir, si clisterize le malaide de clistere mordant et aspre por laver ceu qui est ou fondement, si qu’il puist issir apertement;	and if the foundation cannot issue, then cleanse the patient with a harsh and biting enema so that what is in the foundation may be washed out, so that it can issue openly;
cant li malaides se preint, et se li fil sont fuer dou fondement, si est li cure legiere;	and if the patient feels pain, and if the threads are strong from the foundation, then the cure is light;
et est que tu les preignes a ton ungle ou as tenailles, et les cope, puis les cure si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez, et qu’il redoute l’incision par fer.	And it is that you prick them with your finger or with tongs, and cut them, then cure them as we have said, until they are healed, and he fears the incision by iron.
Si covient que tu amenistre la costure selonc ceste maniere: pren .i. fil tort, et le boute en une aguille, et puis trai le fil au desus et fai percier l’aguille d’autre part, et torne les .ij. chiez dou fil desoz l’aguille,	If it is necessary that you administer the suture in this manner: take one twisted thread, and put it into a needle, and then draw the thread upward and make the needle pierce from the other side, and turn the two ends of the thread below the needle.
et si soit dou large; et estraint le fil forment, puis noe le fil, et estrai l’aguille, et fai ensi de toz les autres, et en laisse .i. por corre la superfluiteit dou sanc;	And if it is of a wide size; and tighten the thread firmly, then knot the thread, and extract the needle, and do the same with all others, and leave one to correct the superfluity of blood;
puis met sus le fondement .i. drapeil moilliet en oile roset ou en cerote, et met sus le fondement, et comande au malaide k’il repose;	Then place on the foundation one layer of moistened cloth in rose oil or in cerate, and place it on the foundation, and instruct the patient to rest;
et puis le laisse tant qu’il chiecent, et quant il seront cheut, si les cure d’oignement et d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	and then leave it until it bleeds, and when it is healed, then cure with ointment and other cures, until it is healed.
dou sechement dou fiens ou fondement	of the drying of the wounds or foundation
Maintes fois avient sechement de fiens en l’intestine, et par constrignement de nature, et quant li maladie est vielle et medicine n’i vaut.	Many times there is drying up of wounds in the intestine, and by constriction of nature, and when the disease is old and medicine is of no use.
Si covient que tu reses a la point d’un spatumile ou a ton ungle l’escorce desus, qui ne le laisse a moistir;	Then it is necessary that you scrape to the point of a spatula or with your fingernail the bark on top, which does not let it moisten.
puis le cure tant qu’il soit sodez si com il covient;	then treat until it is healed as is fitting
et s’il ne puet soder, si rencomence la rasure plus fort que devant, tant qu’il saine mout, et soit escorchiez;	and if it cannot heal, then begin the scraping more strongly than before, until it heals well, and is scabbed over
puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	then treat until it is healed.
dou fremit	about trembling
Formice est une petite apparance fautree antor le cors, et va mout em parfont;	An ant is a small creature made before the body, and it goes much by itself.
et aucune fois la trueve li frois, et le sent on ausi comme mort de fremit, et vient en tout le cors, et plus as mains que autre part.	And sometimes it is found cold, and one feels it as dead from shivering, and comes throughout the body, and more to the hands than any other part.
Et li cure si est que tu pren une cainne d’une penne d’oie, ou une penne de vultul fort, et met celle caine sus le fremit, tant que li cercles porpreigne le fremit tot entor;	And the cure is that you take a cane of an ostrich feather, or a raven's feather very strong, and put that cane on the shivering, until the purple circles chase away the shivering all around.
puis torne ta main a tout la cainne tant que tu copes tout entor le fremit, et le met em parfont, et esraiche le fremit de ses racines.	Then turn your hand to the whole cane until you draw all around the shivering, and put it by itself, and root out the shivering from its roots.
Et se tu vues, si fai ceu d’une caine d’arain ou de fer selonc ceste forme, et soit subtilz desoz et traians desus:	And if you see, so do those of a dog of iron or steel according to this form, and be subtle below and trailing above:
ne mie perciet, por mues tenir au doi, et mues presser Et se tu vues, si cauterize lou fremit, si com il est devant ou chapistre de cautere.	do not pierce it, for to keep it in the two, and move pressing And if you see, so cauterize the edge, as it is before or chapter of cautery.
de la forme dou clistere	of the form of the clyster
Aucune fois fait on clistere d’argent ou d’archaut, ou d’arain fondut ou mailliet; et aucune fois fait on de ces estrumens petis et grans, selonc ces a cui il sont amenistrez.	At no time is made a clyster of silver or pewter, or iron melted or wrought; and at no time are these instruments made small and large, according to those to whom they are administered.
Cil donques c’on amenistre en la cure des enfans et qui sont foible et dolorous, sont petis.	Those therefore whom one administers in the care of children and who are weak and painful, are small.
Li forme dou clistere petit et grant si est desus large, ou li ventres est liiez selonc ceste maniere:	The shape of the clyster small and large is as above wide where the belly is tied according to this manner:
et i ait une desevrance ou li ventres soit liiez, si com tu vois, et li chiez soit dedens perciez; et ait a l’un des costez .ij. pertus, et en l’autre .i.;	and there is a severance where the belly is tied, as you see, and the shoulder is inside pierced; and on one side 2. pierced, and on the other 1. ;
et soit li ventres ou om met les medicines d’une vessie de beste ou de parchemin, et soit perciez tout entor de menus pertus,	and the belly is where one puts the medicines of a bladder of beast or parchment, and it is pierced all around with small piercings,
et ait entre chescun pertus .i. doit d’espaice, puis boute en ces pertus .i. fil fort de fil crut tort en .x. ou enqui entor, et assemble le ventre si com est une chievre;	and between each pore one should put space, then put into these pores one strong thread of wool twisted in ten or in whatever way it turns, and assemble the belly as if it were a ram;
et quant li medicine est dedens, si la lie a l’estrument devant d’un fil fort, puis clisterize; et c’est li forme dou cercle:	and when the medicine is inside, then tie the linen to the instrument with a strong thread, then clench it; and this is the shape of a circle.
Et soit li medicine ne trop chaude ne trop froide, et oint le chief dou clistere d’oile ou d’aubun d’uef, ou de semblant chose, puis le boute ens legierement;	And let the medicine be neither too hot nor too cold, and anoint the head of the clyster with oil or egg yolk, or something similar, then insert it gently.
puis l’espreigne li ministres a ses .ij. mains ensamble, tant qu’il soit toz vuis, puis estrai lou clistere, et lieve li malaides ses jambes a la paroit,	Then squeeze the minister with his two hands together, until it is all expelled, then remove the clyster and lift the patient's legs to the side.
et se li medicine vuet issir, si la teigne tant com il puet; et s’il dort une nuit atot, si est plus grans aide.	and if the medicine wants to work, then let it rest as much as possible; and if it sleeps one whole night, it is more helpful.
Et se tu le clisterizes em maladie de decorrement de ventre, et li medicine se haste d’issir, si le rencomence tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you clysters him in the sickness of a rumbling belly, and the medicine hastens to work, then he begins again until he is cured.
Et se li emorroide sont ou fondement, ou aposteme, si soit li clistere ausi subtilz com por .i. enfant;	And if the hemorrhoids are at the foundation or an abscess, then be the clyster as subtle as for one child;
et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil sus coi li cuir soit estraint:	and this is the form of the subtle clyster on which the skin should be restrained:
des plaies	of wounds
Nos avons jai dit en la division la cure des plaies; or vos dirons les cures de mains et de medicine, selonc l’acomplissement.	We have already said in the division the treatment of wounds; now we will tell you the treatments of hands and medicines, according to completion.
Je dis que les plaies sont diverses selonc ceu qu’elles sont faites, et selonc les leus ou les plaies sont faites, et de coi elles sont faites.	I say that wounds are diverse according to how they are made, and according to the places where the wounds are made, and from what they are made.
Les choses par coi plaies sont faites sont par gitement de piere, et taille d’espee et de couteil, ou de lance ou de fust ou de siette, ou de semblans choses;	The things by which wounds are made are by blows of stone, and cuts of sword and knife, or by spear or staff or arrow, or similar things.
ou que sont faites selonc les leus dou cors, si com plaie que chiet sus le col, ou sus le chief, ou le peis, ou le ventre, ou le foie, et semblans membres;	or which are made according to the parts of the body, such as a wound that falls on the neck, or on the head, or on the chest, or on the belly, or on the liver, and similar members.
et je vos dirai la cure de chescune plaie, et encomencerai as plaies dou chief simples, car li remenbrance venra en son chapistre.	and I will tell you the cure of each wound, and I will begin with simple wounds of the head, because remembrance comes in its chapter.
Je dis que quant simple plaie vient ou chief, et li os n’est brisiez, si pren garde se c’est de gitement de piere ou de semblans choses, et li cuir est toutevoie rompus et est li plaie grans,	I say that when a simple wound comes to the head and the bone is not broken, if you take care if it is from a stone or similar things, and the skin is entirely torn and the wound is large,
et tu doutes levement d’aposteme chaut: si le fai tantost sainier de la cephalique meismement s’il vient poc de sanc de la plaie, et soit li sainie au contraire de la partie navree;	and you doubt strongly of a hot abscess: if it does so soon bleed from the cephalic itself even if it comes little blood from the wound, and be the bleeding on the contrary of the wounded part;
et eschuisse li malaides repletion de vin et de viandes grosses.	and avoid the patient repletion of wine and large meats.
Et s’il ne vuet sainier, si soit amenuisie sa viande, et ne boive point de vin, ne ne menjuce point de char;	And if he does not want to bleed, then let his meat be less, and he shall drink no wine, nor eat any flesh.
et met sor la plaie, se apostemes chaus i vient, coton moilliet en oile roset soulement, ou en vin stiptice;	and put on the wound, if an abscess comes there, a cotton moistened in rose oil only, or in spiced wine.
et s’il n’i a aposteme chaut, si met sus la plaie, s’elle est fresche a tout son sanc, et elle n’est muee par l’air, poudre, que je dirai un poc ci aprés;	and if there is no abscess hot, then put on the wound, if it is fresh and all its blood is present, and it is not moved by air, powder, which I shall say a bit after;
et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucuns oignemens, tant qu’il soit sanez.	and if the bone has been moved, then put some ointment on it, until it is healed.
Et se li plaie est grans si com de tailleure d’espee et de semblans, et les levres ne se pueent assembler par tentes, si les assemble par cousture, si com je dirai as plaies dou ventre, de la costure.	And if the wound is large, like a sword cut and similar, and the edges cannot be brought together by tenting, then assemble them by suture, like I will say about wounds of the belly, with stitching.
Se li plaie est descoverte de l’os, et pent, et ne tient mais que a un poc, si le cope; puis cure la plaie de medicine, et restoure char dure en leu de cuir,	If the wound is open to the bone, and hanging, and holds only by a piece, then cut it away; then cure the wound with medicine, and restore hard flesh in its place of skin.
et comande au malaide a mengier grosses viandes, si com testes et froment cuit, ausi com poulz, et semblans choses.	And command the patient to eat thick meats, like beef and cooked wheat, also as poultry, and similar things.
Et se tu trueves ou cuir porriture, et il n’aert a l’os, si cope lou porrit tot, et giete fuer, puis le cure;	And if you find oneself or skin rot, and it does not reach to the bone, so cut out the rottenness all, and throw it away, then cure it.
et se il ait artere en la plaie ou voine, dont sans cort, et il ne puet estainchier par medicines, si quier l’artere, et se tu la trueves desloie, si la lie d’un fil;	And if there is an artery in the wound or vein, which without cutting, and it cannot be stopped by medicines, so seek the artery, and if you find it dislocated, tie it with a thread.
et se ceu ne profite mie, si la cauterize.	And if that does not help, then cauterize it.
Et se ces plaies sont petites et simples, si est li cure legiere: et est que tu mettes ens ceste poudre qui soude ainsois que li ars l’ait muee.	And if these wounds are small and simple, then the cure is light: and that you put in this powder which closes as though the sun had dried it.
Et li maniere de la poudre si est: pren encens une partie; sanc de dragon .ij. parties; chalz vive .iij. parties, et le poudre subtilment,	And the manner of the powder is this: take frankincense one part; dragon's blood two parts; quicklime three parts, and grind the powder finely.
et emple la plaie, et l’estraint forment, tant qu’elle s’aerse bien et se joigne a tout son sanc;	And apply it to the wound, and hold it firmly in place, until it dries well and closes with all its blood.
et puis la lie bien, et la laisse sens desliier, s’elle n’enfle; car on n’oste la madicine tant qu’ele soit sanee.	And then cover it well, and leave it uncovered, unless it swells; for the medicine is not removed until it is healed.
Et aucune fois fait on ceu de chalz soulement, quant on n’ait l’encens ne lou sanc de dragon, mais que li ars n’ait muee la plaie.	And no times is this made with only quicklime, when one has neither frankincense nor dragon's blood, but that the fire has not cauterized the wound.
Et se li ars ait mueit la plaie, meismement en esteit, si n’i met om mie ceste poudre;	And if the wound has moved the flesh, even in its state, do not put on this powder.
mais met sus aucuns oignemens digestis, ou poulz de farine d’orge faites d’aigue et de miel, tant qu’ele giete bowe;	But place on some ointments digested, or poultices of barley flour made with water and honey, as long as it weeps pus.
puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then treat with other treatments until it is healed.
Et se li brisure d’os vient avec la plaie, et elle est petite, si l’estrai as pinceures subtilz;	And if the fracture of bone comes with the wound, and it is small, then extract it with subtle pincers;
et je vos dirai ci aprés les brisures dou chief.	and I shall tell you hereafter the fractures of the head.
de la plaie dou col	of the wound of the neck
Se plaie vient ou col et elle est simple, si n’a point de difference entre li et celi dou chief, mais se li ners dou col ou li artere est copee.	The wound comes to the neck and it is simple, if there is no difference between it and that of the head, but if the nerve of the neck or the artery is cut.
Se c’est li ners, si n’i a autre engien que laissier la cure, et n’i mettre nulle chose restraignant, car il nuit as ners et les fait retraire;	If it is the nerve, there is nothing else to do but leave it to heal, and put nothing restraining upon it, for it harms the nerves and causes them to retract.
et ne mettre sus la plaie rien froit, car li substance des ners est froide, et li continuation d’aus si est avec le cerveil, qui est li plus haus membres;	and do not put on the wound anything cold, because the substance of the nerves is cold, and the continuation of them is with the brain, which is the highest member;
mais soit li medicine souez, si com chalz lavee en aigue douce, et mellee avec oile roset, et cucie lavee ausi en aigue douce,	but let it be the medicine warm, as calx washed in sweet water, and mixed with rose oil, and cupped water also in sweet water,
et autres pieres de mine selonc ceste maniere, et oignemens moistes.	and other stones of the mine according to this manner, and moist ointments.
Et se li plaie est grans, si la cout et lie de bendes, puis la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the wound is large, then sew it up and bind it with bandages, and keep dressing it until it is healed.
Et se les plaies sont parfondes et ele est chevee et pleinne de bowe, si la perce ou plus bas leu;	And if the wounds are deep and it is broken and full of bowel, then pierce or lower them.
et se li artere est copee, et decorremens de sanc en vient, si la desoivre, et la loie, et la cauterize se mestier est;	And if the artery is cut, and there comes bleeding, then close it, and stop it with a ligature, and cauterize as needed.
et se li espinee de la gorge est copee, ou li keurs, et li conduiz est gardez, par coi la viande va,	And if the spine of the throat is cut, or the guts, and the conduit is kept, so that the meat goes.
si cout le keur sus la cainne de la gorge, et ne touchier la gorge mais la remet selonc sa figure naturel;	Then sew the heart upon the neck of the throat, and do not touch the throat but put it back according to its natural form;
et puis l’estrain avenanment, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le cure d’oignemens desechans tant qu’il soit sanez;	and then he strains it carefully, and leaves it for several days, then cures it with ointments that are drying until it is healed.
et se li plaie a fait empression en l’os, si la quier;	And if the wound has made an impression in the bone, then you must [do something].
et s’il i a pieces d’os, si les trai fuers toz se tu pues, et ces que tu ne pues avoir, si laisse tant que li plaie porrisse,	And if there are pieces of bone, you must treat them all as best you can, and those that you cannot get, leave them until the wound decays.
et soit desevree et aligie li issue;	and be careful and align the edges.
et se li plaie est fresche, si poudre sus la poudre que j’ai dit.	and if the wound is fresh, so powder on the powder that I have said.
Et s’il a en la plaie os et il i a fistule, si la cure ensi com j’ai dit en son chapistre.	And if there are bones in the wound and there is a fistula, then treat it as I have said in my chapter.
de la plaie de lance ou de coutel	of a wound from a lance or knife
Se c’est cop de lance ou de coutel, et li plaie est parfonde, si regarde se de la plaie saut ventositez cant li malaides alainne: saiches adonques que li plaie est mortelz;	If it is a wound from a lance or knife, and the wound is deep, then look if from the wound there is wind blowing where the patient breathes; know then that the wound is mortal;
et s’elle n’est parfonde, et elle est fresche a tout son sanc, si n’i mettre mie a la premiere houre la poudre, ne ne la liier mie por le sanc que ne demorse em parfont,	and if it is not deep, and it is fresh with all its blood, then in the first hour do not put any powder on it, nor tie it up so that the blood does not clot.
et reviegne au cuer, et ocie lou malaide;	and return to the heart, and instruct the patient;
mais i met oignement atractif, et le lie .ij. fois le jor;	but I put attractive ointment, and tie it twice a day;
et se tu n’as oignement, si met en la plaie viel coton por succier fuers la moistor,	and if you do not have ointment, then put old cotton in the wound to suck out the moisture,
et fai dormir le malaide sus la plaie .iij. jors, ou .iiij., ou plusors;	and make the patient sleep on the wound for 3 days, or 4, or more;
si n’i venra mie spasme, ne tremor male de cuer n’es traingnemens d’alainne;	if there comes not a spasm, nor ill trembling of heart nor dragging of the arm;
et quant tu vois les bones dispositions, si saiches que li plaie est sauve.	and when you see good arrangements, then you know that the wound is saved.
Cure la donques de tentes et d’autres cures, tant qu’il soit sanez;	Treat it then with tents and other dressings, as long as it heals;
et s’elle ne puet saner, et oevre, adés saiches que il i a fistule; si la cure si com on doit.	And if it cannot heal, and work, know that there is a fistula; thus treat it as one should.
Et se li plaie est d’incision d’espee ou de coutel, et elle est simple, ou pis ou au dos, si la cure de ceu qui est devant;	And if the wound is from a sword or knife incision, and it is simple, or worse or on the back, then treat it as before.
s’elle est grans, de cousture; et s’elle est petite, de poudre, et s’elle est empressee en l’os, et en a copeit pieces, si quier la plaie, et les trai fuers s’il sont desevrez;	If it is large, suture it; and if it is small, treat it with powder; and if it is pressed into the bone, and has broken pieces, then sew the wound, and pull out the stray fragments.
et s’il ne sont desevrez, si laisse porrir la plaie, si aligera li estractions;	And if they are not dislodged, let the wound rot, so it will lighten the extraction
et des autres plaies as autres membres est li jugemens si com nos avons dit.	and for other wounds on other limbs, judgment is made as we have said.
dou derrompement dou ventre	of the stomach's displacement
Li derompemens dou ventre est grans et moiens et petis;	The stomach's displacement is great and medium and small;
de la grant plaie saut aucune fois li intestine, ou li ners des intestines, par coi li intromission d’aus;	From the large wound no organ or nerve of the intestines ever leaps out, by which their intrusion is prevented.
et li costure est plus malaisie, et aucune fois vaut pis li petite plaie que li grans,	and the suture is more troublesome, and sometimes worse the small wound than the large
por ceu c’on remet plus a poinnes les intestines en, s’on ne les i remet de chaut en chaut;	for this reason one puts back the intestines in, if one does not put them back hot in hot.
