por ce que li intestine enflent tantost qu’il sentent le froit, si rentrent plus a poinnes,	because the intestines swell immediately when they feel cold, so they enter less easily.
et por ceu vaut mues li moieinne plaie, por ceu c’on ramoine mues l’intestine a son leu que as autres .ij.	and for this reason the smaller wound is worse, for this reason one resets the intestine to its place as others do.
Et saiches que li routure dou ventre est selonc .iiij. manieres:	And know that the rupture of the belly is according to 4 manners:
les .ij. costures communes avienent en la costure dou ventre,	The 2 common sutures occur in the suture of the belly,
et li costure des autres plaies dou cors et .ij. autres costures propres sont communes as autres plaies;	and the sutures of other wounds of the body and 2 other special sutures are common to other wounds;
et toutevoie elles sont plus propres avec la costure dou ventre, et je dirai une chescune et declairerai.	and nonetheless they are closer with the suture of the belly, and I will say one of each and declare.
Je di que quant li plaie est petite, et aucune chose de l’intestine ist fuer,	I say that when the wound is small, and nothing of the intestine is outside.
et griés chose est dou remettre, ceu est par l’une des .ij. manieres:	and the thing grazed is to put back, this is by one of the two manners:
ou por la petitece de la plaie, si com nos avons dit,	or for the smallness of the wound, as we have said.
ou por ce que li intestine est enflez por le froit.	or because the intestine is swollen from the cold.
Et quant il est frois, eschaufez lou en teil maniere:	And when it is cold, warm it in such a manner:
moillie une esponge ou .i. mol drapeil en aigue tede soulement,	Soak a sponge or a soft cloth in tepid water only,
ou tu cuis en aigue squinant et cipre et spique,	or you cook it in water by adding and boiling  juniper and spice.
et arose l’intestine tant que li enfleure soit ostee;	and raise the intestine until the swelling is gone;
et aucune fois fait ce vins restraingnans, et est muedre que awe soule por desenfler.	and sometimes do this by restraining it, and let it move only a little to deflate.
Et quant tu vois l’enfleure departir, si amoiste l’intestine d’aigue ou altee et malves soient cuites,	And when you see the swelling depart, moisten the intestine with water or wine and let them be cooked.
car par ceu est aligie li entree a poc de chose;	because by this it is aligned the entrance to little things;
et s’il n’i puet entrer, si fent un poc la plaie a l’estrument de coi on cope les emorroydes;	and if it cannot enter, then make an opening in the wound with the instrument with which hemorrhoids are cut.
et li premiere cure est muedre que li taille,	and the first cure is to move the tail,
que nus n’i doit taillier sens grant necessiteit n’i ait;	that we should not cut it without great necessity there be;
et c’est li estrumens por le fendre:	and that is the tool for splitting it:
si trenche dedens en la corbeure et defuer non, et vez ci la forme:	if it is cut within the curve and not outside, and see here the form:
Et quant li plaie est enlargie, et li intestine saut fuer,	And when the wound is enlarged, and the entrails are thrown out,
si le remet arer selonc la forme naturel en son leu propre,	if it is put back in place according to its natural form in its proper place,
se tu en as pooir, car ce vaut mues.	if you have the power, because it matters much.
Quant li plaie est large, et elle est en la partie desoz lou ventre,	When the wound is wide, and it is in the part below the belly,
si covient que tu faices gesir lou malaide sus son dos,	So it behooves you to make the patient lie on his back.
et met ses jambes plus haut que son chief;	And put his legs higher than his head;
et s’elle est en la partie desoz le ventre,	and if it is in the lower part of the belly,
si met le chief et le pis plus haut que les parties desoz,	then put the head and buttocks higher than the lower parts,
et ausi se li routure dou ventre est en l’une des .ij. parties	and also if the rupture of the belly is in one of the two parts
si met t’entente en ceu que li partie navree soit plus haute que li autre;	if you put attention to this that the sunken part be higher than the other;
et ensi covient amenistrer ceu que je dis en plaies grans et moienes.	and thus it is necessary to administer what I say in great and small wounds.
Es plaies petites met ceu que t’est apparilliet,	For small wounds, put that which has appeared to you,
puis aies entre tes mains .i. ministre pitous ki teigne toute la routure a sa main,	Then hold in your hands i.e., minister pitiful who holds all the rupture with his hand,
et assemble les levres;	and bring together the lips;
et c’est la maniere commune de costures,	and that is the common manner of suturing,
et est que tu preignes une aguille ou plusors, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce de la plaie,	and that you pierce a needle or more, according to the quantity and width of the wound,
puis laisse des le chief de la plaie .i. doi d’espaice, et i fiche une aguille ou il ait .i. boin fil fort;	then leave from the head of the wound i.e., two of space, and there put a needle where it has i.e., a good strong thread;
et perce les .ij. chiés dou cuir avec les .ij. chiés dou siphac,	and pierce the two pieces of skin with the two pieces of sheepskin;
qui est desoz le cuir dedens, tant que tu la faices percier de celle partie,	which is under the skin inside, as long as you make it pierced from that part,
et assemble les .ij. chief dou siphac les .iiij. ensamble;	and assemble the two heads of sheepskin the four together;
puis l’estrain d’un fil double entor l’aguille de .ij. pars,	then the strain of a double thread wound around the needle of two parts
puis assemble les .ij. chiés de la plaie avenanment,	then assemble the two ends of the wound together
et puis laisse .i. doi d’espaice, et i fiche une autre aguille;	and then leave one-two of space, and insert another needle;
puis la lie dou fil si com tu as fait la premiere aguille,	then tie the thread like you did with the first needle,
et ne cesser de ceu faire selonc ceu que tu as mestier des aguilles,	and do not cease to do this according to what you need of needles,
tant que toute li plaie soit restrainte;	until all the wound is restrained;
et soient les aguilles moienes, entre subtilz et grosses,	and be the needles medium, between subtle and large,
car les aguilles subtilz copent toute la char, et les trop grosses si ne pueent mie bien entrer:	for the subtle needles cut all the flesh, and the too large ones cannot well enter:
por ceu covient qu’elles soient moienes;	for this reason they must be made shorter
et ne covient mie bouter les aguilles trop au defuer de la char et dou cuir,	and it is not fitting to push the needles too far from the flesh and skin
k’elles ne copent et oevrent la plaie devant la soudure;	so that they do not pierce and open the wound before the soldering;
et puis cope les chiés des aguilles, qu’elles ne blecent lou malaide au dormir,	and then blunt the points of the needles so that they do not prick the patient while sleeping
et i met tentes ou drapelz au chiés des aguilles por mues tenir,	and there I put tents or cloths at the head of the needles to keep them moving
et les laisse tant que li plaie soit soudee;	and let them stay until the wound is healed.
et ceste maniere de costure as aguilles est plus covenauble en petites plaies,	and this manner of suturing with needles is more advisable for small wounds
car il i soffist une aguille ou .ij.	because one or two needles are sufficient there
Li seconde costure si est commune,	The second suture is common
et est que tu assemble les .ij. chiés dou cuir et les .ij. chiés dou syfac ensamble a une aguille ou il ait .i. fort fil moien;	and it is that you assemble the two pieces of skin and the two pieces of flesh together with a needle or thread which has strength medium;
et quant tu avras perciez ces chiez toz .iiij. ensamble,	and when you will have pierced these four pieces together,
si ramoinne l’aguille a la partie ou tu as encomenciet, en la maniere c’on cout les dras;	then withdraw the needle to the place where you began, in the manner one sews draperies;
et met d’espaice entre chescune costure la grossece d’un menor doi;	and put space between each stitch the thickness of a man's finger.
ceste costure sevent li home,	this suture should be for the man
et je cousi une plaie c’uns hons avoit ou ventre,	and I stitched a wound that a man had on his belly,
qui estoit navrez d’un coutel,	which was slashed with a knife,
et estoit li plaie plus d’une palme de grant,	and the wound was more than a palm wide,
et issoit des intestines bien .ij. palmes de grant,	and it was two palms of width across.
et estoit li plaie enmi le ventre.	and the wound was in the middle of the belly.
Je li ramenai l’intestine puis k’il ot esteit .xxiiij. houres fuer,	I returned the intestine to him after it had been  twenty-four hours.
et fut li plaie soudee jusc’a .xv. jors, et le curai, et fut sanez.	and the wound was sutured for xv days, and I treated it, and it healed.
Et li mire l’avoient jugiet qu’il morroit, et ce fut miracle;	And the onlookers had judged that he would die, and it was a miracle;
et ne le curai mie d’oignement, car je estoie en .i. leu ou on n’en trovoit point, ne nule medicines;	and I did not treat him with ointment, because I was in one place where none could be found, nor any medicines;
et metoie sens plus sus la plaie coton viel .ij. fois le jor, et le lavoie d’aigue de miel tant qu’il fut sanez.	and put half a handful more on the wound of cotton twice a day, and washed it with water mixed with honey until it healed.
Or vos dirai les .ij. propres manieres de cousture:	Or I will tell you the two proper ways of stitching:
pren l’aguille, et la boute des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens;	Take the needle and thrust it from the outside part to the inside;
quant elle a perciet le keur de droit en droit, si lai le chief dou siphac ou cousteit ou tu as bouteit l’aguille,	when it has pierced the middle of right to right, then lay the head upon the siphon or sewing or where you have thrust the needle.
et la fai percier d’autre part des la partie dedens jusc’a celi defuer;	and make it pierce from the other side from the inside to the outside;
et li entendemens de ceste costure si est que tu cous ausi com li peletier font les pelz,	And the understanding of this suture is that you sew as the furrier does furs,
et que tu laisses une fois le syfac d’une part, et le reprent d’autre, tant que li costure soit toute acomplie.	and that you leave once the thread on one side, and take it on the other, as long as the suture is entirely completed.
Li seconde maniere de costure, que Galiens dist proprement,	The second manner of suturing, which Galens states properly,
si est si com aucun font, qui assemblent les .ij. parties ensamble naturelment,	is like how any one joins the two parts together naturally,
et apploient l’un des chief dou syfac a l’autre chief, en teil maniere:	and apply one end of the stick to each other end, in such a manner:
fiche une aguille ou chief dou mirach prochiene, et fai percier celui leu soulement,	Insert a needle or piece of wood near the root, and have him feel only that.
et laisse les .ij. chiés dou syfac;	and leave the two ends of the stick;
puis torne l’aguille, et la fai percier des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens,	then turn the needle, and have him feel from the outer part to the inner part,
as .ij. chiés dou syfac;	as the two bones of the shoulder
puis fai percier l’un et l’autre des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, en .ij. autres chiés dou mirach que sont on l’autre costeit;	then make each one be measured from the outer part until the inner one, in two other bones of the shoulder that are on the opposite side
et c’est li muedre maniere de costure et li plus commune.	and this is the most common and usual way of suturing.
Galiens si dist ceste parolle, et aucun le tesmoignent,	The Gauls call this word thus, and no one testifies to it.
c’on doit coudre le ventre a .ij. aguilles, ou il ait fil en chescune;	one must sew the belly with two needles, or there is thread in each
et doit on bouter l’une aguille d’une part, et l’autre d’autre, en la maniere de ces qui cousent corroies;	and one must insert one needle on one side, and the other on the other, in the manner of those who sew corsets;
et saiches que quant li routure est enmi lou ventre,	and know that when the rupture is in the middle of the belly,
si est li cousture plus griez que des autres leus dou ventre.	it is the stitching more dangerous than the other parts of the belly.
Li jugemens de la plaie si est telz com li jugemens des autres plaies:	The judgments of the wound are such as the judgments of other wounds.
et est que quant tu trueves la plaie fresche a tout son sanc, ainsois que li ars l’ait muee,	and it is that when you find the wound fresh with all its blood, then as the pain has moved
si remet arer l’intestine, et lou cout; puis met sus la poudre enjanrant char,	then put back the intestines and the gut; then put on top of it powdered charcoal powder
et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucun oignement que soit present, tant que li plaie bowe;	and if the pain has moved, then put on top of it any ointment that is present, as long as the wound bleeds;
et chicent li fil, et soient soudez li sifac, et li mirach;	and tighten the thread, and weld together the fascia, and the periosteum;
puis cure la plaie si com les autres, tant qu’il soit sanez;	then treat the wound as with others, until it is healed.
et se tu n’as medicines, si met sus, tantost qu’ele comance a giter bowe, coton viel,	and if you lack medicines, place on it, as soon as it begins to fester, old cotton.
et le remue .ij. fois le jor tant k’il soit sanez.	and change it two times a day until it is healed.
Car tu n’as mestier d’autre medicine en plusors dispositions cant les plaies sont simples;	Because you do not need other medicine in several dispositions when the wounds are simple;
et se tu doutes que li plaie ne faice communiteit as membres principelz,	and if you doubt that the wound does not make community with principal members;
si covient ke tu moilles lainne legiere en oile de tempree chalor, ou en oile roset,	then it is fitting that you moisten the linen lightly in oil of temperate heat, or in rose oil,
et la met entor les angres, et desoz les asselles;	and place it around the edges, and beneath the buttocks;
et s’il sent dolor ou porriture en bouelz, et maintes fois avient,	and if he feels pain or rot in the bowels, and this happens often
si les clisterize de vin noir tede, et meismement se li porriture vient jusc’a l’intestine;	if enemas of black wine help, and similarly if the rot comes to the intestine;
et le perce dedens, et saiches que quant c’est li gros intestines, si est plus legier a saner que li petis.	and you pierce within it, and know that when it is the large intestine, it is easier to heal than the small one.
Li intestine qui est apelez «jeun» ne puet saner quant il est navrez,	The intestine which is called "jejunum" cannot heal when it is rotten,
et c’est por la planteit des voinnes que i sont, et por la subtiliteit de tout le cors, et l’aprochement de sa nature des ners.	And this is because of the position of the veins that are, and for the subtlety of the whole body, and the proximity of its nature to the nerves.
Et si li zirbe saut de la plaie, si le remet arrier ausi com l’intestine, tandis qu’il est fres;	And if the worm jumps from the wound, put it back in as if it were an intestine, while it is fresh;
et s’il est vielz et devenus vers ou noir, si covient que tu lies le leu qui est noir, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne,	and if it is old and has turned to worms or black, then you must tie the place that is black, so that bleeding does not come from it.
car il i a voinnes et arteres;	for there are veins and arteries there;
puis cope ceu qui est entre le liien,	then cut what is between the joint,
et met les .ij. chiés pendans des la partie desoz la plaie jusque defuer por aligier l’estraction quant li zirbes chiet, et li plaie bowe.	and put the two heads during from the part below the wound until outside to align the extraction when the bones fall, and the wound bows.
de la routure dou boueil	of the rupture of the boil
Quant li intestine est rons, et li plaie est petite,	When the intestine is round, and the wound is small,
si la puet on restorer en aucuns homes,	if one can restore it in some men
por ceu que je vis que uns hons fut navrez ou ventre d’une lance;	because I saw that a man was struck or pierced in the belly by a lance;
et estoit li plaie au destre de l’estomac,	and the wound was on the right side of the stomach,
et fut envillie et devint fistule, et en issoit li egestion et li ventositez;	and it became infected and turned into a fistula, and through it he expelled excrement and flatulence;
je i mis cure selonc ceu que je poi, et ne cessai de subtilier tant qu’il fut sanez, et li leus soudez.	I set the cure according to what I could, and did not cease to work on it until it was healed, and the bones joined.
Et quant je le vis souder, je doutai que li malaides n’eust mal en son ventre;	And when I saw it join, I doubted that the patient would be unwell in his belly;
et il n’i ot point de mal, mais demora en millors dispositions, et menjans et bevans;	and there was no ill, but he remained in better dispositions, and eating and drinking;
et dirent aucun experimentors que quant il a petite plaie en l’intestine, qu’il doit estre liiez en teil maniere:	and said any experimenter that when he has a small wound in the intestine, it should be bound in such a manner:
pren fremis a grans testes, puis assemble les levres de la plaie,	Take fresh thread with large stitches, then assemble the lips of the wound
et quant li fremis ait overte la bouche, si la met sus les .ij. levres,	and when the thread has covered the mouth, place it on top of the two lips,
si qu’elle estraigne sa bouche sus;	so that it pulls its mouth up;
et puis li cope la teste, et ce se tient si qu’il ne puet desliier,	and then close the head of the thread and make it stay so that it cannot unravel,
puis met .i. autre fremit aprés en celle maniere que devant, tant que li plaie soit toute porprise;	Then put another bandage after it in the same manner as before, until the wound is completely covered.
et cout la plaie.	and cover the wound.
Cil chief si s’aerdent en l’intestine, et ne vient nulle nuisance au malaide,	If this chief [refers to a medical tool] is burned inside the intestine, and no harm comes to the patient,
et se puet on liier l’intestine d’un fil subtil qui est copez de l’intestine d’une beste,	and if it can be bound to the intestine with a fine thread that is cut from the intestine of an animal,
en teil maniere:	in such manner:
pren le chief de cest fil d’intestine que soit mout descharnez,	take the head of this thread of intestine that is very cleaned,
et puis lie au chief de cest fil .i. fil de lin subtil tort,	and then tie to the head of this thread one thread of fine linen twisted,
puis boute le fil en l’aguille, et en cout l’intestine, et le ramoinne en la routure;	then put the thread in the needle, and sew the intestine, and stitch it in the rupture;
et ceste maniere de costure de fremis nen est fuers que selonc la voie de fiance et d’esperance;	and this manner of sewing of fringes is not worse than according to the way of hope and trust;
et se li plaie est grans et large, meismement quant elle est en l’un des grailes intestines, si n’i a engien ne santeit, fuer que subtiliteit.	and if the wound is great and wide, even when it is in one of the intestines, there is nothing else needed, except for subtlety.
de fistule ou qu’ele soit	of fistula or wherever it may be
Saiches que toute plaie ou aposteme, quant il enveillist, si est apelee universement «fistule»,	Know that every wound or abscess, when it opens up, is universally called "fistula,"
et meismement quant elle est chevee et rent bowe.	and also when she is raised and bent back.
Et fistule est selonc la verteit nodation fautree dure et blainche, ou on ne sent dolor,	And a fistula is according to truth a knotted false swelling hard and white, where one does not feel pain,
et est ausi chevee com li penne d’un oiseil;	and is also raised like the feathers of a bird;
et aucune fois en saut clere bowe, et autre fois espesse;	and sometimes clear and bright in jump, and other times thick;
aucune fois poc, et autre fois assez;	Some times much, and other times enough;
et je en ai jai parleit en la division des plaies, que toute plaie que n’est sanee, et il n’i a char,	and I have spoken of it in the division of wounds, that any wound that is not healed, and there is no flesh,
ce n’est fuers que par une des .viiij. causes:	it is only due to one of the eight causes:
c’est a savoir, par la petitece dou sanc ou cors;	that is to say, by the smallness of blood or flesh;
ou por sa malice;	or because of its wickedness;
ou por ceu qu’il i a char dure dedens, et sus les levres, que n’i laisse naistre char;	or because within it there is hard flesh and on the lips that do not allow flesh to grow;
ou il i a trop de bowe;	where there is too much swelling;
ou li leus est porris, et li matiere est de male qualiteit;	or the  flesh is rotten and the material is of poor quality;
ou li medicine n’est mie bone en la cure;	When the medicine is not good in the cure.
ou por ceu que li corruption est maniere de pestilence;	Or because the corruption is a manner of pestilence;
ou por la proprieteit en la region est tardive li digestion, et tarde li santeit, et enflee par nature;	or because the property in the region is late digestion and late health, and swollen by nature;
ou il i a voinnes ou os:	or there are veins or bones:
et j’ai ja mostreit toutes ces causes, et les signes, et les cures de medicines en la division.	and I have already shown all these causes, and signs, and cures of medicine in the division.
Or covient que je te faice a savoir la cure de fistule qui est faite par oevre de mains.	It is necessary that I make you know the cure for fistula which is done by the work of hands.
Saiches que fistule avient en tous membres dou cors;	Know that fistula occurs in all parts of the body;
car il i a fistules que vienent as grans voines, et as arteres, et as ners,	for there are fistulas that come from large veins, and arteries, and nerves,
ou au syfac, ou a l’intestine, ou a la vessie, ou a aucunes des costes,	or to the spleen, or to the intestine, or to the bladder, or to any of the ribs
ou a l’espinee dou dos, ou a aucune jointe des mains ou des piez;	or to the spine of the back, or to any joint of the hands or feet;
et si a teil que vient a la proprieteit dou membre principeil, et as semblans leus.	and if it comes to the property of the principal limb, and similar ones.
Et toutes les fistules que sont de ceste maniere sont de grief sanation, et n’i a fors que labour, et ignorance;	And all fistulas that are of this kind are of grave healing, and there is only labor, and ignorance;
et se il i a aucune fistule que ne veigne mie jusc’a leu que j’ai dit, et tu as fiance de la cure,	and if there is any fistula that does not come to the place I have said, and you have faith in the cure,
et tu la vues conoistre, si pren une tente d’arain ou de fer, se li fistule est droite, si la quier;	and if you see it is known, then take a tent of linen or iron, if the fistula is straight, if the other way around;
et se li fistule est torte, si la cerche d’une subtil tente de plonc,	and if the fistula is crooked, then circle it with a fine tent of wool;
car li plons se ploie mues entor la tortuositeit;	for wool can be molded and follow the curvature;
et se li fistule a mains pertus et tu ne la pues mie bien cerchier par tentes,	and if the fistula is pierced with hands and you cannot well search it with probes,
si la clisterize par l’un des pertus,	then clysterize it by one of the openings,
car la moistors si cort d’un pertus a autre, et la mundifie;	for the moisture goes from one opening to another and cleanses it;
puis la quier saigement a ton pooir, que tu conoisses s’il i a os ou nerf, et est chevee em parfont,	then carefully feel with your power, so that you know if there is bone or nerve and whether it is closed completely;
et demande bien au malaide de la dolor qu’il sent au presser de ta main, et le leu ou il la sent;	and ask the patient well about the pain he feels when pressing his hand, and where he feels it.
et quant tu savras vraiement le leu ou elle est, et s’elle est loing de jointure, ou de nerf, ou d’artere ou de voine,	and when you will know truly the place where it is, and if it is far from a joint, or a nerve, or an artery, or a vein,
ou en aucuns des leus que je t’ai dit, si la cope selonc ceu que je t’ai dit,	or in any of the places that I have told you, if the cut according to what I have told you,
et oste fuer la fautreure et les chars corrumpues que sont dedens;	and has removed the fracture and the corrupted matter that is within;
et puis la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee,	and then the care until it is healed,
et se li fistule est bien parfonde de droit endroit, si covient que tu copes em parfont, tant com tu pues,	and if the fistula is deep from right place, then you must cut it deeper, as much as you can,
puis i met tentes moillies en medicine ague, et les boute jusc’au chief de la fistule,	then put moist sponges in medicine ague, and push them to the top of the fistula,
tant que li medicine corrode la superfluiteit qui est demoree au fons;	as long as the medicine corrodes the excess that is at the bottom;
et puis i met oignemens enjanrans sainne char, tant qu’il soit sanez;	and then he puts on ointment strengthening sinew, until it is sound
et s’il n’est sanez par ceu, si le cauterize si com nos avons dit,	And if it is not sound by this, then cauterize it as we have said.
et se li os est corrompus de la fistule, si le cope.	and if the bone is rotten from the fistula, then cut it away.
Se voinne ou ners ne te greve ou membres principelz, si com nos avons dit;	If a vein or nerve strikes or touches principal members as we have said;
et se li os est descovers, et il i a corruption et noiror, si lou reis tant que li corruption soit toute ostee,	and if the bone is uncovered, and there is corruption and blackness, then let the king cleanse as long as all the corruption is removed.
puis le cure de choses enjanrans char tant qu’il soit sanez;	then cure the flesh wounds until it is healed.
et s’il n’est sanez, et rent bowe si com devant,	and if it is not healed, and returns bowed as before,
saiches que tu n’es mie alez jusc’a font:	know that you have not gone all the way yet.
si descuevre et quier tant que tu soies au fons,	if you uncover and want as long as you are at the bottom,
et oste toute la corruption, puis restore le leu;	and remove all the corruption, then restore its place;
et s’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	and if it is thus healed, that's well.
Se ceu non, saiches que la corruption est trop en parfont, que tu n’i pues avenir;	If this does not happen, know that the corruption is too deep, that you cannot succeed there;
si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier a nature;	if there is no other thing than to leave to nature;
et s’il i a i petit os corrumput, et tu le pues traire as tenailles,	and if there is a small bone corrupted, and you can draw it out with pliers,
si l’estrai a .i. estrument covenauble a ceu,	if the extraction with a suitable instrument  is done
et s’il i a maint os, si les trai trestoz, ne n’en laissier nes un;	and if there are many bones, draw them all out together, and leave none behind.
et se li moistor te fait contraire, et il n’i a error ne paour,	and if moisture opposes you, and there is no error or fear,
si cope et moistor et char, et delivre les os.	if you cop and moisture and flesh, and deliver the bones.
Et se tu ne les pues oster a une houre, si met sus la plaie chose enjanrant porriture,	And if you cannot remove them in an hour, then put on the wound something preventing rot,
et laisse tant que li leus soit porris entor les os,	and leave it until the flesh is rotten around the bones,
et adonc si avront plus legierement les os;	and therefore they will have more easily the bones;
et se c’est uns grans os, si com de jambe ou de cuisse,	and if it is a large bone, like of the leg or thigh,
si reis tant soulement la corruption tant que li noiror soit toute ostee,	if you remove only the corruption as long as the blackness is totally removed,
puis restoure la plaie;	then restore the wound;
et s’il en i a grant partie dou corrumput, et vient jusc’a mole de l’os;	and if there is a great part of corruption, and comes up to the flesh of the bone;
si le covient soier et coper tout jusc’a la corruption, et puis le cure tant qu’il soit soudez;	if it is necessary to be clean and cover everything up to the corruption, and then cure it until it is healed;
et je te dirai d’une fistule qui avint .i. home en sa jambe,	and I will tell you of a fistula that happened to one man in his leg,
si que tu i preignes exemple et aide en ton ovraige.	so that you may take it as an example and help in your work.
Il fut .i. jovencelz entor .xxx. ans, qui ot une dolor en sa jambe d’une cause que vint dedens le cors,	There was one young man around thirty years old, who had pain in his leg from a cause that came from within the body,
tant que les matieres vinrent a la jambe, et fut enflee d’un gros aposteme, et n’ot point de cause defuer por ovrir;	as long as the materials came to the leg, and was swollen with a large abscess, and had no external cause to open;
mais li mire par lor folie ovrerent tant sus que li apostemes ovri,	but the surgeon by his foolishness opened it so much that the abscess opened,
et en corroient mout de matieres, et devint fistule, et i vint mout de pertus que tuit gitoient bowe et moistor dou cors;	and in corrupting a lot of matter, it became a fistula, and there came out much pus that all reeked and was moist from the body;
et maint mire i mirent cure entor .ij. ans, et n’i ot nul saige en l’art de mains,	and many a miracle is cured within  two years, and there is no sage in the art of hands
tant que je i fui apelez, et vi sa jambe et les medicines dont on le curoit,	as long as I was called upon, and saw his leg and the medicines with which he was treated,
et ceu que corroit par les pertus a grant cors;	and those that were running through the cuts to great length;
et devenoit rouges li cors dou jouvenceil, et avoit color citrine.	and becoming red the body of the young man, and had a citrine color.
Je boutai une tente en l’un de ces pertus, et puis cerchai toz les pertus,	I placed a tent in one of these holes, and then I searched all the holes.
et trovai que li uns venoit encontre l’autre de toutes les parties de la jambe.	and found that some came against each other from all parts of the leg.
Je me hastai donques, et copai en l’un des pertus tant que je descovri une partie de l’os,	I then pried it open and dug into one of the holes until I uncovered a part of the bone,
et le trovai corrumput et perciet, et venoit li corruption jusc’a l’os dedens;	and found it rotten and pierced, and the corruption came all the way to the bone inside.
je soiai ceu qui m’aparissoit de l’os corrumput, et cuidai qu’il n’i eust autre corruption, fuer que celi que je ostai;	I was that one who appeared to me of the corrupted bone, and I thought that there was no other corruption except that which I removed;
et comensai a restourer la plaie de medicines sodans par lonc tens, et ne pot souder;	and began to restore the wound with medicinal ointments for a long time, and it could not heal;
et puis rencomensai, et descovri l’os si com devant,	and then I began again, and discovered the bone as before,
et trovai la corruption continuee en l’os, et la soiai, et puis l’ostai, et me penai de souder le leu;	and found the corruption continued in the bone, and I removed it, and then I removed it again, and I tried to solder the place;
mais je ne pou tant que je copai entor une palme de l’os, et le traï fuer a tout son mole,	but I could not reach as far as one palm of the bone, and the vein was drawn to its full extent.
puis le restourai de medicines; et il fut sanez et soudez hastanment,	then I restored him with medicines; and he was healed and soundly joined together.
et ne covint plus rencomencier l’ovraige fors por la foibleté dou malaide, qui ne pooit soffrir,	and it was no longer necessary to begin the work except for the weakness of the patient, who could not endure it.
et por la paour de mort que je avoie de lui.	and because of the fear of death that I had for him.
Car por l’evacuation sanglotoit sovent, mais il fut sanez entierement,	For often blood evacuation happened, but he was made whole entirely.
et nasquit en leu de l’os une char dure, et fut de bone disposition et n’ot point de nuisement ne de contraire dou tout en tout, ne a l’aleir ne a venir.	and there grew in the place of the bone a hard cartilage, and he was of good disposition and had no nuisance nor contrary from all or to all, neither in walking nor coming.
Et se li os est brisiez en aucun leu dou cors, si le covient soier en ceste maniere:	And if the bone is broken in any place of the body, then it should be treated in this manner:
pren .i. liien, et l’estrain au chief de l’os qui apert,	Take one linen cloth and strain it to the head of the bone that is open,
et comande aucun k’il l’estende en haut;	and instruct anyone that they extend it upwards;
et met .i. autre lien de lainne plus gros dou premier liien, et le lie sus la char qui est desor l’os,	and put one other linen bandage larger than the first one, and tie it on the skin that is over the bone,
et estent le chief, si que tu traies la char corrumpue au desoz,	and extend the head so that you pull the corrupted flesh down.
et descuevre la char sus le leu ou tu vues soier, que li soie ne blece la char;	and uncover the skin in the place where you want to see that it does not bleach the skin;
et met .i. tison ou une tauble desoz l’os por mues coper la char corrumpue;	and put one coal or a board under the bone to cover the corrupted flesh;
et covient tant soier com on puet veoir et sentir la corruption, et soier ancor autre fois.	And it is necessary to be as careful as one can see and feel the corruption, and to be even more careful other times.
Et se li os est corrumpus, et n’apert mie, et li corruptions est en mileu ou en une partie,	And if the bone is corrupted, and does not open, and the corruption is in the middle or in one part,
si descuevre la char toute; puis met .i. tison desoz,	then uncover all the flesh; then put one coal under,
et puis soie des l’une partie a l’autre la corruption, et soit li soieure dou lonc de la corruption .i. poc, si com nos avons dit;	and then there is the corruption from one part to another, and be the silk thread long of the corruption that is to say, as we have said;
et se li corruptions est en la jointure, si cope la jointure corrumpue, et soie l’os ou elle contient de l’autre part;	and if the corruption is in the joint, cut the corrupted joint, and tie the bone on which it lies from the other side;
et se li corruptions est en la continuation des .ij. jointes, si n’i a autre angien que dou coper;	and if the corruption is in the continuation of the two joints, there is nothing else to be cut;
et se li corruptions est ou poignil de la main, ou ou poignil dou piet, si est mout fort celle chose,	and if the corruption is in the finger of the hand or the finger of the foot, then it is a very serious thing,
mais toutevoie il covient que tu enquieres celle corrosion, coment elle t’apert;	but nonetheless, it is necessary that you inquire about that corrosion, how it opens to you.
et la mundifie en toutes les manieres que tu pues, mais que li voine ou li nerf ne te faicent contraire;	and purify it in all the ways that you can, but that the vein or nerve do not make you contrary.
et saiches que li incisoire et les soies por coper ces os sont maintes, selonc l’assise des os et l’aparance d’ous,	and know that the instruments and threads for covering these bones are many, according to the arrangement of the bones and the appearance of each one.
et lor grossece et lor subtiliteit, et lor grandor et lor petitece, et lor duresce;	and their thickness and fineness, and their size and smallness, and their hardness;
et por ceu covient il apareillier a chescune semblance d’ovraige son estrument;	And for this reason, it is necessary to prepare each kind of work with its instrument.
et saiches que l’uevre te moustrera l’estrument dont tu avras mestier, selonc la conissance de cest art,	and know that the work will show you the instrument which you will need, according to the knowledge of this art,
et le tesmoignaige des manieres des maladies;	and the testimony of the ways of the illnesses;
si porpense l’estrument dont tu as mestier selonc ceu qu’il le covient.	so consider the instrument which you need according to what is fitting.
dou feu	of fire
Li chiés porrissent ou par cause dedens, ou par cause defuer;	The shoulder can be dislocated due to internal or external causes.
et quant tu avras medicinee celle corrosion par la cure des medicines, et il ne profitent mie,	and when you will have treated that corrosion by the use of medicines, and they do not benefit
si covient coper celui membre jusques au leu ou li corrosion vient,	then it is necessary to cover that limb up to where the corrosion comes from,
si que li malaides eschaipe par ceu de la mort, ou par la malice, qui est plus grans, de la defaute dou membre;	so that the patient escapes by this from death, or by the malice, which is greater, of the fault of the limb;
et li signes si est que li membres devient noir, si qu’il semble qu’il soit ars dou feu,	and the signs are that the limb becomes black, so that it seems to be burned by fire.
et porrist aprés la noiror, puis va celle corrosions de membre em membre,	and then after the blackness, then goes that corrosion of limb from limb,
et prent par tout le cors; si te haste dou coper,	and takes hold throughout the whole body; if you hasten to cover it,
et se c’est par la percussion d’aucunes venimouses bestes, si com scorpion de mer et wivre et semblans,	and if it is by the percussion of some venomous beasts, such as scorpions of the sea and viper and similar.
se li corrosion est au chief dou doi, si le cope, et ne li doner mie espaice de venir jusc’a la main.	if the corrosion is at the head of the thigh, so cut it, and do not give him any space to come up to the hand.
Et s’elle vient jusc’a la main, si la cope a la jointe, si que la corrosion ne viegne jusc’a bras;	And if it comes up to the hand, so cut at the joint, so that the corrosion does not come up to the arm.
et s’elle vient au bras, si le cope au coute; et s’elle passe le coute, c’est li mors,	And if it comes to the arm, so cut it at the elbow; and if it passes the elbow, it is death.
et n’i vaut amenistremens fuers que li quantitez de sa vertut;	and there is no worth of administering forces other than the quantity of its virtue;
et tot ensi fai quant li corrosion vient ou piet: s’elle vient en la premiere jointe, si la cope aprés l’autre jointe;	and thus entirely do as when the corruption comes or foot; if it comes in the first joint, so after the other joint;
et s’elle vient ou piet, si cope tout le piet;	and if it comes on the foot, so cut all of the foot;
et s’elle monte en la jambe, si cope a la jointure dou genoil;	and if it goes up into the leg, so cut at the joint of the knee;
et s’elle vient desus le genoil, si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier le malaide a mort;	and if it comes from above the knee, there is no other remedy but to let the patient die.
et li maniere dou coper ou dou soier le membre si est que tu le lie desus et desoz,	And the manner of covering or soothing the limb is that you bind it above and below,
et estende uns menistres l’un des liiens aval, et uns autres ministres l’autre liien amont,	and extend some ministers one on the lower binding, and others ministers the other binding above,
et tu dessevre la char qui est entre les .ij. liiens a .i. spatumile large, tant que li os soit descovers;	and you should sever the flesh which is between the two bindings to one span wide, so that the bone is uncovered;
puis le cope ou soie, et met de chescune part .i. drapeil de lin, si que li soie ne touche le leu sain,	then the coping or soiling, and put on each side one drapery of linen, so that the soiling does not touch the healthy place.
et viegne au malaide autre lesion et aposteme chaus.	and bring to the patient another lesion and abscess chaus.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient quant tu oevres, si cauterize le leu hastanment,	And if bleeding occurs when you work, then cauterize the place carefully.
ou tu met sus aucunes poudres restraignans; puis revien a ta medicine tant qu’elle soit acomplie,	or you put on any powders restraining; then return to your medicine until it is completed,
puis lie le membre navreit d’un liien covenauble, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	then tie the limb with a suitable bandage, and treat it until it is healed.
et je te conterai k’il avint a .i. home en som piet:	and I will tell you that it happened to one man in his foot:
il li avint une noiror qui sembloit arsure de feu,	He had a blackening that looked burned by fire,
et celle corrosion vint premier en son doi dou piet, tant qu’elle porprist tout le piet;	and that corruption first came in the heel of his foot, until it encompassed the whole foot;
et quant li hons vit la corrosion, si se hasta de coper le piet, et fut sanez;	and when the man saw the corrosion, he tried to cover his foot, and was healed;
et lonc tens aprés li revint li corrosion ou doi de la main, et il vint a moi,	and long time after he returned the corrosion on two of his hand, and he came to me,
et je li mis sus choses repercussives aprés la mundification dou cors, et ne pot cesser li corrosions;	and I put upon him things  receptive after the purification of the body, and could not cease the corrosions;
et il vot que je li copasse la main, et je ne vou, que je avoie esperance de repercuter la matiere;	and he wished that I would cut off his hand, and I did not want to, because I had hope of repelling the matter;
et doutai ausi que se je tailloie sa main, qu’il ne morist,	and also fear if he cuts his hand, that he will not die,
car li vertus de l’ome estoit foible; et il se despera toz, et revint en sa terre,	for the virtue of the man was weak; and he despaired of all, and returned to his land,
et se hasta de coper sa main, et fut sanez;	and took courage to cover his hand, and became healthy;
et je n’ai ceu conteit fuers que por ceu c’on faice autreteil, s’on en a mestier.	and I have set this tale down for this reason, that if one has need of it, they may do something similar.
Aucune fois vient aposteme en leu charnut, et demore si longement qu’il fait grant assemblee de bowe;	Sometimes an abscess comes to its fleshy place, and remains so long that it causes great gathering of bowels;
et puis ront et perce, et en saut li bowe, et demoure li leus vuis, ausi com uns vasselz;	and then bursts and pierces, and the bowels jump out, and remain in their place, like a vessel.
et li cuir qui est desus est ausi subtilz com .i. drapelz deliiez,	And the skin that is above is as fine as one sheet of delicate linen;
et ne corront mie jusc’a l’os, ne jusc’au nerf, et telz maladie si est apelee «sain»,	and it does not reach down to the bone, nor to the nerve, and such a disease is called "clean";
et n’est mie apelee «fistule»;	and is not called a "fistula";
mais s’elle est si alongie qu’elle viegne jusc’a l’os em parfont, si est apelee «fistule»;	but if it is so long that it comes to the bone and pierces through it, then it is called a "fistula";
et li cuire si est que tu cope celui cuir tout entor, et meismement quant il est subtilz, ausi com uns drapelz;	and the treatment for this is that you cut all around the skin, and also when it is thin, like a little cloth;
et ne s’aert mie por sa corruption.	and does not become infected because of its corruption.
Et se tu as fiance que li cuirs s’aerde, et li corruption n’est mie en parfont,	And if you have faith that the skin is hard, and the corruption is not yet complete,
et li cuir est espés de char, si le cure de clistere ensi:	and the skin is thick with flesh, then treat it with this enema:
regarde se li seins est grans, et li bowe qui en ist est de puant odor,	look if the breasts are large, and the belly that contains them is of foul odor,
adonques le clisterize de medicine egiptiaine qui est ensi faite:	then administer a clyster made with Egyptian medicine, which is prepared as follows:
prenez aisil, et oile, et litargire, igalment, et metez cuire en .i. vassel au feu,	Take thus, and oil, and litharge, equally, and put to cook in one vessel over the fire,
tant que li medicine soit rouge, et deviegne ausi espesse com miel;	until the medicine is red and becomes as thick as honey;
et puis pren de ceu selonc ta necessiteit, et le font en aigue et en miel,	and then take of this according to your need, and make it in water and honey,
et en clisterize lou sein, et estraint le pertus;	and in clysters the womb, and extract the pus;
et laisse la medicine ens par .ij. houres, puis l’estrai en espreignant;	and let the medicine remain in for 2 hours, then remove it by pressing.
fai ce mout de fois, tant que li seins soit mondefiiez, et soit ostee li puor;	do this many times, until the breast is defined, and the fear is removed;
et aucune fois est clisterizeis d’aigue de cendres,	and never once is it cleansed with water of ashes
quant ceste medicine n’est presens, et est que tu preignes cendres de fust de vigne, et giete aigue desus,	when this medicine isn't present, and is that you take ashes from grapevine wood, and pour water on top,
puis la coule, et en clisterize, tant que tu saiches que li seins est bien mondez;	then the colure, and in a clister, as long as you know that the breast is well-closed.
et se li malaides ne le puet soffrir, ne la medicine egiptiaine ne l’aigue de cendres,	and if the patient cannot bear it, neither Egyptian medicine nor the water of ashes,
si le clisterize d’aigue et de miel ou il ait un poc de litargire broiet;	then clysterize with water and honey or where there is a piece of litharge ground.
ou tu la clistirize de miel et de vin melleit, que li mielz ait proprieteit de mundifiier et de laver,	or you clysterize him with honey and sweet wine, that the honey may have the property of purifying and washing,
et li vins fait aerdre le sain;	and wine makes blood red;
et quant tu as ce fait, et tu as fiance que li seins est bien mundifiiez,	and when you have done this, and you have faith that the breasts are well purified,
si le clisterize de ceu que fait naistre char en li,	if the clyster of those makes flesh grow in them,
et est que tu preignes emplaustre diafinit, et le font avec oile roset et en vin;	and is that you prepare a plaster diaphinct [thin and transparent], and make it with rose oil and wine;
ou tu le clisterize d’aucunes medicines et d’oignemens, dont j’ai dit les proprietez ou traitier des oignemens;	or you cleanse it with some medicines and unguents, about which I have spoken of the properties or treating ointments;
et se li pertus dou sein est petis, et li cainne dou clistere n’i puet entrer,	and if the opening from the breast is small, and the tube of the enema cannot enter there,
si l’eslarge d’un fer un poc, et met ens une tente de l’oignement egiptiein,	if you enlarge it with an iron a bit, and place inside a tent of Egyptian ointment,
ou oignement basilicon, tant k’il soit eslargiez;	or basil ointment, until it is enlarged;
et se li plaie est trop large, si la cout et i laisse tant soulement .i. leu ou li clistere puisse entrer,	and if the wound is too wide, so the cloth and it leaves only as much .i. there where the clyster can enter
et se li pertus que giete bowe est au desus, si le cope ou plus bas leu que i est.	and if the opening that protrudes is above, so the cup or lower there than it is.
Car quant li bowe est en parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char;	For when the bowel is in full form, so do not let enter flesh;
et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues,	and if you cannot cover the breast below as you see.
si appareille en tel maniere que li bowe corre au plus bas leu que i est,	if it is arranged in such a manner that the bowel goes to the lowest place that it is.
car quant li bowe est parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char	for when the bowel is full, if one does not allow it to be emptied
et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues,	and if you cannot cover the breast below as you want,
si apareille en teil maniere: que li bowe corre legierement aval, et n’i lassier rien de la bowe;	if it is arranged in such a manner: that the bowel goes lightly downwards, and nothing of the bowel remains;
et pren medicines consolidatives por mettre sor le sein,	and take medicines consolidating to put upon the chest,
et estent sus .i. drapeil de lin que cuevre tout le sein;	and place over it one linen cloth that covers the whole chest;
puis cope as forces endroit le pertus dou sein .i. poc plus large dou premier,	then make a strong bandage on top of the wound of the chest,  one finger wider than the first,
pues estent oignement souef sus .i. autre drapel selonc la quantiteit dou pertus,	then place upon it another cloth smeared with ointment according to the quantity of the wound,
et le met sus le pertus dou sein por aligier la bowe, et n’oster mie le grant drapeil fuers que aprés maint jor une fois;	and place it on the chest hole to align the rib, and do not remove the great curtain outside until after many days once.
et celui qui est sor le pertus dou sein, oste sovent por oster la bowe,	and he who is out of the chest hole, often removed to remove the rib,
et saiches ceu que corra de la bowe, se c’est venin ou poc ou assez, ou digeste, ou indigeste;	and know that which runs from the rib, if it is venom or pus or enough, or digestible, or indigestible;
et pren warde se li patiens sent dolor ou nom, et s’il i a aposteme ou non,	and take care if the patient feels pain or no, and if there is an abscess or not,
et quant ta medicine s’est en teil maniere estendue et tu vois la nature que saut sus le pertus dou sein,	and when your medicine has spread in such a manner and you see nature rising above the chest wound,
si saiches que li seins s’aert ja, et aproche li santez;	if you know that the chest will close quickly, and approach health;
et puis le deslie le matin, ou le tier jor, et quant tu delies la plaie,	and then unbind it in the morning, or the third day, and when you unbind the wound,
si chainge .i. autre drapeil, et renovele l’oignement.	if you change one other bandage, and renew the ointment.
Et se li seins giete bowe indigeste aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie.	And if the breast lies bowed indigested after many days, know that the breast does not heal well.
Et se venins subtilz cort aprés lonc tens, si ne te desperer mie de la santeit,	And if subtle venoms cut after a long time, so do not despair of health.
car li santez aproche. Car il i a homes cui tarde enjanremens de char en ses plaies, et de ces que font le contraire;	For health approaches. For there are men whose  healing in their wounds is slow, and some who do the opposite.
et se bowe indigeste saut dou sein aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie;	And if it is bowed and indigested from the breast after many days, know that the breast does not heal well;
et se li seins tarde d’aerdre, et est porloigniez, si ajoste medicines sechans moistes en substance et seches en vertut,	and if the breast is late to heal, and is swollen, then apply drying medicines moist in substance and dry in virtue,
si com oignement diafinit, car il i a grant partie de vitriole, et c’est li derriene medicine;	as for example diaphinit ointment, because it contains a great part of vitriol, and that is the last medicine;
pren oignement dyafinit, et le font avec oile roset, et l’arose de viel vin igal en substance;	take diaphinit ointment, and make it with rose oil, and the rose of old wine equal in substance;
puis le confit et en use; et ceu meisme fait mielz cuit engroissiez,	then mix it and use it; and the same thing, cooked honey mixed into it,
quant oignemens dyafinit n’est presens,	when pain has been eliminated
ou tu pren mirre et aloen et encens, et le broie, et le poudre sus le miel quant il est sor le feu;	and you take myrrh and aloe and incense, and grind it, and powder it on honey when it is over the fire;
et puis en glue .i. drapel, et l’estent sor le sein, et aucune fois i aministre on aristologe longe,	and then you smear it with one cloth, and place it upon the chest, and once administered you apply an elongated licorice
et racines de lis celeste, qui est ausi com farine de veces et centoire;	and roots of celestial lilies, which is also as flour of wormwood and centaury.
et en use de simples ou de compostes: broie les, et en fai poudre, et met sus le miel que j’ai dit, et en use;	and in use of simples or composites: grind them, and make it into powder, and put on the honey that I said, and in use;
et se li cure est alongie, et n’est curez par ceste cure,	and if the cure is prolonged, and is not cured by this cure,
adonc saiches que la corruptions est em parfont, et fait empression en l’os, ou as membres durs, ou as liemens;	then know that the corruption has entered deep, and makes impression in the bone, or the hard members, or the limbs;
si le cure de la cure de fistule, si com nos avons dit ci devant.	if the cure of fistula, as we have said before.
de l’aposteme de l’ungle	of the abscess of the joint
Panarice est un aposteme que naist desoz l’ungle dou pouchiet de la main,	Pustule is an abscess that arises below the joint of the hand's finger
ou dou piet, ou par aventure naist en autres dois;	or in the foot, or by chance it arises in other places
et quant il est envielliez, et on n’i prent garde, si i vient .i. aposteme chaus,	and when it is neglected and one doesn't take care of it, then it becomes  one abscess
et corront et giete bowe tant qu’elle corront la racine de l’ungle, et par aventure la corront toute;	and it is stretched and laid down as long as it stretches the root of the bone, and perhaps all of it;
et vient li corrosions jusc’a l’os, tant qu’il i vient dolor puant, et est li chiés dou doi larges, et est li color fuxe.	And the corrosion comes to the bone, as long as there is a painful throbbing pain, and the head of the joint is double its size, and the color is livid.
Quant tu le cures si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie,	When you treat it as we have said in the division, and the treatment does not help;
si covient que tu copes a i. fer toute la superfluiteit qui est demoree de l’ungle,	then it is necessary that you cut with iron all the superfluousness which is hanging from the bone;
puis cauterize la plaie aprés.	then cauterize the wound after.
Li cauteres est mout grans aide se li os est sains, et li ungle est sainne;	The cautery is a great help if the bone is healthy and the joint is healthy;
et se li ungle apresse la char ens, et l’encomence a poindre, et la blece,	and if the joint follows the flesh inwards, and begins to prick, and the white part
si covient que tu mettes lou rait desoz l’ungle que point la char,	then it is necessary that you place a cloth under the joint that pricks the flesh
et la boute en haut, et cope celi char subtilment et legierement,	and the top part, and cut this carefully and lightly
et met sus le remenant de la char medicines ardans et corrosives por oster tout;	and put on the rest of the medicine hot and corrosive to remove all.
puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	then care for it with dressings until it is healed.
Et se li corrosion est en l’os, si le cope, et trai fuer, car tant com li os corrumpus i est, si ne puet saner;	And if the corruption is in the bone, then cut into it and treat it thoroughly, because as long as the bone is corrupted, it cannot heal.
et se tu vois le doi corrumpre, si le cope en .i. des nous si com il est devant dit,	and if you see the two do corrupt, so cut it in one of us as it is said before
puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	then cure it until it is healed;
et s’il est ferus, et boutez, et il sent grant dolor, si covient que tu le sainnes premier;	and if it is broken and swollen, and he feels great pain, then you must first heal it.
puis cope l’ungle dou spatumile agut en taillant de travers desus,	then cut the angle of the spatula sharp by cutting across from above,
et warde que li taille ne viegne jusc’a la char qui est desoz l’ungle, car li malaides sentiroit trop grant dolor;	and guard that the hip does not come up to the bone which is below the angle, for the patient would feel too great pain;
et s’il avient, si met chose sus qui apaise.	and if it happens, put something on top that soothes.
la dolor dou sourdoit de la main	the pain from the sore hand
Li dois ajostez qui naist en mains d’aucuns homes par aventure est toz charnus,	The two joints which are born in the hands of some men by chance are all fleshy,
et par aventure i a teil ou il a osses, et aucune fois i a ungle,	And by chance there are some where there are bones, and sometimes there is a nail.
et aucun d’aus naissent en la racine de la jointure, ou li naissance est en aucuns nous des dois.	And none of them are born at the root of the joint, where the birth is in no one of us two.
Cil qui naist en aucune nout dou doi ne se muet,	Those who are born in any of our two do not move.
et cil qui naist a la jointure dou doi, par aventure se muet;	And those who are born at the joint of the two, by chance may move;
la taille de celui qui est charnus si est legiere, en teil maniere:	The waist of one who is fleshy is light, in such a manner:
taille le en sa racine d’un large spatumile.	cut it at its root with a wide spatula.
Cil qui naist en la racine de la jointure si est grief a curer: si te tien dou coper.	He who is born in the root of the joint, there is grievous to cure; so keep it from being cut.
En celui qui naist ou doit au derrien nout, si covient que tu copes premier la char reondement jusc’a l’os,	In one who is born or must be at the back of the buttock, it is necessary that you first cut the flesh around until the bone,
puis cope l’os a une soie convenable a ceu, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	then set the bone with a suitable bandage to it, then treat it until it is healed.
Li soudemens que vient as dois ensamble vient par naissance, ou par soudement de plaie, ou par arsure de feu, ou par semblans choses.	The sores that come to the two assemblies come by birth, or by welding of a wound, or by burn of fire, or by similar things.
Si couvient que tu copes celle soudeure, si que li doit repairent selonc lor formes naturelz;	If it is necessary that you set that sore, so that the parts rejoin according to their natural forms;
puis met entre dous tentes ou drapelz moilliez en oile roset, qu’il ne se soudent;	then put between two tents or cloths moistened in rose oil, so that it does not close up;
ou tu met entre dous pieces de plonc subtilz, tant que li leus soit soudez, si com il covient.	or you put between two pieces of fine lead, until the bones are united, as is fitting.
Se soudemens vient a aucun de ses dois avec la paume, si cope celle sodure si com il covient.	If the soldering comes to none of its two with the palm, then cover that soldering as is fitting.
Des vils	Of evils
Vis sont voinnes grosses envoloupees pleines de superfluitez melancoliouses, que vienent em plusors membres dou cors;	Veins are large and full of melancholic superfluities, that come into more members of the body;
et plus avient en jambes de ces qui vont a piet et qui travaillent et portent, que a autres.	and more often happens in legs of those who go on foot and who work and carry, than in others.
Il covient donques que tu li aministres aucune fois espurgement de cole, et puis le saine de la basilique.	Therefore it is fitting that you administer to him once purging of mucus, and then the salve of the basilisk.
Li cure de fer si est selonc .ij. manieres: l’une est c’on les cope, et traie on fuer le sanc noir;	The cure with iron is according to .ij. manners: one is when they cut open and draw out the black blood;
et li autre maniere si est que tu lieves la voinne, et la trai toute fuer.	and the other manner is that you open up the vein and draw it entirely out.
Li taille si est selonc ceste maniere: arose li premier la jambe d’aigue chaude mout fort, tant que li gros sans soit subtiliiez,	The waist is treated in this manner: first raise the leg with very hot water, so that the large joint becomes soft.
puis estrain la jambe dou malaide des desus la cuixe jusc’a la partie desoz le genoil;	Then restrain the leg of the patient from above the hip to the part below the knee;
puis cope la voinne en .i. leu, ou en .ij. ou en .iij., d’une taille large,	then cut open a vein in one place, or in two or in three, with a wide incision,
puis eslieve et trair fuer le sanc noir a ta main, des l’un chief jusc’a l’autre, tant que tant de sans en isse com li vertus dou malaide puet soffrir;	then lift and draw out the black blood with your hand, from one end to the other, as much blood as the patient's strength allows.
et puis la lie, et li comande qu’il se teigne de viandes enjanrant cole noire;	and then the boil, and command him to bathe in black poultice.
et recomence l’evacuation et la sainie quant les voinnes sont plainnes, et nuist au malaide.	And restart the evacuation and bloodletting when the veins are full, and it harms the patient.
Li alevemens de li est selonc ceste maniere: reis la jambe dou malaide, s’il i a mout de poil,	The raising of the leg from the sick person is according to this manner: raise the leg of the sick person, if there are many hairs,
puis le met ou bain, et li. arose la jambe d’aigue chaude tant qu’elle deviegne rouge, et enflent les voinnes;	then put him in a bath, and raise the leg with hot water until it becomes red, and the veins swell;
et se tu n’as point de baing, si le chaufe au feu, et puis le cope endroit la voinne dou lonc au chief dou genoil, ou en la partie desoz a la cheville;	and if you have no basin, heat it over the fire, and then apply it to the vein where it is long from the arm to the knee, or in the part below to the ankle;
puis aoevre le cuir a l’oncine, et escorche la voinne de chescune part, tant qu’ele apere quant on la sent;	then work the skin with the knife, and scrape the vein from each side, until it appears as you can feel it;
et on la voit rouge et noire, et quant elle entre ou cuir si semble ausi com une corde blainche;	and you see it red and black, and when it enters the skin, it looks like a white cord;
puis boute le rait desoz, tant qu’ele soit alevee dou cuir, et puis la pent a l’oncine legier,	then push the end below, until it is lifted from the skin, and then cut it lightly with the knife;
puis le cope en .i. autre leu ensus iij. dois; puis escorche le cuir sus la voinne tant qu’ele apere,	then the cut in one other place above three fingers; then scrape the skin above the vein until it appears
puis la lieve au rais, si com tu as fait, et la pent a un autre uncine, si com tu as fait premiers;	then raise the vein to the source, like you have done, and apply it to another incision, like you have done first;
puis cope une autre taille, ou plusors se tu en as mestier, puis la lieve, et la cope au doi dou piet,	then cut another size, or more if you need them, then raise the vein, and cut at the two-finger length,
puis la trai et lieve jusc’a la seconde taille; puis l’estrai de taille en taille, tant qu’elle isse toute fuer, puis la cope;	then trace and lift it up to the second size; then extract it size by size until it is entirely free, then cut it;
et se tu ne la pues traire et lever, si i boute une aguille a tout .i. fil fort double,	and if you cannot draw it out and raise it up, then put a needle through the whole thing,
et la lie et la trai, et i boute desoz .i. rait, et torne ta main d’une part et d’autre, tant qu’il en isse;	and tie it and draw it out, and put it below one rib, and turn your hand from one side to the other, as long as it comes out;
et garde qu’elle ne cope, car s’elle cope, si ne la puet on traire ne lever, et en vient nuisement au malaide;	and keep it so that it does not break, because if it breaks, then one cannot draw it out or raise it, and it causes great pain to the patient;
et quant tu l’as toute traite, si met sor le leu de la plaie laine moillie en vin et en oile roset; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	and when you have drawn it out completely, put on top of the wound a woolen cloth soaked in wine and rose oil; and keep it covered until it is healed.
Et se li vis est contraite et torte et envoloupee ensamble, et ele n’est mie droite, si com nos avons dit,	And if the bone is contracted and twisted and wrapped together, and it is not straight, as we have said,
si covient que tu la fendes tortement, mais ne la coper mie; et la trai si com nos avons devant dit.	if it is necessary that you cut it crookedly, but do not cover it; and treat it as we have said before.
Li forme dou fer dont on cope la vis si est corbes, et ne trenche mie, qu’il ne cope la voinne;	The shape of the iron with which you cut the bone is curved, and does not cut, so that it does not cut the vein;
et est de grosse corbeure, car s’il estoit subtilz, si coperoit la voine, mais soit gros si com nos avons dit, et ci est li forme:	and is of a thick curve, because if it were subtle, it would cut the vein, but be thick as we have said, and here is the shape:
De la voinne civile	Of the civil vein
Ceste voinne est enjanree en jambes, en chaudes parties ou il ne naist herbes ne arbre, et en terre ou il n’a point de moistor;	This vein is found in legs, in hot parts where it does not give birth to herbs nor tree, and in earth where there is no moisture.
et par aventure naist autre part qu’en jambes, et ceu avient de la porriture que vient desoz le cuir,	And by chance it is born elsewhere than in legs, and this happens because of the rot that comes from under the skin,
si com il vient dedens le cors serpens et vers, enjanrez entre cuir et char.	as it comes from within the body of serpents and worms,  growing between skin and flesh.
Et se li signes de l’encomencement de ceste voinne si est qu’il vient en la jambe une tres grans enflammation,	And if the signs of the beginning of this vein are that there comes in the leg a very great inflammation,
puis se chainge li leus, et comence li voinne fors issir, ausi com une racine d’une plante.	then the veins change, and the vein begins to burst forth, like the root of a plant.
Quant li chiés apert, si covient que tu envoloupes entor une piece de plonc des une З et demi jusc’a .ij. З., et la noe,	When the shoulder opens, then you must wrap around it a piece of plank from one and a half to two inches, and knot,
et laisse le plonc pendant a la jambe, et totes les fois qu’il en ist point au defuer, si l’envoloupe entor le plonc, et la nowe;	and leave the plank on the leg, and all times that it aches in the fire, then wrap around the plank, and knot it;
et s’elle est trop longe, si en cope une partie, et envoloupe le remenant, et ne la coper mie en sa racine, tant qu’elle soit toute issue;	And if it is too long, cut a part of it, and wrap the remaining part, and do not cut it at its root, until it is all emerged.
car se tu la copes, si rentre en la char, et fait venir aposteme et porriture ou leu, et male maladie;	For if you cut it, it will go back into the flesh, and cause an abscess and rot there, and a bad illness.
por la queil chose il covient qu’elle soit traite poc et poc jusc’a chief, et n’en remaigne rien ou cors;	Therefore for that reason it is necessary that it be treated carefully and bit by bit until the head, and nothing of it remains in the flesh.
et est aucune fois ceste voinne quant elle est traite de .v. paumes de lonc, ou de .x.,	And it sometimes happens this vein when it is treated to be .v. palms long, or .x.,
et uns hons vint ja a moi, a cui elle issit de .x. paumes de long, et quant tu la copes, si boute .i. rais ou pertus, et la perce jusc’a fons,	and one man came to me, who had a bone that was 10 palms long, and when you cut it, it shoots out 1 spear or thrusts, and the pierces to the bottom
si que tout en isse; et soit vuidie li matiere qui est dedens, et amenistre au leu medicines enjanrans porriture aucun jor, puis le cure si com les apostemes.	so that all of it exits; and empty the material which is inside, and administer to the place medicines preventing rotting any day, then cure it like abscesses.
Et aucune fois a ceste voinne mains rains, et meismement quant elle apert en la jointure dou piet, ou ou piet,	And no times at this vein mains veins, and also when it opens in the joint of the foot, or foot,
et i vient mout de pertus, et dont il saut rains; cure le donques si com nos avons dit devant.	and there comes much blood, and from which it jumps veins; cure it therefore as we have said before.
Des vers qui naissent entre cuir et char	Of worms that are born between skin and flesh
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «maladie de buef», por ceu qu’elle avient maintes fois as bués,	This disease is called in our land "ox's malady", because it often happens to oxen,
et est un petis vers qui naist entre cuir et char, et va par tout le cors montant et dessendant,	and is a small worm that is born between skin and flesh, and goes throughout the body going up and down,
et le sent om bien a l’aler de membre en membre, tant qu’il desront le cuir ou il vait, et saut fuer;	and one feels it well as it moves from limb to limb, until it reaches the skin where it goes, and leaps forth;
et est enjanrez de porriture d’aucunes humors, si com vienent vers et serpens et lumbris et ascarides ou ventre;	and it is caused by rotting of some humors, such as come serpents and worms and ascaritides in the belly.
et doute on de son malice, car quant il va par le cors, et il monte au chief, et il vient a l’oil,	and one doubts its evil, because when it goes through the body, and it ascends to the head, and it comes to the eye.
par aventure rentre, et destruit l’oil; et ceu avient maintes fois.	by chance enters, and destroys the eye; and this happens many times.
Quant tu le vues curer et traire, si ne puet on fuers que quant il vait:	When you see it being cured and drained, there is nothing to be feared but when it goes:
si covient donques que tu lies le leu desus et desoz d’un fort liien bien estroitement,	so then it is necessary that you bind the place above and below with a strong linen very tightly
puis cope sus et le trai fuer, et se li vers est em parfont en la char, et tu ne le trueves,	then cut on top of it and bring out the thread, and if the arrow is buried deep in the flesh, and you don't find it
si le cauterize de feu sus, tant qu’il muire;	then cauterize it with fire until it dies.
et li plus grans nuisemens que il fait, si est qu’il corront l’oil, si com nos avons dit;	and the greatest harm that it can do is that it corrupts the eye, as we have said;
et se tu le vois venir ou chief pres de l’oil, si estraint desoz lui le sorcil forment, puis cope sus, et le trai fuer;	and if you see it coming or near the eye, hold under it the eyebrow shape, then cut above and the treat further.
et covient user le malaide de mundifiement de cors de medicines solutives por les males humors porries,	And it is necessary to use the patient of purification of body of medicines solutives for the bad humors corrupted.
et se warse de viandes enjanrans porriture.	and if there are rotten meats preventing putrefaction.
De la dolor qui vient de ventositeit	Of the pain that comes from windiness
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «vakirir», et est une dolor que vient en aucuns membres,	This illness is called "vakirir" in our land, and it is a pain that comes in certain limbs.
et pues se mue de membre en membre; et je vis ceu que je vos di.	and then moves from limb to limb; and I have seen what I tell you.
Je fui apelez a une femme malaide, et me descovrit som bras, et vis une petite enfleure en la voinne dou brais;	I was called to a sick woman, and she uncovered her arm, and I saw a small swelling in the vein of the arm;
et .i. poc aprés, li vis monter ausi com un ver a l’espaule,	and just a little after, I saw it rise as if a worm to the shoulder,
plus tost que nulle chose, ausi com vif argent quant il cort de leu a autre;	Sooner than anything else, as quickly as living silver when it departs from its place;
li dolor se departit de celui leu, et se ficha en l’espaule,	The pain departs from that place and goes into the shoulder.
et puis un poc aprés corrut par tout le cors, tant qu’ele vint en l’autre brais;	And then a little while after it spreads throughout the body, until it reaches the other arm;
puis me contait qu’elle tornioit adés entor le cors, si com je la vis.	then she told me that it returned to its original place around her body, as I saw it.
Je me mervillai mout coment elle se movoit ensi de membre em membre, car je n’avoie onques veut ceste maladie selonc ceste maniere.	I marveled greatly how she moved thus from limb to limb, for I never wanted this sickness in this manner.
Toutevoie, je avoie veut maint que bien avoient veut movoir dolor de leu a autre,	However, I had seen many that well moved pain from one place to another,
mais je ne l’avoie mie veut, si com je le vis en la femme;	but I had not seen it like this, as I saw it in the woman;
et je me pensai que c’estoit por ceu que li femme avoit sec cors, et les voinnes descovertes,	and I thought to myself that it was because the woman had a dry body, and veins uncovered,
et por ceu apparoit celle ventositez constrainte;	and because of this appears that constraint of windiness;
et n’aperent mie selonc ceste raison a ces qui sont delicious, et qui ont moistes cors et voinnes reponues.	and do not appear according to this reason to those who are delicate and have moist bodies and veins full.
Et quant tu vues curer ceste maladie, et li malaides sent celle dolor, s’elle t’apert si com nos avons dit,	And when you see curing this disease, and the patient feels that pain, if it appears to you as we have said,
si la lie desus et desoz hastanment, et puis cope sus tant que cele ventositez constrainte au leu isse fuer;	if the  lump above and below evenly, and then cut until that windiness constraint in its place has disappeared;
et cauterize le leu; et se tu ne la vois a tes eulz,	And cauterize the place; and if you do not see it with your eyes,
si le cure de ceu qui deboute les ventositez, si com pilules fetides, et pilules de serapin, et semblans autres.	if you treat this by those who expel wind, such as foul pills, and pills of serpent, and similar others.
Des saiettes	Of arrows
Les saiettes sont diverses, selonc lor semblances et selonc les leus dou cors ou elles chient.	Arrows are diverse, according to their appearances and according to the places in the body where they lie.
Li diversitez de lor si est qu’il i a de celles qui ont grans pointes, et petites, et chevees, et soudees;	The diversity of them is that some have large points, and small, and hairy, and soldered.
et de celles qui ont .ij. angles, et de celz qui ont lengues, et de celles ou il a pieces;	and some which have two angles, and those which have tongues, and those which have pieces;
et celle qui chiet en aucun membre si chiet selonc .ij. manieres: ou en membre principeil cheveit,	and those which fall in any member if they fall in two ways: either in the principal member it falls,
si com cerveil, cuer, foie, pormon, rains, intestine, vessie, et semblans membres.	such as brain, heart, liver, stomach, lungs, intestines, bladder, and similar members.
Quant elle chiet donques en aucun leu de ces membres, et li signe de mort, que je te dirai ci aprés, t’aperent:	When it falls therefore in any place of these limbs, and the sign of death, which I shall tell you afterwards, appear to you:
si covient que tu te warses de l’estraction de ceste saiette, car li mors vient aprés en plusors dispositions;	if it is necessary that you take care of the extraction of this arrow, because death comes afterwards in many dispositions;
et quant cist mal signe ne t’aperent mie, et li saiette n’est mie em parfont, si la trai, et cure la plaie.	and when this bad sign does not appear to you, and the arrow is not deeply embedded, then treat it, and care for the wound.
Et li signe dou cerveil quant li saiette i chiet et perce l’os, et saut li syfac fuer qui est sus le cerveil,	And the sign of the brain when the arrow falls and pierces the bone, and leaps the dura mater which is above the brain,
est quant scotomie et sode et esvertin et roujor ens eulz, et enflammation et roujor de lengue, et spasme et permixtion d’entendement, et vomissemens de cole;	is when there is scotomia and sode and esvertin and redness in the eyes, and inflammation and redness of the tongue, and spasm and confusion of understanding, and vomiting of bile.
et per aventure ist sans fuer des narines, ou des oreilles; et par aventure pert la parole et la voix;	and perhaps it is without fever of the nostrils, or of the ears; and perhaps he loses speech and voice;
et saut de la plaie moistor blanche semblant a poulz, et en saut ausi com bruee de char;	and leaps from the wound moisture white seeming to pus, and leaps also like burning of flesh;
et se cist signe t’aperent, si te tien de la cure, et trai la saiette s’elle n’est ens.	and if this sign appears to you, then hold back from the cure, and treat the arrow if it is not yet inside;
Li signe de la siette quant elle chiet ou cuer, sont qu’elle est pres de la mamele senestre, et sent ausi com s’elle estoit fichie en chose dure, ne mie vuide;	The sign of the seventh when it falls or heart, are that it is near the left breast, and it feels as if it were tied in something hard, not empty.
et par aventure li siette se muet ausi com li poulz, et en cort noir sanc, et vient froidor et suor froide, et sincope:	and by chance the seventh moves like the hand, and in short black blood, and comes coldness and cold sweat, and syncope:
saiches adonc sens doute ke li mors dessent.	know then without doubt that death approaches.
Et li signe de la saiette que nevre lou pormon est que sans plains d’escume saut de la plaie, et li gorge enfle, et li malaides mue color, et sospire haut et quiert le froit ar.	And the sign of the seventh that never moves is that without pains, foam leaps from the wound, and the throat swells, and the patient turns blue, and gasps loudly and seeks cold air.
Et se li saiette chiet en la coverture dou pis, si est delez les petites costes; et giete grant alainne et grant dolor et sospire; et li muevent tuit li membre des espaules.	And if the arrow falls into the covering of the hip, it is near the ribs; and throws great pain and great pain and sighing; and they move all the members of the shoulders.
Et se li saiette chiet ou stomac, par aventure si saut de la plaie aucune chose de la viande indigeste.	And if the arrow falls into the stomach, perhaps it leaps from the wound any thing indigestible flesh.
