Et se li saiette chiet ou ventre, et en saut point de fien par l’intestine rout, si n’a point d’esperance en la cure, ne en l’estraction de la saiette.	And if the arrow falls into the belly, and leaps no point of straw through the intestine rout, it has no hope in the cure, nor in the extraction of the arrow.
Et se li saiette chiet en la vessie, et li urine en saut et vient defuer, et li malaides sent fort dolor: saiches que li plaie est mortelz.	And if the arrow falls into the bladder, and the urine leaps out and comes outward, and the patient feels great pain: know that the wound is mortal.
Li autre membre, si com li faice et li colz et li gorge et li espaule et li adjutoire et li espinee dou dos et li forcele et li cuixe et les jambes, et li membre semblant, sont sauf selonc plusors dispositions.	The other member, such as the arm and neck and throat and shoulder and auxiliary and spine of the back and hip and legs, and the similar members, are safe according to more dispostitions.
Quant li saiette est en lou nerf ou l’artere, et elle n’est venimouse, si com je vos dirai qu’il m’avint, por ceu que vos faciez autretel.	When the arrow is in the nerve or artery, and it is not venomous, as I will tell you that it happened to me, for that reason that you do otherwise.
Il avint a .i. home c’une saiette li chut ou larmier en la racine dou neis:	It happened to one man with an arrow lodged or fell into the root of the nose:
je la tentai, et la traï d’autre part desoz la graisse de l’oreille, et fut sanez sens nusement.	I tried it, and pulled it out from the other side below the fat of the ear, and was healed without any trouble.
Et traï a un jeu une saiette que li chut en la graisse de l’oil desoz la papiere desoz,	And treat one wound with an arrow that fell in the fat of the eye under the eyelid
et li saiette estoit reponue, et n’en poi ataindre que la pointe devers lou fust,	and the arrow was positioned, and one could only reach its tip towards the shaft
et estoit li saiette grans d’un arc turcois, a tout .i. fer legier sens oreilles; li jeus fut sanez, et ne li vint nulz mavais accidens.	and the arrow was large as a Turkish bow, with one and a half light iron without ears; the wound was sound, and no bad accidents befell him.
Et traï une saiette de la gorge a un crestien, et estoit li saiette arabique a oreilles:	And treat an arrow from the throat of a Christian, and the arrow was Arabic with ears:
je soiai les barbions, et subtiliai tant que je la traï, et fut sanez li crestiens.	I shaved the bristles, and subtly so that I tricked him, and he was healed among Christians.
Et traï une saiette a .i. home, que li estoit cheue ou ventre, et pensai qu’il moroit;	And tricked an arrow into a man, who it was in his back or belly, and thought that he would die.
et puis qu’il ot passez .xxx. jors, si ne mua point sa disposition;	and then when he had passed thirty days, he did not change his condition;
je taillai sus la saiette, et l’engignai, et la traï fuer, et n’ot point de mavais accident.	I cut above the arrow, and I enwrapped it, and I drew it out, and there was no bad accident.
Et si vis .i. home cui une saiette chut ou dos, et fut li plaie soudee sus;	And if you see a man who has an arrow shot or through his back, and the wound was sewn up above;
et demora li saiette dedens li, et ne chainja point ses dispositions naturez,	and the arrow remains inside him, and does not change its natural position,
ne ne trova nuisement en aucune de ses oevres naturelz.	nor feels any discomfort in any of its natural works.
Et vis .i. autre homme, cui il chut une saiette en sa faice, et fut soudee li plaie;	And see another man, to whom an arrow was shot into his face, and the wound was sewn up;
et demora ensi sens soffrir grant dolor; et mout d’autres semblans.	and endures thus suffering great pain; and many other similar things.
Et traï une saiette a .i. home des princes le roi, que li estoit cheue enmi lou neiz,	And treat an arrow in the head of Prince the king, who it was stuck in his middle
et estoit un poc declinans a la destre partie; et estoit li saiette toute reponue	and was slightly leaning toward the right side; and the arrow was completely retracted
Je fui apelez a la cure aprés ceu qu’elle fut cheue .iij. jors. Si trovai la plaie mult estroite.	I was called to treat it after three days had passed. I found the wound very tight.
Je la quis a tout une subtil tente, et ne la sentis mie;	I took it with a whole fine tent, and did not feel it at all.
et il sentoit pointure et dolor desoz sa destre oreille.	And he felt pricking and pain below his right ear.
Je pensai que c’estoit de la pointe de la saiette	I thought that it was from the tip of the arrow
Je mis sus lou leu emplaustre atratifet digestif, por ceu que li leus n’enflast;	I put on its place a plaster atramentous and digestive, because the lesion did not swell;
et m’aparut li leus de la saiette.	and appeared to me the tracks of the arrow.
Je i mis l’emplaustre mains jors, et resouda li plaie derechief, et demora ensi li malaides lonc tens,	I laid the plaster on it for some days, and closed up the wound directly, and kept the patient there a long time.
tant qu’il sentit la saiette .i. jor dedens son neis; et il le me dist.	until he felt the arrow i.e., one day inside his flesh; and he told me this.
Je mis sus la plaie medicine ague corrosive par mains jors, tant qu’elle fut overte,	I put on the wound a corrosive medicine for some days, until it was open.
et la tentai, et sentis le chief de la saiette qui s’aerdoit au leu;	and feel the head of the arrow which hardens in place;
puis ajostai en l’overture de la plaie par celle medicine ague, tant que li chiés de la saiette m’aparut visablement;	then I adjusted it in the opening of the wound with that sharp medicine, until the head of the arrow appeared visibly to me;
et trespassa bien li termines entor .iiij. mois,	and pierced well the extremities for four months;
et puis eslarja si li plaie que je i boutai les tenailles, et le meus d’une part et d’autre, et ne pot issir;	and then widened so the wound that I put tweezers in it, and mine on one side and the other, and it could not exit;
adonques ne cessai de subtiliier et d’engignier de manieres d’estrumens, tant que je la pris .i. jor as tenailles bien faites,	Therefore, do not cease to subtlety and devise ways of instruments, until I took one day pliers well made
selonc ceu que sa forme venra en la fin de cest chapistre, tant que je la traï, et restourai la plaie.	according to what its form will come at the end of this chapter, as long as I treated it and restored the wound.
Et li mire jugent que li cartillaige dou nez ne puet restorer:	And the wise judge that the cartilage of the nose cannot be restored:
je la restourai adonques, et fut soudee li plaie, et fut sanez li malaides entierement.	I restored it then, and the wound was closed, and the patient was healed entirely.
Or t’ai dit la qualiteit de l’estraction d’aucunes saiettes,	I have said to you the quality of the extraction of some arrows,
si que tu mettes ta cure sus ceu que je ne dis mie, car li livres ne puet mie tout porprendre;	so that you put your care on those that I do not say, because the books cannot take in everything;
mais li saiges maistres compere sus bien poc grant chose, et sus ceu que li est present et defaillant,	but the wise masters compare well only on a few things, and those that are present and lacking
trueve nueve oevre, et nuef estrument, au dessendement des choses estrainges qui avienent en cest art.	find new works, and new instruments, for the arrangement of strange things which happen in this art.
Je dis que les saiettes n’issent des membres ou elles sont fichies fuer que selonc .ij. manieres:	I say that arrows are not removed from limbs where they are lodged except according to two ways:
ou par lou leu ou elles entrent, ou par d’autre part;	or by the place where they enter, or by another side;
et celle que saut fuer par lai ou elle entre, c’est saiette entrans en leus charnus, et saut fuer aucune fois maintenant.	and that which must be removed by the place where it enters is an arrow that has entered into the flesh, and must not be removed at any other time.
Et s’elle ne saut maintenant, si la laisse tant que li chars soit porrie entor, et soit alegie li issue;	And if it cannot be removed now, then let it remain until the flesh is healed and the opening closes;
et ausi s’elle est fichie en l’os, et elle ne puet issir, si la laisse ensi aucuns jors, et la muef chescun jor;	and also if it is fixed in the bone, and it cannot move, leave it like that for some days, and move it every day.
et adonques elle saut, et s’elle ne saut, si perce entor a tout .i. foret subtil, tant que li leus entor soit eslargiez, et puis la trai.	and then if it does not jump out, pierce around it to all i.e., the forest fine, as long as the surrounding tissues are spread wide open, and then treat it.
Et se li saiette est fichie en l’os dou chief, et vait jusc’a l’un des ventres dou cerveil,	And if the arrow is fixed in the bone of the head, and goes up to one of the ventricles of the brain,
et aucuns des accidens que j’ai dit apert au malaide: si ne la traire mie, mais la laisse tant qu’elle soit igalz aprés aucuns jors,	and some of the accidents that I have said appear to the patient: then do not treat it, but leave it until it is healed after some days,
car se li saiette vient jusc’a syfac, c’est li mors.	for if the arrow comes to the shaft, it is death.
Et se li saiette n’est fichie fuer qu’en l’os soulement, et ne vient jusc’a syfac,	And if the arrow is only lodged in the bone and does not come to the shaft,
et demoure li malaides aucuns jors sens mavais accident, si l’engigne dou traire.	and the patient remains for several days without bad accidents, then the engine of healing.
Et s’elle est mout fichie ensi et ne puet issir fuer, si i aministre tareres entor, si com je t’ai dit; puis cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it is deeply lodged and cannot be extracted further, then administer tarers around it, as I have told you; then cure the wound until it is healed.
Et se li saiette est reponue en leu dou cors si c’on ne la puisse veoir, si la quier a tout la tente;	And if the arrow is returned to its place in the body so that one cannot see it, then search all around.
et se tu la sens, si la trai a aucun estrument covenauble;	and if you feel it, treat it with no suitable instrument;
et se tu ne pues por l’estrecement de la plaie, et por la parfondesce de la saiette,	and if you cannot because of the narrowness of the wound, and the depth of the arrow,
et il n’i a os ne nerf ne voine, si la fens tant que li plaie soit grans;	and there are no bones or nerves or veins, then widen the wound as much as possible.
et trai la saiette se tu pues, et s’il ait en la saiette oreilles a coi elle tient,	and treat the arrow if you can, and if it has ears at its base where it holds
si oste la char qui est ens fichie de .ij. pars au mues que tu pues,	if remove the bone that is embedded in two parts as much as you can
et puis brise ou ploie les oreilles de la saiette, tant que tu la puisses traire;	and then break or bend the ears of the arrow, as much as you can draw it out;
et subtilie bien que tu ne brisier la saiette, que tu la trairoies plus griement.	and do it carefully so that you don't break the arrow, but rather draw it out more easily.
Et se tu ne pues a une fois, si la lai jusque li leus entor soit porris, puis la trai, car li estraction iert alegie.	And if you cannot at one time, then let it stay until the place is healed, then treat it, for the extraction hurts.
Et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de la cure en son chapistre;	And if the flow of blood opposes you, then administer what we have said in the treatment chapter.
et te warde de l’incision dou nerf et de la voinne, et met engien coment tu pues mues traire la saiette sens peril,	and guard yourself from cutting into the nerve and vein, and put  everything you can to remove the arrow without danger.
ou tost ou tart, ou fermement ou belement; et met le malaide selonc la forme qu’il estoit quant li saiette li chut ens,	Whether quickly or slowly, whether firmly or gently; and put the patient according to the form that he was in when the arrow struck him.
car c’est li plus grans aide que i soit, et se tu ne pues, si lou met selonc ceu que li signe lou te mostrent.	because this is the greatest help that it is, and if you cannot, place it according to what the signs show you.
Li saiette que vient fuer d’autre part, ou il apert aucune chose de li, ou li cuir est enflez endroit si c’on le voit ou sent aparamment:	The arrow that comes from another part, or where it does not appear anything of it, or the skin is swollen in the place if one sees it or feels it apparently:
taille donques sus, tant que les tenailles i puissent prendre, et puis l’estrai: si saut fuer maintenant.	Cut then above, as long as the pliers can take hold, and then extract it: if it jumps out now.
Et s’elle est retenue en l’os, si tornoie ta main rondement, tant qu’elle entre en l’os, et eslarge l’os, puis la trai.	And if it is held in the bone, then turn your hand roundly, until it enters the bone, and enlarge the bone, then extract it.
Et s’elle ne puet issir, si la laisse encor, et puis rencomence l’estraction tant qu’elle isse fuer;	And if it cannot move out, leave it there still, and then begin the extraction again until it moves out.
et se li fust de la saiette i est, se le boute a tout le fust;	and if the arrow shaft is in it, pull it out with all your strength.
et se li fust chiet, et tu vues aministrer boutement, si i aministre .i. estrument cheveit,	and if the shaft has fallen, and you see to administer pressure, then administer one instrument which is pointed,
si que li pointe de la saiette entre en la cheveure de l’estrument; et puis boute fuer,	so that the point of the arrow enters into the opening of the instrument, and then pull it out.
et se li saiette est chevee, se i boute .i. estrument a pointe entrant ens, por alegier l’estraction.	And if the arrow is lodged, thrust one instrument with a point entering it, to aid extraction.
Et se li saiette est entouchie, si covient que tu copes toute la char entor ou li venins est, se tu pues,	And if the arrow is encircled, then it is necessary that you cut all the flesh around where the venom is, if you can.
puis cure la plaie si com il couvient.	then treat the wound as is fitting.
Et se li saiette chiet ou peis ou au ventre ou a la vessie ou au costeit, et elle est prochiene, et tu pues coper sus, se i cope;	And if the arrow strikes in the leg or abdomen or bladder or ribs and is close (to the surface), and you can cut into it, then cut.
et te garde de coper la voinne et lou nerf, et puis l’estrai, et puis cout la plaie, se mestier est;	and keep yourself from covering the vein and the nerve, and then extract it, and then sew the wound, if it is necessary;
et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	and treat it until it is healed.
Li forme des tenailles dont on trait les saiettes sont semblans au bec d’oiseil, et vez ci la forme:	The form of the pliers that one treats arrows with are similar to an eye's beak, and see here the form:
Et en sont mout de manieres: grans, moienes, et petites, selonc la quantitei de la saiette.	And there are many ways: large, medium, and small, according to the quantity of the arrow.
Li forme dou boutant cheveit est ausi com li penne d’un oisel,	The form of the hair end is like the feather of a bird,
por bouter a la pointe de la saiette, si com ci est li forme:	to put it to the tip of an arrow, as such is the form:
li forme des tenailles por bouter et por sachier si est ci:	the form of the pliers for putting in and taking out is this:
des voinnes dou cors communes	of the veins of the common body
Des voinnes dont on se saine sont .xxxi., de coi il a ou chef xvi.,	There are thirty-one veins from which one heals, of which there are sixteen at the head.
c’est a savoir: .ij. batans qui sont aprés les oreilles, qui sont apelees les dous «herbech»;	That is to say: two bats that are after the ears, which are called the two "herbesch";
et les .ij. arteres qui sont en .ij. temples apparans;	and the two arteries that are in the two temples appearing;
et .ij. voines que sont en .ij. larmiers des .ij. eulz, que sont apelees «aspires»;	and two veins that are in the two tear ducts of the two eyes, which are called "aspirates";
et li voine que est emmi le front; et li voinne que est au chief dou neis;	and the vein that is at the forehead; and the vein that is at the top of the nose;
et les .ij. guindeges qui sont ou col;	and the two veins that are on the neck;
et les .ij. voinnes que sont en levres desus de la bouche, et ce sont les voines que sont apelees «augeherich»;	and the two veins that are in the lips above the mouth, and these are the veins called "augeherich";
et .ij. voinnes que sont desoz la lengue.	and two veins that are under the tongue.
Les voinnes dont on saine communement sont .v. en chescun bras:	The veins which are commonly used are five in each arm:
l’une est li cephalique, et est dou senestre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou chief»;	One is the cephalic vein, and it is on the inside of the arm, and the common people call it “vein of the head”;
et li moiene est apelee «faste», et est composte de la cephalique et de la basilique,	And the middle one is called “median”, and it is composed of the cephalic and the basilica.
et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou cuer»; et li basilique si est ou destre costeit,	And the common people call it “vein of the heart”; and the basilica is on the outside of the arm,
et l’apelent li laie gent «voinne dou ventre», et est sus le foscile,	and the common people call it "vein of the belly," and is on the hollow
et est celle dont on saine, qui apert manifestement sus le pouchet.	and is the one that is opened, which clearly appears on the pouch.
Et li salvatelle est li voine qui est entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire, et si a .ij. rains;	And the sap vein is the vein between the little finger and the ring finger, and it has two veins;
et en la jambe et ou piet sont .iij. voinnes: l’une si est desoz la corbeure dou pochet dou senestre costeit,	and in the leg and where the foot is there are three veins: one is below the curve of the pouch of the left side;
et li seconde sophene qui est a la cheville dou destre costeit; et li voine qui est apelee «nesse», que est en la cheville de l’autre costei;	and the second saphenous vein which is at the ankle of the right side; and the vein which is called "nevus," that is in the ankle of the other side.
et en l’autre jambe sont .iij. voinnes desoz celles.	and in the other leg there are three veins below those.
Li sainie des voinnes que sont aprés les oreilles si aide as catharres anciens, et a emigraine;	The vein of the veins that are after the ears so helps with old catarrhs, and migraines;
et li qualiteis dou sainier, si com je te dis, et est que tu reises lou chief dou malaide,	and the qualities of the vein, as I tell you, and is that you raise the head of the patient,
et frote lou leu ou les voinnes sont d’un drap aspre; puis estrigne li malaides son col a une vis,	and rub the place where the veins are with a rough cloth; then tighten the patient's neck with a vise
tant que les .ij. voinnes aperent derrier les oreilles en .ij. leus dependens dou chief:	until the two veins appear behind the ears in two lengths depending on the head:
quier les donques a ton doi, et ou tu sens lou poulz desoz ton doi, si seigne d’enche;	who then to your back, and where you feel the pulse below your back, reign it in;
puis pren la lancette, et la boute par desoz la voine jusc’a l’os, puis lieve ta main a tout la voinne amont,	then take the lancet and insert it beneath the vein to the bone, then lift your hand all along the vein upwards,
et cope et lou cuir et la voinne bien .ij. dois dou traver, et fai issir dou sanc tant que tu vues;	and scrape and the skin and the vein well two times to traverse, and make blood flow as much as you see.
puis l’estrain et lie, tant qu’ele soit sanee;	then restrain and bind it, until it is healed.
et j’ai ja dit l’incision et le cautere ou premier livre.	and I have already said about incision and cautery in the first book.
Li sainie des .ij. arteres que sont en .ij. temples, si vaut a emigrainne anciene,	The  blood letting of the two arteries that are in the two temples, is good for ancient migraine,
et sode, et obtalmie acostumee, et au cors des larmes agues as eulz;	and suddenly, and habitual squinting, and on the body of sharp tears to the eyes;
et li qualitez dou sainier si est si com je dis:	and the qualities of the vein are so as I say:
et est que li malaides estraigne son col, tant que les .ij. voinnes aperent apertement;	and that the patient stretches his neck so that the two veins appear clearly;
et sent lou polz desoz ton doi, et puis seigne d’enche;	and feel the pulses below your back, and then he will know which one to open;
puis lieve lou keur sus la voinne en haut a ton doi indice, et boute la lancette desoz,	Then lightly place your finger on the vein above your right index finger, and thrust the lance underneath.
et lieve la voine en haut, et la cope, si com tu as fait en .ij. autres voinnes, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit;	And lightly raise the vein above, and cover it, as you have done with two other veins, and make a cut of blood according to your need;
puis deslie lou malaide, et met ton doi sus la voine une houre, puis met sus coton;	Then unbind the patient, and place your hand on the vein for an hour, then put cotton on top;
et puis la lie forment, et la laisse tant qu’elle soit sanee; et nos en avons jai parleit et de lor copement et de lor estraction, ou comencement dou livre.	And then form a bandage, and leave it until it is healed; and we have spoken about their covering and extraction, as the beginning of this book.
Li sainie de la voine dou front si vaut autant com li sainie de la cephalique as maladies de la faice ancienes, et a emigraine, et a roujor;	The bloodletting of the vein of the forehead is worth as much as the bloodletting of the cephalic for illnesses of the face ancient, and to migraine, and to redness.
et li qualitez si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant, tant que li voine apere;	and the qualities are that the patient strains their neck by twisting, until the vein appears;
puis pren l’estrument qui est apelez «fosseur», dont ci est li forme:	then take the instrument which is called "fossor", whose shape is:
Et met la pointe sus la voinne, et fier sus de ta main, ou d’autre chose, et laisse dou sanc issir selonc la quantiteit que tu vues;	And place the point on the vein, and steady it with your hand, or something else, and let the blood flow according to the quantity that you see.
puis delie au malaide le col, et lie la voine tant qu’elle soit saneel et aucune fois l’uevre on d’un flaime large.	Then bind the patient's neck, and tie the vein until it is healed and never once work with a wide flame.
Toutevoie, il ne covient mie que li flaimes soit trop agus; et le saine de travers, car li os est pres, et par aventure brise li flaimes quant il est subtilz.	However, it is not proper for the flames to be too large; and the healing across, because the bone is close, and by chance breaks the flames when they are subtle.
Li sainie des .ij. voines que sont en .ij. larmiers si aide as eulz, et a la tigne, et a la roujor, et a l’oriuel en l’oil, et as maladies de la faice;	The healing of the two veins that are in two tear ducts helps the eyes, and the beard, and the redness, and the oriflamme in the eye, and illnesses of the face;
et li qualitez de lor sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant d’aucun liien, si com devant;	and the qualities of their healing are that the patient strains his neck by twisting with a rope, as before;
puis le saine, et soit li sainie dou traver, un poc dou lonc dou flaime un poc large, car il n’i a point de char.	then make it sound, and whether it is healed through the traversing, one part of the long of the flame one part wide, because there is no flesh.
Et se li flaimes est subtilz, par aventure si brise; puis fai corre dou sanc, tant com tu en as mestier, et puis lie sus couton, et le lie bien.	And if the flames are subtle, by chance it breaks; then make correction of the blood, as much as you have need, and then tie on cloth, and tie it well.
Li sainie de la voine dou neis si vaut a ague, et a sode forsenee, et a maladies de faice,	The  opening of the vein of the needs is good for fever, and for snake bites, and for diseases of the face
si com emigraine et roujor que vient en la faice, et meimement quant elle est anciene;	such as migraine and redness that comes in the face, and even when it is old.
et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estrigne son col, puis estrain son neis a ta main senestre,	And the qualities of the vein are such that the patient constricts his neck, then strains his nose to your left hand
et pren lou flaime subtil lonc, et le fiche emmi la levre en l’espaice qui est entre les .ij. narines,	And takes a subtle long flame, and inserts it between the two nostrils in the space.
car li voinne n’apert mie bien enqui, et li sans comencera maintenant a corre;	For the vein does not open well then, and the blood will now begin to flow;
et n’aler mie trop em parfont, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit, puis la lie une nuit, car elle est mout tost restoree;	And do not allow it to go too far in depth, and make blood flow according to your need, then tie it up for the night because it is very quickly restored;
et c’est li forme dou flaime:	and this is the form of the flame:
Li sainie des .ij. guindeges si aide a l’estrecement de l’alainne, et a l’encomencement de meselerie, et a mout de maladies, et a empetigine, et a corrodens, et a herpes, et estiomenes;	The blood of the two reeds helps in the treatment of burns, and at the beginning of leprosy, and many diseases, and scabies, and erosion, and herpes, and boils.
et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col desoz l’une et l’autre, si com nos avons dit;	and the qualities of the blood are that the patient extracts his neck under both, as we have said.
et soit li maistres estans sus lou chief dou malaide, et li malaides siece sus .i. siege,	and let the master be standing above the head of the patient, and the patient sitting on one seat,
puis saine la voine dou lonc un poc largement, puis trai dou sanc tempreement, ou tant com mestier est;	then heal the vein long a little widely, then treat of blood moderately, or as much as is necessary;
puis refai autreteil en l’autre voinne, puis deslie lou liien, et estraint andous les voines moienement,	then redo the other side in the other vein, then untie the linen, and strain all the veins moderately,
que li malaides n’estrangle; et le laisse jusc’au matin, que li plaie soit sanee.	so that the patient does not strangle; and leave it until morning, so that the wound is healed.
De la sainie des leivres	Of healing the veins
Li sainie des voinnes des levres desus si aident a cole en la bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et fendures de levres, et dou neis et entor.	The blood of the veins of the lips above helps to heal in the mouth, and corruption of gums, and splits of lips, and wounds and sores.
Et li qualitez de la sainie si est de faire seoir lou malaide devant toi, et estraint son col si com j’ai dit;	And the qualities of the blood is to make the patient sit before you, and restrain his neck as I have said;
puis torne la levre, et regarde as .ij. voinnes, dont l’une est a la destre levre et li autre a la senestre,	then turn the lip, and look at the two veins, one on the right lip and the other on the left,
et les conoist on par ceu qu’elles sont noires, et par ceu que entor elles a voines menues noires:	and you will recognize them by those that are black, and by those that around them have small black veins:
cope donques l’une et l’autre, et se tu ne les conois, et tu en es en doutance,	cope therefore one and the other, and if you do not know them, and you are in doubt,
si cope la plus grosse de chescune part, et tout ausi fai des .ij. voinnes que sont desus et desoz, car c’est une meisme maniere.	if cope the largest of each part, and also make two veins that are above and below, because it is a same manner.
De la sainie desoz la lengue	Of the vein below the tongue
Li sainie des voinnes que sont desoz la lengue si aide aprés la sainie de la cephalique, et c’est a l’estrecement de la gorge, et as maladies de l’uve, et as maladies de la bouche;	The vein below the tongue is helpful after the cephalic vein, and it is for the treatment of the throat, and diseases of the eye, and diseases of the mouth;
et li qualitez dou sainier si est que li malaides siece entre tes mains devant lou soleil, et li lieve la lengue, et regarde desoz en chescun costeit une voinne noire:	and the qualities of the veins are such that the patient lies between your hands before the sun, and lifts the tongue, and looks below on each side a black vein:
saine donques l’une et l’autre, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car desoz sont les arteres.	then prick both, and do not pierce too deep, for underneath are the arteries.
Les voinnes dou coute dont on saine communement sont sainies selonc .ij. manieres:	The veins of the arm which are commonly pricked are punctured in two ways:
ou em poignant a tout .i. flaime mirtin large, ou olivaire subtil si com coutez trenchans, et est apelez «anesil»;	either by pricking at one flame, of about an inch wide, or with an olive-shaped subtle lancet as the surgeons use, and it is called "anesis";
et sont large et subtil selonc la largesce et l’estrecement des voinnes.	and are wide and subtle according to the width and narrowness of the veins.
Li forme dou flaime mirtin si est mout renommee, et est large si com tu vois:	The form of the flame mirror is very renowned, and is wide as you see:
Et ait mestier por ovrir les voinnes chevees plaines de gros sanc apparent, et que contienent gros sanc et trouble;	And it is necessary for opening the veins that are deeply knotted with large, visible blood, and that contain large, turbid blood;
et c’est li forme dou flaime olivaire:	and this is the form of the olive flame:
et est plus subtilz apointé, et est por sainier les voinnes subtilz, ou il a subtil sanc citrin.	And it is more subtle pointed, and is for healing veins subtly, where there is subtly citrine blood.
Li sainie de la basilique, qui est une de ces voinnes, si aide as maladies que sont desoz la gorge, et ou col, et ou peis, et ou ventre;	The vein of the basilica, which is one of these veins, so helps with illnesses that are under the throat, and neck, and chest, and belly.
et covient au sainor qu’il saine saigement, et qu’il se warse de l’artere qui est desoz.	And it is necessary for the healer to heal sagely, and that he avoids the artery that is under (it).
Et s’il cope l’arterre, et decorremens de sanc vient, si le covient estainchier, si com j’ai dit;	And if he cuts the artery, and a flow of blood comes, then it is necessary to staunch it, as I have said;
et ne doit mie estre poignans li flaime, mais taillans si com anesil.	and the flame must not sting but cut like a knife.
Et se li basilique n’apert manifestement, si covient que tu l’estrainges, et chainge une autre;	And if the basilica does not open manifestly, then you must restrain it, and change another one.
ou tu quieres aucun rain de li, ou tu saine en leu de li la voinne emmi le bras: elle apert manifestement;	or you want no vein from it, or you drain in its place the vein in the arm: it opens manifestly;
et la cope au flaime anesil, si com nos avons dit.	and the cautery to the knife, as we have said.
Et se tu vues conoistre le leu de la sainie, si covient ainsois que tu estraignes lou bras, que tu touches le leu tant que tu conoisses le poulz;	And if you see to know the place of the sinew, then thus it is fitting that you draw out the arm, that you touch the place as long as you know the pulse;
puis signe le leu d’enche, et puis lie lou bras, et cope la voine dou flaime anesil;	then mark the place with an incision, and then tie the arm, and cut the vein of the flame under.
et warde que tu ne ferir en l’artere quant tu vois le leu enfleit, car c’est de l’artere: eschui la donques.	And guard that you do not wound the artery when you see the place inflamed, because it is from the artery: therefore avoid it.
Et se tu vois saillir en haut ausi com l’urine d’un enfant, et li sans est rouges et subtilz, saiches que c’est sans de l’artere:	And if you see it rising high like the urine of a child, and the blood is red and fine, know that it is blood from the artery:
haste toi donques, et met ton doi sus longement, puis oste ton doi se li sans estainche, que maintes fois avient;	Haste yourself therefore, and put your hand upon length, then take your hand off if it without ache, that many times happen.
se lie lou bras, et laisse ensi, et ne lou mueve li malaides; et soit sus paour, et ne lou mueve tant qu’il soit sanez.	Bind his arm, and leave it so, and let not the patient move it; and be on fear, and do not move it until it is sound.
Et se li sans n’est estainchiez, et il te vaint, et li medicine ne t’est presens, si cope l’artere s’elle apert, car li chief de li retraient; et estainche li sans.	And if the pain is not aching, and he weeps, and the medicine is not present, then cauterize the artery if it opens, for the head of the retreat; and staunch the blood.
Et pren une escorce de fistice, et la fent, et pren l’une des moitiez et lie sus bien jusc’a l’autre jor;	And take a strip of fig bark, and break it, and take one of the halves and tie it well until the next day.
se li sans estainche, c’est bien; se ce non, si le cure, si com nos avons dit, des poudres qui estainchent sanc;	If the wound is clean, that is good; if not, cure it, as we have said, with powders that staunch blood.
et li estainchemens n’est mie griés em plusors dispositions por le petit leu de la plaie, et la possance dou liien dou bras.	And the stanching is not always good in many arrangements for the small place of the wound, and the strength of the arm's ligament.
Li sainie de la voinne em mileu si aide qu’elle trait sanc dou chief desus, et dou cors desoz,	The vein in the middle is so helpful that it draws blood from the head above, and from the body below,
por ceu qu’elle est composte de la basilique et de la cephalique, si com nos avons dit;	because it is composed of the basilica and cephalic, as we have said;
et covient au sainor qu’il se warse por lou nerf qui est desoz, et s’il point trop em parfont, et il trueve lou nerf,	and it is necessary for the healer to feel along for the nerve which is beneath, and if it is not too much in pain, and he finds the nerve
et il enfle et li santez soit griés, et par aventure ne puet saner;	and he swells and the healers are grieved, and by chance cannot heal;
et cist nerf apert mult de fois, et s’il n’apert en aucuns homes por sa subtiliteit, si covient que tu lou saines de l’estrument anesil; et eschui lou nerf a ton pooir.	and this nerve is opened many times, and if it does not open in any men for its subtlety, then it is necessary that you cleanse it with the instrument anaesthetic; and carefully remove the nerve from your power.
Et se il a voinne entre les .ij. ners, si la fent dou lonc.	And if he has a vein between the two nerves, then make a cut along the length of it.
Li sainie de la cephalique si aide, qu’ele atrait sanc dou chief, et aide as eulz;	The cephalic vein so aids, that it draws blood from the head, and aids the eyes;
et covient sainier em poignant au flaime olivaire ou au flaime mirtin, car c’est li plus sauve de toutes les voinnes, car il n’a desoz li ne nerf ne artere.	and it is necessary to vein by pricking the olive flame or the myrtle flame, because it is the safest of all veins, because it does not have nerves nor arteries.
Toutevoie, covient querir lou plus legier leu, et ne grieve rien s’on faut la premiere fois, et on rencomence;	However, it is necessary to seek the lightest place, and it does not matter if one fails the first time, and one begins again;
et par aventure enfle li leus a aucuns homes, cant on faut la premiere fois, mais il ne grieve rien.	and by chance inflates the places in some men, when one fails the first time, but it does not matter.
La qualitez de la sainie si est selonc ta pensee.	The quality of the blood is according to your thinking.
Li premiere chose que tu dois savoir de sainier, si est que sainie n’est amenistree fuer que por garder santeit,	The first thing you must know about bleeding, is that it is administered only for the sake of health.
et por eschuir les maladies a venir;	and to ward off diseases to come;
et soit li sainie faite en l’une des .iij. voinnes que sont ou coute: c’est a savoir, cephalique, faste, et basilique;	and let the bloodletting be done in one of the three veins that are or should be used: namely, cephalic, femoral, and basilica;
et se doit on sainier en l’encomencement de prientens a geun, et en autompne et en yver aprés mengier, quant li signe de repletion aperent;	And one must bleed at the beginning of Lent, in autumn, and in winter after eating, when the sign of repletion appears.
et se doit on sainier le premier jor ou le tier, aprés .ij. houres ou .iij. dou jor.	And one must bleed on the first day or the third, after two or three hours of the day.
Li sainie qui est aministree as maladies n’a point d’oure determinee, mais que quant besoing est de jor ou de nut, en toutes houres et en toz tens;	The bloodletting that is administered to illnesses has no determined hour, but when need is of the day or of the night, at all hours and in every time.
et ne covient mie sainier les enfans jusc’a .xiiij. ans, ne femme portant fuer que des lou quart mois jusc’a septime.	And it does not behoove to bleed children until fourteen years old, nor women carrying fruit from the fourth month until the seventh.
Ne ne se doient mie sainier li viel qui ont passez .lx. ans.	Do not bleed those who are past .lx. years old.
Et quant aucuns se vuet sainier, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient k’il mondefie les intestines d’un clistere legier,	And when anyone wishes to be bled, in whatever manner, it is necessary that they cleanse the bowels with a light clyster.
s’il a mout de fiens retenut, si que les voines n’atraient des intestines les superfluitez porries nuisans as membres principelz;	If he has much phlegm retained, so that the veins do not draw the harmful impurities from the bowels to the principal limbs;
ne ne se saine mie cil qui est trop saolez de viandes, ne qui est yvres, tant k’il en soit fuer, ne ydropiques;	do not bleed those who are too full of meat, nor who are drunk, as long as they are still intoxicated, nor the dropsy-stricken;
et se warse on de sainier aprés colique passion, et vomissement, et decorrement de ventre, et multipliement d’abiter a femme, et de traval, de veiller et de juner, et ceu que tot la vertu, ou par chose de l’arme ou dou cors;	and if one is harmed after colic passion, and vomiting, and swelling of the belly, and multiplication of labor in women, and travails, of watching and fasting, and those that by all virtue, or by thing of the arm or of the body;
puis subtilie les humors, se li sans est gros, par viandes et par bevraiges et par medicines, se tu en as lou poir;	then subtly thin the humors, if one is fat, by meats and by drinks and by medicines, if you have their power;
puis entre ou bain, s’aucune chose ne lou deffent, por subtiliier lou sanc,	then go into a bath, if nothing forbids it, to subtly thin the blood;
et te saine de la voinne dou pis entor la tierce, si com nos avons dit;	and heal of the vein of the lower arm about the third [part], as we have said;
et te garde celui jor de travail, et de poinne, et de luxure, et de semblans choses;	and keep yourself on that day from work, and from pointing [at things], and from lust, and from similar things;
et soies liez et joians, et soit li sainieres plus haut que cil cui on saine, et li frote lou bras .ij. fois ou .iij.,	and be bound and joyous, and let the hand of the one who heals be higher than that of him who is healed, and rub his arm two or three times.
puis estraigne lou liien desus moienement, car quant il est trop estrois ou poc, si ne puet corre li sans;	then stretch the ligament in the middle, because when it is too tight or loose, he cannot cure without it.
et puis le frote le leu as mains, tant que les voines enflent, et les sente on;	and then rub that place with your hands until the veins swell and are felt.
puis moille li sainieres le flaime d’un poc d’oile viel, puis mette son doit de sa main senestre sus celle voinne desoz lou leu un poc ou il vuet sainier,	Then moisten the vein with a drop of old oil, then place his finger of his left hand upon that vein below its location one spot where he wants to bleed.
que li voinne ne fue et faille au ferir.	so that the vein does not be and fail at being pierced.
Car il i a voinnes que fuient ausi com cordes au sainier, et si a de telz que sont plainnes de ventositeit,	For there are veins that are as thick as cords for bleeding, and some that are full of windiness,
si que quant on met sus le flaime, si retrait a flaime, et ne puet ovrir li voinne, et ensi est on de ceus;	so that when one puts the cautery upon it, it retracts from the heat, and cannot open the vein, and thus is one of these.
et s’il aoevre la voinne, si est li plaie trop estroite, por ceu si covient que li sainieres soit avisez en ces choses.	And if he works the vein, if the wound is too tight, for this it is necessary that the healers be advised in these things.
Et se li voine oevre la premiere fois, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence ancor un poc desoz celui leu ou sus hastanment, se li leus n’est enflez.	And if the vein is worked for the first time, it is good; if not, begin again a little below where it was, or above slightly, if the area is not inflamed.
Et se li leus est enflez, et li malaides s’espoante, se li laisse .i. jor ou .ij., et ne liier mie le bras:	And if the area is inflamed and the patient fears, let him leave it for one or two days, and do not bind up his arm:
par aventure i venra apostemes chaus; ne n’entre ou bain, puis rencomence la sainie s’elle li plait;	for fear perhaps an abscess will come; nor let him enter into a bath, then resume the bloodletting if he desires.
et se li pertuis est petis, ou li sans cort subtilment et tu doutes qu’il n’isse mie tant de sanc com tu vues, si fier en celui pertuis meisme a tout le flaime droitement;	and if the opening is small, or the vein short and subtly, and you doubt that it is not as much blood as you see, then fire in that same opening to the entire flame straightly.
et l’uevre un poc hastanment, ainsois que li leus soit enflez; car ceu avient maintes fois, quant li plaie est petite.	and work a little gently, so that the eyes are swollen; for this happens many times when the wound is small.
Se tu vois le leu enfleit, si ne rencomencier mie la sainie, et met sus un poc de lie d’oile, car elle alige lou cors dou sanc, et est muedre en cest leu li lie que li oile;	If you see the place swollen, then do not begin the bloodletting again, and put on a little bit of olive oil, for it calms the body from blood, and is applied in this place the olive oil;
et ensi aministre la lie de oile en chescune sainie que tu saines les voines, por estanchier lou cours dou sanc;	and thus administer the olive oil in each bloodletting that you bleed the veins, to stop the flow of blood;
et ceu meisme fait triaicle et bowe d’eus, quant on le met sus le leu; si subtilie li sans et s’espart quant il est trop gros.	and the same thing happens triple and bows of them, when one puts it back in its place; so subtle the sinews are and separate when it is too large.
Et s’il i vient uns apostemes gros, qui avient maintes fois, meismement quant il n’est sainiez fuer que a celi fois ou li overture de la voinne est petite,	And if there comes an abscess large, which happens many times, even when it is not drained further than at the time when the opening of the vein is small,
si te haste, et met sus le leu esponge moillie en aigue et en seil un poc chaut, et l’estraint une houre;	if you hurry, and put on top a sponge moistened in water and in some salt a little hot, and hold it for an hour;
et covient que tu faices ceu aprés l’issue dou sanc de la voinne, et s’il demoure au leu aprés aucuns jors aucune noiror ou verdor, si ne li nuist mie;	and it is necessary that you do this after the blood has flowed from the vein, and if it stays in place afterwards for a few days without any blackening or greening, then it does not harm him;
et se tu vues, met sus aucune chose de aloes ou de mirre remise en jus de calament, monstastre, ou semblant.	and if you see, put on nothing of aloes or myrrh mixed with juice of calamine, mustard, or similar.
Et maintes fois avient aposteme et aparance a la sainie de la basilique: met donques ta main sus, et se tu trueves le leu mol a la compression de la main, si est celle aparance male.	And many times abscesses and appearance at the shrine of the basilica happen: put therefore your hand upon it, and if you find the place soft to the pressure of the hand, then is that appearance bad.
Eschui donques que tu ne mettes sus aucune chose de ceu que nos avons dit, car par aventure en cort sans de l’artere; mais li fai .i. emplaustre sec por endurcir le leu, puis le cure d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Therefore shun that you put on anything of those things we have said, for perchance it comes without the artery; but do apply one plaster dry to harden the place, then its cure with another cure, until it is healed.
Et trai a chescun dou sanc selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu, et de la color dou sanc.	And treat each wound according to the quantity of its virtue, and the color of the blood.
Car se li sans est noir, si en laisse issir tant qu’il soit rouges; et se tu lou vois gros, si lou laisse tant qu’il soit subtiliiez; et s’il est trop chaus, si le laisse refroidier.	For if the wound is black, let it drain until it is red; and if you see it swelling, let it drain until it is smaller; and if it is too hot, let it cool.
Et covient a celui qui est plains et fors, et ait mestier d’estraction de sanc, c’on li faice plus large plaie, et soit li flaimes larges;	And for one who is pale and weak, and needs bloodletting, it should be made into a larger wound, and the flames should be wide.
et a celui qui est foibles, fai le contraire, et le covient sainier poc et sovent, et le doit on sainier en taillant de travers, ne mie en poignant;	And for one who is weak, do the opposite, and it should be bled frequently and often, and it should be bled by cutting crosswise, not by pricking.
et ceste maniere de sainie est sauve de decorrement de sanc et de copement de nerf, et vaut mues que li sainie dou lonc ne dou large.	And this manner of bloodletting is safe from the decrease of blood and cutting of nerves, and it is better than bleeding from the long or wide (vein).
Et a celui cui li cors faut a la sainie, covient doner pain moilliet en jus de pomes grenates; s’il est eschaufez, si trai dou sanc .iij. fois ou .iiij.	And to one whose body is lacking in blood, it is necessary to give soft bread in pomegranate juice; if it is dried, treat with blood three or four times.
Et s’il est de froide complexion, si menjuce devant la sainie pain moilliet en sirop muzé, ou en sirop de miel aromatique avec espices, si com poivre, canelle, gingibre, et chiches, et sirop bien odorant.	And if he is of cold complexion, mix soft bread before the blood with syrup made from figs, or with aromatic honey syrup with spices, such as pepper, cinnamon, ginger, and chickpeas, and a well-smelling syrup.
Et s’il paume a la sainie, aprés l’issue de mout de sanc, si covient qu’il hume brouet de char, et sirop odorant subtil,	And if he faints after the issue of blood, it is necessary that he suck broth of meat, and subtle fragrant syrup.
et use des autres choses que nos avons dit en la division ou chapistre de sincope, por l’evacuation de voinne.	and use the other things we have said in the division or chapter of fainting, for the evacuation of blood.
Et s’il vuet esventer som bras, et sainier autre fois, si covient, quant il est afoiblis par grant sainie, k’il se saine poc et poc, selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu continueement.	And if he wants to bleed his arm, and bleed another time, if it is necessary, when he is weakened by great bleeding, that he bleeds little by little, according to the quantity of his strength continuously.
Et qui vuet esventer som bras aprés la premiere sainie, et il a cors fort, si se saine .vij. houres aprés la premiere sainie, ou aprés la nuevime houre.	And who wants to bleed his arm after the first bleeding, and he has a strong body, then he bleeds seven hours after the first bleeding, or after the ninth hour.
Et qui se vuet sainier d’autre part, si se doit sainier lou secont jor ou le tier.	And who wants to be bled from another part, then they must be bled on the second day or the third.
Car il a mout de sanc dedens le cors qui est ja eschaufez, et fait venir fievre; si en covient traire grant quantiteit, et eslargir le pertus tant qu’il chiece em pameson;	Because he has much blood within the body which is already exhausted and brings on fever; so it is necessary to draw a great quantity, and enlarge the opening until it flows in streams.
puis que tu rewardes toutes les conditions de sainie, et met ta main sus som poulz quant il saine, que li mors ne viegne en leu de pameson,	Since you have treated all the conditions of health, and put your hand upon his pulses when he is healthy, that death may not come in place of pain.
et ceu avient maintes fois, quant li sainieres est negligens;	And this happens many times, when the healer is negligent.
et ne covient mie quant tu vues desliier lou bras, et faire issir sanc la seconde fois, et li pertus est clos, que tu presses forment sus;	And it is not right when you see that the arm is dislocated, and make blood flow the second time, and the wound is closed, that you press strongly on top.
ne s’il est corbes, qu’il estende lou bras hastanment, car ce seroit malz;	And if it is curved, let him extend his arm as much as possible, for this would be bad.
mais le laisse tant qu’il saine la seconde fois; ou tu i point a la pointe dou flaime, tant que li sans qui est congelez a pertus de la voinne isse fuer,	but let it alone until it heals the second time; or you point it to the tip of the flame, as long as the vein which is frozen from opening up does not return.
et met sus .i. poc de seil remis en aigue, et presse sus legierement.	and put upon it i. piece of silk moistened in water, and press lightly.
Et se li voine est enflee, si la laisse et ne l’estreindre mie, tant que li aposteme soit apaisiez.	And if the vein is swollen, leave it alone and do not constrict it at all, until the abscess is calmed.
Et se necessitez est dou traire dou sanc la seconde fois, si le saine en celui leu meisme, ou en un autre voinne, ou en l’autre bras.	And if necessity requires drawing blood a second time, let it be done in the same place, or in another vein, or in the other arm.
Li voinne emmi le bras est sainie en leu de la voine dou chief por ceu qu’elle est composte.	The vein in the arm is bled in place of the vein in the neck because it is composed.
Et li maniere de la sainie si est que li malaides boute sa main en aigue chaude, tant que li foscile soit rouges;	And the manner of bleeding it is that the patient puts his hand in hot water until the bone is red;
puis soit liiéz moienement, si que li voinne apere bien, puis le saine maintenant dou travers, ne mie dou large ne dou lonc;	then be bound moderately so that the vein appears well, then bleed now across, not through wide or long;
et soit li pertus larges, et soit sainiez bien pres de la jointe de la main, et se sans n’en puet issir, si remet la main en aigue chaude, et laisse corre lou sanc en l’aigue, tant que tu en aies assez;	and let the puncture be wide, and bleed well near the joint of the hand, and if without it can issue, then put the hand back in hot water, and leave to drain the blood in the water, until you have enough;
et se c’est en esteit, si ne rebouter mie la main en aigue chaude, car on l’i met plus en yver que en esteit;	and if it is in this state, do not put the hand back in hot water, for one puts it more in winter than in summer.
et li sainie de ceste voine est plus sauve de toutes autres voinnes, qu’il n’i a ne artere ne nerf.	and the vein of this vein is safer from all other veins, that there is neither artery nor nerve in it.
Li sainie de la salvatele de la main destre si vaut a toutes les maladies dou foie, et c’est li maniere:	The vein of the salvation of the right hand is good for all diseases of the liver, and this is the way:
estrain la main, et boute en aigue chaude, tant que li voinne soit enflee, si c’on la voie;	strain the hand, and put it in hot water, until the vein is swollen, if one can see it.
et se la saine de travers, et se tu la copes dou tout en tout, si ne grieve rien;	and if it is broken crookedly, and if you cut it all around completely, it will not harm anything.
et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car li nerf sont desoz toz desnuez de char,	and do not make it too deep in cutting because the nerves are beneath all without flesh,
et puis remet la main en aigue chaude, se li sans est congelez en la plaie, et n’en puet issir.	and then put the hand back into hot water if it has become frozen in the wound and cannot be pulled out.
Et quant tu avras trait dou sanc tant com mestier t’est, si met sus la voinne oile et seil por souder hastanment, et ensi fai de chescun rain.	And when you have treated the blood as much as is necessary, then put oil and silk on top of the vein to hold it together firmly, and do so for each vein.
Li sainie de li en la main senestre si vaut a la maladie de la mice, et fai tout ausi com je t’ai dit devers destre.	The bloodletting of the hand on the left side is as good for the disease of the mouse, and do everything as I have said to you towards the right.
Li sainie de la sophene si vaut a toutes les maladies que sont desoz le cors,	The bloodletting of the spleen is as good for all diseases that are below the body.
si com maladies de la marris, et retenement de flors, et maladie des rains, et des cuixes et des jambes ancienes, et semblans maladies.	as for diseases of the bowels, and retention of fluids, and diseases of the hips, thighs and old legs, and similar diseases.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides boute som piet en aigue chaude, et frote sus la voinne tant qu’elle pere,	And the qualities of its bloodletting is that the patient puts his foot in hot water and rubs on the vein until it throbs.
et lie desus la jointure dou piet; et li voinne si est a la cheville, et par desus lou piet en vont mout de rains;	and bind above the joint of the foot; and the vein is at the ankle, and above the foot go many veins;
saine la donques ou plus large rain, ou a la cheville, que mues vaut.	so then take the larger vein, or at the ankle, that you judge best.
Et se tu la saines sus lou piet, si te warde des ners qui sont desoz, et la saine de traver ausi com en copant; et soit li flaimes anesil.	And if you cut it on the foot, guard the nerves that are below, and cut through as when cutting; and let the flames be unyielding.
Et se li sans n’en puet issir, si remet lou piet en l’aigue, et laisse bien vuidier la voine.	And if he cannot feel it, put the foot in water, and let the vein bleed well.
Et se li sainieres faut la premiere fois, si rencomence la seconde au desus un poc, car li leus est salz;	And if the first time the incision is needed, it must be started again above a little, because the salt is present.
ne ne douter de nerf, si com nos avons dit, et ensi fai de la sophene de l’autre piet igalment.	Do not doubt the nerve, as we have said, and do likewise with the sophian of the other foot equally.
Li leus de la voinne sciatique est a la cheville de fuer, et sa sainie vaut a la dolor de la hainche, quant c’est por sanc chaut.	The vein of sciatica is at the ankle of force, and its incision is worth to the pain in the hip, when it is for hot blood.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides entre ou bain, et estraigne desus la cheville .iiij. dois en tordant,	And the qualities of its incision are that the patient enters or bathes, and is strained above the ankle four fingers in twisting,
car autrement n’apert li voinne; et s’elle apert, si le saine en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et en traversant;	for otherwise it does not open the vein; and if it opens, then seal it in all ways that you can, and across
et vaut mues que tu la copes, car li leus est saus, et elle est mout reponue a mains homes.	and it is better that you cut it, because the flesh is dry, and it is very full of blood in men's hands
Et se tu ne la trueves, si saine aucun rain de li qui apert ou dos dou piet, et vers lou petit doi, et te warde des ners;	And if you do not find it, then seal any vein that opens or below the foot, and towards the small toe, and guard the nerves;
et fai tant corre dou sanc que tu vues, et puis deslie lou lien, et met sus coton et l’estraint; ele est maintenant sanee.	and do as much bloodletting as you see fit, and then untie the bandage, and put on cotton and restrain it; she is now healed.
Des sainies de ventouse	Of leeching wounds
Ventouses sont fait de cornes, ou d’arain, ou de voirre; et ventosation si est faite selonc .ij. manieres: ou par ferir et atraire sanc, ou sens ferir.	Leech cups are made of horn, or wood, or glass; and ventosaion is done in two ways: either by piercing and drawing blood, or without piercing.
Et ceste ventosation qui est sens ferir si est selonc .ij. manieres: ou elle est a tout feu, ou sens feu;	And this ventosaion which is without piercing is done in two ways: either it is applied with heat, or without heat;
et ventosation qui est faite par ferir et par estraction de sanc si est faite en .xiiij. leus dou cors,	and ventosaion which is done by piercing and extracting blood is done in fourteen places of the body,
de coi li uns est tout en som le chief; et li autres est emmi le col;	of which one is entirely in the sum of the head; and the other is amid the neck
et .ij. autres en .ij. costeis dou col; et li ventouse desoz lou menton;	and two others in two ribs of the neck; and the windpipe below the chin;
et li ventouse des .ij. espaules; et li ventouse sus les crupies;	and the windpipe at the two shoulders; and the windpipe above the hips;
et les ventouses emmi les .ij. bras; et les ventouses des .ij. jambes;	and the windpipes amid the two arms; and the windpipes of the two legs;
et les ventouses des .ij. chevilles; et li ventosation ne trait point de sanc, fuer que des menues voinnes que sont esparses en la char,	and the suction cups on the two ankles; and the cupping does not treat blood, except for the small veins that are scattered in the flesh.
et por ceu n’en afoiblist om mie, si com on fait de sainie de voinne;	and therefore it does not weaken one as much, as is done with bloodletting from a vein;
et ne covient mie qu’elle soit aministree, ne a tout feu ne sens feu, en aucune maladie qui vient de repletion, tant que toz li cors soit vuidiez.	and it is not appropriate that it be administered, neither to hot nor cold fire, in any illness that comes from repletion, until the whole body is emptied.
Et se par necessiteit de maladies covient ventoser, ou por acostumances, si l’amenistrons chescune houre en l’encomencement dou mois, ou en la fin, et emmi et en chescun tens;	And if by necessity of illness it is necessary to cupping, or by custom, then we administer it each hour at the beginning of the month, or at the end, and in any time between.
car il i a de telz qui, quant il ont mestier de ventoser, si ont pesant chief;	because there are some who, when they need to wind, have heavy head;
et si a telz qui truevent repletion et roujor en lor faice, et en lor chief, et au col, et tenebrour as eulz;	and there are some who bloat and redness in their face, and in their head, and in the neck, and darkness in their eyes;
et telz qui truevent une goute de sanc en lor bouche, et ont enflee la lengue, et raichent sanc;	and some who have a drop of blood in their mouth, and have a swollen tongue, and spit blood;
et si i a de telz qui songent, et voient par nut sanc et navrez et mors et semblans choses.	and there are some who dream, and see through blood and nausea and death and similar things.
Et quant nos voions ces signes, et meismement quant c’est emmi lou mois, nos lou commandons a ventoser aprés .iij. houres dou jor.	And when we see these signs, and even if it is in the middle of the month, we command them to fast after three hours of the day.
Li sainie de la muze si aide a la grieteit dou chief … que vient as eulz, et ne covient mie que ce soit aprés l’evacuation de tout lou cors;	The bloodletting from the temple helps with the great pain of the head… that comes to the eyes, and it does not befit that it should be after the evacuation of all the body;
et ceste ventosation si est en leu de la sainie de la cephalique,	and this fasting is in place of bloodletting from the head,
et ne covient mie que cil qui est de froide complexion en use, ou qui ait chatharre, car ce lor fait mout grant nuisement;	and it does not befit those who are of cold constitution to use it, or who have a catarrh, for this does great harm to them;
et por ceu ne covient mie que li veillart en usent, ne qui ont ou chief froides maladies.	and for this reason it is not fitting that the old people use it, nor those who have or head colds diseases.
Et cil qui s’en saine sovent, si devient oblious, et por ce covient mettre la ventouse un poc plus aval par la doutance d’obliance.	And those who become cured of it often, they become oblivious, and for this reason it is necessary to place the suction cup a little lower due to the fear of oblivion.
Li ventosation emmi le col est en leu de la sainie dou chief et de la basilique, et por ceu vaut elle a l’estrecement dou pis,	Suction on the neck is in place of the vein from the head and basilica, and for this reason it is good for the treatment of phlegm.
et a fendure de la chenal dou pormon, et a toust, et a repletion;	and to the fissure of the channel of the groin, and to all boils, and to swelling.
et la covient poc bouter, car s’elle tient trop fermement, si enjanre obliance ou stomac et ou cuer.	And there it is necessary to not put too much pressure, because if it holds too firmly, it can cause obstruction or stomach and heart.
Li ventosations as .ij. costelz dou col si vaut as dolors dou chief, et obtalmie et emigrainne, et a l’estranglement, et a la dolor as racines des dens,	The two ribs of the neck, when they are ventilated, are worth it for the pains of the head, and ophthalmia and migraine, and in strangulation, and the pain at the roots of the teeth.
et est en leu de la sainie de la basilique; et covient que tu comandes au sainor qu’il espresse sa main au mettre, qu’il ne cope l’artere, et ne veigne decorremens de sanc.	and it is in the place of the basilica's vein; and it is necessary that you command the healer to be careful when putting it on, that he does not cut the artery and does not bring a hemorrhage of blood.
Li ventosations desoz lou menton si vaut a maladie de bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et semblans maladies qui sont en la bouche; et est en leu des sainies des .ij. levres.	The cupping below the chin is good for mouth diseases, and gum rot, and similar illnesses that are in the mouth; and it is in the place of the veins of the two lips.
Li ventosations des espaules vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de remplissement.	The ventilation of the shoulders is good for illness that comes from heat and congestion.
Li ventosations des coutes si vaut autant com des .iij. voinnes dou bras,	The ventilation of the armpits is as good as three veins of the arm.
car elle atrait sanc de ces grosses voinnes;	because it draws blood from those large veins;
et comande au sainor qu’il ne fiere mie trop em parfont, car li leus est nus de char, et sait desoz ners et arteres.	and instructs the healthy one that he should not hit it too hard, because the skin is thin and lies above nerves and arteries.
Li ventouse qui est sus la croupe si vaut as emoroydes dou fondement, et as maladies desoz, et covient que li ventouse soit grans, et soit d’arain, qu’elle a mestier de bien traire; et par aventure, s’elle estoit subtilz, si briseroit; et i fai grans plaies.	The suction cup which is on the rump is good for hemorrhoids of the foundation, and for diseases of below, and it is necessary that the suction cup be large, and be of iron, that it has need to well suck; and by chance, if it were subtle, it would break; and there makes great wounds.
Les ventouses des jambes si sainent apertement, car elles atraient sanc de tout le cors, et valent as dolors ancienes des rains, et de la marris, et de la vessie, et ramoinnent les flors; et sont en leu des .ij. sophenes, et des .ij. chevilles, et toutevoie elles afoiblissent lou cors aprés lonc us, et font venir paumison em plusors dispositions.	The suction cups of the legs are used openly, because they attract blood from the whole body, and are good for old pains of the hips, and of the thighs, and of the bladder, and soften the flowers; and are in their place at the two shins, and the two ankles, and nonetheless they weaken the body after long use, and bring weariness in more dispositions.
Li maniere de mettre la ventouse si est que tu la mettes premier vuide, et succe tempreement, et la met hastanment, et remue igalment, et ne cesser de ceu faire, tant que tu voies lou leu rouge et enfleit, et apere li roujor dou sanc; puis fier, et remet les ventouses, et pren warde en la disposition des cors, car il i a telz qui ont tanre char, et clers porez: si covient ferir une fois soulement, et covient faire larges plaies, et un poc parfondes; et suce legierement.	The manner of putting the suction cup is that you put it first empty, and succeed moderately, and put it carefully, and move equally, and do not cease to do so until you see the place red and inflamed, and appear the color of blood; then firm, and put back the suction cups, and take ward in the disposition of the body, because there are such who have tender flesh, and clear pores: so it is necessary to strike only once, and it is necessary to make large wounds, and a bit deep; and suck lightly.
Et se li sans est gros, si couvient ferir .ij. fois: la premiere fois por subtiliier la voie dou sanc gros.	And if the vein is thick, it is necessary to prick it twice: the first time to make a path for the thick blood.
Et se li sans est tres espés, si covient ferir la tierce fois; et quant nos volons traire dou sanc poc et poc, si nos soffist soulement une fois.	And if the vein is very thick, it is necessary to prick it a third time; and when we want to draw blood little by little, we prick only once.
Et se nos volons mout de sanc, si rencomensons sovent; et se li sans est espés, si fier em parfont, et li termines si est que li keurs soit perciez soudement,	And if we want a lot of blood, we must often return to it; and if the vein is thick, prick it deeply, and the end is that the needle should be pierced firmly,
et couvient a celui qui a gros cuir et dur, et qui ont estrois porelz, que tu oignes les leus des ventouses d’oile aperitif et dissolutif:	and it is necessary for those who have thick and tough skin, and whose pores are obstructed, that you anoint the places where the blisters will be put with oil that is aperitif and dissolving:
se c’est en esteit, d’oile violet, ou d’oile d’amandres douces, ou d’oile de semence de cucurbite;	If it is in this state, of violet oil, or sweet almond oil, or oil of pumpkin seed;
et se c’est en yveir, d’oile de cresson, ou de lis, ou de camomille, ou autre semblant.	And if it is in summer, of cresson oil, or lily, or chamomile, or something similar.
Et se li superfluitez est grosse et froide, si pren oile amaratin, ou de balsamite, ou oile d’anet, et les semblans.	And if the superfluity is thick and cold, then take wormwood oil, or balm, or anise oil, and similar ones.
Et se cil cui on saine a tendre char et larges porelz, se n’i covient mettre point d’oile,	And if the one whom you are treating has loose skin and large pores, then it is not necessary to put any oil on them;
mais le covient laver aprés la ventosation d’aigue rose, ou d’aigue froide, ou d’aigue de morelle, ou d’aigue de cucurbite, ou d’aigue de porcelainne, ou autre semblant.	but it is necessary to wash after the suction of rose water, or cold water, or mulberry water, or gourd water, or porcelain water, or something similar.
Et cil qui a mout de moistor, si se leve d’aisil, ou d’aigue de mirte, et de sumac, et de semblans choses.	And he who has much moisture, let him rise of myrtle water, and of sumaq, and of similar things.
Et cil qui ont grosses superfluitez se levent de vin viel, ou d’aigue de seuc, ou de decoction d’anet ou de camomile, ou d’autres semblans;	And those who have large superfluities rise from old wine, or of succory water, or decoction of fennel or chamomile, or other similar things;
et ne se covient mie sainier de ventouse devant le bain ne em bain, mais aprés lou bain une houre ou .ij.; et ne dorme mie aprés la ventosacion,	and it is not necessary to  cupping before the bath or in the bath, but after the bath an hour or two; and do not sleep after cupping,
et covient k’il se warse, quant il se doit ventoser et quant il est ventosez.	and it is necessary that he wear it when he must be bandaged and when he is bandaged.
Et warde se cil qui se saine est coleriques, et se li sans est trop agus et enflamez;	And guard those who are jaundiced in health, and if their skin is too much inflamed and swollen;
si covient qu’il preigne choses froides, si com pomes grenates et endives et laitues a l’aisil, et semblans choses;	if it is necessary that they eat cold things, such as pomegranates and endives and lettuces at the waist, and similar things;
et menjuce pucins, et char de chastron, et viandes moistes.	and  soft turnips, and broth of mutton, and moist meats.
Et cil qui a froide complexion, si preigne syrop de miel, et vin odorant moien, qui est entre viel et noveil, et menjuce poc, et menjuce pucins et petis oiselz et pijons;	And he who has a cold complexion, take syrup of honey, and fragrant wine, which is between old and new, and quince, and quince seed, and small onions, and pigeons.
et lou jor qu’il se ventousera, si doit plus boivre que mengier;	And on the day that he will be purged, he must drink more than eat.
et covient doner a aucuns homes aucune fois triaicle ou muscate devant la ventosacion, ou aprés, por conforter les membres principalz;	And it is necessary to give no one at any time triacle or musk before or after the purging, in order to strengthen the principal members.
et soit subtiliiez li sans, mais il ne covient mie que cil qui sont chaut le boivent.	And let it be subtle the wine, but it is not fitting that those who are hot drink it.
Les ventouses que sont mises sens ferir sont celles que sont mises sus lou foie, et sus la mice, et podagre, et sus lou ventre et la boude et les rains et la hainche, car cil membre ne soffrent mie ferir sus oulz,	The suction cups that are applied without harming are those that are placed on the liver, and on the spleen, and gout, and on the belly and the chest and the hips and the groin, because these members do not suffer being pierced.
et ne le fait on fuer que por atraire sanc de membre em membre,	and it is done only to draw blood from limb to limb
si com nos mettons sus les mameles quant li neis sainne; por oster la viscositeit qui est au membre, si com nos metons ventouses sus lou ventre et sus la boude por amenuisier le membre;	as we place them on the breasts when they are nursing; to remove the viscosity that is in the limb, as we place suction cups on the belly and on the chest to reduce the swelling of the member
et oste la dolor, quant il i a opilation ou piere, si oste par sa vertu atractive par aventure l’opilation, ou desaert la piere de son leu;	and remove the pain when there is an obstruction or stone, as it removes by its attractive virtue perhaps the obstruction, or dislodges the stone from its place;
et ensi fait ele quant on le met sus lou foie et sus la mice quant il i a ventositeit retenue,	and thus it is done when one puts it upon the liver and upon the mouse when there is wind retention,
et ces ventouses sont aministrees vuides por sucier tant soulement; et aucune fois sont aministrees ensamble feu, et aucunes fois plainnes d’aigue tede,	and these cupping glasses are administered empty to suck only thus; and sometimes they are administered together with fire, and sometimes filled with warm water.
si com em maladies dou pleuresin, et en tel maniere c’on emplisse la ventouse d’aigue chaude soule, ou d’aigue ou il ait cuit herbes covenaubles a ceu.	as in illnesses of the pleura, and in this way one fills the cupping glass with hot water alone, or with water which has boiled herbs suitable for it.
Li forme de la ventouse aministré a feu si est ci:	The form of the cupping glass administered with fire is as follows:
Et ait .ij. dois de large et demi palme de parfont, et ait ou costeit entor lou mileu .i. petit pertus, ausi com por bouter une aguille,	And have 2 pieces of wood of width half a palm and length a palm's breadth, and have or cost at the middle one small hole, as for putting a needle.
et soit d’arain, souef devant si qu’ele ne blece lou malaide au mettre sus lou membre;	and let it be of wood so smooth that it does not prick the patient when placed upon the limb;
et ait em mileu une verge de travers d’arain ou de fer, por mettre une chandoile emprise,	and in the middle have a crosspiece of wood or iron to put a burning candle in,
et en soient et grans et petites selonc les maladies et l’eaige de ces qui les prenent;	and let them be both large and small according to the illnesses and the age of those who take them;
car les ventouses des enfans sont autres que des vielz, et des maigres que des gras.	for the suction cups of children are other than of the old, and of the thin ones than of the fat.
Et doit on ensi mettre ceste ventouse sus lou membre:	And must one thus place this suction cup upon the limb:
empren la chandoile de cire ou .i. linement, et le met emmi la ventouse au traver de la verge qui est emmi la ventouse,	take the handle of wax or one linen wrap and place it inside the suction cup across from the stick that is inside the suction cup,
si que li clartez soit au fons de la ventouse qu’elle ne brule le malaide;	so that the brightness be at the bottom of the suction cup so that it does not burn the patient.
et puis la met sus lou membre, et tes dois soit sus lou pertus que nos avons dit, si que quant on vuet, si en va li vapor, et oste on la ventouse;	And then place it on the limb, and you must do so on the opening that we have said, so that when one wants to, the vapor goes in, and one removes the cupping glass;
et emprent on le linement si com devant, et le rencomence sovent, se tu as mestier.	And apply the linen as before, and repeat it often if you need to.
En la ventouse donques qui est aministree em maladie de pleuresin, a tout aigue, n’a point de verge ne de pertus, et n’est amenistree fuer que quant ele est plaine d’aigue, et est mise sus lou membre tant soulement;	In the cupping glass which is administered in disease of pleurisy, for all kinds of pain, there is no point nor opening, and it is administered only when it is full of water, and it is placed on the limb only so long.
et c’est li forme:	and this is its form:
Sansues ne sont amenistrees fuer que en membres ou on ne puet mettre ventouses por lour petitece, si com levres et gencives, et semblans leus;	Suckings are not administered except in members where one cannot put cupping glasses because of their small size, such as lips and gums, and similar ones.
et en leus desnuez de char, si com doi ou neis, et autres semblans;	And in their naked flesh, such as two or the like, and others similar;
et li qualitez de l’user si est que quant tu trueves sansues que sont en aigues douces nettes sens porreture, si les pren;	And the qualities of the user are that when you find suckings that are in clear fresh waters without rotteness, take them;
et les met une nut en aigue douce, tant qu’elles soient famillouses, et n’aient rien en ventres;	and place them in fresh water until they become accustomed and have nothing in their bellies;
et puis soit sainiez de voinne et de ventouse, puis frote le membre tant k’il soit rouges, et met sus les sansues;	and then be drained of bloodletting and cupping, then rub the limb until it is red, and put on the poultices.
et quant elles seront plainnes, et cherront, se c’est leu ou on puisse mettre ventouse, se li met, car ce vaut mout aprés.	and when they are swollen, and fall, if it is their place where one can put cupping, then put it, because it is very good afterward.
Se ceu non, si leve le leu d’aisil, et puis d’aigue, mout bien, et puis l’espreint;	If those are not there, lift the place with ease, and then with water, very well, and then squeeze it;
et se li leus saine trop aprés lou cors des sansues, si moille .i. drapel de lin en aigue froide, et met sus, tant que li sans soit estenchiés;	and if the place is healing too much after the poultice, moisten one cloth of linen in cold water and put it on top until the swelling subsides;
et se li sans est multipliez, si met sus vitriole broié, ou gales, et semblans choses, tant qu’il soit estenchiez;	and if the wounds are multiplied, put on crushed vitriol, or saltpeter, and similar things, until they are stretched.
ou tu met sor le leu moitiez de feves pelees, et les laisse tant qu’elles s’aerdent au leu, si estanchera maintenant;	or you put on the site half of peeled beans, and let them until they dry out on the site, then it will now stop.
et se tu en as de plus mestier, si pren autres sansues.	and if you need more of this, take other bandages.
Et se les sansues ne se vuellent prendre, si frote le leu de sanc fres, ou tu i fiche une aguille tant que li sans en isse,	And if the bandages do not want to be taken, rub the site with fresh blood, or you put a needle there until the bandage comes out.
et puis les met sus, et tantost com elles sentent lou sanc, si s’aerdent;	and then place them on top, and as soon as they feel the blood, they flare up;
et quant tu vues qu’elles chieent, si poudre sus un poc d’aloen et de seil broiet, ou de cendre, si cherront maintenant.	and when you see that they are bleeding, put some powder of alum and willow bark crushed, or ashes, on top, now they will stop.
Ci comence li livre des brisures	Here begins the book of fractures
Cist chapistres est maintes fois necessaires en l’art de medicine, et est restorement de brisure et de desaluement.	This chapter is many times necessary in the art of medicine, and it is the restoration of a fracture and dislocation.
