Saichiez, chier fil, que li fol mire se gietent de cest chapistre, qu’il ne virent onques nul des anciens livres, ne lettre n’en lurent;	Know this, dear son, that the fools who mock this chapter will never see anything in any of the old books, nor have they read a letter from them.
et por ceste cause est estraingie li science en nostre terre, car je n’en trovai onques nul boin;	And for this reason the science is hidden in our land, because I never found any good one.
et n’en sai nient, fuer que par la science des anciens livres, ou j’ai tant estudiiet que je en ai traite la science, et par experiment, et par l’acostumance de ma vie;	And I know nothing of it, except by the science of the old books, in which I have studied so much that I have mastered its science, and by experience, and by the custom of my life;
et je vos ai jai descrit en cest chapistre ceu qui est contenut, et l’ai abregié en la fin, et ai mostreit clerement les formes des estrumens que sont amenistrez, si com j’ai fait en ces .ij. chapistres ci devant.	And I have described to you in this chapter what is contained therein, and have abridged it at the end, and have clearly shown the forms of the instruments that are brought, as I have done in these two chapters before.
Il covient donques que nos disons ou prologue de cest livre les sommes de la parole et les chapistres ou li saiges met son entendement, et demore sus la verteit, si que cil qui sont esproveit saichent et aprenent cest art noble, et l’aprenent a autrui.	It therefore behooves us to say in the prologue of this book the sums of words and chapters where the wise puts his understanding, and remains on truth, so that those who are experienced know and learn this noble art, and teach it to others.
Je dis que quant brisure ou dislocation ou torsions ou quasseure vient a aucun, si covient que tu te hastes de sainier lou malaide d’une part et d’autre, s’aucune chose ne lou te tot, si com foiblece de cors, ou enfes, ou viellars;	I say that when fracture or dislocation or torsion or sprain comes to anyone, it is necessary for you to hasten to heal the patient on one side and the other, if nothing hinders him, such as weakness of body, or infirmity, or old age.
ou se li tens n’est tres chaus, ou trop frois; et menjuce cholz frois, c’est a savoir froides joutes, et char d’oiseil et de chevril, et ne boive point de vin, ne menjuce nules grasses chars, et ne s’emplisse mie trop de viandes qui remplissent les voinnes de sanc, tant que tu n’aies doute d’aposteme chaut, ne d’espandement de matiere au membre; si reviegne li malaides a som premerain governement k’il a useit.	or if his constitution is not very strong, or too cold; and avoid cold foods, that is to say, cold meats, and venison, and mutton, and do not drink wine, nor consume any fatty meats, and do not overfill himself with meats which fill the veins with blood, until you have doubts of a hot abscess, or expansion of matter in the limb; so that the patient returns to his first government as he used it.
Et quant li os brisiés comence a restourer, si covient que on norrisse le malaide de viandes que font gros norrissement, ou il ait viscositeit, si com froment cuit en aigue, et ris, et testes, et piez, et pance de vaiche, et oefz, et poissons fres, et gros vin, et semblans chose.	And when the broken bone begins to heal, it is necessary that one nourishes the patient with meats that make a thick nourishment, or there is viscosity, such as wheat cooked in water, and rice, and testes, and pies, and belly of calf, and eggs, and fresh fish, and strong wine, and similar things.
Car a teil norrissement se reprent mues et plus tost li brisure.	For with such nourishment they recover strength and the fracture heals more quickly.
Et saichiez que li os brisiez des vielz et des decrepites ne se pueent mie bien reprendre ne souder selonc lor nature por la sechor des membres, ne cil ausi qui sont trop tendre, si com os de petis enfans;	And know that broken bones of the old and the decrepit do not well recover or heal according to their nature because of the dryness of the limbs, nor those that are too soft, such as bones of small children;
mais n’a cure, ramoinne sus l’os brisiet .i. gros tenrons qui s’aert et joint le membre ensamble, tant qu’il enforce si com il fut devant; et ne li tot point de son oevre, et por ceu le covient norrir de grosses viandes, si com nos avons dit.	but if there is no cure, reset the broken bone that is, large splints which are set and join the limb together, as much as it was before; and don’t let any part of its work, and for this reason it must be nourished with coarse meats, as we have said.
Et saiches que les briseures sont diverses em maintes manieres.	And know that fractures are diverse in many ways.
Car li brisure dou chief est autre que li brisure dou pis, ou de la jambe, et je vos dirai en cest chapistre toutes manieres de brisure.	For the fracture of the head is different from the fracture of the leg or hip, and I will tell you in this chapter all kinds of fractures.
Car il i a brisure que vait a arvol, et autre en aguisant, si com li taille d’une penne por escrire.	For there is a fracture that goes into a groove, and another in sharpening, like the edge of a pen for writing.
Et si a brisure avec plaie, et brisure a tout une petite fendure.	And if with fracture and wound, and fracture to a small crack all around.
Et a chescune maniere ait son engien, et son estrument propre en la restauration, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient en son leu;	And in every manner have its tool, and its proper instrument in the restoration, according to what memory comes in its place;
et est conue li brisure de l’os par ceu que li leus est tors, et apert bien par defuer, et sone au presseir de la main;	And is known the fracture of the bone by those that are twisted, and open well from outside, and felt by pressure of the hand;
et quant il n’i a tortuositeit ne son au tochier, et li malaides ne sent mie grant dolor, se n’i a point de brisure;	And when there is no torsion nor feeling upon touching, and the patient feels no great pain, then there is no fracture;
mais il puet bien avoir tortuositeit, ou fendure, ou petite brisure.	but it can well have twisting, or rupture, or small fracture.
Si ne covient mie que tu lou mueves a la main, mais met sus medicines que vienent ci aprés, et puis l’estraint maintenant subtilment.	If you must not move it by hand, but put on the medicines that come after here, and then restrain it subtly.
Et saiches que li brisure que vait en arvol, et sont les .ij. parties desjointes, il les covient maintenant mettre a point igalment, ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne;	And know that the fracture that goes in a circle, and are the two parts disjointed, you must now put them together equally, so that abscesses may not come.
et se apostemes chaulz i vient, si lou laisse aucun jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez;	And if abscesses do come, then let it alone for no day, until the abscesses are appeased;
puis le met igal au mues que tu pues legierement et saigement, et saiches que li restauration de li est plus legiere que li restaurations de celi ou il ait pieces; puis l’estraint, si com il covient ci aprés.	Then place it straight in the joint as you can easily and wisely, and know that the restoration of this is lighter than the restoration of the one which has pieces; then restrain, as it is necessary here after.
Et se en l’os a piéces brisies, si l’estent de .ij. pars, se c’est mains ou piet, ou a ta main se c’est uns petis membres, ou a .ij. cordes, ou a une corde et a ta main;	And if the bone is broken into pieces, if it's two parts, if it's hands or feet, or at your hand if it's a small limb, or two cords, or one cord and at your hand;
et met le membre selonc sa figure natureil, si que quant les parties dou membre brisiet sont desevrees, si ramoinne par toz engiens les additions en lor leus au mues que tu pues, et garde que par ton ovraige ne viegne au malaide lesion ne doulor;	and place the limb according to its natural form, so that when the parts of the broken limb are separated, you carefully put all the pieces back in their places in the joint as much as you can, and make sure that through your work no injury or pain comes to the patient.
et ajoste bien les .ij. chiés des os selonc les millors formes.	and adjust well the two ends of the bones according to the best forms.
Et le sent bien a la main s’il te semble k’il ne soit mie bien: si la dresce bellement, et ne l’estraindre mie trop, ne presser si com font cil qui i font venir par lor ovraige aposteme chaut et contraction au membre, si com nos avons veut maintes fois.	And he feels it well by the hand if it seems to you that it is not well: if he arranges it well and does not restrain it too much, nor press as those do who bring it by their work abscess hot and contraction to the limb, as we have wanted many times.
Et quant li membres est a point, si chastie bien lou malaide qu’il ne lou mueve, ne en veillant ne en dormant, ne en tornant, ne en autre maniere;	And when the member is in place, so chaste the patient well that he does not move it, neither watching nor sleeping, neither turning, nor in any other way.
et warde bien que li membres soit si asseurez qu’il ne sente nule dolor.	and ward well that the member be so assured that he feels no pain at all.
Car quant il sent nulle dolor, si n’est mie a point, et le covient mettre en teil disposition qu’il ne sent nule dolor;	For when he feels no pain, it is not yet in place, and it behooves to put him in such a disposition that he feels no pain.
et te garde k’il soit mis droitement, que tortuositez n’i veigne quant il iert restorez;	and guard that it is placed straightly, that twisting does not come when it is restored.
et li qualitez dou membre brisiet est selonc ceu que je te dis.	And the qualities of the broken limb are according to what I tell you.
Saiches que li membre brisiet sont divers em petitece et en grandor et en forme.	Know that broken limbs are diverse in smallness and in greatness and in form.
Car il i a petis membres, si com brais et dois et semblans: si covient envoloupeir drapelz de lin molz et subtilz;	For there are small limbs, such as arms and legs and similar ones: so it is necessary to wrap them with cloths of soft and fine linen;
et cil qui sont gros, si com cuixe et jambe: si covient envoloupeir d’un liien large et dur, car li larges liiens embraice tout le grant membre, et l’estraint de toutes pars igalment, si qu’il n’i a nule taiche;	and those that are thick, such as the thigh and leg: it is necessary to wrap them with a wide and hard bandage, because the wide bandages embrace the whole large limb, and restrain it from all sides evenly, so that there is no gap;
puis lie entor estoupes legieres, .iij. tours ou iiij. selonc lou membre, et estraint ta main un poc a tout le liien, puis vai au desus de la brisure et l’estraint moins, que la brisure puis esloigne un poc la brisure;	then tie lighter wrappings, three or four turns according to the limb, and restrain your hand a little on the whole bandage, then go above the fracture and restrain it less, than the fracture then distances a little from the fracture;
et mollifie lou liien poc et poc, tant que tu preignes grant partie dou leu sain, puis repren .i. autre liien, et torne entor derechief sus lou leu brisiet;	and soften the bandage a little by little, until you reach a large part of the healthy area, then take another bandage, and turn it again directly above the broken area;
puis revai a la partie desoz de la brisure, et l’estraint moienement, ne mie trop fort ne trop molement, si com nos avons dit en la premiere lieure desus;	Then return to the part below the fracture, and restrain it moderately, not too hard nor too lightly, as we have said in the first place above.
puis met entre les liiens estoupes de lin ou drapelz, tant qu’il soit toz igalz, puis lie tout par desus .i. bendeil, et puis met tes esteles bien faites sus, s’il n’i a aposteme ou enfleure.	Then place between the splints of linen or cloth, until it is all equal, then bind everything above with a bandage, and then put your well-made dressings on top, if there is no abscess or swelling.
Et s’il i a enfleure ou aposteme, si met sus chose apaisant aposteme chaut, et qui oste l’enfleure, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors;	And if there is an abscess or swelling, put something soothing on top of the abscess that warms it and removes the swelling, and leave it like that for several days.
puis estrain sus tes esteles, et soient de moitiet d’une large cainne rese saigement, ou de fust dont on fait les clives, ou de rains de palme, et soient selonc ceste figure:	Then restrain the top dressing, and be of half a wide cane cut neatly, or of wood from which they make flutes, or of palm leaves, and be according to this figure.
mais il covient que li estele que om met sus la brisure soit un poc plus grosse et plus large que les autres;	but it is necessary that the splint that one puts on the fracture be a little larger and wider than the others;
et soit ausi longe com il covient au membre de petitece ou de grandor;	and also as long as is necessary for the limb of smallness or greatness;
puis estraint sus les esteles ausi com tu as fait a la premiere lieure, puis lie desus un fil avenanment, si com en la premiere lieure sus la briseure;	then bind on the splints also as you have done at the first hour, then tie above with a thread evenly, as in the first hour on the fracture;
plus estroit est ensus, adés moins; et covient que li fil soient moien, ne trop gros ne trop menus, et soient de lin mol;	tighter it is above, less below; and it is necessary that the thread be medium, neither too thick nor too thin, and be of soft linen;
car se li fil sont gros, si com j’ai veut des oevres des folz qui font lor lieures des cordes de linement tort, et c’est grant error, car li lieure ne puet estre igal s’il est trop subtilz, et ne covient mie qu’il ait entre chescune estele moins dou doi d’espaice.	for if the thread is thick, as I have seen in works of fools who make their stitches with linen cords twisted, and this is a great error, because the stitch cannot be even if it is too thin, and it should not have between each star less than two fingers' width of space.
Et se li malaides est navrez par les chiés des esteles aprés l’estrignement en leus sains, si met desoz elles estoupes de lin, ou lainne charpie, si qu’il ne se blece.	And if the patient is sore at the sites of the stitches after the tightening in their healthy parts, put under them poultices of linen, or wool felt, so that it does not become blistered.
Quant li plaie est avec la briseure, et li keurs est rompus, je en dirai la cure ci aprés.	When the wound is with a fracture, and the bone is broken, I will say its cure here after.
Et saiches qu’il ne covient mie estraindre d’esteles toz les membres brisiez le premier jor.	And know that it does not behoove to straighten all the broken limbs on the first day.
Car quant li membres est grans, se n’i covient mie mettre esteles fuer que aprés .v. jors ou .vij., ou plus selonc ta seurteit d’aposteme chaut sorvenant;	For when the limb is great, it does not behoove to set it straight sooner than after five days or seven, or more according to your surety of an abscess that comes hot.
et vez ci la maniere des emplaustres anciiens por restorer brisure, dislocation, et torsion: et est que tu pren de la farine que se tient as parois dou molin, et la confis avec abun d’uef, et met ceste confection, ne trop clere ne trop espesse, et en use, et c’est li commune maniere de l’emplaustre restorant la brisure a plusors dispositions, et meismement as femmes et as petis enfans, car il n’est mie ne trop chas ne trop frois.	And see here the manner of ancient plasters for restoring fracture, dislocation, and torsion: and it is that you take flour that is kept at the walls of the mill, and mix it with plenty of egg, and put this mixture, neither too thin nor too thick, and use it, and this is the common way of the plaster restoring fracture in many dispositions, and even to women and to small children, because it is not too hot nor too cold.
Autre maniere d’emplastre restorans la brisure et la dislocation et la torsion: pren З abareis et ladani et enule et asefetide et gomme arabique et mugat, ana .x. З.; mirre et aloes, ana .v. З.; alechil .viiij. З.; et en fai poudre, et les melle avec aubun d’uef; se li complexion de l’ome est chaude, si use de cest emplaustre, car il est de bone composition, et restoure les os brisiés hastanment, et vaut a plusors homes.	Another manner of plaster restoring fracture and dislocation and torsion: take  three ounces of barberry, ladane, and rue, and asafetida, and gum arabic, ana .x.  oz.; myrrh and aloes, ana .v. oz.; alechil .viiij. oz.; and make it into powder, and mix it with the white of an egg; if the complexion of the man is hot, use this plaster, because it is of good composition, and restores broken bones quickly, and is worth to many men.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a torsion: pren mugat et vismalve, ana .x. З.; mirre et aloes, ana .viiij. З.; acaice vi. З.; bolic armenic .x. З., et broie bien, et confit avec aigue ou abun d’uef, et l’aministre.	Another manner of ointment that is good for torsion: take mugwort and wormwood, ana x; myrrh and aloes, ana viiij; acacia vi; Armenian bolus x, and grind well, and confit with water or white of egg, and administer it.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a jointes et as os desevrez de lor leus, et apaise la dolor sorvenant, et le taille usent de l’os, et la briseure: pren lainne novele, et la moille en aisil et en oile cuit, et met sus lou leu. Cist emplastres ne restoure mie, mais il est boins por apaisier d’aposteme chaut, et oste proprement les dolors.	Another manner of ointment for joints and bones dislocated from their places, and it soothes the pain that arises, and the use of bone, and the sprain: take new linen, and moisten it in oil and cooked butter, and put on the sore place. This plaster does not restore [the joint or bone], but it is good for soothing a hot abscess, and properly taking away the pains.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre qui restoure les os brisiez: pren foilles de figuier seches, et foilles de pavol terrestre, et broie ensamble, et fai emplaustre.	Another manner of ointment that restores broken bones: take dried fig leaves, and ground ivy leaves, and grind them together, and make a plaster.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a la restoration de la brisure de l’os et por amenusier lou remenant de l’aposteme. Pren racine de vismalve, camomille, flors de violettes, farine de veces, de chescune une partie; et broie, et confis avec vin, et se li membres est eschaufez, se le confis avec aigue de coriandre moiste, ou d’aigue, et en use.	Another manner of plaster for the restoration of the fracture of the bone and to lessen the remnant of the abscess. Take root of wormwood, chamomile, flowers of violets, flour of beans, of each one part; and grind, and cook with wine, and if the limb is dried, cook it with coriander water, or water, and use it.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre plus fors que li premier, quant aposteme dur vient a la restauration dou membre. Pren racines de vismalve, et semence de lin, balauste, mellilote, et sansuce, et flors de violetes et de camomille, de toutes ana une partie; et broie, et confit avec aigue de salz, ou aigue douce, ou avec vin, selonc la chalor du membre, et son repos.	Another manner of plaster more potent than the first, when a hard abscess comes to the restoration of the limb. Take roots of wormwood, and flaxseed, balm, melilot, and henbane, and flowers of violets and chamomile, of all one part; and grind, and cook with water of salt, or sweet water, or with wine, according to the heat of the limb, and its rest.
Ypocras dist en son livre c’on ne mette sus lou membre brisiet por restorer fuer que cerote fait de cire et d’oile, et nulle autre chose plus, et dist qu’il soit entre dous ne trop molz ne trop durs.	Ipocras says in his book that one should not put on the broken limb for restoration other than a certain one made of wax and oil, and nothing else more, and he says that it should be between two, neither too soft nor too hard.
Et il semble galien c’on doit mettre sus lou membre brisiet, por restoreir, choses seches un poc chaudes, si com mirre et aloes et encens et semblans choses, si com nos avons dit.	And it seems Galen one must put on the broken member, to restore, things dry and a little warm, such as myrrh and aloe and incense and similar things, as we have said.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a lesion et a dolor: pren mugath et chevolz d’omes decopez, ou pennes d’oiseil, et vismalve, et seil igalment, et les broie, et en fai emplaustre et lou lie.	Another manner of poultice that is good for the wound and pain: take mugwort and  chevolz of sheep decocted, or feathers of an owl, and vismalve, and equal parts of these, and grind them up, and make a poultice of it and apply it.
Et puis lou deslie un poc aprés, et pren garde se li malaides ne sent nule dolor, ne ne s’est meus li os de son leu; si ne lou deslie par mains jors	And then loosen the bandage a little after, and take care if the patient feels no pain, nor has the bone moved from its place; so don't loosen it for many days.
Et se dolor vient au leu, ou prurite, sens repos ou enfleure, si te haste, et le deslie, et oste l’emplaustre maintenant; et pren drapeil legier, et esponge de mer moiste, et plonge en aigue, et en leve lou leu, tant que li prurite cesse, et soit apaisie li dolor;	And if pain comes to the place, or itching,  lack of rest, or swelling, then haste, and loosen it, and remove the poultice now; and take light cloth, and a sponge of sea moistened, and dip it in water, and raise the place, until the itching ceases, and the pain is appeased.
puis laisse reposer lou membre une houre, puis met sus lainne seche, moillie en aigue ou en oile roset, et lie sus une nut, tant que tu soies seur d’aposteme chaut;	then let the member rest for an hour, then put dry cloth, soaked in water or rose oil, and tie it on with a nut, as long as you are sure of a hot abscess.
et repose li enflammation dou membre, et soit ostee li dolor, puis rencomence la lieure subtil, et un poc d’emplaustre, et ne l’estraindre mie si fort com devant; et subtilie tant qu’il soit sanez.	and let the inflammation of the member rest, and remove the pain, then begin the subtle binding, and a little bit of emplastrum, and do not constrain it as strongly as before; and be subtle until it is healed.
Et se tu vois que aposteme chaus et roujor et dolor et enfleure sont jai osteit dou tout, et tu as mestier d’emplaustre et de liien, si le rencomence, si com tu a fait premier igalment.	And if you see that the abscess is hot and red, and the pain and swelling are all gone, and you need emplastrum and binding, then begin it again, just as you did at first.
Et s’il ne vient au membre nient de ceu que nos avons dit, si ne le desliier fuer que aprés .iij. jors ou .iiij. ou .v. ou .vij.; et aucune fois le laisse .xx. jors, selonc ce c’on voit, tant que li briseure s’aert, et aproche li ajostement de la char sus;	And if nothing of what we have said comes to the member, then do not unbind it until after three days or four or five or seven; and never leave it for twenty days, according to what you see, as long as the bruise heals, and the joining of the flesh approaches.
adonques lou restraint plus que premier, et li engroisse sa viande, si com j’ai dit devant; et se tu vois lou leu sechier plus que mestier n’est, saiches que norrissemens n’i puet venir;	therefore you restrain it more than before, and thicken its flesh, as I have said before; and if you see the place drying more than is necessary, know that no nourishment can come there
arose lou donques d’aigue chaude tede, toutes les fois que tu lou deslies, et ce soit chescun tier jor, et eslaiche un poc la lieure;	then apply hot water, every time you untie it, and moisten the part a little.
par cest ovraige donques cort li norrissemens au membre, et esmende hastanment ceu que font li fol mire, que restourent le membre tortement: c’est malvais, et si est ovraiges paourous, et je n’i voi autre chose que dou lassier et de l’ovrer droitement.	By this work, the nourishment returns to the limb and quickly mends what the foolish mire do, who leave the limb twisted: it is bad, and this work is dangerous, and I see nothing else but to let it be and work it straight.
des diverses manieres de brisure	of diverse ways of breaking (bones)
Maintes manieres de brisures sont, et diverses figures, et les causes sont destintees;	Many ways of fractures are, and various forms, and the causes are destined.
car il a brisures que sont faites de percussion d’espee, et li colz oste tout l’os jusc’a syfac qui est desoz l’os, si com fait haiche ou fust; et por ceu est apelee ceste maniere de briseure «haichure».	For there are fractures that are made by the percussion of a sword, and the bone's neck all the bone until its face which is under the bone, as done high or shaft; and for this reason this kind of fracture is called "haitchure".
Ou li espee cope l’os par desus sens percier, et est apelee ceste maniere de brisure «absolue»; et est li plaie de ces .ij. brisures grans ou petite.	Or the sword cuts through the bone from above without piercing, and this kind of fracture is called "absolute"; and the wound of these two fractures great or small.
Et s’il i a percussion emboee, ou fendure ou de colz de piere, ou de cheoir sus piere, ou d’autres semblans.	And if there is an enmeshed percussion, or a split or of the bone's neck, or of the head on a bone, or similar things.
Et s’il a brisure persant, qui aproiche jusc’a la toile qui est desoz l’os, ou elle est sus l’os, et est ceste plaie ou grans ou petite.	And if it has a fracture penetrating, which approaches up to the skin that is below the bone, or it is above the bone, and this wound is great or small.
Et si a plaie qui est reponue en l’os ausi subtil com uns chevous, et est li fendure petite, et por ceu est apelee ceste brisure «capillaire»;	And if the wound that is rejoined in the bone as subtle as a hair, and it is the fissure small, and for this reason this fracture is called "capillary";
et si la plaie qui est faite ou par ferir de piere, ou par cheoir, ou par semblant chose, et fait entrer la piece de l’os aval, et est li leus chevez si com font li chaudelier quant il fierent sus les chaudieres; si entre li piere dedens.	and if the wound that is made either by a blow of stone, or by falling, or by similar thing, and makes enter the piece of the bone inward, and it is the joint like how they make the blacksmith when they forge on the cauldrons; so enters the piece inside.
Et ceu avient plus a sous qui ont ou chief moistes os, si com chief d’enfant;	And this happens more to those who have or chiefs moist bones, such as those of a child;
et avient a toutes ces manieres de brisure que pieces menues en sont desevrees si com esteles; et je em parlerai en son leu.	and there occur in all these ways of fracture that pieces are scattered into small parts like stars; and I shall speak of it in its place.
Et conoissons toutes manieres de briseures par la detraction sus elles, et l’inquisition a tentes, et par la char corrumpue qui est sus.	And let us know all the ways of fractures by retracting upon them, and by probing with probes, and by the corrupted flesh that is on it.
Li semblance capillaire est conue par ceu que quant on a descovert l’os, et on frote enche sus, si apert li brisure noire.	The seeming capillary is known by this: when one has uncovered the bone, and rubs upon it, the fracture appears black.
En la cure de la brisure, pren garde as accidens dou malaide, et se tu vois nul malvais accident, si com vomissement de cole, et amission d’entendement, et estension, et paumeson, et fievre ague, et les eulz issir fuer et rougir, et autres semblans em plusors dispositions, si ne puet saner sens doute.	In the cure of a fracture, take care of the accidents of the patient, and if you see no bad accident, such as vomiting of bile, and loss of understanding, and extension, and paleness, and fever ague, and eyes becoming inflamed and red, and other similar things in more dispositions, then it cannot heal without doubt.
Et se tu ne vois accident espoantauble, et tu esperes salut, si comence la cure.	And if you do not see an escapable accident, and you hope for salvation, so commence the cure.
Et quant li navrez vient premier a toi, et c’est en yver, si covient oster l’os devant lou quatorzime jor au mues que tu pues.	And when the fracture comes to you first, and it is in winter, then it is necessary to remove the bone before the fourteenth day as much as you can.
Et se c’est en esteit, si te haste d’oster l’os devant lou septime jor, ainsois que li toile desoz l’os soit corrumpue, et vienent li accident que nos avons dit.	And if it is in summer, then hasten to remove the bone before the seventh day, so that the tissue under the bone does not rot, and comes the accident that we have said.
Et se li brisure de l’os vient jusc’a la toile que cuevre lou cerveil, si covient que tu fendes la partie fendue ensi: et est que tu preignes lou chief dou malaide navreit, et descuevre sus l’os en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et sus la figure de la plaie plus souef que tu pues,	And if the fracture of the bone comes right up to the tissue that covers the brain, then it is necessary that you split the broken part like this: and it is that you place the head of the sick person navreit [I'm unsure what "navreit" means in this context], and uncover above the bone in all the ways that you can, and on the figure of the wound more carefully than you can.
et se decorrement de sanc vient au descovrir l’os, ou aposteme chaus, se li aide de ceu qu’il covient, et est que tu emplisses lou leu de drapelz moilliez en oile roset;	And if blood flows when revealing the bone, or abscess is opened, help with what is necessary, and that you fill the space with soft cloths soaked in rose oil.
et fai reposer la plaie tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et soies asseurez de decorrement de sanc; puis comence entor l’os a oster, et c’est fait selonc .ij. manieres d’ovraige: l’une manieres si est que tu copes au taillement estroit devant, et c’est li forme:	And let the wound rest until the opened abscess is calmed and be sure of the blood flow; then begin to remove around the bone, and this is done in two ways of work: one way is that you cut with a narrow incision in front, and this is the form:
Et puis i boute .i. autre taillement plus grant que lou premier.	And then put another incision larger than the first one.
Et li seconde maniere si est que tu aies nombre de taillemens divers, les uns estrois et les autres larges, et soient a pointe, et soient de fer inde; et en oevre legierement, que tu ne bleces le chief.	And the second way is that you have a number of diverse incisions, some narrow and others wide, and pointed, and made of iron; and in work lightly, so that you do not bruise the bone.
Et se li os est fors et durs, si covient que tu lou perces entor, ainsois que tu i aministres taillemens avec tareres, ne mie parfont qu’il ne percent outre l’os dou test, et doit avoir desus la pointe une marge ou .i. cercle, que ne laisse passer la pointe outre l’os; et t’en covient avoir plusors, si que chescuns viegne en son leu de l’espés de l’os, si que tu aies tareres por toz test; et c’est li forme des .iij. manieres de tareres:	And if the bone is hard and stiff, then it is necessary that you pierce it around, so that you administer splints with tarers, not so deeply that they go beyond the bone of the test, and it must have above the point a margin or circle, which does not allow the point to pass beyond the bone; and it behooves you to have more than one, so that each comes in its place from the thickness of the bone, so that you have tarers for all tests; and this is the form of the three kinds of tarers:
Li qualitez por percier entor l’os brisiet est que tu mettes .i. tarere sus l’os, et torne a tes dois tant que tu saiches que li os est perciez; puis remet lou tarere autre part un poc aprés, et ensi fai tout entor, puis cope as incisoires l’espaice de l’os qui est entre les pertu, et fai ceu plus subtilment que tu pues, et legierement, si com nos avons dit, tant que tu en traies l’os a ta main, ou a aucun des estrumens que tu as si com tenailles, pinceures; et garde que tu ne touchier au cerveil ne au syfac.	The qualities for piercing around the broken bone are that you put one tarer on the bone, and turn to your two hands until you know that the bone is pierced; then put the tarer elsewhere a little after, and thus do all around, then cut with the incisors the space of the bone which is between the pertu, and make them more subtly as you can, and lightly, as we have said, until you draw the bone to your hand, or to any of the instruments that you have such as tongs, pliers; and guard that you do not touch the marrow nor the sifac.
Et quant tu avras l’os perciet, et trait, si couvient que tu reses l’apreteit qui est demoree de l’os a tout .i. autre estrument semblant a un incisoire, mais il covient qu’il soit plus tenves et plus subtilz que li autre incisoire;	And when you will have the bone pierced, and treated, then it behooves that you remove the appendage which is adhered to the bone with any other instrument resembling an incisor, but it behooves that it be more sturdy and more subtle than the other incisor;
et s’il demore rien des petis os, ne nulles escailles, si les oste legierement a .i. des estrumens; puis cure la plaie de tentes et d’oignemens que nos avons dit.	and if it remains nothing of the small bones, nor any scales, then lightly with instruments to the bones. Then cure the wound of tents and bandages as we have said.
Et li autre maniere d’ovraige si est cil que Galiiens dist, qui est plus saus; et le loa molt fort, et c’est sa parole.	And the other manner of work is that which Galen says, which is drier; and the load very strong, and that is his word.
Il covient premier que tu descuevres une partie de l’os, lai ou li brisure apert mues, si que quant tu avras descovert celle partie, si metras desoz lou chief de cest incisoire lenticulaire, de coi ci est li forme:	It is necessary first that you uncover a part of the bone, where the fracture appears to move, so that when you have uncovered that part, then place under the head of this lentil-shaped incisional instrument, for this is its form:
Et ne trenche mie d’une part, et est li partie ague en .ij. costez, si que li trenchans est devers l’os; puis fier d’un petit maillet sus, si que tu copes legierement l’os tout entor, et te done bien en garde de la toile que est desoz;	And do not cut from one part, and it is the sharpened side in two coasts, so that the cutting edge is towards the bone; then strike with a small mallet above, so that you gently chip away at the bone all around, and take good care of the cloth that is underneath;
s’elle est aerse a l’os, si l’oste legierement, car on l’oste bien sens nuisement, et sens paor.	If it is caught to the bone, gently loosen it, for one loosens it well without pain, and without fear.
Et se li brisure de l’os ne perce jusc’a la toile, et li os est copez tant soulement par desus, et il i a petites pieces, si couvient rere celle asperiteit, et oster les escailles au raseur subtil dont tu dois avoir diverses quantitez, por amenistrer en chescun leu le plus covenauble, selonc l’ovraige et la figure de la brisure.	And if the bone fracture does not reach the skin, and the bone is broken only from above, and there are small pieces, it is necessary to first apply this asperity, and remove the scales with a fine rasp which you must have in various quantities, to administer in each place the most suitable one, according to the work and the figure of the fracture.
Si reis devant de grant raseurs, et aprés de plus subtilz, et ne cesser de ceu faire tant k’il soit bien.	If you begin with coarse rasps, and afterwards with finer ones, and do not cease doing this until it is well.
En chescune des autres tailleures capillaires et brisure subtil, covient que tu amenistres cause selonc son adrecement; et c’est chose que n’est mie reponue a celui qui a mis son estude en cest art.	In each of the other capillary cuts and subtle fractures, it is necessary that you administer  cause according to its place; and this thing is not replied to by him who has put his study into this art.
Et se li syfac est descovers, si covient que tu preignes .i. drapeil de lin, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et le moille en oile roset, et le mete sus la plaie;	And if the ulcer is uncovered, it befits you to take one linen cloth, according to the quantity of the wound, and moisten it in rose oil, and place it on the wound;
puis pren .i. autre drapeil doublé en .ij. ou en .iij., et le moille en vin et en oile roset, et le met sus le premier drapeil; et fai ceu plus legierement que tu pues, que tu ne grever lou syfac, puis aministre par desus .i. autre liien, et ne l’estraindre mie fuer que tant k’il teigne la plaie soulement;	Then take another cloth doubled in two or three, and moisten it in wine and rose oil, and place it on the first cloth; and do this more gently than you can, that you do not injure the ulcer, then administer by above one other linen, and do not constrain it more than enough so that it only holds the wound.
et le laisse ensi .i. jor ou .ij., tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, puis le deslie, et i aministre medicines si com racines de lis, et farine de veces, et poudre d’encens, et aristologe, et semblans choses; et de ces choses fai poudre, et met sus la plaie, et i aministre adés medicines mondefians sens mordication;	and let it so for one or two days, until the abscess is calmed, then untie it, and administer medicines such as roots of lilies, and powdered vetiver, and incense powder, and aristolochia, and similar things; and of these things make a powder, and put it on the wound, and administer additional medicines compounded without mordication;
et warde que li plaie soit adés nette, que tu n’i laissier mie l’oignement, ne n’i laissier mie assembler bowe, car quant bowe s’asemble sus la toile dou cerveil, si la corront et porrist, et avient au malaide grans malice; car quant on met sus lou syfac chose mordant, si nercist par desus.	And guard that the wound be always clean, that you do not leave any ointment there, nor let any bowe assemble there, because when bowe assembles on the cloth of the brain, it corrodes and pierces, and brings great malice to the patient; for when one puts on top of this thing biting, it bites from above.
Pren warde donques, se nulz mavais accidens vient au malaide, si com nos avons dit, si est doutable sens doute.	Take ward then, if no bad accidents come to the patient, as we have said, so it is doubtful without doubt.
Et se noiror n’i vient fuers que por la medicine c’on a mise sus, que teil vertu ait, si covient que tu preignes une partie de miel, et .iij. parties d’oile roset et en glue .i. drapel, et lou met sus lou syfac;	And if no other blackness comes there except from the medicine we have put on, that it has virtue, then you must take one part of honey, and three parts of rose oil and in glue one drapel, and put it on the thing.
puis lou cure de manieres de cures qu’il couvient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	then the cure of manners of cures that it is fitting, until it is healed.
Saiches que aucune fois sont brisies les .ij. parties dou neis desus, ou li une par li soulement, car ce sont .ij. os; et cil desoz est cartillaginous, et ne brise mie, si ne fait fuer k’enbower ou tordre, et puis saine.	Know that sometimes the two parts of the lower jaw are broken, or one by the other alone, because they are two bones; and this one below is cartilaginous, and does not break unless forced to bend or twist, and then heals.
Et se l’une des .ij. parties est brisie, si covient que tu boutes ton petit doi ou pertus dou neis, et met igal cele brisure dedens a ton doi indice, et au pouchet par defuer, tant que li neis reveigne selonc sa figure natureil;	And if one of the two parts is broken, it is necessary that you put your little finger or point of the index finger into the mouth, and place the broken piece inside with your index finger, and to the pocket outside, until the jaw returns according to its natural form;
et fai ce legierement, et warde que li malaides ne sente dolor par ton ovraige.	and do this gently, and guard that the patient does not feel pain from your work.
Et se li brisure est en la partie desus lou neis, et ne puet venir li dois au leu, si couvient que tu lou mettes igal au chief d’un rait un poc gros.	And if the fracture is in the part above the nose, and it cannot come to its place, then you should put it even on top of a rail a little thick.
Et se li brisure est de .ij. pars, si refai autretel, et te haste de restorer lou premier jor, se tu pues;	And if the fracture is of two parts, do so again, and hasten to restore it the first day, if you can.
se ce non, aprés lou septime ou le disime, quant li apostemes chaus est apaisiez, puis bouthe au chief dou neis tentes de drapelz de lin, se li brisure est en une partie.	If not, after the seventh or tenth day, when the abscess has calmed, then bandage to the top of the nose ten sheets of linen, if the fracture is in one part.
Ou tu boutes .i. autre d’autre part, se li brisure i est; et soient les tentes si grosses qu’eles emplissent les pertus dou neis.	Or you put one on the other side if the fracture is there; and let the sheets be so thick that they fill the nostrils.
Et dirent aucun restorour c’on doit moillier les tentes em burre, et muer chescun jor. Il ne me semble mie que ce soit bien, mais covient qu’elles soient moillies en confection d’aubun d’uef, et de poudre de molin; puis laisse la tente, tant que li os soit fers, et li cartilaiges endurcis.	And some restorers say that one must moisten the tents in butter, and change each day. It does not seem good to me, but it is necessary that they be moistened in the confection of albumen of egg, and powder of mill; then leave the tent, as long as the bone is hard, and the cartilages hardened.
Et aucune fois boute on ou neis pennes d’oie en leu de tentes, et si a .i. souef drapeil entor, et se tient la briseure, et soffle li malaides parmi; or fai lou kel ke tu vues.	And sometimes one puts goose feathers in their place, and so i.e., one sheet of drape around it, and it holds the blister, and blows the patient among; do what you see fit.
Et se apostemes chaus vient au neis tandis com tu i oevres, si i met cerote ou coton moilliet en oile roset, ou en .i. poc de dyaquilon.	And if an abscess comes to the new while you work on it, put cerote or cotton moistened in rose oil, or in i. p. of diaquilon.
Et se apostemes chaus n’i vient, si met emplastre par defuer, de farine de sisament, et de poudre d’encens, confites avec aubun d’uef, puis met sus estoupes legieres, et ne liier mie lou neis;	And if an abscess occurs there, place a plaster from outside, of sesame flour and incense powder, cooked with egg yolk, then put light bandages on top, and do not bind it tightly at all.
et se li brisure dou neis est petite, et il est brisiés em menues pieces, si l’estrai as estrumens covenables a ceu, puis cout la fendure, et la cure de choses enjanrans char, et soudant, si com emplastres et oignemens covenables a ceu;	And if the bone is broken in small pieces and fractured, then extract it with suitable instruments, then sew the fissure together, and cure it with things like cartilage and soldering, and suitable plasters and ointments.
et s’il n’a dedens lou neis nule plaie, si lou cure de tentes, et i met cainnes de plonc, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if there is no wound inside the bone, then cure it with splints and put bandages of linen inside, until it heals.
de la routure de la mandibule	Of the jaw fracture
Quant li mandibule est route desoz, et il n’i a point de plaie defuer, et li brisure est defuer tant soulement, et n’est mie brisiez en dous, fuer que corbelz dedens, si le conoist on legierement.	When the jaw is broken below, and there is no external wound, and the fracture is only outside, and is not broken in two, except for a bulge inside, if one knows it lightly.
Il covient, se li brisure est en la destre partie, que tu boutes ton doi indice en la bouche dou malaide; et se li brisure est en la mandibule senestre, si boute ton doi indice de la main destre, et boute la brisure dedens legierement, et l’afaite a l’autre main par defuer, et met igal.	It is necessary, if the fracture is on the right side, that you put your left index finger in the mouth of the sick person; and if the fracture is on the left jawbone, put your right index finger, and push the fracture inside lightly, and make it with the other hand outside, and put it straight.
Et se li brisure de la mandibule est desevree en .ij., si covient que tu aministres extension de .ij. pars, tant qu’il soit igalz.	And if the jawbone fracture is broken in two, it is necessary that you administer an extension of two parts, until it is straight.
Et se commovemens des dens avient, ou routure, si les estrain d’un fil d’or ou d’argent ou de soie, puis met sus la mandibule brisie cerote, et met sus .i. drapel double; et met sus lou drapel une grant estele bien faite, ou une piece de cuir igal, longe et large selonc la mandibule, et la lie sus au mues que tu pues, et comande a malaide qu’il se repose, et menjuce viandes legieres.	And if movement of the teeth happens, or breakage, so restrain with a thread of gold or silver or silk, then place upon the broken jaw carefully, and place one double cloth; and place upon the cloth a great star well made, or a piece of leather equal, long and wide according to the jaw, and tie it up on the as much as you can, and command the patient that he rests himself, and eats light meats.
Et se tu vois que li figure se chainge, si le deslie au tier jor, et puis remet a point ceu que c’est chaingiet; et met emplaustre sus, de la poudre dou moulin avec abun d’uef ou farine de sisament, aprés ceu que tu as osteit lou cerote; et met sus l’emplaustre lainne legiere, et se li emplaustres s’aert, et li disposition dou malaide ne se chainge, laisse le tant k’il soit sanez; maintes fois est sanez en .iij. semainnes.	And if you see that the figure changes, so untie it on the third day, and then re-apply what has changed; and place a plaster on top, of powder from the mill with plenty of egg or sesame flour, after that you have removed the cerote; and place a light cloth over the plaster, and if the plasters adheres, and the disposition of the patient does not change, leave it as long as it is healthy; many times it is healed in three weeks.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit maintes fois.	And if an abscess comes, administer what we have said many times.
Et s’il i a brisure et plaie ensamble, rewarde se nule piece de l’os en est ostee; si subtilie de l’oster as estrumens covenaubles a ceu.	And if there is a fracture and wound together, reward no piece of the bone is removed; so subtly of the removing with instruments suitable to that.
Et se li plaie est estroite, si l’eslarge a flaime selonc ta necessiteit.	And if the wound is narrow, then enlarge it with flame according to your need.
Et quant tu avras ostees toutes ces pieces, et il n’i demore nule, si cout la plaie, s’ele est large, et met sus .i. des emplaustres covenaubles a ceu, por enjanrer char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you will have removed all these pieces, and there is none remaining, then cover the wound, if it is wide, and put upon it one plaster suitable to that, in order to hinder flesh, until it is healed.
de la forcele	of the forceps
Li forcele brise plusors fois devant, devers l’espaule, et li brisure si est selonc .iij. manieres: ou elle est brisie et desevree en .ij., et i a pieces, et est li plus legiere a restorer; ou il i a brisure avec plaie.	The fracture breaks many times in front, towards the shoulder, and the fracture is according to three ways: or it is broken and severed in two, and there are pieces, and it is the lightest to restore; or there is a fracture with a wound.
Et li ovraiges si est quant li brisure est sens plaie, que tu aies .ij. ministres, si que li uns teigne l’ajutoire que sent la forcele brisie; et li autres estende lou col vers la partie; puis met igal la brisure a tes dois, si que li forme soit si com il covient, et n’i ait ne apparance ne chevement.	And the work is like this when the fracture is without a wound, that you have two ministers, so that one holds the shoulder that feels the broken bone; and the other stretches the neck towards the part; then put equal the fracture with your hands, so that the form is as it should be, and there is neither appearance nor misalignment.
Et se tu a mestier de plus estendre, si met desoz l’espaule au malaide une spere reonde de drap, ou de lainne, et soit grosse selonc ta necessiteit; et estent et lieve la forcele, et estraint le spere a ta main, si que tu mettes igal la brisure, si com il covient.	And if you need to extend more, put under the shoulder of the patient a round sphere of cloth or wool, and be it large according to your necessity; and being and lightly raising the bone, and restraining the sphere with your hand, so that you put equal the fracture, as it should be.
Et se tu ne pues traire le chief de la forcele au defuer, por ceu qu’elle vient em parfont, si covient que li malaides gise sovin sus son hatereil, et met desoz l’espaule .i. oreillier moien, et boute li ministres l’espaule aval, tant que li os de la forcele soit levez.	And if you cannot draw the head of the shoulder with force because it comes back in place, then it is necessary that the patient lie prone on his arm and place below the shoulder 1 hour glass, and push the ministers' shoulder down until the bone of the shoulder is lifted.
Et puis adrece la brisure a tes dois, et se tu lou trueves debrisiet, si covient que tu fendes sus; et trai fuer les pieces legierement, et se li os ne puet joindre por aucun sormontement, si le cope a l’un des incisoires que tu as; mais que tu mettes desoz la forcele cest estrument, por warder lou syfac:	And then address the fracture to your two, and if you find it fragmented, it is necessary that you split further; and treat the pieces gently, and if the bone cannot join by any elevation, so cut to one of the incisors that you have; but that you put under the shoulder this instrument, in order to guard the shaft:
et semble une cuiller, et n’est mie chevez, et soit ausi large com il lou covient, selonc la grandor de l’os et la possance de l’uevre; et ait .ij. chiés, si com tu vois, et soit li uns larges, et li autres estrois, si com est li routure de la plaie que tu as fait quant tu as trait les os;	And it seems like a spoon, and is not at all hollow, and be also wide as it is convenient, according to the size of the bone and the strength of the work; and have two heads, as you see, and one broad, and the other narrow, as is the rupture of the wound that you made when treating the bones;
et quant tu es asseurez d’aposteme chaut, si cout la plaie, et se li routure est petite, ou tu doutes aposteme chaut, si emple la plaie de drapelz et de tentes, selonc sa quantiteit.	and when you are sure of the hot abscess, if cut the wound, and if the rupture is small, or you doubt the hot abscess, then apply the wound with bandages and tents, according to its quantity.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si moille .i. drapel en oile roset et en aisil et en vin, et met sus.	And if a hot abscess comes, then moisten one bandage in rose oil and in honey and in wine, and place it on top.
Li estrignement de l’os, quant il est sens plaies et sens tailleure, est que tu mettes sus l’os l’enplaustre de la poudre dou molin et d’aubun d’uef, et met estoupes legieres sus, et met une spere desoz l’assele, se tu en as mestier;	The strapping of the bone, when it is without wounds and without cuts, is that you put on top of the bone the plaster of ground flour and yolk of egg, and put light bandages on top, and put a spear underneath the ass-  if you need.
puis pren une tres grant bende d’une palme de large, puis met .i. drapeil double sus estoupes, et l’emplaustre; puis pren une estele subtil de .iij. dois de large et de lonc, et l’envoloupe entor celui bendeil, si que li chief dou bendeil soient pendant;	Then take a very wide bandage of one palm's width, then put one double bandage on top of the bandages and plaster; then take a strip subtly of three digits wide and long, and wrap it around that bandaged one so that the head of the bandage hangs down;
et met l’estele sus la briseure, et torne le bendeil sus lou col, et desoz l’asselle sainne, et desoz l’asselle malaide; et la ramoinne de chescune partie, et quant tu vois ke li lieure tient la briseure avenanment, et tu vois clerement que li estele ne se muet desus l’os brisiet, si le rewarde chescun jor, et quant li liiens eslaiche, si lou restraint;	And put the splint on the fracture, and turn the bandage around the neck, and below the healthy shoulder, and below the broken shoulder; and move each part, and when you see that the splint holds the fracture properly, and you clearly see that the splint does not move above the fractured bone, then reward them every day, and when the ligaments loosen, then restrain it.
et fai gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li met quant il dort .i. petit orillier desoz l’assele, por lever l’ajutoire en haut; si aligera li brisure de la forcele par l’aligement de l’espaule, ou tu li lie lou bras au col, et ne lou desliier se malvais accidens n’i vient, jusc’a .xx. jors;	And make the patient lie on his back, and put him when he sleeps 1 small pillow under the shoulder, to raise the arm up; thus it will lighten the fracture of the clavicle by the elevation of the shoulder, or you tie the arm to the neck, and do not untie it unless a bad accident occurs, until 20 days;
puis rencomence l’emplaustre, se tu vois qu’il en ait mestier, et l’estraint et le laisse ensi, tant qu’il soit restorez; et elle est restoree au plus en .xxviij. jors, et en moins a aucuns homes.	then begin the plaster again, if you see that he needs it, and restrain him and leave him so, until he is restored; and it is restored in at most 28 days, and in less for some people.
de la brisure de l’espaule	of the fracture of the shoulder
Poc avient que li espaule brise ou large leu ne em mileu, et ne lou seit on fuers que par lou touchement; si l’apareille selonc la figure de la brisure, et la ramoinne selonc sa forme natureil, en toutes les manieres que tu pues; puis met sor le leu poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, et estoupes legieres, et met sus .i. drapeil double; puis met sus une estele large et subtil, un poc plus large de l’espaule, et se desoz l’estele est chevemens en aucun leu de l’espaule, si emple celle cheveure d’estoupes de lin, si que li estele siece igalment; et puis l’estraint a tout une grant bende fermement, si que li estele ne se mueve de son leu, et regarde le liien chescun jor; et toutes les fois k’il amolist, si l’estraint, et met igal l’estele s’elle est fuer de son leu, et gise li malaides sus son costeit; et li espaule est restouree en .xx. jors ou en xxv,  Et quant cist nombres est acomplis, si le deslie, et soies seur, car ce n’est mie os qui se mette fuer legierement.	It happens that the shoulder breaks or dislocates far from its place, and it is not known whether by force; so, according to the shape of the fracture, and set it according to its natural form, in all the ways that you can; then put on the place powder of the mill with abundance of egg, and light bandages, and put over .i. double drapeil; then put on a large and fine splint, a little wider than the shoulder, and if the splint is chafed in any part of the shoulder, so use the chafing of linen bandages, so that the splint lies evenly; and then bind it with a strong bandage firmly, so that the splint does not move from its place, and watch the joint every day; and whenever it softens, bind it again, and put back the splint if it is out of place, and make the patient lie on his side; and the shoulder is restored in .xx. days or in xxv, and when this number is completed, unbind it, and be sure, for it is not bone that easily sets itself apart.
Et se une piece de l’os tent avant, et point desoz lou keur, si fent sus, et l’oste, et fai ceu que nos avons dit en la brisure de la forcele d’apaisier aposteme chaut.	And if a piece of bone protrudes forward, and not below the joint, so do it above, and the bone, and do what we have said in the fracture of the collarbone to soothe the hot abscess.
de la brisure dou pis	of the fracture of the leg
Li peis est aucune fois brisiez em mileu, mais ce avient poc; mais il brise sovent au defuer. Et quant il est brisiez emmi, si decline au desoz, et sent li malaides grant dolor, et faute d’alainne, et toust, et par aventure vomist sanc, et apert li chevemens en l’os brisiés, et lou sent om bien.	The leg is sometimes broken in the middle, but this happens little; but it breaks often at the outside. And when it is broken in the middle, it leans to the lower side, and the patient feels great pain, and loss of strength, and all, and perhaps vomits blood, and the veins open in the broken bone, and it feels well all over.
Et li restoracion si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, et li met .i. cussin entre les espaules, puis presse les espaules, et li assemble les costes des .ij. costelz a tes mains, et subtilie dou mettre igal a toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que li figure de l’os soit si com il covient; puis met sus emplaustres et estoupes desus l’estele subtil de salz, ou d’autre fust legier, et l’envoloupe en .i. drapeil, et la lie sus l’os brisiet, si qu’elle ne se mueve; et torne le liien reondement au dos, et l’estraint avenanment, et rewarde chescune houre la liure, et s’elle ramolist, si l’estraint; et s’il lou covient desliier, por corrosion ou por prurite que vient au leu, ou dolor ou aposteme, si te haste, et lou deslie, et raie l’emplaustre, et adresce ceu qui i est venus de manieres de cures; puis ramoinne l’emplaustre, et l’estraint tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the restoration is that the patient lies often on his back, and he puts 1 cushion between the shoulder blades, then presses the shoulder blades, and he assembles the ribs of the 2 ribs with your hands, and subtly does put it equal in all ways that you can, until the figure of the bone is as it ought; then puts above plasters and bandages above the subtle layer of salt, or another light husk, and enwraps it in 1 drape, and lays it on top of the broken bone, so that it doesn't move; and turn the bandage round to the back, and strain it well, and reward each hour the bond, and if it softens, then strain it; and if it comes to him to loosen, for corrosion or for itch that comes to the place, or pain or abscess, then hasten, and loose it, and wipe the plaster, and address what has come there by ways of cures; then put back the plaster, and strain it until it is healed.
de la brisure des costes	of the breakage of the ribs
Saiches que li briseure des costes ne vient fuer que en leus gros aprés le dos, et au chief dedens, et ne ploient fuer que por ceu qu’eles sont glairouses; et le sent om bien a l’inquisition as dois.	Know that the breakage of the ribs comes only in their thickest parts after the back, and at the head inside, and they bend only for that reason because they are brittle; and one feels it well at the examination of the two sides.
Et li restoremens si est que tu met igal la brisure, si com il covient. Et puis met l’emplaustre, et l’estraint d’une estele, se tu en as mestier.	And the restoration is that you put the breakage equal, as it is right. And then put the bandage, and restrain with a splint, if you have need of it.
Et se li brisure des costes est declinans au dedens, si sent li malaides tres grant dolor, et pointure, ausi com de pleuresin, car li os point la toile; et alaine a poinnes, et toust et vomist grant planteit de sanc, et c’est de grief santeit, et li ancien i ont mis grant engien.	And if the breakage of the ribs is leaning inwards, the patient feels very great pain, and sharpness, as well as from pleurisy, because the bone pierces the membrane; and besides pains, and coughing, and vomiting a large quantity of blood, and this is a serious illness, and the ancients have put much care into it.
Et si a de ces qui dient qu’il le covient aministrer viandes qui enflent le ventre, por bouter la briseure au defuer.	And if some say it is necessary to administer meats that swell the belly, to expel the wind outward.
Nos ne faisons mie ceu, que apostemes chaulz n’i viegne, s’il n’i est venus.	We do not do this, except for hot abscesses, if they have not yet come.
Et s’il i est venus, si le saine.	And if it has come, then treat it.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on met ventouses sor le leu, por sucier forment, et c’est semblant a raison; toutevoie, doutance i a que li ventouse n’atraie les superfluitez au leu por la disposition de foiblece.	And some of us say that one should put suction cups on the area to draw out fluids strongly, and this seems reasonable; nonetheless, there is doubt that the suction cup draws the superfluities to the area for the sake of weakness.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on doit covrir le leu de lainne moillie en oile chaut, et met on tentes entre les costes por metre igal la lieure entor, puis soit curez de la cure de pleurisin, de viande et de medicine.	And they say any one of you should cover the place with a woolen cloth in hot oil, and put tents between the ribs to make equal the lying wound, then be cured of the plague of pleurisy, meat, and medicine.
Et se li malaides sent grant dolor qu’il ne puet soffrir par l’os qui point la toile, et doutance est au malaide, si covient fendre sus lou leu de la coste brisie, et covient mettre desoz .i. estrument por warder lou syfac; et adonques doit on trenchier l’os, et traire legierement, et puis coudre les .ij. levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, et le curez d’emplaustres, tant qu’il soit sanez. Et se apostemes chaus vient, si met sus drapelz moilliez en oile roset, et met sus lou leu; et cure tandis le leu de ceu qu’il covient a aposteme, et soit gisans sovins sus lou costeit ou il doit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the patient feels great pain that he cannot bear because of the bone pointing through the cloth, and there is doubt in the patient, it is necessary to cut above the place of the broken rib, and it is necessary to put under one instrument to ward off the syfac; and then must one trenchier the bone, and draw lightly, and then sew the two lips of the wound, if it is large, and cure it with plasters, until it is healed. And if an abscess comes, then put on soft cloths in rose oil, and put on the place; and cure while the place of that which it is necessary to abscess, and be lying still upon the side where it must, until it is healed.
de la brisure dou col	of the breaking of the neck
Aucune fois vient briseure as os dou col, et poc avient k’il ploie; et ausi a l’espinee dou dos.	Sometimes comes a break of bones of the neck, and sometimes it happens that it bends; and also in the spine of the back.
Et quant ce avient a aucun, et tu vues savoir s’il sera sanez ou non, si pren warde se tu vois ses mains mollifiies et enflees et mortes, et ne les puet movoir ne estendre, et quant tu les poins d’une aguille, si ne lou sent. Saiches qu’il est mortelz em plusors dispositions, et s’il les muet et sent bien quant on les estraint et point, saiches que li jointure de l’os est sauve, et que li malaides iert curez, s’on i met cure.	And when this happens to anyone, and you want to know if he will be healed or not, then take heed if you see his hands softened and swollen and dead, and he cannot move them nor stretch them, and when you prick them with a needle, he does not feel it. Know that he is mortal in many dispositions, and if he moves them and feels well when they are stretched and pointed, know that the joint of the bone is saved, and that the patient will be cured, if one puts care to him.
Et se semblans chose vient a l’espinee dou dos, et tu vues savoir s’il iert sanez ou non, si pren warde se li piez sont amollis, et se li accident i sont qui sont em mains, et sus lou dos saut ventositeit et egestion sens volonteit; et quant on l’a sovineit sus son ventre, si saut egestion sens volonteit. Et quant il est sovinez sus son dos et il vuet asseller, si ne puet. Saiches qu’il est mortelz: si ne laboreir mie en sa cure.	And if similar things happen to the spine of the back, and you want to know if he will be healed or not, then take heed if his legs are softened, and if the accident is in his hands, and on his back there is a sauteness and excretion without will; and when one supports him on his belly, there is an excretion without will. And when he is supported on his back and wants to sit up, he cannot. Know that he is mortal: if he does not labor well in his cure.
Et se cist accident ne li vienent, si est li chose plus legiere.	And if this accident does not happen to him, then the thing is lighter.
Et li cure si est que tu rewardes s’il i a aposteme chaut, si met sus l’espinee oile roset ou oile de moieuf d’uef, tant qu’il soit apaisiez; puis met sus un des emplaustres confortans et sechans, et le lie d’un liien, et comande au malaide a reposer; et ne dorme mie sus celle partie ou il sent la dolor, tant k’il soit sanez.	And the cure is that you reward it if there is an abscess hot, so put on the spine rose oil or egg yolk of an egg, until it is appeased; then put on a comforting and drying plaster, and bind it with a bandage, and command the patient to rest; and do not sleep on that part where he feels pain, as long as he is healed.
Et se aucuns os se dessevre, si covient coper sus lou keur; et oste l’os, puis assemble les .ij. levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, a une costure, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li chiés de l’os est brisiez, ki est apelez li «chiés de la kowe», se i boute ton pouchet de ta main senestre, et le met igal a l’autre main a ton pooir, puis met l’emplaustre et l’estele sus, se tu en a mestier; puis l’estraint, et s’il i a os desevreit, si fent sus, et l’oste, et cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And if any bone is broken, it is necessary to cover the wound; and remove the bone, then assemble the two edges of the wound, if it is large, with a suture, then treat it with ointment that promotes healing, until it is healed; and if the head of the bone is broken, which is called the "head of the cow," put your thumb of your left hand in it, and place it equal to the other hand at your power, then put the plaster and splint on top, if you need it; then restrain it, and if there are bones that have been displaced, do this again, remove the bone, and treat the wound until it is healed.
de la brisure de l’os de la hainche	of the break of the bone of the hip
Poc avient que li os de la hainche soit brisiez, et s’il avient, si n’avient fuer c’un poc d’amenuisement au chief; et fent dou lonc, et decline au pardedens, et vient au malaide dolor au leu, et pointure, et enfle ceu que brise.	It happens that the bone of the hip is broken, and if it happens, it should not have been for a little weakening at the top; and making long, and declining to the sides, and coming to the patient pain in the place, and prickling, and swelling that breaks.
Et li restoration si est que tu estendes ta main sus, tant que tu soies sus la briseure; et saiches quelz est li brisure et li figure de li; et se li brisure est au chief soulement, si met igal cele brisure, tant qu’ele soit a figure natureil.	And the restoration is that you extend your hand above, as long as you are on the fracture; and know which is the fracture and its figure; and if the fracture is at the top only, so put equal the fracture, as long as it is to a natural figure.
Et se li brisure est dou lonc, ou elle decline au dedens, si fai gesir le malaide sus son ventre, tant que li restauration de cele brisure te soit aparillie.	And if the fracture is long, or it declines inward, so make the patient lie on his belly, as long as the restoration of that fracture be apparent to you.
Et quant tu l’avras mise igal, si met sus l’emplaustre, puis met sus une estele de fust ou de keur, et estraint la briseure, si qu’ele ne se mueve; et emple le leu desoz les costes, tant que li lieure soit igalz.	And when you have put it even, place it on the emplasters, then place a splint of wood or of horn, and restrain the fracture so that it does not move; and apply the plaster below the ribs, as long as the limb is even.
Et comande au malaide k’il dorme sus son costeit sain, ou sus son dos.	And command the patient that he sleep on his healthy side or on his back.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si n’i tochier, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et met sus ceu que nos avons devant dit; et puis revien a la restauration, et l’estraint si com il covient, s’il n’i a nul mavais accident; et c’est li maniere.	And if an abscess appears there, do not touch it until the abscess is calmed, and put on what we have said before; and then return to the restoration, and restrain it as appropriate, if there is no bad accident; and this is the manner.
de la brisure de l’ajutoire	of the fracture of the shoulder
Li adjutoires est ceu qui est entre lou coute et lou chief de l’espaule, et s’il est brisiez, si le doit on restorer selonc l’une des .ij. manieres: dont l’une est que tu pren .i. fust plain de moiene groissor, selonc ceste forme:	The adjuitor is that which is between the shoulder and the head of the shoulder, and if it is broken, one should restore it according to one of the two ways: one of which is that you take one staff of medium thickness, according to this form:
Et lie as .ij. chiés .ij. liens, et les pent en haut, et siece li malaide sus .i. siege; puis li giete som bras brisiet sus le fust, tant qu’il viegne a l’aissele, et ait em mi une corbeure de fust, puis pent sus aucune pesant chose ou li ministres l’estende aval; puis mette li mires la briseure igal a ses mains ensamble, tant que li briseure retorne si com il covient.	And tie the two ends of .two. strings together, and lift them up, and place the patient on one seat; then put his broken arm upon the staff, until it comes to the armpit, and has a curve of staff in the middle, then put upon any heavy thing or minister its extension down; then put the hands of the fracture equal together, as long as the fracture returns as it should.
Et li autre maniere si est que on sovine le malaide sus son hatereil, et li lie la main a son col, puis comande a .ij. ministres que li uns teigne ceu qui est sus la briseure a ses mains, et li autres teigne desoz a tout .i. liien, et estende chescuns a sa partie.	And the other way is that one supports the patient on his bed, and ties his hand to his neck, then commands two ministers that one holds what is above the fracture in their hands, and the other holds below at all .i. point, and extends each to its part.
Et se tu vues que li estraction soit plus fors, si estraint .i. liien desoz la briseure, et sus la briseure, et estende chescuns des ministres a sa part. Et se li briseure est prochiene au chief de l’espaule, si covient que tu mettes .i. liien moien desoz l’assele, et .i. autre vers lou coute, desoz la briseure; et ausi se li briseure est devers lou coute, si i covient mettre .i. liien legierement, sens labor, tant que li briseure soit igalz sus lou leu, et sus lou coute; puis met igal la brisure, si com il covient, et l’estraint, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	And if you see that the extraction is more forth, constrain  that is, the linen under the bruise, and on the bruise, and extend each of the ministers to its part. And if the bruise is near the head of the shoulder, it behooves that you put one linen in the middle under the arse, and one other towards the outside, under the bruise; and also if the bruise is towards the outside, then it behoves to put one linen lightly, without labor, until the bruise is equal on the top, and on the outside; then set the bruise equal, as it behoves, and constrain it, if an abscess does not come.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si ne l’estraindre mie jusc’a .vij. jors, et met sus lainne moillie en aisil et en oile roset, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez; puis l’estraint, et li maniere de l’estraindre si est que tu mettes l’emplaustre sus la briseure, puis assemble le bras sus l’ajutoire, et met ta main sus l’espaule ou sus lou sein; et met le drapeil, et estraint sus l’ajutoire, et sus lou bras, si que li bras soit en leu d’esteles, s’aucune chose ne le te deffent, ou se li os n’est muez.	And if an abscess comes to the place, do not constrain it until seven days, and put on linen moistened in oil of roses, as long as the abscess is appeased; then constrain it, and the manner of constraining it is that you put the bandage on the bruise, then assemble the arm upon the shoulder, and put your hand upon the shoulder or upon the breast; and put the cloth, and constrain upon the shoulder, and upon the arm, so that the arm is in its place, unless anything prevents you, or if the bone is not moved.
Et se tu doutes que li os ne se mueve, si use d’esteles, et met sus la brisure une estele plus large et plus fort des autres, et ait entre chescune estele .i. doi d’espaice, et soit chescune estele si grans qu’elle passe la briseure .iij. dois de chescune part; puis estrain sus les esteles, ensi com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre sus la briseure, plus fort et moins en aloignant.	And if you doubt that the bone is moved, use splints, and put on the bruise a splint wider and stronger than the others, and have between each splint one digit of space, and let each splint be so large that it passes over the bruise three digits on each side; then constrain upon the splints, as I said at the beginning of the chapter on the bruise, more strongly and less widely.
Et se tu vois l’assise des esteles, et l’estrignement, si com nos avons dit, en l’oure que tu restoures le membre brisiet, et tu doutes l’aposteme chaut, si le laisse a liier jusc’a septime jor, si com nos avons dit; puis regarde chescuns .iij. jors lou lien, que prurite ne enfleure n’i viegne au leu, ou li norrissemens ne puist venir au membre por ceu k’il est trop estrois. Si l’adrece, si com nos avons dit.	And if you see the position of the bones, and the constriction, as we have said, in the hour that you restore the broken limb, and you doubt the hot abscess, leave it tied until the seventh day, as we have said; then look every three days the ligature, that pricking nor swelling does not come to the place, or that the purulence may not come to the member for because it is too inflamed. If this is the case, as we have said.
Et se nulz telz accidens n’i vient, si ne lou desliier fuer que aprés .iij. jors ou plus, et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ait ses mains sus son stomac; et met desoz l’ajutoire .i. cussin plain de laine igalment, et regarde chescune houre dou jor ou de la nut, que li figure dou membre brisiet ne se mueve, ou ne soit amollis li liiens; si l’adrece par la vertu de medicine, et li done la viande que nos avons devant mis, en teil maniere que li viande soit au premier subtilz; et quant il comance a reprendre, si soit grosse. Et est costume que li ajutoire et li jambe doient estre repris en .xl. jors dou tout; et adonques lou doit on desliier et aministrer bain et medicines d’oignemens por le leu adrecier.  Et se li estricture est laide et emboee, si demore a desliier .l. jors ou .ij. mois.	And if no such accidents come to pass, do not untie it before three days or more, and have the patient sleep on his back, and place his hands upon his stomach; and put under the shoulder one cushion full of wool evenly, and look each hour of the day or of the night that the figure of the broken limb does not move, or that the ligaments are not softened; if this is so by virtue of medicine, then give him the meat as we have previously set forth, in such manner that the meat be at first subtle; and when he begins to recover, it should be thick. And it is customary that the shoulder and leg ought to be recovered in forty days of all; and thereupon one must untie it and administer bath and medicines of emollient for the place to be healed.  And if the constriction is ugly and encumbered, it remains untied for one day or two months.
de la brisure du bras	of the fracture of the arm
Li bras est compos de .ij. os, qui sont apelez li dui «foscile», de coi li uns est petis, et est cil qui enseut le pouchet; et li autres est grans, et est cil qui est desoz, devers lou petit doi; par aventure brise li grans foscile soulement, ou li petis, et par aventure andui ensamble.	The arm is composed of .ij. bones, which are called the two "fosciles", because one is small, and that is the one that follows the pouch; and the other is large, and that is the one that is below, towards the little joint; by chance breaks the large foscile alone, or the small one, and by chance both together.
Quant li petis fosciles est brisiez, li restaurations est legiere, et li sanations; et quant li grans est brisiez, si est li sanation male, et plus griés que quant il sont brisiez andui ensamble. Se c’est li petis foscile qui est brisiez soulement, si le covient poc estendre legierement, et mettre igal.	When the small foscile is broken, the restoration is light, and the healing; and when the large one is broken, the healing is bad, and more grieved than when they are broken together. If it is the small foscile that is broken alone, then it is necessary to gently stretch it, and put it straight.
Et se c’est li grans foscile, si le covient estraindre plus fort; et l’estende sus .i. cussin, et teigne le pouchet de la main plus haut des autres, et li petis dois plus bas des autres dois, et soit li malaides croisiez sus lui meisme, et .i. cussin devant lui plus haut, que li malaides ne soffre nule labor; puis estende li ministres som bras a la partie desoz a sa main, ou a .i. liien, et uns autres ministres a .i. autre au desus. Et puis le mette li mires igal, selonc sa millor forme.	And if it is the large foscile, then it is necessary to pull harder; and place it on one cushion, and hold the pouch of the hand higher than the others, and the little joints lower than the other joints, and let the patient be crossed on himself, and one cushion in front of him higher, so that the patient does not suffer any labor; then extend the ministers of his arm to the part below his hand, or at one line, and the other minister at another above. And then put the pieces straight, according to their best form.
Et se en la brisure a pieces, si met chescune en son leu, et s’il en i a nule desevree ke poigne lou keur, et tu ne la pues restorer en son leu, si fent sus et l’oste, si com nos avons dit devant.	And if in the fracture there are pieces, put each one in its place, and if there is any detached that pricks the heart, and you cannot restore it to its place, then do as and the bone, as we have said before.
Et se avec la briseure a plaie, je en ai parleit au chapistre singuler; si pren la cure.	And if with the fracture there is a wound, I have spoken of it in the singular chapter; so take care of it.
